# Igros Kodesh

[The following is a translation of the requested section from Igros Kodesh, Vol. 27.]

Regarding your question concerning the matter of *bitul* and *dveikus* in the midst of one’s *avodah* and daily affairs:

Seemingly, these two concepts—the state of *bitul* and the engagement in the mundane activities of the world—are mutually exclusive. Yet, as we find in the *maamarim* of the Rebbeim, the true *avodah* of a *Chossid* is precisely to bridge this divide. It is not that one must retreat from the world to achieve *dveikus*, but rather that one must permeate the world with the light of *Elokus*.

This is the deeper meaning of the *mitzvah* to "know Him in all your ways." It is not merely an act of *hiskafya*—subduing the material—but an *is'hapcha*, transforming the mundane into a vessel for *Kedushah*. When a *shaliach* engages in his *shlichus*, his *bitul* to the *Nasi* and to the *Ribono shel Olam* is not a state of passivity. On the contrary, it is the very engine that drives his *avodah*. 

As the *Alter Rebbe* explains in *Tanya*, the *neshamah* is clothed in the *nefesh habahamit* specifically to elevate it. Therefore, when you find yourself in the midst of the "marketplace," do not view it as a distraction from your *dveikus*. Rather, view it as the arena where your *bitul* is tested and refined. Through this, the *hispaalus* of the heart is channeled into concrete action, and the *taanug* of *dveikus* becomes a lived reality, not just an abstract concept.

May you be successful in your *avodah*, and may you see *brachos* in all your endeavors, both spiritual and material.

## 9998

9998

B"H, 25 Tishrei, 5731
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

I have received your letter requesting a blessing in connection with the New Year. May the Ribono shel Olam fulfill your heart’s desires for good and for blessing, in both material and spiritual matters alike.

It is surely unnecessary to emphasize that daily conduct in accordance with the will of the Creator—even though it is an obligation to be performed without the intent of receiving a reward—is the conduit for receiving the blessings of the Ribono shel Olam in all that one requires. And in matters of goodness and holiness, there is always room for addition, and whoever adds is granted more for himself and his household.

As has been discussed many times, and as is explained in our Torah, the Torah of life, the Ribono shel Olam arranges for a Jew, from time to time in his personal life, matters and instructions from which he can learn regarding spirituality and the avodah of man. Those who are in the army see and feel it as a natural and simple matter that when they receive an order from a trusted commander, they first and foremost carry out the order, and afterwards, when there is time for it, they contemplate the reason for the order, and so on. And even if they do not find a reason, they explain it based on the reality that the commander of the army certainly knows better than an officer in the army, and it goes without saying, better than a simple soldier.

On the other hand, it is also understood that not carrying out the order, or delaying the fulfillment of the order until one understands it with his own intellect, is not merely a private matter or a matter concerning only him and his officer; rather, it affects the entire company. And if it is a time of emergency, it is possible that it affects the entire army, the entire country, and so on.

And another point in this regard: that the fulfillment of the command, with all the importance of the action that depends on it, is first and foremost important because there must be decisive discipline, without any delay in fulfilling the orders immediately, without hesitation, and all the more so without refusal.

All these things and this entire scenario are, in many ways, analogous to the commandments of the King of Kings, the Holy One, Blessed be He, which He gave in His Torah to His people Israel, to each and every one until the end of all generations. He made it known that He does not ask according to His own unlimited power, but according to the power of the human being who is commanded. Rather, a person must fulfill them in the manner of ["na'aseh v'nishma (we will understand)," which is the foundation of the acceptance of the Torah and the mitzvos at the standing at Har Sinai.

And one must know that all of Israel are responsible for one another. Furthermore, our Sages of blessed memory have said—and the great teacher, the Rambam, brings this as a clear halacha—that when a Jew is about to perform an action, and likewise in speech and thought, he must consider that he is balanced [on a scale] and the entire world is balanced, and by one action of his, he will tip the scales both for himself and for the entire world.

It is surely unnecessary to add further explanation to what has been said.

It is understood that the intention is for you and all your friends, may they live and be well, who are in your vicinity, and even more so for all the Children of Israel wherever they may be, for they are all in a state of spiritual warfare. As the verse states, "For you are the fewest of all the peoples," and on the contrary, with even greater intensity, because "na'aseh v'nishma" and mesiras nefesh in a physical army are primarily connected to matters of the body and physicality, whereas "na'aseh v'nishma" regarding the Torah and its mitzvos affects both this world and the World to Come.

With blessings for success and for good tidings in all the aforementioned.

## 11

11

B”H, 4 Marcheshvan, 5731
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the distinguished, G-d-fearing, and learned individual, a man of stature and high standing, who seeks the good of his people and possesses noble character, a scion of a noble lineage, R’ Schneur [Zalman](#_ftn_23) Shlita,

Peace and blessing!

I am a bearer of good news today: regarding your request from some time ago as to whether it is possible to [print](#_ftn_24) the maamarim of the Alter Rebbe in Kfar Chabad in the Holy Land—may it be rebuilt and established—I had previously seen difficulties in this, as it is impossible to send many *biechelach* of *D’chassidus*, etc., there. However, upon searching through the manuscripts, [one biechel](#_ftn_25) (or two) was found that will likely contain enough maamarim for one volume. Therefore, to fulfill your wish, I desire to have it printed in Kfar Chabad, even though the editing will be done here—which will naturally cause some delay, though I hope it will not be for too long.

Another piece of happy news, which also became clear during the search—though it is still ongoing—is that there will likely be more maamarim, both long and short, from the Alter Rebbe for an additional volume, and perhaps more.

It is my firm hope that you have taken a full measure from the matters of the month of Tishrei for the entire year, [as is explained in D’chassidus](#_ftn_26) that Tishrei consists of the letters of *reishis* (beginning)—for [in the verse](#_ftn_27) "from the beginning (*merishis*) of the year until the end of the year," the *alef* is missing, which are the letters of Tishrei. [As the Alter Rebbe explains,](#_ftn_28) the concept of "head" in the Holy Tongue (Rosh Hashanah, Rosh Chodesh), as well as the concept of "beginning," is like the head, which includes all the limbs and directs them according to their place and function. This means, in our context, that all the matters of the month of Tishrei—and especially *Zman Simchaseinu* and Simchas Torah—should be drawn down into all the days of the year. [As is known,](#_ftn_29) the Lubavitch custom was to announce on Motzaei Simchas Torah, ["And Yaakov went on his way"](#_ftn_30); may it be His will that this journey be one of joy, through the joy of Torah, throughout the entire year.

A special joy was caused by the news—which I hope is correct in all its details—that you participated in the *hakafos shniyos* in Jerusalem, the Holy City—may it be rebuilt and established—and that you led the singing of the *nigun* "Jerusalem shall be inhabited as towns without walls" (*Prazos teishev Yerushalayim*). [32]

With appreciation, honor, and a blessing for proper health and good tidings.

## 12

12

[B"H], 5 Marcheshvan, 5731
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished individual, engaged in communal affairs,
Mr. Yaakov Rosenthal

Greetings and blessings!

Following up on my previous letter, I will address, albeit briefly, some of the points raised in your letter:

You explain in your letters, with good reason, that the **initial** failure lay in the preceding laws, where the phrasing was inappropriate, etc.

Now, to my knowledge, this is the first time that the law has attempted to define the term "Jew." Even if the solution had been adequate, the very possibility of doubt in this matter—to the point where it became necessary to vote on it—indicates the most degraded state, etc. All the more so, given that what happened, happened, and they resolved the matter by defining it in a way that omits "according to Halacha."

And even if you were to say that the failure is rooted in the prior law, this does not rectify the failure; it merely explains the *seder hishtalshelus* of how it came to be.

It seems your intention is that had they amended the previous law—as you suggest, by omitting the registration items of religion and nationality, etc.—there would naturally have been no room for the entire aforementioned failure. But now, it is already impossible to restore matters to how they were in the past. It is understood, and also simple, that the attempt to abolish the registration items of religion and nationality would be tied to a struggle with the political parties. Furthermore, and most importantly, as long as the definition of "who is a Jew" remains in any law as it is now, the failure remains in its place.

b) Regarding your writing that so-and-so proposed the phrasing and is therefore the one to blame, etc.—this, too, cannot be changed now.

c) Naturally, I agree with you that even if they were to amend the matter of conversion in the aforementioned law by adding the word "kehalacha" (according to Halacha), it does not guarantee one hundred percent that all matters will be arranged in perfect order. However, any other phrasing is even worse. For example, the proposal to write "according to the Chief Rabbinate"—aside from the fundamental point that this concept has no source in Torah (for according to Torah, all rabbis have equal authority—provided they are equal in yiras shamayim, etc.)—given the deterioration in this field even in our Holy Land, one can surmise that the composition of the Chief Rabbinate in the future is questionable. As is known, the argument in the name of "democracy" is that since there are Reform and Conservative temples, etc., they are certainly also entitled to representatives from among their rabbis, etc., etc. And who knows, perhaps the Karaites should also be included under the banner of *ahavas Yisrael* and *kiruv halevavos*, and so on.

The weak point in the entire matter—though I have not found a solution for this either in the current situation—is the situation itself: that a body elected by every single person living in Eretz Yisrael, regardless of religion, or even those who fight against religion, has the power to decide such a question. In other words, the term "Jew" is a term in Halacha and religion; this means there is no place for the opinion of those who are not **experts** in matters of religion and Halacha and do not identify with them, and all the more so—to vote and decide on this. However, since, as mentioned, the current situation is that two and a half million Jews have enacted a law for themselves that is a **huge lie**—to say that conversion is possible even not according to Halacha, a contradiction in terms—one must find a way to repeal the law as soon as possible.

And if one were to wage a war to prove that conversion is a term in Halacha, and likewise that "Jew" is a term in Halacha, etc., etc., against those for whom no proof through evidence and sources will be of any use—for there is only one decisive proof for them, and that is which party is stronger, and which of the members of such-and-such a party has more connections, etc.—then this war will drag on for days and years, and it is impossible to know the results at all.

This is not the case with the demand to write "conversion kehalacha," which is merely a demand for the status quo, and not as the newspapers and philosophers describe it—that it is a new demand, etc. On the contrary, until the [Shalit] affair, it was understood simply who is a Jew and what is a conversion, especially after the [poll] that Mr. B.G. conducted, which was so simple that it immediately removed the entire issue from the agenda.

As for those who innovated this matter, for some of them it was for inter-party calculations, or for reasons and arguments that have **no** connection to the essence of the issue. For example, the argument that has been pointed to several times with great fanfare: where is the justice and fairness if a person who shed his blood for the defense of the homeland is not registered as a Jew? And when I asked what the connection is between the two matters—for it is understood that for one who shed his blood, there is room to give him rewards of all kinds, etc., but this does not change matters that depend on birth and the **structure** of the body or the neshamah, etc., similar to many matters that depend on special conditions—it has never been heard of in any nation or tongue that such a demand would exist. After all, the Druze have been guarding the borders for twenty years, and yet not one of them has been counted for the High Priesthood, or even for priesthood in general, or even to be called a Jew.

One could elaborate further on the above and on other points in your letter, but it seems I have already pinpointed my fundamental approach to the entire issue: that every single day, conversions are being performed that are not kehalacha, both in Eretz Yisrael and outside of it. And after a short time, I fear it will be impossible to verify how they were converted, for all documents are equal.

In such a time of emergency, one must do everything within one's power to annul the decree as quickly as possible, and after that, to try, at the very least, to eliminate the other weak points. May that "after that" period come soon.

With respect and blessing,

**M. Schneerson**

## 15

13 Cheshvan, 5731
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Mr. Eliezer [Levna](#_ftn_43)
Peace and Blessing!

I am writing to acknowledge receipt of your letter, albeit with some delay.

After asking your forgiveness, I will return once more to the matter of [Hebron](#_ftn_44). It is most astonishing who it was that told you otherwise in an unofficial capacity. As I wrote in my previous letter, in our times, a statement—even when made in a formal and official manner, etc.—is already understood to mean very little, if anything at all. What is most painful and distressing regarding Hebron is that they did not settle for a mere statement, nor even for a mere letter, but specifically for a law, which was passed unanimously and with the consent of all the government ministers.

Regarding your writing that you were told the apartments to be built are a 10-minute distance from the Me'aras HaMachpeilah: I am puzzled as to the relevance of this to the issue we are discussing, which is whether there exists a law of the Israeli government prohibiting a Jew from building an apartment in Hebron. The fact that they designated a location **outside** of Hebron, at a distance of 10 moments or less from the Me'aras HaMachpeilah, changes nothing.

There is another point to add to the matter, which is the basis for the negative attitude even toward the clause in the aforementioned law that apartments will be built outside the city of Hebron, and this is for several reasons:

(a) Accepting this clause automatically necessitates accepting the law in its entirety, and the wise will understand;

(b) The emphasis on building apartments specifically outside the city means that anyone participating in the construction of an apartment outside the city is also lending a hand to this emphasis;

(c) Those who wish to quiet public opinion and lull it to sleep with hints or whispers that this is similar to what happened in Nazareth—where, by Jews settling around the Arab settlement, the Arabs eventually moved away, etc.—this is not at all similar to Hebron. There are several reasons for this, two of which are primary: First, the Arab settlement in Hebron is well-established, and according to reports, they number approximately 50,000 people, with all the amenities, etc., which will not be the case in terms of quantity or quality for the apartments being built around it; that is to say, there is no hope, even if there were such a desire among those setting the policy (which, for now, there is not at all), that what happened in Nazareth will happen in Hebron. And secondly, here there is an official law that has been publicized to the entire world, as mentioned above.

Although I have already [written](#_ftn_45) about this, because of the seriousness of the matter I will repeat it once more: it is worthwhile to alert public opinion in good time so that they do not hand over Jerusalem, our holy city, to the two religions—and, lehavdil, etc., etc., to the religion of Israel. For even though they officially declare that Jerusalem is not a subject of discussion, to my great sorrow and shame, the search now is to find a formula that will not stir up the public opinion of the children of Israel in Eretz Yisrael, in order to cover up the reality that they will hand over the Old City of Jerusalem (naturally, for reasons of justice, democracy, fairness, etc.) to three owners. I pray that the outcry now will forestall the evil in time, and that the aforementioned will not, chas v'chalilah, come to pass—not even under the guise that the three parties have equal standing, or that the police will be joint, and so on and so forth. As I wrote, they have not yet reached a conclusion as to what formula will not change the alarming reality mentioned above, while at the same time allowing the propagandists to emphasize that it is an "achievement"—similar to the "achievement" of the ceasefire along the [Canal](#_ftn_46) for the security of the holy nation in Eretz Yisrael (which, by means of this "achievement," wiped out in one moment all the achievements of the IDF on the banks of the Suez Canal), and similar to the "achievement" of the terrible law regarding [who is a Jew](#_ftn_47), according to which any conversion by anyone, without distinction, makes one a Jew, and that this is an achievement for the religion of Israel, etc., etc.—a matter worthy of shame, anger, sorrow, and heartache.

With respect and with wishes that, finally, you too will be able to share good news regarding true achievements.

The way to receive the blessings of the Ribono shel Olam is by strengthening oneself in daily conduct according to the instructions of the Torah, *Toras Chaim*, including the *middah* of *bitachon*.

## 10

[16 Cheshvan, 5731]

The importance of the matter is certainly clear and simple; however, many yeshivos and circles already have something of this nature, or an office that deals with a portion of the aforementioned problems.

To unify them as mentioned above—it is doubtful whether it is worthwhile (even if there were someone prepared to do so).

It is understood that it is **highly** worthwhile that each of the aforementioned should expand their activities, and take an interest not only in their own limited circle; and it goes without saying that the conversation with each one must be direct.

## 11

11

B”H, 20 Marcheshvan, 5731
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the congregation of Yeshurun, lovers and supporters of Torah and mitzvos,
May Hashem keep them alive,

Greetings and blessings!

Today, on the birthday of the Rebbe Rashab, of blessed memory, the founder of Tomchei Temimim in Lubavitch—which, after many wanderings, was transplanted to America by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory—I come with this appeal.

This year, on Simchas Torah, it was 70 years since the [sichas-kodesh](#_ftn_54) of the founder of the Yeshiva, which was delivered in connection with the third anniversary of the founding of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim.

In that sicha, the Rebbe predicted a time of *cherpu ikvos meshichecha*—those who revile and push away the footsteps of Moshiach Tzidkeinu. He then expressed the certain hope that the students, the "Temimim," would serve as a counter-measure, and would be the *mesiras-nefesh* soldiers, the Torah-warriors, who would drive away the darkness and bring the Geulah closer.

In our generation, we see clearly how the eternal words of the founder of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim are being realized. On one hand, we see a generation of youth who are, unfortunately, very confused, internally torn, and externally unbridled and destructive. But on the other hand, we see the yeshiva youth, especially the students of Tomchei Temimim, as exemplary, living examples of how Jewish youth should conduct themselves; they are *neros leha'ir*—lights that shine and illuminate their surroundings with the radiance of *ner mitzvah v'Torah ohr*, and with the *maor shebaTorah*, the teachings of Chassidus. They justify the great hopes that the founders of Tomchei Temimim, our Rebbes, of blessed memory, have placed upon them.

In the coming weeks, on the eve of the annual celebration of Merkaz Yeshivos Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch, I hope and am certain that Anash, may they live, in particular, and the lovers and supporters of Torah, may they live, in general, will respond warmly to the call of the administration. I urge everyone to do—each according to their fullest ability—everything that depends on them to ensure that the annual celebration is carried out with great success, not only in spiritual matters but also in material ones, simply to provide the necessary financial assistance for the yeshiva to continue its holy work and to carry out the intent of the founder of the Yeshiva to the **fullest** extent—which means in a manner of *mosif v'holech, mosif v'ohr* (increasing and continuing, increasing and shining).

May Hashem Yisbarach help each and every one to fulfill the above, and may this also be a channel and vessel for the fulfillment of their hearts' desires for good and for blessing, for themselves and their families, may they live, in everything they need, both materially and spiritually.

With honor and with blessings for success and for good tidings,

**M. Schneerson**

12

[B"H], 21 Cheshvan, 5731
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed Rabbi and Chassid, G-d-fearing and learned, who occupies himself with [the publication of] Chassidic discourses and Chassidic writings, etc. [Rashi]—may he live.

Peace and blessing!

I acknowledge receipt of your letter, and in accordance with your note, I am enclosing a copy of my letter to the esteemed Rabbi Hutner—may he live.

This is the place to come with a request and an entreaty, etc., to you as well, especially since you are the one urging and pressing me to write to the aforementioned and to provide my own comments. I ask that you, too, do everything in your power to facilitate the publication of additional volumes, and at the fastest possible pace. In the language of the Alter Rebbe in Iggeres HaKodesh, Epistle 21: "with wondrous alacrity," to show his joy and desire, etc. And "there is nothing that can stand before the will" (not even the intellectual rationale that it must be perfect, etc., which I was told is one of the reasons for the slow pace of publication).

Regarding your letter concerning my words about Jerusalem—the Holy City, may it be rebuilt and established speedily—where you were told that "there is no such thing" [that the situation is not as I described]: I wish it were so. But to my regret, the current situation is **not at all** as they say, and what increases the apprehension even more is that they are lulling the public and the community to sleep. In the well-known idiom: "They claimed wheat and he agreed with barley." I have already warned about this in my previous remarks. It should be known that the delay now is **only** because they are searching for a formula that will satisfy the "world-golem," and the politicians, as is their way, operate on the premise that this "world-golem" constitutes the vast majority of all those surrounding them. How many formulas have they already invented? Among them is the one I mentioned, which would be (not a "city of a great king," but) a "city of three kings." And since there is no king in Israel and everyone does what is right in his own eyes—for we live in a democratic regime—it would be "three partners," ordered according to quantity, for that is what is decisive in a democracy: the Christians, the Muslims, etc. [Last night, a new formula was updated and printed in the **most** important newspaper here—the TIMES—taken from the words of the Foreign Minister in the name of the entire **government**, which, translated into Hebrew, means that the *desire* of the government is political control of Jerusalem, and not to relinquish the places upon which security depends, such as the Golan Heights, as well as specific points on the West Bank of the Jordan. And this is well understood.]

May it be the will that as we approach the month of redemption, the month of Kislev, we will be redeemed—even before the coming of Mashiach Tzidkeinu—from the Hellenists of our current era. And through your "wellsprings spreading outward," the matter and content of the Festival of Redemption, the 19th of Kislev, will immediately ignite in every single person candles with pure oil specifically, which has not been touched by the hand of a non-Jew (and not even moved), to illuminate at once both the home and the outside, in a manner of "increasing and adding light."

To your relatives—may they live—who are there: you should send regards **if** they agree to it, but you must not pressure them.

With respect and blessing for proper health and good tidings in all that was mentioned, and with a blessing of Mazal Tov for the birth of your grandson—may he live and be well.

**M. Schneerson**

13

21 Cheshvan, 5731
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Rabbi Yehoshua Hutner

Greetings and blessings,

I have received the 13th volume of the Talmudic Encyclopedia, and I cannot refrain from expressing the extent of my impression and joy at seeing this additional volume. Although the preceding volumes are also great—with the true greatness of our Torah, which is "longer than the earth in measure and broader than the sea" —each additional volume, as I believe I mentioned to you in our conversation, not only adds clarification to various matters and rules within the general and specific principles of Torah, but also adds to all the previous volumes. As we spoke then, the nature of an encyclopedia is such that the true completeness of the first volume depends also upon the last volume and the final entry within it.

Continuing our conversation from that time, this is the place to mention again and again, with every expression of request, regarding the publication of the subsequent volumes with the **greatest** possible alacrity. As the saying goes, "an hour earlier is better," and as mentioned, this affects all the volumes that have already appeared. Surely, for one such as yourself, no further explanation is needed.

May it be the will of Hashem that the desire of Hashem will succeed in the hands of all those participating in this most exalted endeavor, to publish volume after volume with the greatest possible speed, until you are able to celebrate the completion of the work soon. Following that, one should immediately begin a second edition (or additions, etc.), for surely the very appearance of the volumes adds to the innovations of Torah in general, and to this type of encyclopedia in particular, as mentioned above—that it is "longer than the earth in measure."

This also serves as an answer to the argument I have heard several times, that the delay in publication is due to the effort to make it more and more complete. In addition to the response that if so, there is no end to the matter, as mentioned above, it is impossible that new insights will not arise. Surely, several matters have already been clarified in entries that have already appeared. Moreover, this is precisely one of the wonders of the Torah, the wisdom and will of the Holy One, Blessed be He: that it is like a fountain and a source of living waters that flow and continue to increase, as the great teacher, the Rambam, says at the conclusion and seal of his book: "The earth will be full of the knowledge of Hashem as the waters cover the sea".

With respect and blessings, and especially with a blessing for success in the aforementioned, to bring good tidings very soon regarding the publication of volume 14, 15, and so on.

As is my custom, I will permit myself to add a suggestion regarding the encyclopedia, which has long been on my mind and was strengthened significantly upon receiving this volume. Its important part is the matter of *chazakah* (presumption/status). It is this: it would be worthwhile to add to the explanation of the entries the names of the books that explain the matters of the entry specifically and in detail. It is standard in many encyclopedias to add at the end of the entries (especially the important ones) what is now called a "bibliography"—a list of books and sources. Especially since, in this case, there would be no (excessive) burden, as surely everyone who has worked on a specific entry has used and continues to use these books, and it is only necessary to clarify if there are others, etc.

Even though several volumes have already appeared and do not contain the aforementioned bibliography, surely in this case the principle of "do not cast aspersions on the earlier ones" does not apply, especially since the matter is being added by the publisher of the earlier ones. To complete the bibliography for the entries that have already appeared, there is room to publish a special booklet of bibliography for these entries, in the format and typeface of the encyclopedia.

It is simple that although every entry contains several cross-references within it—which are **extremely** necessary and essential—and in great abundance, they do not provide the benefit expected of the aforementioned bibliography. Especially since the cross-references are numerous, and not every mind is capable of selecting from among them which are the foundational and specialized books.

I ask your forgiveness for these comments, and my hope is that they will be discussed, and the merit of the many will assist, and "from my flesh I shall see" the great benefit expected.

P.S. At the time, I received your telegram regarding my relative, Rabbi Yehoshua, and the development of matters is surely known to you.

## 14

[B"H], 26 MarCheshvan, 5731
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed Rabbi, the G-d-fearing, Torah-learned, whose work is the work of Heaven, etc.,
Rabbi Yitzchak [may he live],

Shalom u’Bracha!

In response to your letter, in which you raise a point regarding the words of the Tzemach Tzedek in *Derech Mitzvosecha*, Mitzvas Ner Chanukah, section 2, where he writes near the beginning of the subject: "And in this manner, one can understand on a lofty level the concept of *tikkun* and *emes* in the 'two apples' of the cheeks of *Arich*, etc. [as it is written], 'Give truth to Yaakov'."

You question this, noting that it is explicitly stated in the *Zohar* [in the *Idra Rabba*] that the *tikkun* and *emes* of the [Thirteen Attributes of Moshe] correspond to *yashuv yerachameinu*, etc., whereas "Give truth to Yaakov" in the Thirteen Attributes of Michah corresponds to *nosei avon* in the Thirteen Attributes of Moshe.

Seemingly, one can further strengthen this difficulty: one cannot say that this is a novel point (an addition, or the like) in Kabbalah (the accepted Kabbalah of the Arizal) beyond what is written in the *Zohar* (in the parts available to us)—in the manner of the many concepts found in the writings of the Arizal that are not found in the *Zohar*—for in the writings of the Arizal, the aforementioned is cited from the *Idra Rabba* as a matter of **practical** *halacha* in the *kavanos* of *Tashlich* (see the writings of the Arizal; see also *Shaar HaKavanos*, *Drushei Rosh Hashanah* before *Drush* 4; *Pri Etz Chaim* in its place; and elsewhere).

Furthermore, it is impossible to say that this is a novel point of Chassidic teaching (in the manner we find regarding the *kavanos* of the *mikveh*, and in the language of the Mitteler Rebbe in his *Siddur* [at the beginning of Part 2, in the *maamar* entitled *Lehavin Klalus Kavanas HaMikveh*]: "For the Arizal, the general *kavanah* is mentioned, etc., but regarding the *kavanah* of the *mikveh* printed in the name of the Baal Shem Tov, etc.")—for the Alter Rebbe also cited the aforementioned [in his *Siddur*] in the *kavanos* of *Tashlich*.

However, the matter is this: The Tzemach Tzedek (and likewise in *Likutei Torah*, *maamar* beginning *Eileh Masei* (93c), which the Tzemach Tzedek cites here) is not bringing a proof **from the *tikkun*** of Michah [and it is obvious that his intention is not that **this** (*tikkun* and *emes*) is the *tikkun* of Michah, "Give [truth] to Yaakov"]. Rather, he is proving from the **verse**, "Give truth to Yaakov"—that *emes* (in whichever level it may be) is given to Yaakov (who relates to that level).

This is similar to the many instances where our Sages derive from verses of the Thirteen Attributes of Mercy—including the verse "Give truth to Yaakov" (as noted in *Beis Aharon* and elsewhere)—matters that have no connection to the Thirteen Attributes of Mercy. Moreover, we find this even in practical *halacha* in the revealed Torah: *Dun minei* (even a literal law, but) *u’oki b’asra* (apply it in its place).

With respect and blessing,

[The letters from the Rebbe] were surely received in due time.

## 1023

B"H, 17 Kislev, 5731
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed and distinguished individual, who engages in communal needs with many accomplishments, etc.,
Rabbi Yaakov [Goldman](#_ftn_144)

Greetings and blessings!

I received your letter, albeit with some delay, in which you write regarding matters of Yeshivas Toras Emes.

First and foremost, I wish to express my thanks for your attention and interest. Surely this is not merely a matter of sentiment—though that, too, is essential—but rather you are acting in a way that leads to practical results. It is certainly possible for you, directly and through your colleagues and friends, to do and accomplish much in this regard.

Given the magnitude of the matter, it is superfluous to urge you further, even according to your own letter. I will only recall a [saying](#_ftn_145) that was frequently on the lips of my father-in-law, the Rebbe: regarding money and the like, one can "make it up"—it is possible to pay a debt tomorrow or the day after. But regarding accepting one more student and another, firstly, every day is a whole world in the matter of Torah study and Torah-based education. One cannot fulfill the obligation of yesterday, [for](#_ftn_146) every single day performs its own work, and it is enough to satisfy oneself with fulfilling the measure of work that must be done on that day. Furthermore, especially in our current era, it is understood that one must immediately accept anyone who expresses a desire to enter a kosher educational institution, for after this "time of favor" passes, who knows, etc.—and a word to the wise is sufficient.

May it be the will of Hashem that each of us, within the entirety of Klal Yisrael, acts in matters of education in purity and holiness, and in matters of Torah and mitzvos, in a manner appropriate to the instruction of the upcoming days of Chanukah. May we do so with *mesiras nefesh*, as instructed by our Alter Rebbe—whose *Chag HaGeulah* these days are—and with joy and goodness of heart.

With respect and blessing.

P.S. It is understood that I reviewed the contents of your letter with attention. At the end of my letter above, I have also included my response to the conclusion of your letter, where you mention that "this year you reach the age of [retirement](#_ftn_147) from work." Surely there is no need for someone like you to be reminded that there is no retirement age from work in the dissemination of Yiddishkeit, especially in the field of education. On the contrary, according to the [instruction](#_ftn_148) that we increase in holiness, it should be the opposite of retirement—namely, addition and ascent. Even if you were to say that in a certain institution or position there are restrictions that necessitate retirement, etc., [in the words of the verse](#_ftn_149), "The whole land is before you." Who knows better than you the magnitude of the responsibility and the seriousness of the situation regarding the dissemination of traditional Yiddishkeit without compromise, especially concerning the youth? The time is not at all appropriate for retirement, etc., but rather, on the contrary, for more and more addition. We are promised that one who comes [to purify](#_ftn_150)—and according to the precision of our Alter [Rebbe](#_ftn_151): to purify oneself and to purify others—is assisted with great assistance.

And last but not least, I was happy to read in your letter about the definitive confirmation regarding the grant in question for Yeshivas Toras Emes, and I thank you especially for this.

## 10:24

[B"H], Erev Yud-Tes Kislev, 5731
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To all participants in the annual dinner
of the Merkaz Yeshivos Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch
May Hashem preserve them and grant them life,

Shalom u’vracha!

The annual celebration of the Merkaz Yeshivos Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch takes place this year between the auspicious days of Yud-Tes Kislev and Chanukah. These two dates share a close connection, which also underscores the special significance of this undertaking.

The historical events that led to Chanukah and to Yud-Tes Kislev share common themes, both in their content and in the directives they offer to each and every one of us in our daily lives.

**Chanukah** reminds us of the mesiras nefesh of a handful of Jews—the Chashmonaim and their followers—who fought to preserve the purity and uncompromising nature of the Torah Hakdosha at a time when darkness and confusion threatened true Jewish faith and authentic Jewish values. With the help of the Ribono shel Olam and through many miracles, they secured the purity and holiness of *ner mitzvah v’Torah ohr* in daily Jewish life.

**Yud-Tes Kislev** reminds us of the mesiras nefesh of the Alter Rebbe, Baal HaTanya and Shulchan Aruch, to disseminate the inner light of Torah and mitzvos through [Toras] the Baal Shem Tov—the teachings of Chassidus—and how he, too, fought for this on behalf of Klal Yisrael, with Hashem’s help and through many miracles. Since then—for nearly 200 years—Chassidus has been a fountainhead of uncompromising Torah-Yiddishkeit for authentic Jewish living in all parts of the world.

Just as Chanukah expresses itself in three main aspects, symbolized by the mitzvah of *ner Chanukah*, which emphasizes: (a) the purity of Torah (the untouched *pach shemen* with the seal of the Kohen Gadol), (b) the necessity to spread the light of Torah and mitzvos even outside (*al pesach beiso mibachutz*), and (c) in an increasing measure (*mosif v’holech*),

So too, Yud-Tes [Kislev] expresses itself in these same three main aspects, in the slogan and approach of *yafutzu mayanosecha chutzah*: (a) to spread in an increasing measure (*yafutzu*), (b) the pure fountains of Torah and mitzvos, permeated with the light and warmth of Chassidus (*mayanosecha*), (c) to reach and penetrate even those who are currently still "outside" (*chutzah*). Yud-Tes Kislev is, in essence, a continuation and completion of Chanukah.

The Merkaz Yeshivos Tomchei Temimim unites and embodies the spirit and content of Chanukah and Yud-Tes Kislev. The Lubavitcher Yeshiva has raised, and continues to raise, generations of *temimim* who disseminate Torah and mitzvos *al taharas hakodesh*, permeated with Chassidishe vitality, warmth, and mesiras nefesh. They are living lights; not only do they shine and illuminate their surroundings, but with a deeply ingrained ahavas Yisrael, they ignite many sparks in circles that are, unfortunately, still "outside," in a manner of *mosif v’holech mosif v’ohr*—more lights and more illumination.

The Merkaz Yeshivos Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch therefore deserves the fullest support of all who understand the preciousness of Torah and mitzvos and who recognize the responsibility that lies upon every Jewish man and woman to strengthen Torah-Yiddishkeit in general, and among the younger generation in particular.

The annual undertaking of the Merkaz Yeshivos Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch is a challenge, and at the same time an opportunity, to express in a concrete way one’s inner Jewish consciousness and responsibility by providing the necessary financial assistance to enable the Lubavitcher Yeshiva to continue and expand its vital work.

May Hashem Yisbarach grant each and every one success in this to the fullest measure. This is also the path to receive Hashem’s blessings for oneself and one’s family, in everything one needs, both materially and spiritually.

With respect and blessing for much success and for good tidings in all the above,

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 126

126

[B"H], between 19 Kislev and Chanukah, 5731
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the Women and Girls of Chabad
May Hashem grant them life

Blessings and peace!

During these days between 19 Kislev—the Chag HaGeulah of our Alter Rebbe, founder of the Chabad Chassidic teachings—and the upcoming days of Chanukah,

It is my hope that each and every one of you, within the entirety of Klal Yisrael, will utilize these auspicious days to increase activities of spreading Torah and mitzvos, illuminated and permeated with the light and vitality of Chassidus, both within the home and in the surrounding environment, in accordance with the lessons of these days.

And it is surely known to you that one of the primary lessons of the Chag HaGeulah of 19 Kislev is **"spreading the wellsprings outward" (hafatzas hama'ayanos chutzah)**, which contains three elements:

a) To influence even those—individuals and circles—who are still "outside";

b) To revive them with the living waters of the **wellsprings** of Torah and Chassidus;

c) And to do so in a manner of **spreading (hafatzah)**, constantly increasing and growing.

And this is also one of the primary lessons of the days of Chanukah, through the mitzvah of lighting the Chanukah candle "at the entrance of his house from the outside," in a manner of "increasing and going," adding light. For even though by lighting one candle on the first night of Chanukah one fulfills the mitzvah according to the law and in its entirety, we add another candle on the second night, and continue to increase—to teach that this is how it should be regarding the spreading of the "candle of the mitzvah and the light of Torah."

And there is a special lesson in this for the women and girls of Israel in general, and the women and girls of Chabad in particular, based on the statement of our Sages, of blessed memory: "They (the women) too were part of that miracle."

With blessings for success in all that is mentioned, and to continue the influence of these days throughout the entire year, increasing and shining,

**M. Schneerson**

a) To influence those—individuals and circles—who are still "outside";

b) To enliven them with the living waters of the wellsprings of Torah and Chassidus;

c) And to do so in a manner of **Hafatzah**—spreading ever further and further.

This is also one of the primary directives of the days of Chanukah, through the mitzvah of the Chanukah candles, which one lights ["at the entrance of his house from the outside"], [adding] another candle each night of Chanukah. For [although] when one lights a single candle on the first night of Chanukah, one has fulfilled the mitzvah according to the law and in its entirety, one must nonetheless add another candle on the second night, and so on, with one more candle each night. This demonstrates that one must likewise spread the light of [the mitzvah candle and the Torah light].

There is a special significance in this for Jewish women and girls in general, and for N'shei U’Bnos Chabad in particular, in accordance with what [our Sages] have said: "They (the women) also had a share in this miracle."

With wishes for success in all of the above, and to draw down the influence of these days into all the days of the year—adding light,

**M. Schneerson**

## 29

[20 Kislev, 5731]

Regarding what you wrote in your *hadran* : We will discuss this (as a continuation and conclusion) on the *Shabbos* following the *chag*. And the point (which pertains to your letter) is:

1) Every **detail** in the language of the *Gemara* (and consequently, in a **halachic** narrative as well) must contain a lesson in that *halacha*—for otherwise, it would **not** have been cited. This is the foundation of the *hadran*.

2) The explanation that it refers here to *bishulei akum*—it does not need to be explicitly stated by the *poskim* (as they are not commentators on the *Gemara*), and regarding the final ruling—there is no practical difference (except that according to the *poskim* who hold there is no prohibition of *bluah* [absorbed taste] in *bishul akum*, it refers here to a case where it was *b'ayin* [the food itself was present]).

3) That an *esrog* (fried, see *Shabbos* 108b) is fit for a king’s table—it is explicitly stated that *Shavor Malka* (King Shavor) had it brought before him.

## 13

13

[B"H], Days of Chanukah, 5731
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of the letter...

The concept of Chanukah – they established the miracle through candles. Now, there are two things in a candle, and both are called a "candle": the oil and the wick that one lights, and the vessel that holds the oil and the wick within it.

Regarding a wax candle and the like, one could say that the part of the candle that has not yet melted serves as the vessel, or that the vessel is not strictly required, even *lechatchilah*.

Chazal explained the verse "The candle of Hashem is the soul of man," for "a mitzvah is a candle and Torah is light."

For the wick and the oil are (in *avodas Hashem*) the person and the *mitzvos*.

And when one lights the candle (which is its purpose and perfection), when one performs a *mitzvah*—one "lights" the object through which the *mitzvah* is performed (and in combination with the power of this *asiyah*, a part of the "wick"), light is created.

There are many types of light in a candle, and in the language of Chazal, they are collectively referred to as: *nehora oukma* (black light) and *nehora chivra* (white light).

*Nehora oukma* is that which is close to the wick—the performance of the *mitzvah* in a way where the existence of the person performing it is still evident. *Nehora chivra* is the performance of a *mitzvah* *lishmah*. In the language of the Rambam: one engages in Torah and *mitzvos*, etc., not for the sake of anything in the world, etc., but rather one does the truth because it is true, etc.

Now, Torah and *mitzvos* are specifically in this world, where man must perform them and thereby refine his portion in the world for which he was created.

One could say that this is the concept of the vessel (of the candle). And just as no two people are alike, so too are there many types of vessels.

Even though, in a general sense—every "candle of Hashem is the soul of man" which is in the Menorah—the entire Menorah is of "beaten gold," from its base (the lowest foot) to its flower (the greatest *tzaddikim*).

May it be Hashem’s will that every man and woman light their candle—their soul, the *nefesh elokis* and the *nefesh habahamis*—and their portion in the world.

And in the manner of the *halachah* of Beis Hillel—that it increases and continues, adding and shining—until the fulfillment of the prophecy, "The night shall shine as the day."

With blessings for success in spreading the *maayanos*,

**M. Schneerson**

Regarding your note on the *Shema Yisrael*—see also the *maamar* "Lehavin..." on the *Seder HaNikudim* (by the Alter Rebbe), which is relevant to this.

## 10:35

[B"H], days of Chanukah, 5731
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To my relative, the great Rabbi, the great Chossid, G-d-fearing and learned, whose work is the work of Heaven, etc.,
R' Chaim Shalom, may he live, Halevi

Shalom u’Bracha!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from the fifth night of Chanukah, as well as your book, *Tosafos Rashi*. Many thanks, many thanks. See the end of the letter.

Regarding the matter of Chanukah...

The entire *pidyon nefesh* will be read, *bli neder*, at the *tziyun*.

With wishes of *mazal tov, mazal tov* for the wedding of your son, Avraham Tzvi, may he live.

P.S. As a token of affection – regarding your book:

To interpret a verse outside of its context is **not** the way of *peshat* (**which is** the way of Rashi on the Torah), and it is not a method of study for a five-year-old (beginning *Mikra*). This is especially true when the explanation comes **after** the verse being interpreted, and there is no indication of this in the verse's original place. One must conclude that in its original place, the explanation is unnecessary; rather, the second verse raises a difficulty or the like regarding the first verse, and it is resolved by the new explanation. Alternatively, the new explanation is merely for the sake of clarity, and at the time of studying the first verse, there was no room for it, or no source for it, or in its original place the new explanation is simple and does not require interpretation, or some similar reason. Based on this:

**Bereishis 1:1**: "Es" (את) – even according to *peshat*, it comes to include (see Rashi there 4:1-2), but sometimes it is merely for linguistic elegance (ibid. 1:4 and in countless other places). Based on this:

In its place, it is **impossible** for Rashi to interpret "Es hashamayim" etc., as including their offspring, etc. – for this is the **opposite** of the *peshat* of the subsequent verses (that each was created on its own day). Only the difficulty in the wording "Yehi me'oros" (unlike what was written previously, "Tadshe ha'aretz" and the like), which **compels** one to say that they were **already created**, makes it possible to interpret "Es" hashamayim as "including," etc., and not (merely) for elegance, etc.

**Ibid. 3:14**: [In its place] there is no source for the innovation that it is a segment, etc. – and based on this, the precision of Rashi in Yirmiyahu, "We learn from here," is also clarified. *V'kal l'havin*.

**Ibid. 3:17**: In its place, there is no need to explain that *itzavon* does not necessarily mean a feeling opposite to joy, for **previously** he already explained "itzvonecha" as pain (brought about by the growing, etc.) and toil.

And Rashi did not cite this verse in Koheles, but rather the one **after it** – because **in that one** the discussion is about **physical** toil, similar to what is discussed in Koheles. *V'kal l'havin*.

And in this manner, one must explain in **every place**.

I thank you for this and hope that these were words that came from the heart. Furthermore, even regarding that part of our conversation with which you did not agree, this did not affect the transmission of the words as I had said them. Thank you for this as well.

Initially, I had intended to ask you also about the response to my words and my hopes regarding several matters (which, in my opinion, are among the most important for our people, [a nation](#_ftn_238) alone in the land, Eretz HaKodesh and the Diaspora alike). However, reality has come and answered, at least regarding the response of some of the individuals about whom you write: to provoke a great nation even more than in the past, and to exacerbate relations more than until now—a trend that is only increasing—along with conversations behind closed doors regarding further concessions, and so on.

Despite all this, my hope is that this is not the response of the majority in the current situation. Therefore, I thank you in advance if I could know whether there was a positive response, at least from the minority of the individuals with whom you spoke. For in our era, an era of changes and upheavals, the minority of today may well be the decisive majority tomorrow or the day after.

My hope is that your interpretation at the end of your letter is correct; my intention in the closing, "Tzion and the complete Yerushalayim," is—as we discussed—the rejection of [partnership](#_ftn_239) as well, especially since this partnership is one of three partners, meaning two against one. After our conversation, and especially during a time of joy connected to Torah, the Torah of truth, there is certainly no need to add to this.

May it be the will of Hashem that, fitting for these days of Chanukah, there be an increase of light for all Bnei Yisrael wherever they may be. And as in the event of the days of Chanukah, the victory of the Bnei Yisrael who are faithful to Hashem and His Torah over the Hellenists, and to educate the people, in all its strata, with the education of Chanukah (Chinuch-Ha) in all the points mentioned.

With respect and blessing.

## 1042

B"H, Rosh Chodesh Teves, 5731
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, Torah-learned, and distinguished individual, who seeks the good of his people and possesses noble character traits, a scion of a noble lineage, R' Schneur [Zalman](#_ftn_256) shlita,

Greetings and blessings!

I trust you have received my previous [letter](#_ftn_257), along with the enclosed maamar of the Alter Rebbe, which was published in connection with the Chag HaGeulah of 19 Kislev.

Together with the writing of this letter, I have requested the representatives of Anash who visited here to personally deliver to you the **Sefer HaErchim Chabad**, which has just arrived from the bindery. It, too, was intended to appear by the past 19 Kislev, and surely [this](#_ftn_259) is also for the good.

It is a double pleasure for me that the work has been produced with hiddur—in addition to the internal hiddur (the content), it also possesses external hiddur.

[It](#_ftn_260) seems to me that you played a part in securing the grant from the Claims Conference for this project; if so, your pleasure will be further increased as you see the fruits of your labor.

With respect, appreciation, and blessings for an illuminating Chanukah and a good month.

## 1043

1043

B”H, Rosh Chodesh Teves, 5731
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mr. Dov Ettinger

Greetings and Blessings!

I have just received your letter of 19 Kislev, the day of tidings, a day of special virtue, and the Festival of Redemption, in which you write regarding the publication of a memorial book, etc.

Surely you are aware of the [custom] of the Rebbe’s house—I refer to what has been practiced in the house of Lubavitch for many years—that we do not participate with maamarim, letters, and the like in memorial books. There are several reasons for this, which are understood, etc. And surely you have noted that I did not even participate in the "Sefer HaKen," a memorial book marking 150 years since the passing of the Alter Rebbe, and other similar instances.

Since, on the other hand, it is indeed appropriate to publish a memorial book if it is edited properly and adorned as required with words of Torah, both the revealed and the inner dimensions of Torah, etc., then in such a case—and specifically in this matter—there [are] letters in connection with the unveiling of the tombstone of the great Gaon, the great Chossid, the great Tzaddik, etc., Rabbi B.M. z”l Ettinger. There is also room to include—in a respectful place, of course—a [segment] from the memoirs of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, which speaks of him and was printed in the collection **HaTamim**, which has just been republished in the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt and established.

May it be the will of Hashem that you succeed in fulfilling your heart’s desires for the good in the publication of the memorial book for the young man Dov, Hy”d.

– In such a case, it requires consideration whether one should multiply titles after mentioning "Hy”d," which indicates that he fell for the sanctification of Hashem’s name –

And especially since, according to your letter, many Torah insights in both the revealed Torah and Chassidus will appear in the aforementioned book.

In accordance with the content of your letter, I am sending my response urgently and quickly.

With respect and blessings.

## 1044

B"H, Zos Chanukah, 5731
Brooklyn, N.Y.

It was with pleasure that I received the news regarding the organizing of the farbrengen and your participation in the farbrengen of Yud-Tes Kislev, the day of the liberation of Rabbeinu HaZaken [and our own liberation and the redemption of our souls].

May it be the will of Hashem that the inspiration of this auspicious day be carried through all the days of the year, and extend even to actual deed —which is the main thing: strengthening oneself in the study of Torah, both Nigleh and Chassidus, and in the performance of mitzvos with light, vitality, and enthusiasm. And all of this—in a manner that is "increasing and continuing," as is one of the directives of these days of Chanukah.

And especially according to the teachings of the Baal Shem Tov, that from everything one must learn a moral lesson for a person’s avodah to his Creator—and how much more so is this true regarding a fundamental and general matter such as Chanukah.

And furthermore, it can be said regarding this:

The concept of Chanukah...

With respect and blessing for good tidings in the aforementioned,

**M. Schneerson**

## 1046

1046

[B"H](#_ftn_273), 7 Teves, 5731
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed and distinguished individual, who engages in the needs of the community, etc.,
R' [Avraham](#_ftn_274) Yitzchak HaKohen, may he live, known as Prof. Katz

Peace and blessing!

After the longest interval during which I received no news from you at all, and specifically nothing regarding your publications—though regarding news I did inquire and receive information through our mutual friends, which was not the case regarding your publications—it was a most pleasant surprise to receive the book **Ginzei Mishnah**.

Beyond the intrinsic value of uncovering the hidden treasures of our Torah, and specifically the Mishnah of the Tannaim, there is also the matter of *hish'ta'ah* (beautifying) before Him in the performance of mitzvos, in that it was published with such splendor, etc.

[And if](#_ftn_277) in all eras we are commanded to beautify before Him in the performance of mitzvos, how much more so in our own era, where externality occupies such a significant place, and there are many for whom the way to draw them toward something good—and there is no [good](#_ftn_278) other than the living waters of our Torah—is to begin with external beauty. And for one such as yourself, there is no need to elaborate on this.

May it be G-d’s will that you continue to publish the Torah of the Rishonim, and moving from one subject to a related one, may it be His will that you succeed in uncovering within the Acharonim the Torah of the Rishonim—those who invested their very souls and essence into their Torah. My intention is to reveal within those you influence—those you influence directly and also indirectly—the *ma'or* (the light) within their souls, for they are the children’s children of the [Rishonim](#_ftn_279), who were like angels, reaching back to our forefathers Avraham, Yitzchak, and Yaakov. This is a revelation that will be expressed in daily life [contrary to the approach of certain circles in this country who fulfill their obligation for the entire year on three occasions (days) a year], and extending to actual deed.

With respect and blessing,

**M. Schneerson**

P.S. I have received the book and will return it. A volume of **Sefer HaArachim Chabad** was recently published and is being sent to you separately. It will surely be of interest to you.

## 1049

B"H, 8 Teves, 5731
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mr. Naftali Herzog
Tel Aviv

Shalom u’Bracha!

I acknowledge receipt of your letter from the 8th of Chanukah, in which you write regarding the Chabad shul in Tzfas and what you found there and did about it.

Certainly, there is no place for expressing thanks for this, for [the reward](#_ftn_290) of a mitzvah is the mitzvah itself—the act itself is the greatest reward. However, I wish to express my satisfaction and *nachas* regarding your good work in this matter, which surely served as an example to others who were present at the time, and to those who visit there in particular.

For the benefit of the matter, and seeing your interest in it, it would be worthwhile for you to be in contact with my relative, the esteemed *chossid* Rabbi Avraham Zvi Slonim (Jerusalem, Shikun Chabad), who has visited Tzfas several times. As a native of Jerusalem and the director of Kollel Chabad, he has also been in contact with the activists in Tzfas regarding this shul. Thank you in advance for your efforts in this matter.

With respect and blessing.

P.S. In response to the conclusion of your letter regarding your background as coming from *misnagdim* and so on, it is surely known to you as well that at the time when they publicized the [opposition](#_ftn_291) to Chassidus and Chassidim, they also included the reason for the opposition: the fear that the approach of Chassidus would lead to leniencies in the observance of *mitzvos*, and even more than mere leniency, as is explained in the proclamations [and the *kuntreisim*](#_ftn_292) of that era.

This is to say that at the time, they declared that if it were to be proven that this reason had no basis, the opposition would naturally be nullified.

Now, after more than two hundred years have passed, the voice of the masses is clear: [who is](#_ftn_293) a Chassid if not one who is not satisfied with putting on one pair of *tefillin*, but is stringent to also put on *tefillin* of Rabbeinu Tam; who spends more time in *davening*; who is stringent regarding adding time to *Shabbos*; who is meticulous regarding the *kashrus* of food and precise in the *hiddur* of *mitzvos*, and so on. The conclusion regarding the "opposition" and the "misnagdim" is understood.

## 1050

B"H, 14 Teves, 5731
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed and distinguished individual, who engages in communal needs and accomplishes much,
Rabbi A.M. [the scribe]

Greetings and blessings!

Your letter from Sunday, Parshas Mikeitz, has just been received. Since its transit was somewhat delayed and the matter appears urgent, this letter is being sent via express mail as well.

Regarding the job offer in connection with the residential college that is set to open in the year 5732: Since it appears that your attitude toward the offer, as well as the attitude of your friends, etc., is positive, I am somewhat hesitant in my response. In my opinion, your unique talent in your professional field of science requires concentration in order to utilize your ability to its fullest. Through this, you can raise the banner of Yiddishkeit, for in our times—especially when we see and hear of someone who excels in a scientific field in a unique way, being among the few in the world who possess this wisdom, and at the same time is meticulous in Torah and mitzvos with hiddur and educates his household in this manner, etc.—this constitutes a Kiddush Hashem in public and strengthens Yiddishkeit for many, etc.

As for the argument that this position will only require a portion of your time: judging by the program, I only wish that the entire day would be sufficient to fulfill the role as it should be fulfilled—my intention being to influence those present there in the desired manner, etc.

Perhaps a solution can be found if a suitable candidate is found for the position, and you would only serve as the supervisor or the like. Naturally, this would have to be arranged in such a way that the candidate would hold you in awe and carry out your wishes.

With respect and blessings.

## 1052

1052

[B"H], Parshas Va'era, Shabbos Kodesh Mevarchim Shevat, 5731
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the askanim and friends of the Beis Rivkah schools – in general, and to the participants in the annual Melaveh Malkah – in particular,

May Hashem grant them life,

Shalom u'Bracha!

I was pleased to receive the news that this year’s annual Melaveh Malkah will take place on Motzaei Shabbos Kodesh Mevarchim Chodesh Shevat.

The month of Shevat, beyond all the matters associated with this month, holds a special significance for every man and woman who has a connection to Lubavitch and Lubavitcher mosdos. For it is the month of the Yahrtzeit-Hilula of the Nasi of our generation, my father-in-law, the Rebbe, on the 10th of Shevat.

This month also has a particular significance for N'shei U'Bnos Chabad, because in this month (the 13th of Shevat) is the Yahrtzeit of Rebbetzin Shterna Sarah, his mother, and the Yahrtzeit of Rebbetzin Rivkah, his grandmother (the 10th of Shevat).

All these points should evoke a special hispaalus among all the participants in the Melaveh Malkah and the friends of the Beis Rivkah mosdos.

It is surely unnecessary to emphasize the great achievements of the Beis Rivkah schools in the field of chinuch habanos al taharas hakodesh. Throughout all the years since the founding of the Beis Rivkah schools, we have already been privileged to see the good fruits and the fruits of the fruits: Jewish mothers and daughters raised in the spirit of Torah and mitzvos, and imbued with Chassidishe light and good character traits.

It is to be hoped that the appreciation and enthusiasm for the Beis Rivkah schools on the part of the participants in the Melaveh Malkah and all friends of Beis Rivkah will be expressed in maaseh b'po'al — for [maaseh] is indeed the main thing — in providing the necessary financial assistance, which also means the necessary moral support for the askanim of Beis Rivkah, and the necessary spiritual support for the talmidos of Beis Rivkah.

May Hashem Yisbarach help that all the above-mentioned matters be carried out with great success, and may this also create broad channels to receive the Ribono shel Olam's blessings in everything one needs, with children, life, and ample sustenance, in both gashmius and ruchnius together.

With respect and with a blessing for success and good tidings,

**M. Schneerson**

It is a well-known [statement](#_ftn_365) of our Sages of blessed memory that a person is recognized by three things: his pocket (money), his cup (drinking), and his anger. And it may be added that one who is gifted [with the pen](#_ftn_366) of a ready writer can also be recognized in this way, perhaps even more deeply, since a literary creation reflects the character of the author’s soul and their worldview.

It is my hope that if there are future publications, you will send them here, and I thank you in advance.

With respect and blessing,

**M. Schneerson**

## 1083

[B"H], Tuesday, the day on which "it was good" was doubled[ednref_48][ednref_49],

Parshas Im Kesef Talveh Es Ami[ednref_50][ednref_51],

The year "Ki Sisa" the head of the Children of Israel

Brooklyn, N.Y.

The Administration of the Shomrei Shabbos Gemilas Chasadim Society

May Hashem protect them and grant them life

Peace and Blessing!

On the day that concludes and seals the time following the Shabbos of Parshas Matan Torah — which begins with Gemilas Chasadim and ends with Gemilas Chasadim —

I acknowledge with pleasure the receipt of the announcement that on the night following the Shabbos of Parshas Im Kesef Talveh Es Ami, Parshas Shekalim —

The conclusion and seal of the Torah reading of which is: "Ki Sisa... to make atonement for your souls," and it is known from our Sages: Moshe said before the Ribono shel Olam, "With what will You exalt the horn of Israel?" He said to him, "With 'Ki Sisa' (charity)"[ednref_54][ednref_55] —

The annual meeting of the society and the Melaveh Malkah, the "meal of Dovid Malka Meshicha," will take place, as is their good custom year after year —

May it be the will [of Hashem] that it be at a good and auspicious time, and that it serve as an addition to all the activities of previous years, and an ascent in all of this — in accordance with the directive (which is also a granting of strength): "We ascend in matters of holiness"[ednref_57].

And surely you are doing and will continue to do so in the future as well — in a manner of "appeasing" [the recipient][ednref_58], with a friendly countenance and with joy (as is the addition in the Shulchan Aruch) and with a good heart, for through all this one "gladdens the heart"[ednref_60] of the one in need of Gemilas Chasadim and uplifts his spirit, as is evident in a tangible way,

And all that has been said is essential regarding charity, and especially regarding Gemilas Chasadim.

May it be the will [of Hashem] that all this will further hasten the fulfillment of the promise that "You shall exalt the horn of Israel," and "their horn shall be exalted"[ednref_62] with honor,

And "great is charity"[ednref_63][ednref_64] (and Gemilas Chasadim) in that it brings the Geulah closer, as mentioned above — measure for measure, only many times more so — with a friendly countenance, with joy, and with a good heart, for "as in the days of your exodus from the land of Egypt," the Children of Israel will go out with a high hand,

"For Hashem hears the needy..." and "G-d will save Tzion and build the cities of Yehudah, and they shall dwell there and inherit it; and the seed of His servants shall inherit it, and those who love His name shall dwell therein."

With respect and with a blessing for success in the above and for good tidings,

**M. Schneerson**

My contribution is enclosed, bli neder.

## 1086

[Beginning of Adar, 5731]

Rabbi Zevin.

I received your letter today and was alarmed by its content, which suggests that there is a rationale to permit—and even to do so wholesale—the conversions in Vienna. Yet, a number of those converted did not know at all that this is a matter of religion, and they assumed it was merely part of the formalities for easy integration into Eretz Yisrael.

Furthermore, a number of the aforementioned did not know that they were required to leave, or did not accept upon themselves to leave, their previous religion, and they brought their idols with them.

Also, regarding the rest, in some cases there was no one present at the immersion, and in others, those present were there only as witnesses; and even regarding the rest, the converters in such manners as the above are worse than laymen, etc.

With respect and blessing,

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 1087

[Beginning of Adar, 5731]

Rabbi Zevin,

In response to your letter:

Even if there were room for leniency on the grounds of *bedieved* (which, as I noted in my previous [telegram](#_ftn_392) regarding this matter, I do not believe there is), in the current situation, such a ruling would serve as a precedent for every conversion (including Reform) that has taken place in Eretz Yisrael and abroad in the past. Furthermore, it would create a massive breach for the future, as anyone who wishes to convert will do so and claim it is *bedieved*. No qualification will be effective, and *mikol sheken*—as is apparently evident in practice—even a well-founded qualification is ineffective.

With respect and blessing,

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 1088

[Beginning of Adar, 5731]

Rabbi Zevin.

In response to your letter and following up on our previous [telegrams](#_ftn_393), it is alarming that there is no mention at all regarding those [arriving](#_ftn_394) from Vienna who are not on the list of the two rabbis who visited Vienna.

And among them are those who were Christians in their home country, yet now possess documentation as Jews in Eretz Yisrael.

With respect and blessing,

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 1089

B"H, 4 Adar, 5731
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Rabbi, the esteemed Chassid, G-d-fearing and learned, engaged in communal needs, etc., Moreinu HaRav Shlomo [395] may he live,

Greetings and blessings!

The three telegrams [396] were surely received in due time. I have deviated from my usual practice this time—to point out the weak points according to Halacha (which is clear, in my opinion) regarding the matter of your honor and his colleagues, may they live, who are distinguished rabbis, etc., in their ruling—

For it is a matter of astonishment, etc., that I saw in the letter of Rabbi Avraham Chaim, may he live, Glitzenstein, and perhaps the phrasing was not precise.

And to complete the matter, I wish to add here—that in general, in this matter (even if the points I noted in my first and second telegrams did not exist, not even one of them),

There is no concept of *bedieved* here—**from several perspectives**, and your honor does not need an indication from me, for you have explained them **yourself** quite well in the *Encyclopedia Talmudit*, entry *Bedieved* [it is possible to rectify it, one does the thing wholesale (and according to *Beitzah* 16b: it can be said that it is worse than *lechatchilah*, as one is a transgressor), **several** *bedieveds* at once, those standing at the **head** did not require a warning (as each one trusted—and they are confident even now—that it will end like the Shalit affair, G-d forbid] **and so on** in detail.

With respect and blessings.

## 193

193

B”H, 7 Adar, the year **5741**

To the heads of the Bnei Yisrael,

Brooklyn, N.Y.

After a long interval, your letters have been received, along with the enclosed minutes, etc.

For we have been promised that words (and actions) that come from the heart enter the heart and accomplish their effect.

And regarding the matters of these days—that there may be for the Jews light, and gladness, and joy, and honor, as our Sages of blessed memory expounded: "Light" refers to Torah, "gladness" refers to Yom Tov, "joy" refers to circumcision, and "honor" refers to tefillin—in addition to the literal meaning of the verse (for a verse never departs from its literal meaning), that there be light, and gladness, and joy, and honor in their literal sense.
