**M. Schneerson**

## 194

[B"H](http://#_ftn_405), 7 Adar, Year 5701 [1941]

Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the 29th Annual Gathering of the "Netzivei HaYeshiva" supporters of Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch in Montreal,

May they live,

Peace and Blessing!

The participants in the annual gathering—taking place a few days after Purim—will surely bring with them the fresh inspiration that the days of Purim bring to all Jews.

The miracles of Purim, for which we thank the Ribono shel Olam in the *V'al HaNissim* prayer, came about as a direct result of the fact that the Jews withstood the great *nissayon* not to seek an "easy" way out against the [decree](http://#_ftn_406) of Haman the wicked by abandoning Yiddishkeit, Heaven forbid. For the decree of Haman the wicked was directed against Jews as **Jews**, and it would have been "easy" to avoid the decree by casting off, Heaven forbid, the yoke of Torah and mitzvos—even if only outwardly. Nevertheless, the Jews not only held firm to Torah-Yiddishkeit with great *mesiras nefesh* [throughout](http://#_ftn_407) the entire year that the decree hung over them, but they actually strengthened their connection to Torah and mitzvos with a deep feeling of *teshuvah* that permeated all Jews.

In those critical days, the importance of *chinuch* was especially highlighted, as our [Chachamim](http://#_ftn_408) of blessed memory relate: that Mordechai HaYehudi gathered Jewish children and strengthened them in the study of Torah and the performance of mitzvos, even to the point of actual *mesiras nefesh*. And this brought about the miraculous ["v'nahapoch](http://#_ftn_409) hu"—the complete reversal [from mourning to joy](http://#_ftn_410) and, as the Megillah relates, [for the Jews](http://#_ftn_411) there was light, joy, gladness, and honor.

Just as all instructions in the [Torah](http://#_ftn_412) (from the word *hora'ah*—instruction), which come from the [eternal Torah](http://#_ftn_413), are valid in all times and places, the events of Purim teach us how Jews can free themselves from the Hamans of all generations, including our own time: this is by strengthening the bond of Jews with the eternal Torah, through the performance of Torah and mitzvos in daily life, and in particular by strengthening the Torah-education of Jewish children, which should permeate them to the highest level of devotion to true Yiddishkeit, Torah and mitzvos—infused with Chassidic warmth and enthusiasm.

In light of the above, every participant in the annual gathering will surely appreciate to the fullest extent the significance of this great fortress of Torah-education, the Lubavitcher Yeshiva in your city, and express this in actual deed. And in this merit, may the Ribono shel Olam bless and grant success so that there will be "light, joy, gladness, and honor" in all respects, for you and your families, may they live, and for all Jews.

With honor and blessing for success and good tidings,

**M. Schneerson**

## 1075

1075

[B"H](#_ftn_414), 7 Adar, 5731

Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mrs. Hada Reizel, may she live:

Blessings and peace!

Your letter and the enclosed were received.

Since we have entered the month of Adar, a [month](#_ftn_416) of success for all of Israel, may it be Hashem’s will that all matters be resolved for the good, and that you be able to share good news and fulfill the [commandment](#_ftn_417) that "when Adar enters, we increase in joy."

There is a special importance for the women and daughters of Israel in connection with the upcoming days of Purim, as is proven by the fact that the [Megillah](#_ftn_418) is not named after Mordechai—even though he was one of the leaders and great figures of Israel in those days—nor is it named after Mordechai and Esther together, but rather after Esther alone: Megillas Esther.

With blessings for success, for good tidings, and for the joy of Purim,

**M. Schneerson**

## 1076

B"H, 7 Adar, 5731
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mr. Ariel Shimon Ettinger
14 HaBanim St., Ramat Gan

Greetings and Blessings!

Your letter reached me with some delay. At an opportune time, I will mention you and your household, may they live, for the fulfillment of your heart’s desires for good regarding the matters you wrote about.

May it be Hashem’s will that you utilize all your capabilities in your highly responsible position for the benefit of the Jewish people, a holy nation in the Holy Land. And in its inner essence, may it be in accordance with the words of our holy Torah—[for](#_ftn_419) Hashem your G-d walks in the midst of your camp to save you and to deliver your enemies before you; therefore, your camp shall be holy. It is well known [the statement of our Sages, of blessed memory](#_ftn_420): one who comes to purify himself (and according to the [precision of the Alter Rebbe](#_ftn_421), "to purify" implies two meanings: to purify oneself and to purify others) is assisted, and he receives special assistance from Hashem, the G-d of Hosts.

I have already spoken on this matter, that there is a special virtue in the precise observance of the [mitzvah](#_ftn_422) of Tefillin for every single one of us, the Jewish people, and all the more so for those who are in the army. [Our Sages, of blessed memory, said](#_ftn_423) regarding the interpretation of the [verse](#_ftn_424): "And all the peoples of the earth shall see that the name of Hashem is called upon you, and they shall fear you"—these are the Tefillin of the head. This means that the fulfillment of this promise is specifically connected to the observance of the mitzvah of Tefillin.

With respect and blessings for success and for good tidings in all that was mentioned.

Sh. M.
Cardiac catheterization (if you mean the procedure called catheterization) – if it is performed by an expert, there is no fear of harm, etc. And if the doctor not only suggests doing it but also demands it, I see no reason to reject the demand.

Sh. Y.
It is right and good—for her and for the children (may they live)—that you look into and do what is in your power regarding a shidduch for her, and may Hashem grant you success. It is to be hoped that several of her problems will be resolved through this.
Please provide the names of all those you write about (along with their mother’s name), and I will mention them at the Tziyun.

Sh. R.
It is right and good—for her and for the children (may they live)—that you look into and do what is in your power regarding a shidduch for her, and may Hashem grant you success. A shidduch where the age difference is ten years or more is not suitable at all.
In her situation, it is very important that, as you wrote, her parents (may they live) live not far from her, and therefore, it requires thought and consultation whether it is advisable to move to another city (or even another neighborhood).
Please provide the names of all those you write about (along with their mother’s name), and I will mention them at the Tziyun.

D. R.
Regarding yourself: You should look into a shidduch as soon as possible, and through this, several of the problems you write about will be resolved.
Regarding your children (may they live): You should endeavor that they spend as much time as possible in the company of children their own age, and it is not advisable to remind them about their father (may he rest in peace) if they do not ask about him, as this increases the tension in their lives, etc.
Please provide the names and the names of the children (may they live) (along with their mother’s name), as they are mentioned in prayer.

To each of the above and to all of you—may you live:
**A Happy Purim and the fulfillment of what is written in the Megillah of Esther: "The Jews had light and gladness, and joy and honor"—may it be so for us.**

## 1011

B"H, 12 Adar, 5731
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 6 Adar and those preceding it: It is understood that first and foremost, matters of health (as per the instructions of a specialist doctor), livelihood (which must be established, steady, and sustainable—and since a person is biased toward himself and it is difficult for him to judge this objectively, there must be consultation with understanding friends, with the intention of taking their opinion into account), and shalom bayis (which in most cases, if not all, requires concessions, even if one side is one hundred percent in the right) must be in order. Only after all of the above are settled (or at least a significant start has been made) can one engage in sustainable and organized public work.

In public work in general, and especially in our times, there must be well-founded prospects for assistance from many other people, and the larger the plan, the greater the **necessity** for this.

In light of the above, you can clarify my opinion on the questions you wrote about after you have clarified the situation objectively (in consultation with friends, as mentioned above).

It is understood that regarding moving to another country, there must be the consent of the mistress of the house—the wife—as explained in our holy Torah.

I trust you are keeping the three daily study portions—Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya—that are appropriate for everyone.

The *pidyon nefesh* included in your letter will be read at an auspicious time at the holy *tziyun*.

With blessings for a successful resolution and a happy Purim.

120

120

B”H, Erev Shabbos Kodesh, the triple-fold day in the month of Geulah, 5731

Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the distinguished, G-d-fearing, learned, and esteemed individual, a scion of a noble family, who seeks the good of his people and possesses lofty character traits, R’ Shneur [Zalman](#_ftn_478) shlita,

Shalom u’Bracha!

Following your [visit](#_ftn_479) here, I wish to express once again the great satisfaction, pleasure, and joy I experienced as a result of our meeting. This is especially true in light of the [dictum](#_ftn_480) of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, that when two Jews meet, ultimately some benefit emerges from this for yet another Jew, and for still more Jews.

I have just received word by telephone of your return to our Holy Land. And although you have come from a land of mountains and hills, as they said, our Sages of blessed memory [stated](#_ftn_481) that Eretz Yisrael is higher than all other lands. This means that your return to the Holy Land certainly contains an elevation in every respect, both physically and spiritually [which are dependent upon one another, especially regarding Jews, and all the more so regarding the holy nation that dwells in the Holy Land, and even more so according to the teachings of Chassidus, where the purpose of all human avodah is the [ascendancy](#_ftn_482) of form over matter and spirituality over physicality]. And since all matters of spirituality and holiness are infinite—for their source is in the true Ein Sof—even if matters are at the pinnacle of goodness, there is always room for addition, to go from strength to strength and from one level of holiness to the next. Surely there is no need to elaborate on this to you.

I was pleased to learn by telephone that already at the airport you met with Anash shlita and arranged to convey a personal and detailed message. Knowing you, I am confident that you will certainly convey the things that were said explicitly, and especially that which is found "between the lines."

And as we stand on the [eve](#_ftn_483) of the triple-fold Shabbos Kodesh—

In the soul: The beginning of the reading of Toras Kohanim [of which it is [said](#_ftn_485) regarding every one of the Bnei Yisrael: "And you shall be to Me a kingdom of priests and a holy nation"];

In place: Rosh Chodesh [Nissan](#_ftn_486), the month of Geulah [in which](#_ftn_487) they were redeemed and in which they are destined to be redeemed [from the four corners of the earth](#_ftn_488) [to](#_ftn_489) a good and spacious land, the Holy Land;

And in time: Parshas [HaChodesh](#_ftn_490), whose theme is the sanctification of time, "This month shall be for you the head of months"—

I wish to express my blessings that you be blessed with this triple blessing, and that we may hear and be informed of good tidings regarding all that has been mentioned.

With respect, esteem, and blessings for a Kosher and joyous Pesach,

**M. Schneerson**

**Motzoei Shabbos.**

Although it is not my custom to involve you in the matters that follow—as was also mentioned in our conversation here—I have found it appropriate, as an exception, to write what follows, since my words here come as a continuation of one of the topics in our discussion, and it is regarding this that I will write:

A summary of what was discussed at this [farbrengen of Shabbos Kodesh](#_ftn_491) and also two days prior in a [conversation](#_ftn_492) with Mr. M.B. shlita:

They asked me what the reason is that recently I have stopped speaking about the negation of returning the liberated territories, even though some time ago I did speak about this, and on several occasions—

I answered that the reason is simple: the situation has changed in its essence. I spoke about this as long as the matter was practical and there was a possibility not to return them, and I hoped that perhaps through my speaking [in private, and when that did not help—in public], I would contribute to swaying the opinion of those who say not to return them (and thereby place Washington, etc., before **facts**—by establishing permanent civilian settlements in the territories, etc.). The opinion to return them won out (it became publicized among the nations of the world, and the pressure began). And as I said [several](#_ftn_481) weeks ago, this is already after the decision to return them, and Sharm el-Sheikh is under lease, and the like. And now, there is no longer the ability to retract—because of the pressure (according to my information from an absolutely reliable source, they will not agree in Washington under any circumstances to a war, or even to the fear of a war in the Middle East, and they will not refrain from cutting off the supply of arms and aid in general—and they have already invented an "excuse" that this is not pressure, G-d forbid, but rather a lack of assistance and participation in an action that is not to their liking—and then there is no possibility to hold onto the territories, etc. And in Washington, they understand this). And when there is no benefit and it is not practical, there is no place to speak about it. This is in addition to what has already been said—that speaking about this can harm the negotiations to receive maximum aid for the return. Furthermore, since now it is not a matter of life-threatening danger, but rather of increasing the aid as mentioned above, it is forbidden to endanger the lives of the personnel of the Tzeva Hagana LeYisrael through this.

But surely [if, G-d forbid, the coming of Moshiach Tzidkeinu is delayed], when the time for elections comes, Bnei Yisrael will remember who those people are who, immediately after the miraculous victory of the Six-Day War, began negotiations on how to free themselves and rid themselves of the liberated territories.

(And especially if, G-d forbid, the retreat of 1971 brings about results similar to the retreat of 1956—and they will once again need a miraculous victory—the aforementioned will want, after the victory, to begin once again with similar negotiations, etc.)

And they will know who those are who believe—and also regarding actual practice—in the integrity of the Holy Land, in the integrity of the holy nation, and in the integrity of our holy Torah.

Thus far regarding this matter.

– That which is enclosed in brackets was said only to the individual and not to the public at the farbrengen. The reason is understood.

## 1022

3 Nissan, 5731
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the G-d-fearing, those who are meticulous in their observance of mitzvos, the esteemed R’ Eliyahu, may he live, and his family, may they live;
And the esteemed R’ Ephraim, may he live, and his family, may they live;
And the esteemed R’ Yitzchak, may he live, and his family, may they live;
And the esteemed R’ Yisrael Konson, may he live, and his family, may they live
— including also those who ascended from there before them and those who will ascend after them — may they live.

Peace and blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of the telegram regarding your arrival in our Holy Land, in a good and auspicious hour. It is good news upon good news regarding your settling in Nachalat Har Chabad.

My hope is strong that it will be as its name implies: a *nachalah* (inheritance/settlement) without boundaries, and an ascent in a manner of "increasing and continuing," as is the case in all matters of holiness, where we "ascend in holiness." From this, it is also understood that every addition to the number of those settling in this *nachalah*—especially from our brethren, the Children of Israel, who stood the test while they were under siege and in captivity, etc.—is an increase in quantity, and even more so in quality, in all matters of the *nachalah*. Through this, it impacts all matters of Chabad in the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt and established, and through this, all matters of our Holy Land.

May it be the will of Hashem that this, too, will add to the blessing of Hashem for each and every one of them and their families—may they live—with whatever they require, from soul to body, and may the ascent be in both spirituality and physicality together. Furthermore, and this is essential, may this create a breach in the restrictions that have existed until now for our brethren, the Children of Israel, who are there. May all those who must leave there do so without any concealments or hidden obstacles, in a revealed and manifest good. And may all those who must remain, and who will continue in practice to establish Judaism, disseminate it, and spread the wellsprings—especially in that country and its surroundings—continue this holy work of theirs with expansiveness, without any concealments or hidden obstacles, and with joy and goodness of heart. May they illuminate the darkness in those places by awakening each and every one of our brethren, the Children of Israel, who are there to know with strength and persistence that the soul of each and every one of them is truly a "part of G-d from above," the "lamp of Hashem is the soul of man." May they add to the light of this lamp through the "lamp of mitzvah" and "Torah is light," and the light within the Torah, which is the Torah of Chassidus.

Happy is the portion of all those who continue in this holy work. As is known from the *sicha* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, that soon the end of our exile will come with the true and complete Redemption through Moshiach Tzidkeinu, and one will grab his head [in regret], "What a precious time it was, the only time one could accomplish in Yiddishkeit, Torah, and mitzvos, etc.—where can one have such an opportunity after the true and complete Redemption?" And the same applies to our own situation.

With blessings for a successful settlement in both spiritual and physical matters, for good news regarding all that has been mentioned, and for a kosher and happy Pesach,

**M. Schneerson**

P.S. It is obvious that what is written above at the conclusion of my letter also pertains to those who have already ascended to our Holy Land. They should learn from a *kal v'chomer* (a fortiori argument): If in that place they occupied themselves with the dissemination of Judaism and the spreading of the wellsprings in particular, etc., then how much more so in our Holy Land, "the land which Hashem your G-d seeks out, the eyes of Hashem your G-d are always upon it, from the beginning of the year to the end of the year." They must be a living example in this for those who ascended before them and for our brethren, the Children of Israel, in the Holy Land in general. May it be His will that they bring good news in this as well.

## 1025

11 Nissan, 5731
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the sons and daughters of Israel, wherever they may be,
May Hashem grant them life,

Greetings and blessings!

The Yomim Tovim are, as is well known, connected to specific times of the year: Pesach must be in the **month of spring** (*Chodesh HaAviv*); Shavuos is connected to the time of the wheat harvest and is called **Chag HaKatzir** (the Festival of the Harvest); Sukkos is connected to the time of gathering the grain and fruits and is called **Chag HaAsif** (the Festival of Ingathering).

The Torah specifically emphasizes the connection of Pesach to spring, as it is written: **"Observe the month of spring and perform the Pesach for Hashem your G-d."**

Pesach and the month of spring share common traits. One of them is that Pesach is the *"Rosh LaRegalim"* — the "head" of the Yomim Tovim — the first and the beginning of the other Yomim Tovim. Furthermore, the continuation and conclusion of Pesach—the process through which the Jews became a nation—is at the time of the giving of our Torah, Shavuos. And Sukkos is, after all, because: **"I settled the Children of Israel in Sukkos when I took them out of the land of Egypt."** Thus, the month of spring is the first of all the months, and the time of sprouting and blossoming that leads to the harvest and the ingathering.

***

The connection of Pesach to the month of spring also has a deeper significance:

Pesach, *Zman Cheiruseinu* (the time of our freedom), brought about a complete transformation **from slavery to freedom, from deep darkness to a great light**—from the lowest level of servitude to the highest level of freedom, from a deep darkness to a **great** light. Similar to this is the change in nature during spring, when the earth awakens from its deep winter sleep, is freed from the chains and constraints of the cold winter, and begins to sprout and blossom, until the stalks of grain begin to fill out. Or, taken in a specific sense: when from a single kernel, after it decays, new, living, and growing grain sprouts forth. In both cases—Pesach and spring—the change is not a rise from one level to the next, but a change that is *shelo b'erech* (disproportionate)—a change that creates a new existence.

***

As has been noted many times, every matter in Torah (from the word *horaa*—instruction) is a directive and a lesson, especially a matter connected with a Yom Tov, and particularly with a general Yom Tov like Pesach.

A general instruction from Pesach, especially from the connection of Yetzias Mitzrayim specifically with the month of spring—for every Jew, man and woman, in daily life, is:

Human life is, in general, divided into two spheres: one's personal life and one's accomplishments in the world; and in both of these, there is the spiritual life and the physical life.

The task of a Jew is to "take out" everything that exists in the aforementioned spheres—*me'avdus l'cheirus* (from their *mitzrayim* and boundaries)—by "elevating" them to (more) spirituality—until one serves the Almighty with every detail of them.

Even those things which he seemingly cannot change: the Almighty created him in such a way that he must eat, drink, etc.—he transforms that eating, etc., and it is *shelo b'erech*: he eats in order to be able to do good, to study Torah, to fulfill mitzvos—in order to have the strength to serve the Almighty. And furthermore—with the eating itself he serves Hashem: this leads him to make a blessing before eating, a blessing afterward, and so on.

Similar to this is the matter of the month of spring: seemingly, a person can do nothing about it, for the Almighty established the **chukos** (laws governing the conduct of) heaven and earth and declared that "as long as the earth exists... the times of cold and heat and of summer and winter... shall not cease"—yet a Jew observes and looks forward to the spring month in order to perform the Pesach for Hashem your G-d: he understands, and even more, he perceives in the spring the **Almighty's** *chukos* and "shall not cease." And even higher—in the very strength of the natural *hanhagah* (conduct according to the laws of heaven and earth) in the month of spring—is "Hashem your G-d took you out of Egypt"—which is one of the greatest miracles, the very strength of miraculous conduct.

In all these spheres of daily life, a person encounters matters that are "Mitzrayim"—in the sense of *mitzrayim* and boundaries—which hinder and constrain the Jew from developing his true Jewish nature to the fullest extent, as a Torah-Jew. These obstacles and limitations are both internal—innate traits and acquired habits; and external—such as the influences of the environment. A Jew must free himself from these chains and go toward "you shall serve G-d."

***

Even one who calculates that his spiritual state is very low, and wonders how one can expect to completely transform himself *me'avdus l'cheirus* and *me'afelah l'or gadol*—even in this, there is a clear instruction from the Yom Tov of Pesach. For, as stated, Yetzias Mitzrayim was from one extreme to the other: from the lowest enslavement to the lowest idolaters, the Jews were not only freed from physical slavery (*avodas perech*) and from spiritual enslavement (idolatry), but they were soon after—on the seventh day of Pesach—able to say and did say **"Zeh Keili"** (This, this is **my** G-d), pointing, as it were, with their finger—and subsequently reached Mount Sinai, heard "I am Hashem your G-d" from the mouth of the Almighty Himself, and received the entire Torah, both the Written and the Oral—an extraordinary transformation from one extreme to the other.

***

May Hashem Yisbarach help that every one, man and woman, within the entirety of the Jewish people, should utilize the strengths that the Creator has given each of them to overcome all difficulties and obstacles and to emerge from all *mitzrayim* and limitations and reach true freedom by connecting with the Almighty—through His Torah and through His mitzvos,

Including the mitzvah: to mention Yetzias Mitzrayim by day and by night,

And from the individual redemption, may we merit the redemption of the collective, to the realization of the prophecy **"As in the days of your exodus from the land of Egypt, I will show you wonders,"** with the coming of Mashiach Tzidkeinu, very soon.

With the blessing of a kosher and happy Pesach,

**Menachem Schneerson**

127

B”H, 11 Nissan, 5731
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the distinguished Rabbi and Chossid, who is involved in communal affairs etc., may he live,

Greetings and blessings!

In anticipation of the Festival of Matzos, the season of our freedom, which is approaching for us and for all of Israel for good and for blessing, I hereby wish you and all who are yours a kosher and happy Pesach, and a true freedom—freedom from all matters that cause confusion in both material and spiritual affairs—so that you may serve Hashem with joy and a good heart, and to extend this freedom and joy throughout all the days of the year.

With respect and blessing.

P.S. In response to what you wrote regarding the *Sefer HaErchim* in Chassidus: Although time does not permit me to elaborate, I will at least address it briefly. For someone like yourself, there is no need for length. It is as follows:

It is simple that the goal of this book was not to present the teachings of Chassidus in a popular manner, as is the current style, but rather to facilitate the study of the teachings of Chassidus in a fundamental way by concentrating matters that are scattered across many books and maamarim into one place. Furthermore—and this is also essential—by adding citations and references, as I have seen from my own experience how necessary this is in order to understand a concept in Chassidus thoroughly, at least to the extent possible within the time one dedicates to the study of Chassidus.

The great necessity for this is also understood from the abundance of similar books in the study of the *Nigleh*, whether regarding the concentration of material—such as the *Sifrei Erchim* in *Nigleh* arranged by alphabetical order, etc., or by subject matter, etc.—and certainly regarding the summarization of *piskei dinim* in the works of the *poskim*. Even in the study of Kabbalah, there are several books whose purpose is as mentioned above. Yet, specifically in the teachings of Chassidus, nothing of the sort is found. Consistent with the approach of Chabad Chassidus, where one of the primary points is to understand matters thoroughly—and in the well-known style that it should be understood even by the intellect of the *nefesh habahamit*—I have not seen even a beginning of this, except for *Shaar HaYichud* by the Mitteler Rebbe, which is arranged according to the order of *Seder Hishtalshelus*, but it is extremely brief.

I have felt the necessity of the aforementioned for decades, but due to various reasons, the matter was delayed. Decades ago, I began the preparatory work necessary for editing such a *Sefer HaErchim* by compiling indices of subjects for the foundational books of Chassidus.

In my opinion—and here too I speak from my own experience—the *Sefer HaErchim* has succeeded in the form in which it appeared to fulfill, to a significant and great extent, the aforementioned deficiency. And although, naturally, one must fill in and complete many matters explained therein based on what is explained in other books and maamarim, etc., my approach is known, along the lines of what I wrote to you regarding the *Talmudic Encyclopedia*: it is imperative that all volumes appear as quickly as possible. For as long as the final entry in the letter *Tav* is not completed, there is a lack of completeness even in the first entry. The same applies to our *Sefer HaErchim*; I urge that it be published promptly, and not after the study of all the books and maamarim that are in print and in manuscript, and so on.

A sort of assistance to the above—and here too I saw a sign and hint that it is imperative to publish the *Sefer HaErchim*—is the publication of the maamarim of the Tzemach Tzedek arranged according to the order of the Torah and Tanach. This, at the very least, concentrates matters according to the order of the pesukim, which makes them easier to find. And precisely now, the ability existed to publish them, and here too, they are like "waters that have no end" in what has already appeared (26 volumes), in addition to the supplements now being collected from further manuscripts, which apparently also contain material for many more volumes. I encourage those involved in the *Sefer HaErchim* that, although I urge them to hasten the editing—and consequently, it lacks the exhaustion of even all known sources—immediately upon finishing the letter *Tav* (and may it be speedily in our days, literally), they should begin the editing of supplements and a second edition.

I will not deny that my intention in what I wrote above is also that perhaps my words will help hasten the appearance of the 14th volume of the *Talmudic Encyclopedia*, and after it the 15th, etc., as I spoke with Rabbi Hutner during his visit here, who surely conveyed the matters.

## 10,128

10,128

B"H, 11 Nissan, 5731
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed and distinguished individual, who occupies himself with communal needs,
Rabbi Mordechai [Kirshblum]

Greetings and blessings!

I received your letter and report regarding Vienna etc. in due time, and I ask your forgiveness for not having acknowledged it until now. The reason for this is that once I learned that two rabbis were being sent there to investigate the situation, I felt there was no need for a statement from my side regarding what is transpiring there. However, after seeing a copy of their report—which is itself alarming, etc.—there are several points that are not emphasized within it, among them:

a) There were cases where the Christians did not know at all that the entire ceremony involved a matter of religion, because the explanation given to them was that in order to avoid complications in their immigration to Eretz Yisrael and their integration, and to obtain an apartment easily, etc., it would be good for them to register as Jews. This went so far that they took their icons with them, and some even hung them in the corner of the room in their apartments in Eretz Yisrael, and a word to the wise is sufficient.

This is to say that even in a Reform "conversion," there is at least talk that a religious matter is involved, even if the conversion itself is lacking in practice. This is not the case here, where there is not even a preparation for conversion; consequently, the entire act performed has no substance, for the subject remains a Christian.

b) The rabbis who visited Vienna emphasized the number of cases they investigated and added that there is no need to investigate the rest. Yet, you yourself announced in the press that there were many such cases that passed through Vienna. Seemingly, it is obvious that first and foremost, these individuals must be located, for they are on the list of those who arrived from Vienna and are now in Eretz Yisrael, registered as Jews, and no one says a word or makes a sound.

I do not wish to dwell at length on this terrible matter for several reasons, and if the above writing achieves its effect, that will be my reward.

With respect and with blessings for a kosher and happy Pesach.

1133

[Winter, 5731]

[Notes](#_ftn_555) [written in haste](#_ftn_556).

**At the beginning.** *Alav*. *Nezek* – Rashi explains: an ox or a person that caused damage, meaning a person. In the note regarding the Rashi before us: an ox **"that is a mu'ad."** Seemingly, one could argue for the author’s reading based on what we find, that he exerts effort (and it is forced) in *Arachin* (14b) to establish an anonymous Mishnah (which is Rabbi Meir) according to Rabbi Akiva (even though Rabbi Akiva disagrees with the Tanna Kamma of the Mishnah in *Bava Kamma* 33a).

– And one could say the reason is because Rabbi Meir, in the end (and also from the outset), was a student of Rabbi Akiva (*Eruvin* 13a) –

And therefore, Rabbi Meir’s words here should also be established according to Rabbi Akiva.

**There, s.v. *Atu*:** It is not appropriate to raise such a difficulty (i.e., "it is this... it is that") except regarding two matters where from one we know the other, etc. But here (regarding the question – why) he repeated them a second time, it is not appropriate to say "it is this," etc.

And in note 4, regarding the reading of **Rashi** – "it is this" refers to damage, "it is this" refers to injuries. And it should be noted:

a) That they are equivalent only in reading, but the **explanation** of Rashi is that the difficulty is "it is this... it is this" – why did he repeat them a second time?

b) As Rashi explains, "it is this... it is this" – means literally "it is this." This is found in *Shabbos* (118b): "it is this Vardimus, it is this Menachem," and similarly in *Megillah* (23b) and in many other places.

– When the reason is the same (for then from one we know the other) – we find "and this is the reason, etc., and this is the reason, etc." in *Rosh Hashanah* (29b).

**Beginning of Chapter 2. s.v. *Vehu omer tisborachu*:** But when he is comforting others, it is not appropriate to say this, since he does not say to them, "May I be your atonement."

**And in the note, it should say** (instead of – "he says to them") **"they say to him."** It is more plausible to say that the copyist erred between a *yud* and a *vav*, and it should say, "May **I** (the Kohen Gadol) be your atonement." And "it is not appropriate to say this" – means that the "others" should say to the Kohen Gadol "may you be blessed," just as the Kohen Gadol says to the others who are comforting him.

**Beginning of Chapter 3. s.v. *Mai zeh b'zeh, zeh b'zeh lo b'din echad, etc.*:** This is how it is in Rashi’s commentary (and the precision is from the fact that he does not say "this one with this one, a judge, and this one with this one, etc."). And it has already been noted by the *Acharonim* in the *Chiddushei HaRamban* (at the end of *Chamesh Shitos*) who raises a difficulty regarding this and discusses it at length. *HaRan* in his *Chiddushim* there. *Sefer Shaar Mishpat*, section 18.

**At the end. s.v. *Amar lei shamati, etc.*:** – It should be noted (and likewise regarding what was written about this on page 45) from what is written in *Sefer Margalit HaYam* (by Rabbi R. Margalit, shlita, on Tractate *Sanhedrin*).

**In the notes there at the end:** And the Levites in their watches – perhaps this is a printing error and it should be "and the Levites in their *duchan* (platform)," as is the language of the *Shas* (*Megillah* 3a and in many places) – and it should be noted from *Taanis* (26a and there).

## 1034

[B"H], 27 Nissan, 5731
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed Rabbi, the G-d-fearing, etc.
[Rabbi Avraham] (may he live and be well),

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter from Motzaei Shabbos regarding my note that instead of "Leviim in their watches" (*mishmarosam*), it should say "Leviim in their platform" (*duchanam*):

You raised a difficulty regarding this, for it is written, "the Leviim in their watches" (Bamidbar 8:26) and "the Leviim in their watches" (Divrei Hayamim II 8:14).

It is surprising that you did not note something even more significant: that **many, many** times the term "watch" (*mishmeres*) is used in connection with Gershon, Kehas, and Merari as **Leviim** (at the end of Parshas Bamidbar and the beginning of Parshas Naso), and **likewise** in the Nach (as noted in a concordance).

The distinction is simple: "In their platform" (*duchanam*) emphasizes the **uniqueness** of the Leviim in relation to the Kohanim and Yisraelim, whereas "in their watches" (*mishmarosam*) is a term shared by Kohanim, Leviim, (and also Yisraelim) — see Taanis 26a and there. When it appears in the context of Leviim in contrast to the Kohanim, an additional explanation is required, as in Divrei Hayamim (ibid.): "their watches to praise and to serve opposite the Kohanim, etc., and the gatekeepers, etc." Therefore, the phrasing "Kohanim in their service, Leviim in their watches, and Yisraelim in their station" requires correction (or additional explanation). And even if one adds an explanation (along the lines of the aforementioned in Divrei Hayamim), there is still room for discussion, similar to the well-known comment of Chazal (Kiddushin 70a, bottom): "Is it distasteful to say 'Leviim in their platform,' as the Sages said?" (Megillah 3a, and **in many places**).

Indeed, I **prefaced** the answer to the aforementioned difficulty in the note at the end of my aforementioned comment: by pointing to Taanis (26a and there) — for it is explicit there that there were twenty-four watches of Kehunah, **and likewise** of Leviim, **and likewise** of Yisraelim. See also Bamidbar Rabbah (Chapter 11:3). Before that, I also cited Megillah there.

With respect and blessing.

## 137

B"H, 11 Iyar, 5731
Brooklyn.

...You wrote correctly that a person should ask about matters that are not understood to him.

(And it is well-known—the emphasis of Toras Chabad is that one must: **"Know** the G-d of your father," [and in the language of the Rambam](#_ftn_567) "**to know** that there is a First Being, etc.").

However, this should not be a **kushya** (in the common sense of the word), and the main point is that it must not be a prerequisite for action. Rather, [in the style of Chazal](#_ftn_568): the precedence of *naaseh* to *nishma*—

And it is in this manner that our Torah, the Torah of truth and the Torah of life, was given to us, and it is in this manner that we received the Torah. And Chazal explained that it is **specifically** through this approach that one **understands** the Torah [as it is written](#_ftn_569) "The integrity of the upright shall guide them" (Shabbos 88a, at the end. See there).

## 138

B"H, 11 Iyar, 5731
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter containing your request for a blessing and a *pidyon nefesh* dated the 3rd of Iyar. At an *eis ratzon*, it will be read at the gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzukulleh"h, nbg"m, zy"a*.

It is surely unnecessary to emphasize the necessity of strengthening one’s daily conduct so that it aligns with the instructions of our Torah—the Torah of life—and the fulfillment of its *mitzvos*, regarding which it is said "and he shall live by them." Beyond the fundamental fact that this is the command of the *Ribono shel Olam*, it is also the path to receiving the blessings that a person requires. And there is nothing that can stand before the will.

With blessings.

When a person is frequently beset by thoughts and feelings of regret regarding undesirable conduct and actions, one must clarify from which "side" they originate: from one’s *yetzer tov* or from its opponent. The primary test for this is the "offspring" of these thoughts: if the thoughts generate increased energy and vitality in the fulfillment of *mitzvos* and strength in one’s daily conduct according to the *Shulchan Aruch* (including, regarding your father—maintaining the order of the school, etc.), this is proof that their source is pure and good. If they generate sadness, negligence, laziness, or a feeling of despair, this is proof that they come from the *yetzer hara* (which has merely clothed and disguised itself in the garb of *yiras shamayim*), for all of these—sadness, etc.—hinder a person in *avodas Hashem*. Regarding your father, you will cause *nachas ruach* to the soul of your father, *a"h*, through **good deeds**, not through thoughts of despair and the like. Surely, your spiritual guide will explain this at greater length according to what is explained in several places.

## 10,139

B"H, 11 Iyar, 5731
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter and the request for a blessing/pidyon nefesh dated 17 Nissan. At an auspicious time, it will be read at the gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

It is surely unnecessary to emphasize the necessity of strengthening one’s conduct in daily life so that it aligns with the instructions of our Torah—the Torah of life—and the fulfillment of its mitzvos, regarding which it is said "and live by them." Beyond the fundamental fact that this is the command of Hashem, it is also the path to receiving the blessings that a person requires.

Included in this conduct is trust—**as much as is necessary**—in Hashem, the Creator of man and his Guide.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita

P.S. In response to your question: The concept of Hashgacha Pratis (that Hashem oversees each and every individual) is **foundational** to our faith and our Torah,

 and consequently, there is no room for despair, Heaven forbid, nor for anger toward other people—for it is **certain** that they are not the "boss" over other human beings.

Rather, the Torah states that a person must do what depends on them through the natural path.

And furthermore—that the means and the way to draw down the blessings of Hashem in all that is needed is through conduct that follows the will of Hashem, as mentioned above.

## 140

[B"H], Erev Shabbos, 13 Iyar, 5731
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed Rabbi, the Chossid, G-d-fearing, and learned, who engages in communal needs and accomplishes much, etc.
Rabbi Shmuel (may he live and be well),

Peace and blessing!

I acknowledge with thanks the receipt of Volume 12 of the **Otzar HaPoskim**, which, like the volumes preceding it, is a collection of practical halachic rulings from the great luminaries of Israel in the generations before us—the *Rishonim* who were like angels—by whose light we walk in our daily lives.

As has been discussed many times, if in all generations and times there was a great necessity for books such as these, how much more so after the upheavals, the exile within exile, and the destruction—may Hashem spare us—of many centers of Torah, and the scattering of Torah scholars to all corners of the world, lacking rest and inheritance.

This is of special importance in our days, in these very recent years, when there are those who plot against our Torah, the Torah of truth (for truth rejects compromise, and there is only one truth), and they prefer "innovations". As is well known, the witticism regarding this is "an absolutely true innovation"—for one who judges a matter with absolute truth, this is not a true innovation, because everything a veteran student is destined to innovate has already been told to Moshe at Sinai. This is not the case with the aforementioned "innovators"—may Hashem spare us from them and their multitude—who seek to innovate the opposite of what was told to Moshe at Sinai. Surely, the publication of the Torah of the *poskim* and the great leaders of Israel of all the generations that preceded us will set them, too, upon the truth—the Torah of truth—and the word of Hashem, which is *Halacha*, will go forth in all the dispersions of Israel, *Halacha* in practice. By their rulings, the sons and daughters of Israel will conduct themselves and live in their daily lives wherever they may be, and all the more so regarding questions that require explanation and clarification. Knowledge, wisdom, and truth will increase, until the prophecy is fulfilled: "The earth shall be full of the knowledge of Hashem as the waters cover the sea".

Happy is the portion of all those who support this great endeavor—great in quantity, and even more so in quality. Surely, then, the coming volumes of *Otzar HaPoskim* will appear at a faster pace, for this is the demand of the hour, and "one hour sooner is better."

With respect and with a blessing of success to you, to all the members of the administration, and to all those assisting in the publication of these books—may they live and be well,

**M. Schneerson**

## 10,143

B”H, Pesach Sheni, 5731
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Rabbi Menachem Yisrael Fink
Chief Rabbi of The Hague
Peace and Blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from the first day of Rosh Chodesh Iyar, and I will mention it at the resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, for the fulfillment of your heart’s desires for good, as contained in your letter.

Surely, for one such as yourself, it is superfluous to emphasize the magnitude of the responsibility, and along with it, the magnitude of the privilege, that every individual possesses to influence their surroundings. This is true from both ends: On the one hand, according to the statement of our Sages, of blessed memory, that the heart of a Jew is awake to Hashem, to His Torah, and to His mitzvos. We see this tangibly regarding the youth, and to a significant degree regarding the adults among our people as well; they are waiting and yearning for someone to tell them the words of the living G-d, and words of truth are recognizable (for truth rejects compromises, package deals, and the like, and a word to the wise is sufficient). And through words that come from the heart, time and again, there is a strength to this outreach, for it does not return empty.

On the other hand, a lack of effort in this matter is not merely as it was in previous generations—where someone who missed an opportunity to influence caused one who could have been a great scholar to remain a lesser scholar, or instead of being a great G-d-fearing person, to remain less so. It is not so now, when the question is literally *pikuach nefashos*—that a person should remain a Jew, etc.—and this, too, is evidently clear.

And if in all generations and in all places, "Love your fellow as yourself" is a great principle of the Torah, how much more so in certain countries, and specifically in the country where you are now, and in our era—an era of great confusion, bewilderment, and blurring of values, to the point of calling light darkness and darkness light. In light of the above, the responsibility is multiplied many times over, and along with it, the privilege as well.

And since Hashem only demands according to the strength of each individual, surely, and most certainly, the strength is granted from Above to fulfill the aforementioned task. The matter depends only on the will and a firm resolution, without fear of those who mock or those who advocate in the name of compromise, etc.

With respect and blessing for success and for good tidings in all the above.

P.S. Enclosed is a copy of the *Likkutei Sichos* and a [general letter] which I hope will be of interest to you.

## 144

[B"H](#_ftn_596), Pesach Sheni, 5731
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To all participants in the annual dinner
for the educational institution "Oholei Torah,"
May Hashem grant them life,

Greetings and blessings!

The annual celebration is taking place a few days after Lag B'Omer. One of the primary points of Lag B'Omer is that on this [day](#_ftn_597), the unfortunate event involving the students of Rabbi Akiva ceased. The [reason](#_ftn_598) that led to this unfortunate event—[as](#_ftn_599) explained at length on another occasion—was that the conduct of the students toward one another was not at the necessary level, as it should have been for such great students of such a great Tanna.

And since there was a deficiency in the realm of *bein adam l’chaveiro* (interpersonal conduct), it is a sign that there was a deficiency in the education of *bein adam l’Makom* (conduct between man and Hashem).

In these days of Sefirah, which are a preparation for the receiving of the Torah, the event involving the students of Rabbi Akiva underscores that which is clearly indicated in the Aseres HaDibros: [When](#_ftn_600) can there be ["Honor](#_ftn_601) your father and your mother" and all other matters of *bein adam l’chaveiro* as they ought to be? When there is first the recognition and acceptance of the yoke of ["I](#_ftn_602) am Hashem your G-d" and "You shall have no other gods" as the foundation of one's conduct in daily life.

This comes to refute the false notion of those who think that the relationship between person and person—so-called morality and ethics—is independent of Torah education.

The educational institution "Oholei Torah" aims to instill in the children an education *al taharas hakodesh* (in absolute holiness), founded on wholeness in Yiddishkeit, where *bein adam l’Makom* and *bein adam l’chaveiro* go hand in hand. Such an education ensures that they will grow up to be good Yidden and complete Yidden in all respects, who will be a living example for others and an inexhaustible source of Yiddishe nachas—Torah-nachas—for their parents and for Klal Yisrael.

The institution therefore deserves the fullest support, and the merit of sustaining such an educational institution *al taharas hakodesh* will surely assist all supporters and partners to be blessed by the Ribono shel Olam with all that they need, especially with true Torah-nachas from their own children, with abundance in both material and spiritual matters alike.

With honor and with blessings for great success and for good tidings,

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 1015

B"H, Pesach Sheni, 5731
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mrs. Geula [tichyeh](#_ftn_603)
Mr. Aharon [shichyeh](#_ftn_604)

Shalom u’Bracha!

I received your telegram, and I have mentioned you for the fulfillment of your hearts' desires for the good.

Surely a letter with further details will follow, and may it be Hashem’s will that you bring good news regarding both your personal matters and general matters alike.

I am certain there is no need to emphasize to you how much our Torah—Torah of life—values the individual, and according to the well-known [Mishnah](#_ftn_605), whoever sustains [one] soul of Yisrael is as if he sustained an entire world. Furthermore, our [Sages](#_ftn_606) of blessed memory—and in particular the Rambam, the guide for the perplexed of all generations—state, in a laconic style but as a definitive halachic ruling, that every person must view himself throughout the entire year, and likewise the entire world, as half meritorious and half liable; if he performs one mitzvah, he tips the scales for himself and for the entire world to the side of merit and brings salvation and deliverance to himself and to them (Hilchos Teshuvah, ch. 3, halachah 4, in slightly abbreviated form).

It is also understood that anyone who has the possibility and the ability to act on a larger scale does not fulfill his obligation at all through a single action, a limited action, or even an action on a large scale that is not commensurate with his full capacity. This applies both to quantity and to quality.

And if this is the case regarding every mitzvah and action of every person, how much more so for those to whom Divine Providence has given the opportunity and the talent to influence the many, and regarding issues that stand at the heights of our world—especially vital issues that touch upon the very existence of the nation, and in the phrasing of [Rabbeinu] Saadia Gaon: Our nation is a nation only by virtue of its Torah (HaRasag, Sefer HaEmunos VeHaDe'os 3:7).

With respect and with a blessing for good news in all that has been mentioned.

## 10196

B"H, Pesach Sheni, 5731
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Mr. [Mordechai](#_ftn_607) Namir,

Shalom u’vracha!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your book, *Shlichus in Moscow*, and I thank you for your thoughtfulness in sending it to my library.

With respect and blessing.

P.S. I trust you will not mind what follows. By way of introduction, you surely know that in our generation, not everyone who comes across a book actually studies it. Many are content with a superficial reading (without study), and sometimes even just leafing through it. Therefore, it is best to prevent, to the extent possible, any misunderstanding even among those who are most superficial.

Furthermore, many of those who are loud, vocal, and opinionated, and who push themselves to the forefront, are so preoccupied with this that they have no time for study, or even anything less than that.

This introduction—which is relatively long—is regarding the end of your book, the list of names of shuls. Seemingly, one should have added—and perhaps even now, after printing, it could be done—a note at the beginning stating that this is a list of shuls that existed during the years 1948–1950. While this is understood by anyone who reads the introduction, and certainly by one who reads the contents of the book, as mentioned above, these words are not directed toward historians or studious readers, but rather toward the aforementioned type, which I believe is not small in number. Especially since the correction could be made by adding a gummed slip at the beginning of the list.

I ask for your forgiveness for this remark, as the distortion here can have significant consequences.

You have surely already heard from many about the special importance of memoirs and reports from those two years (1948–1950). I will conclude by expressing my own opinion in accordance with the above. Surely, someone will eventually be found to take upon themselves the task of providing a sufficient description, even if it remains incomplete, as not all the material is available regarding that country during that period—a time of many trials and many events in general, and in the lives of our brethren, the Children of Israel, in particular—during the decade following the Second World War.

## 10,147

B"H, Pesach Sheni, 5731
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mr. Yisrael Feinhandler
Ramat HaSharon

Shalom u’Bracha!

In response to your letter of the 8th of Iyar, in which you write regarding the matter of davening with closed lips—which I assume refers to davening in thought alone, without speech or the movement of the lips—

It is surprising that there is a question or doubt regarding this, for it is explained in the [Gemara](#_ftn_609) and the poskim that davening must be done through speech. Even davening *b'lachash* (in a whisper) is defined by the concept of ["her lips](#_ftn_610) **move**, but her voice is not heard (by others)," even though there must also be kavanah, [as our Sages of blessed memory stated](#_ftn_611): "Davening without kavanah is like a body without a soul."

In the words of our Rebbe, the author of the Shulchan Aruch (who rules in the revealed dimension of Torah) and the Tanya (who rules in the hidden dimension of Torah): "The halachic ruling established in the Talmud and the poskim is that thought is not equivalent to speech. If one recited Krias Shema in his thoughts and heart alone, with all the power of his kavanah, he has not fulfilled his obligation and must repeat it. The same applies to Birchas Hamazon, which is a Torah obligation, as well as other Rabbinic blessings and davening. If one articulated the words with his lips but did not have kavanah, he has fulfilled his obligation *b'dieved* (after the fact) and need not repeat it, except for the first verse of Krias Shema and the first blessing of the Shemoneh Esrei davening" ([Tanya, beginning of Chapter 38](#_ftn_612)).

With respect and blessing,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

150

150

 B”H, Lag B’Omer, 5731
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the Sixteenth Annual Convention
of N’shei U’Bnos Chabad
May Hashem grant them life

Blessings and Peace!

This year, the convention takes place on Shabbos Mevarchim Chodesh Sivan, the month of **Matan Torah**. Since everything occurs through *Hashgacha Pratis*, it is appropriate to focus on one of the points of Matan Torah that has a direct connection to this convention.

Torah from Sinai begins with the Aseres HaDibros. The first two commandments—**Anochi** (which includes all positive mitzvos) and **Lo Yihyeh Lecha** (which includes all negative mitzvos)—are the foundation of **Achdus Hashem**. The preface to Matan Torah was the unity of the Jewish people (**Vayichan Sham Yisrael** – **as one man with one heart**). The entire concept of Matan Torah is to bring **Achdus Hashem** down into the world, through the fact that Jews—**a single nation on earth**—fulfill the 613 mitzvos of the **one Torah**.

 Seemingly, this is difficult to understand: How can such unity be achieved, considering that Hashem created human beings with diverse opinions (**no two people’s minds are alike**), in a world that is equally diverse in its climate and natural properties? How can an entire nation achieve complete unity among themselves, and bring unity into such a world?

The explanation for this is as it says in the verse: **Vayisiatzvu B’tachtis HaHar**—that all six hundred thousand Jews "stood **under the mountain**." This means that they completely submitted themselves to Torah from Sinai in such a way that all other matters in the world were as if they did not exist, for they were entirely *batel* within that *kabbalas ol*, together with the great *simcha* of receiving the Torah. And since the "mountain" is the same for everyone, and all were permeated with the same feeling of *bitul* and *simcha*, this brought about a true unity among all six hundred thousand Jews, and in this way, also the unity of *Hashem Echad* in the world through the *Torah Achas*.

The same applies to the Jewish family. Although every member of the family is a unit unto themselves, with a specific task in life, etc., when all members of the family accept the **one Torah** of **Hashem Echad** in such a way that Torah and mitzvos are the *ikar* (the essence), and all other things are merely secondary to the *ikar*—and have value only when they relate to that *ikar*—then there is true unity in the family.

In this very unity of the family—since Jewish families are the building blocks of the Jewish people, and consequently the foundation of the unity of *Klal Yisrael*—the Jewish woman and daughter has a most important role, as the **Akeres HaBayis**, as has been emphasized on previous occasions.

It goes without saying that the aforementioned unity must be constant, without interruptions. That is to say, it must find expression not only on certain days of the year, or at certain hours of the day, but on all days of the year and at all hours of the day. This means that the Jewish home must be entirely set upon the foundations of Torah and mitzvos, and so permeated with the spirit of *kabbalas ol* and *simcha shel mitzvah* that this should be noticeable also in one’s conduct outside the home, in the street, and in the entire surrounding environment.

In this lies the content of the "genuine uniqueness" and unity of the Jewish family and of Jewish family life—the main theme of this year's convention.

It is to be hoped that this point will be brought out at the convention with the appropriate clarity and strength, and with the intention and purpose thereof—its realization in daily life, in accordance with the fundamental principle of our Sages of blessed memory: **Action is the essential thing.**

With blessings for success in both spiritual and material matters, and for good tidings in all the above,

**M. Schneerson**

1054

1054

[B"H](#_ftn_640), 25 Iyar, 5731

Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

. . . Regarding your mention of his name in connection with the issue of some of the bochurim sheyichyu in . . . — the intention was not that he should organize it. For he is **sufficiently** busy, and with the chinuch of the holy Torah, etc. (and it is obvious that I did not intend for him to manage it) — rather, that he should stir those whose holy duty it is to do this, and have been for some time (and unfortunately, to this day, the matter has not been put into action, even though the magnitude of the responsibility, the privilege, and the preciousness of time in this matter is **tangibly** apparent). And it is important that he provide the impetus for this — because the reason the Yetzer has succeeded for so many years in preventing the aforementioned individuals from fulfilling this duty is through the explanation that "nothing can be done," and "so-and-so is not capable of this," and "the proof is that so-and-so is also not capable of it," and "what does he have to do with the whole matter, and it is enough that he sighed three times over the situation," etc. — yet it is within his power to **prove** from the bochurim sheyichyu that, through his influence, the **promise** of Chazal, "You have labored and you have found," can be fulfilled in this type of work and in this area as well. And perhaps also to provide guidance on methods of approach, etc.

A *Kollel* in Canada is not relevant for him.

I will mention it at the *Ohel*.

10157

10157

[B"H]( #_ftn_645), Rosh Chodesh Sivan, 5731
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the graduating students of the "B'rvay" class and the matriculation class
Lubavitch Seminary, Casablanca
May Hashem grant them life

Blessings and peace!

I received your letter of 12 Iyar with pleasure, and I will mention you at the resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, for the fulfillment of your hearts' desires for good and for blessing.

As we stand in the [third month]( #_ftn_646), on this day when our ancestors arrived at the wilderness of Sinai, you surely know the interpretation of our Sages [of blessed memory]( #_ftn_647) regarding the verse, "And Israel encamped there opposite the mountain" (using the singular form) — ["all of them]( #_ftn_648) as one person with one heart." This was the prerequisite for receiving one Torah from one Hashem, and for becoming ["one nation]( #_ftn_649) on earth" — to draw down the unity of Hashem into this [physical]( #_ftn_650) world.

[Seemingly]( #_ftn_651), how is it possible to achieve such unity, given that the Creator fashioned human beings [whose]( #_ftn_652) opinions are not alike, and this world He created is diverse in all its matters and details from one end to the other?

The explanation for this is hinted at in the verse, **"And they stood at the foot of the mountain."** This means that all six hundred thousand of Israel — they, their wives, their sons, and their daughters — established themselves with strength "at the foot of the mountain" — in complete *bitul* and with immense joy in anticipation of receiving the Torah and *mitzvos*, in such a way that all other matters were as if they did not exist. Through this, they became truly as one to receive one Torah from one Hashem, and to draw down the unity of Hashem — through the Torah and *mitzvos* — into the world.

It is surely known to you that the women and daughters of Israel had a primary role in the giving of the Torah at Sinai, [as related]( #_ftn_654) by our Sages of blessed memory, based on the verse, ["Thus]( #_ftn_655) shall you say to the house of Yaakov (these are the women), and tell the children of Israel (these are the men)." The Holy One, blessed be He, commanded Moshe Rabbeinu to speak first with the women and daughters of Israel regarding the acceptance of the Torah, and only afterward with the men of Israel. This means that everything stated above applies to you as well, and indeed, with even greater intensity.

May it be the will of Hashem that your efforts succeed in fulfilling the above with joy and a glad heart, in actual practice, for [action]( #_ftn_656) is the essential thing. May you be a living example to all who see you, for [there is]( #_ftn_657) nothing that can stand before the will.

With blessings for success, for good tidings, and for the receiving of the Torah with joy and inwardness,

**M. Schneerson**

## 1061

1061

By the grace of Hashem, Days of Preparation, 5731
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the participants in the annual undertaking of the N.Y. Committee for the Seminary for Teachers and Schools for Girls in Kfar Chabad in our Holy Land, may it be rebuilt speedily,

May Hashem grant you life,

Blessings and peace!

The days of the **three days of preparation** (*shloshes yemei hagbalah*), which serve as a preparation for the receiving of the Torah, derive their content from the message of Hashem to Moshe Rabbeinu: "Go to the people and sanctify them... and set boundaries for the people."

Just as the [Torah is eternal]() in all its matters and details, there lies within the concept of the three days of preparation an eternal directive: that every Jew, man and woman, must constantly remember that Hashem is perpetually instructing them: "Go to the people and sanctify them"—go and help every single one of this ["holy nation"]() to be permeated with holiness and to be a fitting vessel (*keli*) for the receiving of the Torah and mitzvos in daily, everyday life.

For the Almighty’s [message]() is also a granting of strength to carry it out in practice, for [action]() is the essential thing.

If this is so regarding helping all Jews, even adults, then how much more so regarding Jewish children during the years when their entire personality is being formed and the foundation for their entire life is being laid. And especially regarding Jewish daughters, for the Jewish daughter must be the *akeres habayis* (the mainstay of the home), upon whom depends, to a very great extent, the orientation and daily conduct of the entire home and the entire family.

Therefore, the matter of the education of girls and the institutions that occupy themselves with this is of such supreme importance, especially the **Seminary for Teachers and Schools for Girls in Kfar Chabad**.

I wish you great success in your undertaking and activities to help create the financial means so that the aforementioned institutions may not only continue their educational work, but also be able to strengthen and expand the possibilities to train as many Jewish daughters as possible in the true spirit of Torah, to fulfill their task in life.

May the merit of this work stand by you all to receive the Almighty’s blessings in everything you need, together with your households, may they live, in both material and spiritual matters alike.

With blessings for success and good tidings, and a joyous Yom Tov of receiving the Torah with joy and inwardness.

## 1062

1062

B"H, the Days of Limitation, 5731
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mr. Avraham, may he live,

Shalom u’vracha!

I am writing to express my thanks for your letter, along with the article regarding the visit to Kfar Chabad.

It is my hope that the impression made upon the visitors by the atmosphere and life in Kfar Chabad, etc., will be realized in action and deed, based on the statement of our Sages, of blessed memory, that "the deed is the essential thing." I refer simply to an increase in the performance of the practical mitzvos of our holy Torah—Torah of life—which, as its name implies, is an instruction for daily life, for a life worthy of the name.

And if this applies to every individual, it applies all the more so to the youth, who must still establish a worldview upon which they will determine their lives and the lives of their families when the time comes. And in the same vein, if this applies everywhere, it applies all the more so in the land that is called, even by all the nations of the world, the Holy Land—our holy land, of which it is said, "A land which Hashem your G-d seeks out; the eyes of Hashem your G-d are always upon it, from the beginning of the year to the end of the year."

Especially in our current era, fraught with confusion, and in the international situation where we are in need of increased security and the strengthening of protection for the sons and daughters of Israel wherever they may be, including, in particular, our holy land—for the Torah and its mitzvos are a shield against anything undesirable, and they are the path and the means for the blessing of Hashem, who guards His people Israel. In the words of the verse—in connection with these days of preparation for the festival of the Giving of our Torah and the receiving of the Torah—"You have seen what I did to Egypt... and now, if you will indeed hearken to My voice and keep My covenant, then you shall be a treasure to Me among all the peoples, for all the earth is Mine" (Yisro 19:4-5).

With a blessing to all the students to go "from strength to strength" in the study of our Torah and the performance of its mitzvos, and to bear with righteousness and pride the traditional title for every son and daughter of Israel—a son of Avraham, Yitzchak, and Yaakov, and a daughter of Sarah, Rivkah, Rachel, and Leah.

And with a blessing for a happy holiday, to receive the Torah with joy and inwardness.
