## 1065

1065

B"H, Motzaei Shabbos Kodesh, 12 Sivan, 5731
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed Rabbi, the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, learned, and accomplished, a man of stature, of distinguished lineage, etc., R' Yitzchak [Meir] HaKohen, may he live:

Shalom u’vracha!

I received your letter, and since its content was puzzling to me, I wished to delay my response until I received further information from Eretz Yisrael (may it be rebuilt and established). However, since Rabbi R' S. Elberg—a learned and esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and accomplished activist—informed me that you requested to clarify the matter of the letter with me, I do not wish to delay any longer.

The reason for my bewilderment is that it is known from my practice for many years that I do not mention the name of any private individual, nor of any specific party. This is how I acted during the farbrengen to which you apparently refer.

Furthermore, my request, insistence, and bewilderment were regarding the fact that there was no denial of the rumor about which you write. Before I spoke about this at the farbrengen, I attempted to clarify here as well, within the circles of Agudas Yisrael, why there was no denial, and I received no answer. Even though I was told that the entire matter—my questioning as to where the denial was—was printed in "Shaarim," as mentioned, after several **weeks** there was still no denial whatsoever.

I would add that the request for a denial was, obviously and simply, not for my honor nor for the honor of my father’s house, but rather to negate the interpretation being given to the lack of a denial in circles that are growing ever larger—and the wise will understand.

The request for a denial was not only regarding the matter about which you write, but also regarding what was published in "Haaretz" concerning a conversation with the Prime Minister, and what was supposedly said to her regarding the silence of the "Moetzes Gedolei HaTorah." It is strange that you do not mention anything regarding this. I also spoke with your brother-in-law, the esteemed Rabbi [R' R.S.B.] shlita, (during his visit here) regarding a denial of this.

And since, as the days go by, yet another matter has been added—that a well-known Rosh Yeshivah in Eretz Yisrael (may it be rebuilt and established) supposedly summoned a certain person and told him that although he had promised to act regarding the repeal of the [law] of "Who is a Jew," and to take various actions in this regard, since a booklet was printed, etc., he is canceling all his promises and will not do anything, etc.—it is understood that this, too, is being used by those ever-growing circles, and they are calling the Rosh Yeshivah by name. The interpretation they are giving to this matter regarding the honor of the Roshei Yeshivos in general, etc., etc., is well understood.

May it be the will of Hashem that as we come from the time of the giving of our Torah, when Hashem chose His people Yisrael from all the nations, and as it is stated [in Maseches Sofrim] that on Motzaei Atzeres we read Megillas Ruth (as most of the laws of conversion according to Halacha are learned from there), Hashem will mend the breaches of His people Yisrael, and the entire world will recognize, as it is said regarding the giving of the Torah: "[And you shall keep] My covenant, and you shall be a treasure to Me from among all the nations."

With respect and blessing.

## 166

[Motzaei Shabbos, 12 Sivan, 5731]

. . . I have received your letter, and may Hashem Yisbarach fulfill your heart’s desires for the good.

It is certainly superfluous to emphasize the necessity of strengthening matters of Torah and mitzvos in one’s daily life. In addition to the essential point—that a Yid must live according to the will of the Ribono shel Olam—this is also the path to receive an increase in the Ribono shel Olam’s blessings in everything one needs. And in matters of Torah, mitzvos, and Yiddishkeit in general, no matter how good the situation may be, there is always room to improve and strengthen.

In these present days, immediately following Matan Torah—which is the conclusion and perfection of Pesach, [as the verse states](#_ftn_689): "When you bring the people out of Egypt, you shall serve Elokus on this mountain"—the Yom Tov of liberation from the galus of Mitzrayim, and the Yom Tov of Matan Torah, in both of which the greatest events for Klal Yisrael saw the Jewish women and daughters play a very large part, the Jewish woman and daughter must specifically reflect upon the highly important role that Hashgacha Elyona has assigned to her in ensuring the continuity of the Jewish people.

The [enclosed](#_ftn_691) letter to the annual convention of Agudas N'shei U'Bnos Chabad has a direct connection to the above. And my hope is that the content will have the desired effect.

## 167

[B"H, Monday, Parshas Shelach, 5731]
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the students of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch, Montreal,
On the occasion of the Siyum,
May Hashem grant them life,

Peace and Blessing!

I received with pleasure the news regarding the Siyum celebration, and may it be Hashem’s will that it take place in a propitious and successful hour.

To connect this matter with the [Parsha of the day], [as is the custom], and especially since it is the portion of the reading for the Shabbos [from which] all six days of the week are blessed — including the [day of the celebration]:

One of the points of this Parsha is the slander of the Meraglim: **"Our little ones will be a spoil."**

This was a primary argument, as is also evident from the emphasis in the response of the Ribono shel Olam: **"But your little ones, whom you said would be a spoil, them I will bring in, and they shall know the land..."**

[Seemingly], it is difficult to understand why the Meraglim saw fit to base their slander specifically on the "little ones" (rather than "our children," or similar terms), for surely they intended to refer to all those who were not in the category of those destined to "fall by the sword" (mentioned previously), namely, those under twenty years of age.

Admittedly, in a simple sense, one could say that since young children are most beloved and the love for them is more manifest, the Meraglim sought to arouse pity for them in the face of the danger expected from [a people] strong and of great stature, etc.

However, since the response and the promise of the Ribono shel Olam also emphasized the "little ones," as mentioned above — **"But your little ones... them I will bring in, and they shall know..."** — it is proven that the "little ones" have a special connection to entering the land and knowing it.

The matter is understood based on the [teaching of our Sages] regarding the praise of Yosef, who provided bread according to the "little ones" — for a child crumbles more than he eats, and it is necessary to give them in abundance because they crumble.

Now, it is known that the [bread] and the nourishment of the soul of every one of Bnei Yisrael is our Torah, the Torah of life. In this, there is a difference between those who are "great in knowledge" and those who are "little in knowledge." For the great ones, their Torah is fixed [as the law] given to each individual in the laws of Torah study, [and the study] leads to action — the fulfillment of mitzvos with beauty (*hiddur*).

Not so the "little ones" (in knowledge of Torah) — besides the fact that an important part of their strength is invested in other matters, their Torah and mitzvos are also sometimes mixed with ulterior motives; the study is without the necessary focus and exertion, and therefore it is also crumbled and forgotten more than it is eaten and absorbed into their inner being.

This was also the intention of the [Meraglim] in slandering the land, for they feared that if they were to enter the land and occupy themselves with plowing and sowing, etc., the work of the land and their labor would become their "fixed" occupation, while their Torah would be "temporary," and consequently their knowledge would be "little" — *taf* — and they would become a "spoil" (and perform the work) of the people of the land.

To this came the response: "But your little ones, whom you said would be a spoil, them I will bring in, and they shall know the land." For the "little ones" — each person at the beginning of their study (while they are still small in knowledge), and generally those who spend an important part of their day occupied with physical matters, yet nevertheless **fix** times for Torah and fulfill mitzvos with beauty — this is more precious in the eyes of Hashem than the service of the generation of the desert. For the latter did not have obstacles and hindrances, whereas for those entering the land, their stature is greater due to the virtue of the constraint, the confusion, and the trials that they overcome, thereby drawing the holiness and unity of Hashem into the land. This is according to the [well-known interpretation] of **"One nation in the land"** — that they draw down the unity of Havayah even into the matters of the land.

Now, it is known that the intention of our Rebbes, the *Nesi'im* — the founders of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim — is to produce students who are not only Torah scholars in fear of Heaven and fulfillers of mitzvos with beauty, but who will also be [lamps] to illuminate and kindle lamps — [the lamp] of mitzvah and the Torah of light [with the lamp] of Havayah, the soul of man —

In all the "little ones" and those who are (for the time being) small in knowledge, and to kindle them in such a way [until] the flame rises of its own accord.

May it be Hashem’s will that each and every one of the graduates, among all the students of Tomchei Temimim wherever they may be, will fulfill their aforementioned role in its entirety.

[And after] the promise to the children, telling them that they would enter the land and offer [libations], burnt offerings, sacrifices, and meal offerings,

So may it be for us, through [our deeds] and our *avodah* at the end of the time of exile —

In the true and complete Redemption and the building of the Chosen House by [Moshiach] Tzidkeinu, speedily in our days, as it is written: [For the conductor], a Psalm of David, to bring to remembrance, O G-d, to save me; O Hashem, make haste to my help.

With blessings for success and good tidings in all the aforementioned.

## 170

28 Sivan, 5731
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and learned Rabbi Zerach, known as Dr. Warhaftig,

Shalom u’Bracha!

With much delay, I received your letter of 17 Iyar, along with its enclosure. Thank you for your thoughtfulness in sending it to me.

After asking your forgiveness, I must express my astonishment at its content, which suggests that the matter is being exaggerated. It is surely known to you that the situation is **far more** alarming than what is written in the press, and what is even more alarming is that no one is raising their voice or speaking out, and a word to the wise is sufficient.

As an example regarding what you wrote concerning the conversions in Vienna: it is well known to all, and has even been published in the press, that more than three hundred people who are not of the Children of Israel passed through there, while the shluchim rabbis who visited found information regarding only fifty-two or fifty-four. This means that more than two hundred and fifty did not undergo any conversion process at all—not even a completely empty ceremony. Most of them, aside from those who have already left, are currently in Eretz Yisrael, and their names and addresses are **known**, as they passed through the immigration offices, etc.

As mentioned above, no one is paying any mind to ask a simple question: how is it possible that they were registered as Jews, and they have been in the country for several months, and it is all considered "firm and established"?

I have chosen this example because you mentioned it in your letter. But surely you are also aware of the alarming procedure that was conducted in South America by a single individual (who visited me as well in New York—before traveling to South America), who "converted" people there right and left. When a brazen person asked an official at the Ministry of Interior—how is this possible?—he replied that there is a clear instruction in the law and from his superiors in Eretz Yisrael not to investigate the background of those coming to settle in the country, whether they converted, how they converted, who converted them, etc. We are talking about hundreds of cases. The same is true in California. My intention, as stated above, is not regarding Reform conversion, but rather the total absence of any conversion at all. Their names are also known since they immigrated to the country, and they have files in the Ministry of Interior, etc. The situation in Marseille is similar.

There is much more to add, but there is no point in dwelling on such an alarming matter; as mentioned, it is even more alarming that no one is paying attention to it.

Regarding the phrasing of your letter—that the information is not available—the reality is entirely the opposite. What has been published is only a fraction of a fraction of the scandal in this area: the registration of non-Jews as Jews without any ceremony whatsoever, and conversions that are completely contrary to Halacha, conducted in a ridiculous manner, etc. It has reached the point where some even brought the photographs with them, and they are currently hanging in their homes in Eretz Yisrael, even though they were "converted" in Vienna.

Regarding the conclusion of your letter, that "no personal benefit should be a reason to abandon the interests concerning this (religious) public"—after asking your forgiveness and the forgiveness of your colleagues, I have clear information from first-hand, reliable sources that if you were to leave the government coalition, you would only remain on the outside for a short time. If you had stood firmly on the demand to rectify the terrible decree of "Who is a Jew" and the Law of Return, this law would have been rectified **long ago**.

As I have said on the occasion of a private conversation, the whole matter is like a doctor who advises cutting off the head in order to save the leg, and brings proof for his words by saying that sometimes one cuts off a leg to save the body and the head if there is no other choice. Surely for someone like you, no further explanation is needed.

It is a pity for our generation, an orphaned generation, that instead of having the opportunity to be recorded in the annals of Jewish history as having achieved extraordinary religious accomplishments, it will be recorded, G-d forbid, as an eternal disgrace that this is the **first time** that someone registered as a "representative of millions of Bnei Yisrael"—[Mrs. Shalit] and her two children—as "Jews," and now they are conspiring against the existence of the entire Jewish people wherever they may be, by nullifying the barrier and the distinction between Israel and the nations, using various strange and bizarre arguments.

Among these is the "explanation" I heard, that the "Who is a Jew" law and the Law of Return have nothing to do with religion, but are merely a formal matter of registering citizens, etc.

I replied that even regarding this, there is a clear instruction in our eternal Torah, the Torah of Truth. When a Caesar asked a small child, "Shall I give you a seal, and you bow down and take it, so that they will say you have accepted the authority of the king"—meaning that it is only a formal matter, and the subject was a small child—he said to him, "Woe unto you, Caesar..." (Gittin 57b, see there).

May it be the will of Hashem, the merciful and gracious G-d, that He inspire a spirit from above upon each and every one, and that you and your colleagues will leave the coalition speedily in our days—specifically (with pride and joy) for the reason mentioned above, and not because of secondary matters. May your future letters be happy and good with true goodness—good for Heaven and good for people—according to our holy Torah, of which it is said: "I have given you a good teaching."

With respect and blessing,

**M. Schneerson**

P.S. I received a letter from my friend, the great Rabbi and Chossid, etc., etc., R. S.Y. Zevin, to whom you gave a copy of your letter to me; therefore, a copy of this letter of mine is being sent to him as well.

171

## 172

B"H, 28 Sivan, 5731
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the honorable Rabbis, the pious and distinguished Chassidim, the pillars of the community, members of the Beis Din Tzedek for all Ashkenazic congregations in Jerusalem, the Holy City, may it be rebuilt and established speedily in our days.

Greetings and blessings!

I acknowledge receipt of your letter dated 27 Iyar.

Regarding the man who is threatening with the decree you describe—may Hashem protect us—I have not met with him. However, in my opinion, it makes little difference, for any real influence over him and his associates can only be exerted through public pressure and outcry—by way of the press, notices, proclamations, public rallies, and the like. May it be that this, at least, will succeed.

May it be the will of the Ribono shel Olam, who mends the breaches of His people Israel, that He have compassion and mercy upon the remnant of the survivors, especially in our generation, this orphaned generation. May He, in His kindness and mercy, mend all breaches and pour out a spirit from on high upon every one of our brethren, the Children of Israel, wherever they may be, to walk in the path of Torah and mitzvos in their daily lives. May He hasten the end of our double and redoubled darkness of exile, speedily and in our days, through Moshiach Tzidkeinu, who will come and redeem us, leading us upright to our land.

With respect and blessing.

## 1073

[28 Sivan, 5731]

Regarding the publication of the monthly journal in Russian, I believe you have already been answered.

What I would add to this is that, naturally, the matter itself is very correct—provided that it is at least close to the required standard. For this, there must be a person who is qualified for the task **and who will actually** occupy himself with it.

## 174

174

B”H, Erev Rosh Chodesh Tammuz, 5731
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To all participants in the testimonial dinner
of Yeshivas Achei Tmimim in Newark
May Hashem grant them life

Peace and blessing!

I send my greetings and heartfelt wishes to the esteemed guests and participants at the gathering taking place this coming Rosh Chodesh Tammuz.

This month holds special significance for Yeshivas Achei Tmimim in Newark, as it does for many similar educational institutions in various parts of the world that were founded by, and in the spirit of, my father-in-law, the Rebbe. For this is the month of his liberation 44 years ago, after he risked his life through his *mesiras nefesh* activities for Torah and Yiddishkeit in a confrontation with a powerful regime.

His liberation on 12-13 Tammuz was a turning point not only in his own life and work, but also for the entirety of Russian Jewry, which at that time constituted the majority of the Jewish people and stood in danger of forced assimilation and annihilation, *chas v’shalom*, under the pressure of a colossal power that stopped at nothing to carry out its plans.

His victory over such a powerful opponent was also not merely a [personal](#_ftn_719) victory, but a victory for *Klal Yisrael*, as the coming years demonstrated. Torah-Yiddishkeit and the spirit of *Netzach Yisrael* remained firmly rooted in that land, and Russian Jewry continued to serve as a source of Torah and Chassidus, whose influence is felt to this day in Eretz Yisrael and everywhere else—no less so here in America.

It has often been emphasized that the purpose of a commemoration in Jewish life is not merely to record important events of the past, but that it should serve as a lesson for the present and the future.

True, no one can compare themselves to the *Baal HaGeulah* with his extraordinary powers and *mesiras nefesh* for Torah and *ahavas Yisrael*. However, one must not forget that the circumstances under which he worked and fought are not at all comparable to those we face here in this country. We live, *baruch Hashem*, in a land that cherishes the ideals of freedom and religious values; here, one does not need to risk one’s life to live *al pi Torah* and maintain Torah institutions. All that is required is to strengthen one’s own connection to Torah-Yiddishkeit and to have the firm will to uphold Yiddishkeit, dedicating to this nothing more than time, effort, and money.

The historical events commemorated on 12-13 Tammuz also show clearly that where there is a firm will and firm determination to act, then Divine blessing and success are guaranteed—especially in a matter of *zechus harabim*, the merit of many Jewish children, may they increase, whose entire future is bound up with this Torah institution.

Taking into account that the Yeshiva will soon be moving into [its beautiful new home](#_ftn_720), I wish to hope that all friends of the Yeshiva will further strengthen their support to enable the Yeshiva to continue to flourish and grow and go *meichayil el chayil* (from strength to strength). Thereby, one will also broaden the channels to receive the Almighty’s blessings in everything one needs, in both material and spiritual matters alike.

With honor and blessing for success and good tidings,

**M. Schneerson**

## 1075

B"H, 7 Tammuz, 5731
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 27 Sivan—and in accordance with your request, I am replying without waiting for my turn—in which you suggest that I invite your wife, may she live, etc.,

It is somewhat surprising, as it is surely known to you that it is [not](#_ftn_722) the custom in the Rebbe’s house at all to invite anyone. Rather, when people request to be received, then there is room to discuss the content of their letter and request, naturally in a manner that is appropriate to the words of the visitor, and so on. And I ask for your forgiveness that I am unable to fulfill your suggestion.

May Hashem, who oversees each and every one with Divine Providence, grant you success in an appropriate manner in all that you require, including the matter mentioned in this letter of yours.

Especially as these are auspicious days, a few days before 12-13 Tammuz, the days of the redemption of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, Nasi Yisroel, whose blessings you were privileged to receive. And surely you are aware of the significance of these days and their instruction for each and every one of us, within the entirety of Klal Yisroel.

With respect and blessings for good tidings.

## 178

There is a special segulah in the mitzvah of tefillin, for as our Sages have stated, "all the peoples of the earth shall see that you are called by the name of Hashem, and they shall be afraid of you," and it brings victory to the men of war.

Through all of this, you will cause true nachas ruach to your father, may Hashem avenge his blood, who, from the World of Truth where he resides, watches over what is being done by his children, takes great pleasure in their good conduct, and rejoices greatly in seeing that they are going "from strength to strength" in our Torah—the Torah of truth—and its mitzvos.

With blessings for a mazal tov to you and to the entire family, may they live and be well,

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 1079

[B"H](https://www.chabad.org/library/article_cdo/aid/735/jewish/Footnotes.htm#_ftn_735), Days of Redemption, the year **"When you take** the sum of the Children of Israel" [5731]

Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the residents of [Nachalat](https://www.chabad.org/library/article_cdo/aid/737/jewish/Footnotes.htm#_ftn_737) Har Chabad in our Holy Land—may it be built and established speedily in our days by Mashiach Tzidkeinu—

May Hashem grant them life.

Peace and Blessing!

In addition to the matters discussed at the farbrengen of these days of redemption, when many of our brothers, the Children of Israel, were gathered together—for there is special power in words spoken in a quorum of ten, [for](https://www.chabad.org/library/article_cdo/aid/738/jewish/Footnotes.htm#_ftn_738) where ten are gathered, the Shechinah rests, and all the more so when in the presence of many groups of ten of the Children of Israel—

In order to translate this into actual practice—[for](https://www.chabad.org/library/article_cdo/aid/739/jewish/Footnotes.htm#_ftn_739) action is the essential thing, [and](https://www.chabad.org/library/article_cdo/aid/740/jewish/Footnotes.htm#_ftn_740) "action is superior," especially action that is truly good, [good](https://www.chabad.org/library/article_cdo/aid/741/jewish/Footnotes.htm#_ftn_741) for Heaven and good for people alike—

It has occurred to me, and with your agreement—which I am certain will be given with joy and goodness of heart—to establish in Nachalat Har Chabad a **Gemach fund** for our brothers, the Children of Israel, who have emigrated from there, the birthplace of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, Nasi of Israel—

For these days are his birthday and also the day of his redemption—

And the practical beginning shall be by depositing into the Gemach fund the sum of seven thousand shekels (dollars).

And since a Gemach is, [as](https://www.chabad.org/library/article_cdo/aid/742/jewish/Footnotes.htm#_ftn_742) our Sages of blessed memory taught, for both the poor and the rich, may it be the will of Hashem that in this case the Gemach will be for those who are wealthy but happen to be in need of a loan at that time. May this bring the addition of yet another holy institution in Nachalat Har Chabad, contributing to the growth of all the material and spiritual affairs of the Nachala together. This includes, of course and primarily, that very soon, in our days, they will be reunited with their relatives, friends, and [all who are called by the name of Israel](https://www.chabad.org/library/article_cdo/aid/743/jewish/Footnotes.htm#_ftn_743) in that country and others like it—may they live and be well—

A reunion in joy and goodness of heart for all who meet, they and their households, and may this reunion be a near prelude to the fulfillment of the [prophecy](https://www.chabad.org/library/article_cdo/aid/744/jewish/Footnotes.htm#_ftn_744), "They shall see eye to eye when Hashem returns to Tzion," [and](https://www.chabad.org/library/article_cdo/aid/745/jewish/Footnotes.htm#_ftn_745) it is said, "Hashem has bared His holy arm in the eyes of all the nations, and all the ends of the earth shall see the salvation of our G-d."

With blessings for success in the above, including all the affairs of Nachalat Har Chabad, and for good tidings,

**M. Schneerson**

**It is obvious** that the above does not detract **in the slightest** from the importance and activity of the existing Gemach (in Nachalat Har Chabad, etc.)—but rather is intended to add to it and increase it.

P.S. To solidify the implementation of the above in practice, the individuals listed below will surely take upon themselves the management of the Gemach fund, at least for the time being. They are:

The distinguished Chassid, G-d-fearing man, who occupies himself with communal needs, R. Dober Rikman, R. Yehuda Batrashvili, and R. Naftali Kravitzky.

The letter is being sent via express mail, and they will surely confirm it in this manner as well. Thank you.

## 180

[14 Tammuz, 5731]

Everyone (even one who is a complete tzaddik all his days) prays **every day**, "Do not bring me into a test."

If they return to the United States, arguments (and consequently, tests) will immediately begin regarding their religious observance, which will be evident **in daily life**—as they will be conducting themselves differently from their parents, may they live and be well, in many details **every day** (eating, etc.), and especially on Shabbos, **etc.**

And one cannot demand of parents that they should not care that their child does not eat with them and says the reason is that it is forbidden to eat this.

[This is not the case when the parents visit Eretz Yisrael—where the question of eating and the like is nullified, and the parents' problem of "what will all their friends say when they see the gap between the parents and the children," etc., is **nullified**—especially since the visit is only for a few weeks, whereas their return to the United States is for a long time. After all, it is possible to study medicine in Eretz Yisrael as well.]

If the above is impossible and they do return to the United States, one must minimize the possibilities for tests and arguments as much as possible (by having the wedding as soon as possible, living independently, **etc., etc.**).

I will mention this at the gravesite.

## 181

B"H, 15 Tammuz, 5731
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished individual, occupied with communal needs,
R' Aharon and his wife, may they live,

Peace and blessing!

In anticipation of the wedding celebration of your son, the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished Rabbi Avigdor, may he live, with his bride, may she live, in a good and auspicious hour:

May it be the will of Hashem that it be in a good and auspicious hour, and that they build an eternal edifice upon the foundations of Torah and mitzvos, as they are illuminated [by the light of Torah, which is the teachings of Chassidus.](#_ftn_749)

With blessings of Mazal Tov.

P.S. In addition to the joy of the shidduch itself and the virtues you wrote of, I was pleased to learn—and this is the opportunity to express the great satisfaction I feel—of your generous contribution of $5,000 toward our activities. You surely know that even though one should generally not test Hashem—and on the contrary, "You shall be [wholehearted](#_ftn_750) with Hashem your G-d"—the mitzvah of tzedakah is an exception, as it is said regarding it, "And test Me now with this, etc." (Malachi 3:10; see also Shulchan Aruch, Yoreh Deah, end of section 247). Therefore, I was happy that this act of giving immediately brought about a positive outcome—the greatest blessing for parents: to see their eldest son, may he live, beginning to establish a family life as is fitting and proper.

As mentioned, for a mitzvah, it is not appropriate for a flesh and blood person to say "thank you," especially a mitzvah like tzedakah, which is [good](#_ftn_751) for Heaven and good for people. However, there is room to express the great satisfaction you have caused me, as well as the significant relief provided to the [Lubavitch](#_ftn_752) budget for various activities through your aforementioned donation, which was most timely.

I see from your letter and from the letter of your son, may he live, that you have set the date for the wedding. May it be His will that it takes place in a good and auspicious hour, and that the preparations be made with joy and a glad heart.

## 10182

10182

Students graduating eighth grade, Chabad School, Cholon

May it be the will of Hashem that each and every one of you [goes](#_ftn_754) from strength to strength in matters of Torah and its mitzvos, with persistence and diligence, with good conduct, and with joy and goodness of heart.

Especially as we continue in the days of redemption and joy of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, whose imprisonment and redemption [were not a private matter](#_ftn_755), for he was imprisoned because of his involvement with all his heart and soul in the education of the sons and daughters of Yisroel in Torah and its mitzvos. His redemption is the redemption of this approach, and a directive to every single son and daughter of Yisroel to strengthen themselves in their daily lives according to our Torah, the Torah of life, and the fulfillment of its mitzvos, [regarding which](#_ftn_756) it is said, "and he shall live by them," and to influence their entire environment in this direction.

With a blessing for success in all the above and for good tidings.

## 10,183

[16 Tammuz, 5731]

Regarding the explanation (and **not** through the aforementioned person mentioned in his letter) — that it is not my practice to intervene in the details of the activities, etc. — for to do so, one would need to be present at the meetings, to hear the arguments of all sides, etc.

## 10,184

B”H, 22 Tammuz, 5731
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mr. Simcha Raz

Shalom u’Bracha!

After the longest of intervals, it was a pleasant surprise to receive your letter, accompanied by a draft [of your book](#_ftn_758) which is about to be published, asking for my opinion on the matter.

In general, it is difficult for me to offer an opinion, as I did not personally know the late Rabbi, the Chossid, etc., R’ A.L. zt”l, to whose memory the book is dedicated; my acquaintance with him was only [through letters](#_ftn_759) and through reports of his most exalted activities. However, it is clearly of the utmost importance to publicize his way of life and his activities, especially in our generation, where the youth are wandering on paths that are no paths; they have shattered the idols of the previous generation, yet they have not yet found their own path in life. Out of a great thirst for substance and a great fear of emptiness, they grope in the darkness, grasping at all sorts of "ideals." Therefore, a book from which they can learn about a person who lived among them only recently—who, even though he was a product of the previous generation, maintained close ties with the most progressive individuals of our own generation, etc.—is of the greatest value.

On the other hand, I am not in a position to offer an opinion on the book itself, or on what should be emphasized more, and the like. I can only express my general impression: upon reading the draft, my conviction regarding the necessity of publishing such a book was further strengthened. May you be blessed for it.

Certainly, there are many students of the late R’ A.L. zt”l in Jerusalem; you should consult with them regarding the above, [as it is already said](#_ftn_760), "In the multitude of counselors there is salvation."

This letter is written during the days of the Geulah of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, and I trust that you are familiar with the story of his imprisonment and redemption.

May it be the will of Hashem that, as with all days of remembrance from the history of our nation’s great leaders—in the true sense of greatness—everyone will learn a lesson by bringing to mind the content of the event, its cause, its consequences, and so on. May this remembrance be evident in actual deed, [for as our Sages, of blessed memory, said](#_ftn_761), "The deed is the essential thing."

With respect and blessing.

P.S. Surely, following our conversation during your visit here, you will send to our library the publications of the society and the publications in which you take part, etc. Thank you in advance.

## 10,185

B"H, 22 Tammuz, 5731
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Blessings and peace!

In response to your letter of 11 Tammuz, the essence of which is that you have met with a certain individual, etc., and you are asking for my opinion regarding a shidduch in this matter.

[Here](#_ftn_762) it is generally neither correct nor good to begin establishing a family life in opposition to the wishes of parents, who have labored and nurtured so much in the upbringing of their daughter (or son) and hope to see from her (or him) nachas in every detail. And surely this is also the reason for the opposition of the parents, sheyichyu, as you write, because they do not see this shidduch as good and suitable **for her**, etc.

Furthermore, if the young man is upright and possesses good character traits, surely he, too, would not want to be the cause and catalyst for a rift between a daughter and her parents.

What is written above is, as mentioned, a general rule, but it carries special weight for the reasons stated when the matter concerns the eldest son or daughter in a family, who to a significant degree serves as a guide for the brothers and sisters who follow.

It is understood that my intention in what is stated is not regarding a "sacrifice for the sake of the parents," but rather that it is not good or suitable for the daughter (and likewise for the person in question) to begin establishing life upon a foundation of rift in general, and especially between children and parents.

I would add that based on my impression from meeting with her father, sheyichye, several times, and once with her mother, tichye, they are certainly and absolutely seeking only her best interest.

May Hashem, who watches over each and every one with hashgacha pratis, provide her with her true, good zivug in every detail.

Especially since you wrote on the eve of the days of redemption (12-13 Tammuz) of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, which continues an added measure of blessing for Jews in general, and especially for those who belong to the educational institutions conducted in his spirit, in which you also have a good part as a teacher in one of them.

With blessings for success in all your affairs and for good tidings regarding the aforementioned.

## 1986

[25 Tammuz, 5731]

In response to your question regarding how to help your daughter:

When parents conduct themselves on a daily basis in accordance with the will of the "Healer of all flesh and Who performs wonders" (Hashem), as explained in the Shulchan Aruch, this adds to the success of the treatment provided by a human physician (who is the messenger of the Healer of all flesh) for the children of these parents. And even if it seems to the parents that it is difficult to change their current conduct, they surely do more difficult things for the sake of their children.

There is no need at all to travel here, as the answer is as stated above. Rather, the travel expenses should be given to tzedakah **in the merit of your daughter, may she live and be well.**

I will mention this at the tziyun.

## 10187

10187

[B"H](#_ftn_765), End of Tammuz, 5731

Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of the letter . . .

As we come from the days of Geulah, 12th-13th of Tammuz—the Geulah of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, Nasi Yisrael, from his imprisonment in his native land, where he was held captive for his [great](#_edn_136), powerful, and lofty avodah in strengthening and disseminating Torah and mitzvos, despite the decrees against this that were then at their peak—and through the mercies of Hashem, he emerged victorious, for those who [imprisoned him](#_ftn_766) were the very ones who released him.

[And in the words](#_edn_137) of my father-in-law, the Rebbe (for the first celebration of 12 Tammuz): "The Ribono shel Olam did not redeem only him on 12 Tammuz, but also all those who cherish our holy Torah, those who observe mitzvos, and even those who are [called](#_edn_138) by the name 'Jew,' for every Jewish person (regardless of his personal state regarding the observance and fulfillment of mitzvos) has a heart that is whole with Hashem and His Torah."

[As our Sages of blessed memory said](#_edn_139) regarding the verse, "The [tzaddik](#_edn_140) shall flourish like a date palm": Just as the heart of the date palm is directed upward, so too is the heart of the Jewish people directed toward their Father in Heaven. And they further said: Just as the date palm has no waste, so too the Jewish people have no waste.

Therefore, the days following this are days of segulah for all Jewish men and women, wherever they may be, to increase in strengthening ["Torah](#_edn_141) and Yiddishkeit in every place, according to one's capacity," and to disseminate them, going from strength to strength, ever increasing in light.

Especially when each person contemplates that if, in that land, at that time, and under those conditions, they acted and accomplished in strengthening and disseminating Torah and mitzvos—and succeeded, to the point that even now, after [a jubilee of years](#_edn_142), we see their fruits and the fruits of their fruits—

Then how much more so, and how much more certainly, in countries and conditions that are incomparably easier and better.

May it be the will that each and every one of us, among all our brethren, the Children of Israel, may they live and be well, does all of the above, and does so with [simcha](#_edn_143) and (consequently) with zerizus.

And Hashem is the Helper, [as it is written](#_edn_144): "[Hashem](#_edn_145), make haste to help me; Elokim, make haste to my aid... Hashem, do not delay."

With blessings for success,

**M. Schneerson**

***

[With blessings](#_ftn_773) for success in disseminating the maayanos and Yiddishkeit in general.

The proofs (which begin "And behold, the Torah likens...") were received, and thank you. There is absolutely no time available to review them as their content requires, and I ask for forgiveness. Regarding their publication—if this will cause the reader to desire to study Da'as Chassidus and the like, it is understood that it is worthwhile, provided that there are citations to the seforim of Da'as Chassidus, etc., and that there is an introduction explaining the intended content, and so forth.

***

P.S. I have received your letter . . . The proposal regarding the funds will not be accepted now due to the security situation. And a word to the wise is sufficient.

[With blessings](#_ftn_775) for success in disseminating Yiddishkeit in general and the maayanos in particular, with health and good tidings.

## 10,188

B"H, Erev Rosh Chodesh Menachem Av, 5731
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished bochur, a man of stature, who seeks the good of his people, possessing noble character traits, a scion of a noble lineage, R' Schneur Zalman, shlita,

This is especially relevant as we are at the conclusion and seal of the month of Tammuz, which contains the Chabad theme of the redemption of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, and as he said then, it was not he alone who was redeemed, but rather it was a redemption for all who are connected to him, etc.—and to use his own language in his letter—all who are called by the name Yisrael. And furthermore, and most essentially, the redemption of the approach—the Chabad approach—which is founded upon Ahavas Yisrael, Ahavas HaTorah, and Ahavas Hashem, with the emphasis that [they are all one].

And the [words] of the great teacher, the Rambam, are well known: that maintaining a healthy and sound body is among the ways of Hashem.

With blessings for health and for good tidings in all the aforementioned, and for the imminent fulfillment of the [prophecy] that these days will be transformed into gladness and joy,

With respect and blessing.

P.S. I have just returned from the Tziyun of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, and naturally, I mentioned you in all the aforementioned, as well as your wife, shetichyeh.

## 189

B"H, Erev Rosh Chodesh Menachem Av, 5731
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mrs. Rachel, may she live and be well,

Greetings and blessings!

It is a pleasant duty for me to acknowledge receipt of your telegram in due time.

I wish to express my hope that just as you informed me then of the beginning of the improvement in your husband’s health, shlita, so too, very soon, you will inform me of his complete recovery and healing.

And in the traditional phrasing, may you both lengthen your days and years in goodness and pleasantness, while utilizing the unique opportunities granted to you by Divine Providence for the benefit of the collective and the individual alike.

With respect and blessing for good tidings in all the aforementioned.

## 10,194

B"H, 5 Menachem Av, 5731
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed Rabbi, the Chassid, the G-d-fearing man, a man of fine character, a man of many accomplishments, a man of stature, from a holy lineage, etc., Rabbi [Yitzchak](#_ftn_792) Meir, may he live, Cohen.

Peace and Blessing!

I hereby acknowledge with thanks receipt of your letter from the 21st of Tammuz.

And although [our Sages of blessed memory said](#_ftn_793) that one should not cry out over the past, since I fear that similar matters and events might occur again in the future, I will explain my reasons and justifications for the necessity of a denial and the like. And it is this:

It is understood that I was not concerned about what was written in such-and-such a newspaper or such-and-such a weekly regarding its influence on you or the like, or on me or the like, but rather on the readers of the newspaper and the weekly. That is to say, my personal assessment of these publications and my personal relationship with them is not what matters so much, but rather the value of their influence on the readers and the circle of readers. And the reality is that both the newspaper and the weekly in question have an influence on a broad circle in general, and what is even more relevant to our matter is that they have an influence on a broad circle of those who are ["limping](#_ftn_794) between two opinions," as I also saw in the case regarding which I wrote to you.

And although it is simple that I have no desire to cause you distress, as mentioned above, I fear that this also concerns the future. To the best of my knowledge, the delay of the denial regarding the weekly and the lack of a denial until now regarding the newspaper has caused damage, etc., and a word to the wise is sufficient.

And as we stand in these days, when the hope is that they will soon be transformed into gladness [and joy](#_ftn_795) and all decrees against the Jewish people wherever they may be will be nullified—decrees from the outside and even harsher decrees from our straying and misguided brothers—may it be the will that this nullification be with kindness and mercy, speedily in our days, and may the Children of Israel bring each other only good, in a visible and revealed manner.

With respect and blessing, looking forward to good news regarding the content of our correspondence, and may it be the will that this too happens speedily in our days.

## 196

196

B.H., 15 Menachem Av, 5731
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the N'shei Chabad who are active on behalf of our brethren, the Children of Israel, and their families who have come from those countries—new immigrants to our Holy Land, may it be built and established by Moshiach Tzidkeinu speedily in our days,

May Hashem grant them life,

Blessings and peace!

I received with pleasure your letter in which you write—at least in outline—of your activities to ease the trials of integration for our brothers and sisters who have recently immigrated from lands of distress to our Holy Land [land](#_ftn_797) that is good and spacious, and especially those who have come from behind the "Iron Curtain."

Surely there are many others engaged in this most important work, and you are in communication with one another, which will certainly increase your success.

I am also confident that you emphasize, as much as is necessary, that for every one of our people, the Children of Israel, the way of life is to conduct one’s daily life according to our Torah, the Torah of life.

This is true in every place and at every time, and all the more so in our Holy Land, [land](#_ftn_798) upon which the eyes of Hashem your G-d are at all times, from the beginning of the year to the end of the year.

In accordance with this, each of you who is active in this field helps them, in particular, to organize their lives on the foundation of our Torah, the Torah of life, and its mitzvos, [of which it is said](#_ftn_799) "and he shall live by them," and you encourage them not to be impressed by the difficulties that sometimes exist in this.

As for those arriving from there who, due to circumstances beyond their control, did not have the possibility of providing their sons and daughters with an education based on the purity of our holy Torah—and perhaps, as a result, became accustomed to inappropriate customs—it is clear that in their previous living conditions, they were coerced, etc.

On the contrary: if, under those conditions, they overcame the greatest obstacles and impediments—sometimes even to the point of actual danger—and guarded the ember of Yiddishkeit, the *pintele Yid* that exists in its entirety within every single one of the Children of Israel wherever they may be; and if they risked their lives to observe every law and even every Jewish custom they knew of and were able to practice, even if only through *mesiras nefesh*—then, when they emerge into relief and find themselves in a land whose atmosphere is also holy, and where special powers have been granted by Hashem, Creator of the world and its Guide, to conduct oneself according to the will of Hashem and His instructions in His Torah, then surely, and most certainly, they will organize their lives with relief, joy, and a good heart. First and foremost, they will organize the education of their sons and daughters in a manner befitting a holy nation dwelling in the Holy Land.

And surely, even if at times [the beginning is difficult](#_ftn_800), it is only the beginning that is difficult; afterwards, the difficulties will diminish and lessen until they are nullified. This is especially true through the encouragement and assistance, both physical and spiritual, that they will receive from each of you to whom a single soul of Israel is precious—and all the more so these precious souls who stood with *mesiras nefesh* and guarded the ember, which is [the sparks](#_ftn_801) of the sparks of the fire of the flame of Hashem. This encouragement and help should be given with great joy, vitality, and Chassidic enthusiasm, founded upon the teachings of our Rebbes, the Nesi'im, may their merit protect us, that the love of Hashem, the love of the Torah, and the love of Israel [are one](#_ftn_802).

May it be the will of Hashem that the aforementioned activities will be so effective that those who are in need of encouragement and help today will very soon themselves become those who encourage and help others in their surroundings, and our brothers and sisters, may they live and be well, who have immigrated and will immigrate after them, in a manner that is ever-increasing.

With blessings for success in your greatest and most important work—saving souls in the spiritual sense. Since we are dealing with a holy nation, spirituality and physicality go together; that is to say, salvation in the physical sense as well, in a manner that is ever-increasing and adding light.

And for good tidings regarding all of the above.

P.S. It is understood that although my letter is addressed to you, the words are directed to all those who will join or have already joined you from among the entirety of the Children of Israel, may they live and be well, who will surely, with the appropriate inspiration, also cooperate in all that has been mentioned. Especially since we see tangibly that the woman and the girl succeed in this work even more than the man and the boy. In all this activity and the like, the [words](#_ftn_803) of our Sages, of blessed memory, are well known: "The promise that the Holy One, blessed be He, made to the women is greater than that made to the men."

10,197

B"H, 20 Menachem Av, 5731
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the Bnos Chabad Organization of Kfar Chabad, in our Holy Land, may it be rebuilt
Through Mashiach Tzidkeinu speedily in our days
May Hashem grant them life

Blessings and peace!

I received with pleasure your letter from Motzaei Shabbos Matos-Masei, bearing good tidings regarding the establishment of the organization and the good resolutions concerning the strengthening of Yiddishkeit and its dissemination, especially regarding the schools of the Reshet, and in addition—and this is the main point—regarding the members of the organization.

It is my firm hope that you are making a special effort to increase the number of members in the organization, especially in accordance with the directive of our Torah, the Torah of life, to ascend in holiness. The intention here is both in quantity and in quality; regarding quantity, the primary focus is to increase the number of members. And there is nothing that can stand before the will, especially when it is accompanied by a living example of the importance of the organization and its good activities.

The time is conducive for vigorous activity in all of the above and for success in this, for the period following the fifteenth of Av has begun, regarding which our Sages of blessed memory taught that this is when the avodah begins in a manner of "one who adds, and Hashem will add" (Maseches Taanis, end of the tractate). This holds special importance for the women and daughters of Yisrael, as hinted at in the words of the Sages and their Mishnah (ibid.): "There were no better days for Yisrael than the fifteenth of Av... when the daughters of Yerushalayim would go out..." and in the passage of the Gemara: "The daughters of Yisrael would go out..."

With blessings for success and for good tidings.

## 199

[Rosh Chodesh Elul, 5731]

... regarding the halachos necessary for daily life (whether for her, or for the students in her class).

I will mention [you] at the Tziyun for success.

3 Elul, 5731
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Mr. Aharon Yariv, shlita,

Shalom u’vracha,

It was a pleasant surprise to receive a letter from you after such a long hiatus—though, of course, I have been inquiring about your welfare and the activities of you and your colleagues, shlita, among our friends in Eretz Yisrael.

May it be the will of Hashem that this letter also serves as a good beginning for positive content in our future correspondence.

Regarding the main point of your letter—concerning the "partial settlement"—I am somewhat surprised that the tone of your letter leaves room for the assessment that the entire matter is in doubt, and that there is room to debate the merits or demerits of the matter as a whole. It is well known abroad, and surely known to you and your peers, that the current situation concerns only the details, the timing, what will be received in exchange, and so forth.

I have already stated on an appropriate occasion—though, of course, not for publication, but in conversation with those whom I hoped would convey my opinion to your circles and those close to you—that in the language of the Hebrew legal system, the situation is "its beginning was by choice, and its end by compulsion." My meaning is that while a year ago, and certainly two years ago, the matter rested entirely on the choice of Yisrael—whether to withdraw from the Canal or to remain there, etc.—the beginning occurred immediately after the Six-Day War with the announcement to "all concerned parties" that they were prepared to return the occupied territories (and apparently, there was precision in this, to avoid the term "liberated territories"). This announcement was repeated on numerous and varied occasions. And what is perhaps even more important: the **caution** exercised not to block the Canal in a way that would require many years to reopen it—all of this was tantamount to a clear and open declaration inviting the reopening of the Canal. It naturally never occurred to anyone that ownership of the Canal would be handed over to Yisrael, nor to the United States, but there was room for doubt as to whether ownership would be handed over to Egypt alone, or to Egypt in conjunction with its ally, the Soviet Union, or to Egypt as a satellite of the Soviet Union.

It is also known to any beginner in engineering that what was written in certain newspapers—that it was impossible to destroy the Canal or block it properly—is baseless. Especially since the length of the Canal is 100 kilometers or more, and its eastern bank was not under observation every single night.

This impression is further strengthened by the fact that it is known to anyone interested that despite the ceasefire, and literally within the first twenty-four hours, they brought new missile batteries to the western bank and continued to do so throughout the entire period, without any reaction from Yisrael (except for verbal protests, which from the outset had no prospect of changing the situation, other than at most—that through this, they might receive a bit more weaponry from the U.S., which in any case is far less than the weaponry being brought with such frequency to the western bank).

Since the gap between the forces was steadily narrowing, and it was impossible in any way to match the quantity and quality of the weaponry from the Soviet Union with the measure and weight of the weaponry from the U.S., then, as mentioned above, what began by choice turned into compulsion through the application of pressure from all sides, including the so-called friends, until the situation in the last half-year—and perhaps even before that—is that now there is no choice. And surely it is known to you that one does not need what is termed "pressure" (in diplomatic language) from the United States, but merely the cessation of the supply of weapons and funds, and nothing more.

What is even more distressing and painful is that although a similar situation has occurred in the past—and twice, with the withdrawal from the Canal in 1956 and the announcement in 1967 that they were prepared to return the "occupied" territories—they did not achieve a change in the mindset of the Egyptians, nor the mindset of the Soviet Union, and not even the mindset of the U.S. in favor of Yisrael. This position was interpreted only as a weakness of spirit, at the very least among those who set the policy in Yisrael regarding relations with Egypt, with the Arabs in general, and also with the U.S. and the Soviet Union. And in our world—which is not the gentle world of truth, justice, and integrity—weakness **invites** pressure, not a feeling of pity that would lead to actions of a tangible and decisive nature. Yet, despite all this, they continue along the aforementioned line, and to our great sorrow and pain, not only in speech but also in action, and they attempt to quiet public opinion with strange explanations. For example, that Yisrael has several friends among the governments of the nations of the world, or that since Yisrael has helped African countries in various areas, they will cooperate at least in voting at the U.N. so that Egypt will expel the Soviet Union. And even the explanation heard recently—and I ask your forgiveness for this, as the following was published in the name of military circles—that the strength of the IDF is now much greater than it was during the Six-Day War. While this statement is, of course, true in itself, it has no relevance to the state of affairs, for what matters is the balance between the strength of the IDF **now** versus the strength present across the Canal **now**, not as the strength of the opposing side was three years ago. And it is known that the balance is now much worse than it was in 1967, much worse also in manpower, for the Soviet military personnel now in Egypt are many times greater in quantity, and even more so in quality, than what was there in 1967.

It is true that a miracle occurred, and Egypt, for reasons that are not yet understood at all, has not yet signed a piece of paper—a piece of paper whose content includes conditions that no one expects them to fulfill—and consequently, the situation remains in limbo. But as mentioned above, it requires deep reflection whether this strengthens the situation on the eastern bank of the Canal or the situation on the western bank of the Canal.

By nature, I am not a pessimist, and it is understood that my desire is to find encouraging details in the changing situation from year to year. But despite the strong desire, a person must not deceive himself in any matter whatsoever, and all the more so in a serious matter such as this.

To conclude with something good: I have seen a change for the better regarding the internal situation within the state of Egypt and the Arab world, and the relations between one and another. And if this has any connection to the conversation we had during your visit here regarding the aforementioned, then it is a great merit for you in your influence in that direction, and in this, too, you surely know more than I about the great importance of the matter.

I will conclude my letter as I began: may it be the will of Hashem that the content of your next letter will be joyful regarding the matters written above and in general. May this also be included in the blessing of a good and sweet year coming upon us and upon all of Yisrael for the good, according to the traditional custom of the days of the month of Elul, when one wishes another a good inscription and sealing for the new year, as the month of Elul is the appropriate preparation for this.

With respect and blessing, and regards to your colleagues, shlita. I would be grateful if you would convey my wishes for a good and sweet year to them as well.

P.S. It is understood that you have permission to share the content of this letter with whomever you find appropriate, and I will certainly receive your response to the content, and thank you in advance.

I will take the liberty, since you touched upon the question of a partial settlement, to ask if you could perhaps explain a great wonder I have had for about three years: it is known and accepted by all experts without exception that in our era, defense using a method like the Maginot Line and the like—that is, relying on fortifications and the presence of "pinned down and bound" army companies in bunkers, etc.—is not the way at all in our era, the era of jets and paratroopers, etc., especially when the front is several hundred kilometers long (combining the Canal front and the Mediterranean front). Rather, one must view the army's strength in its mobility and the ability to move it from place to place with agility, etc. This applies even when there are several strongholds in the natural terrain, mountains and hills, etc., in the rear of the line, and all the more so when one is in the desert. And even when the line is several kilometers thick, the minimum of a "partial settlement" is certainly more than the thickness of the line. Yet, they invested great wealth and immense energy in this defense line.

Admittedly, there was also a psychological benefit in saving those stationed there from boredom, a very serious problem in such a situation, but it is not plausible to say that this was the deciding factor.

If you are permitted to reveal the reasons and arguments for this, my gratitude is extended in advance if you would write to me about this as well, with the appropriate detail.

## 1022

B"H, 9 Elul, 5731
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed and distinguished individual, who engages in communal needs and accomplishes much, etc.,
R' Moshe 
Shalom u’Bracha!

...Since this touches upon an interpretation of our Sages (which you cited in my name), I am stepping out of my usual bounds (of not responding, or adding precision to what appears in my name in the press—as there is no end to such matters), and I will further explain what appears to me to be the meaning of the statement of our Sages (Eruvin 86a), "Rabbi would honor the wealthy," regarding which many have labored to provide an explanation:

It is **evident** from the discussion there that our Sages intended "wealthy" in its literal sense. The resolution to the wonderment regarding this is also hinted at in the continuation of the discussion there: Precisely because **Rabbi** was himself an exceptionally wealthy man, he knew from his own experience the **multitude** of trials that arise through wealth. Along with this, he believed with perfect faith that Hashem (the Essence of Good) has **no** intention whatsoever to cause a person to stumble, and He only requires of a person according to their capacity. That is to say, the wealthy person he encountered possesses such an immense internal "strength" that he has the capacity to withstand all the aforementioned trials, and, on the contrary, to use his wealth solely so that ["he may abide before Elokim forever"](http://#_ftn_828) (as the conclusion of the discussion there states). A person possessing such a lofty strength is certainly worthy of being honored [and from this **we** must learn regarding a wealthy person in whatever area or sense it may be—regarding his "strength," and consequently, regarding his responsibility as well].

Based on the above, one can add an explanation as to why it was specifically Shlomo who requested (Mishlei 30:8), "Give me neither poverty nor riches,"

For he was tested in both (and in both—to an extreme degree), [and there is no wise man like one who has experience.](http://#_ftn_829)

## 1013

1013

B"H, 9 Elul, 5731

Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished [Moshe] may he live,

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 5 Elul regarding the fact that several times of revelation of the Baal Shem Tov are mentioned [in the sefarim],

There are various levels of revelation, similar to what we find regarding Moshe, who was the shepherd of Yisrael while still in Mitzrayim, and they believed in him (Shemos 4:31). This was subsequently increased at the time of the splitting of the sea (Shemos 14:31), and reached its essence at the time of Matan Torah (see Rambam, Hilchos Yesodei HaTorah, beginning of chapter 8).

I trust that you are keeping up with the three daily study portions—Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya—which are appropriate for every soul.

The *pidyon nefesh* included in your letter will be read at an auspicious time at the tziyun of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

With the blessing of *Kesivah V'chasimah Tovah*.

## 105

B"H, 12 Elul, 5731
Brooklyn, N.Y.

At that time, anyone who wishes to go out to greet him may do so, and he receives them all with a pleasant countenance and shows a smiling face to everyone. And when he proceeds to the city, they follow him, etc. 'Hashem will shine [Ya'ir](#_ftn_836) His countenance upon you,' etc.—that He will illuminate for the person the aspect of His inner will." (Likutei Torah, Parshas **Re'eh**, page **32**).

**M. Schneerson**

## 10th of Cheshvan

[Elul, 5731]

Since during these days, and especially on Rosh Hashanah, we cherish the **body** of the Jewish people—as it is written, "Eat the fat and drink the sweet..." (Nechemiah 8:10; Shulchan Aruch Admur HaZaken 583:4)—it is not appropriate to enter into any of the aforementioned doubts. Rather, he should celebrate the entire month of Tishrei in his place of residence and daven **within the congregation of the Jewish people**—may they live—in the shul, and the shaliach tzibbur will fulfill his obligation as well, acting as his agent.

## 1119

1119

[Elul, 5731]

With blessings for success in your studies and in guiding the students—may they live and be well—at Beis Rivkah (Casablanca), and especially regarding modesty and yiras shamayim in general.

## 1016

[Elul, 5731]
