## 10-Ria

10-Ria

[B"H,](http://www.chabad.org/library/article_cdo/aid/3658250/jewish/Igros-Kodesh-Vol-27.htm#_ftn_848) Days of Selichos, 5731
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the sons and daughters of Israel, wherever they may be,
May Hashem keep them and grant them life,

Peace and Blessing!

In these days, days of preparation for Rosh Hashanah, it is of primary importance to clearly understand the significance of Rosh Hashanah, which is approaching for us and for all of Israel for good and for blessing. We can learn much in this regard from the matters that the Torah has designated to precede Rosh Hashanah, serving as a preparation for it.

For Torah is **Torah Ohr** — its instructions illuminate and make clear the Jewish way of life in all its details.

***

Among the matters that are directly connected to Rosh Hashanah and serve as a preparation for it is the **fixed** custom that before Rosh Hashanah (the Shabbos before Rosh Hashanah), we "read" what the Torah says and points out to every Jew: **Atem Nitzavim** — the parsha of Nitzavim.

The parsha begins with the declaration: **"You are standing firm today, all of you, before Hashem your G-d: your heads... until the water-drawer, to bring you into the covenant of Hashem your G-d..."**

Seemingly, there is a contradiction in this declaration: First, it says **Nitzavim... kulchem** ("all of you" together, without distinction), and immediately afterward, the various types (categories) are listed, each one separately. Furthermore, why does the Torah list the different levels of Jews, from the highest to the lowest, when the word **kulchem** already includes everyone?

But this itself contains a fundamental instruction: that there must be **both** things together: (a) **kulchem** — which means **le'achadim ke'echad**, all as one, and (b) at the same time, every individual has their own specific task and shlichus, each according to their status and situation.

This, however, raises the question: Since a division is necessary, and indeed an extreme one—from "your heads" to "your water-drawer"—how is a unification and oneness achieved, and at the same time, how does it become *kulchem*—as one?

The answer is: **Atem Nitzavim Hayom Kulchem — Lifnei Hashem Elokeichem.** "Nitzavim" is more than "omdim" (standing); it implies a firm stance, with a deep awareness that one is standing before the Ribono shel Olam, who is **Elokeichem**—your strength and your entire essence. In this, all Jews are equal, and this makes them all one—*kulchem ke'echad*.

One can understand this through a simple comparison: When a group of people unite to form a certain society—whether it is a financial enterprise, a scientific one, or another purpose—the members are united for a certain time and for a certain purpose, which requires from each of them a contribution of their money and effort, or their knowledge in science, etc. In all their other attributes, each member is a "world" unto themselves.

However, when the unification of Jews is, as the Torah requires, **lifnei Hashem Elokeichem**, as stated above, and with the purpose of **"to bring you into the covenant and oath that Hashem your G-d is making with you today"**—a covenant that encompasses the **entire** person, with **all** their kochos (the *kulchem* of each individual)—this is an eternal and complete unification of **kulchem ke'echad** (and this *kulchem*—with **Hashem Elokeichem**).

And the Torah explains further: This **kulchem** is divided into **"your heads... until your water-drawer,"** and **each** of them, in their **specific** capacity (and their **special** actions), is brought into the covenant with the Ribono shel Olam. Every individual action of one of the "heads" as a head, or of the "water-drawer" as such—an action according to the instructions of **Hashem Elokeichem** (in His Torah)—is an expression of the **total** covenant of **kulchem** with **Hashem Elokeichem**. Everyone has their special G-dly shlichus according to their status and situation. And in this way—while each one fulfills their shlichus—the unification of Klal Yisrael is fulfilled: *kulchem*—as one.

***

This brings us to a point that must be emphasized once again as a *davar be'ito* (a matter timely for the moment), and that is regarding those who are in the category of **"your heads"** (l'shivteichem)—spiritual leaders in their communities, or influential people in their circles, down to every person as the head of their family.

It is self-evident that the primary duty and task of spiritual leaders, especially during the time of the Yomim Noraim, the days of hisorerus and cheshbon hanefesh, is to strengthen all matters of Torah and mitzvos among those they influence, in actual deed, in daily life. And for those who, for various reasons, are currently distanced from Yiddishkeit—to awaken in them a feeling of teshuvah, to return to their source and begin living as **whole** Jews with a **whole** Yiddishkeit, **a whole** year.

Regrettably, this best opportunity of the year is sometimes lost—through speeches and lectures on world problems and topics which, no matter how important they may be, are completely beyond the control of the speakers or listeners; they cannot do anything to solve them. It is highly regrettable and painful when, instead of utilizing these moments of spiritual Jewish hisorerus to strengthen and encourage Jews that they stand in an eternal, total covenant with Hashem Elokeichem—and that He Himself has given them—each of them individually, from the "heads" to the "water-drawer"—a shlichus, and explaining the duties of every Jew in daily life—the time and attention are given to a global problem, to state politics, or in general to matters that do not belong at all to this place and this time.

***

And if someone were to argue that in the current times and circumstances it is difficult for a Jew to maintain a whole Yiddishkeit without compromise, all year round and with their entire being,

The Torah says: **Atem Nitzavim Hayom**—You are standing firm today, etc.—not in the language of a command, or a promise for the future, but as a **fact**. Jews must know that they stand firm before Hashem, who is their chayos and their strength. It is only necessary that each one bring this out **min ha'he'elem el ha'gilui** (reveal the hidden within them) and **min ha'koach el ha'po'al** (carry out into action what they have in potential).

And with this assurance of "Nitzavim," Jews come—every Jew and all Jews without exception, from the "heads" to the "water-drawer"—to the *hachtarah* (coronation, k'v'yachol) of the Ribono shel Olam during the days of Rosh Hashanah, **"and His kingship they accepted upon themselves with will"**—Jews accept His kingship with their whole heart and with the greatest enthusiasm, and proclaim the Ribono shel Olam as **Melech Yisrael v'go'alo**—the King of the Jews and their Redeemer, and **Melech al kol ha'aretz**—King over the entire world.

***

May it be the will that every Jew—man, woman, and child—should in the coming days be permeated with the spirit of Rosh Hashanah and begin the new year in a manner of **Nitzavim**, firmness and certainty in carrying out the G-dly shlichus that the Ribono shel Olam gives every Jew according to their status and situation,

Carrying it out in the days of Rosh Hashanah, after Rosh Hashanah, and in all the days of the year—*Hayom*, every day,

And the Ribono shel Olam will surely fulfill His promise, as it says immediately afterward: **"In order to establish you today as a people unto Him"**—to elevate you **today** (every day) as His people,

And also according to the interpretation of our Sages, *Hayom*—just as the day which is first dark and then becomes light, so too will it be for every Jew in particular, and for Klal Yisrael, truly bright,

Until the promise will be fulfilled: "He will eventually shine for you an *ohr olam* (eternal light)"—bright always, forever, in the Geulah HaAmitit VeHaShleima through Moshiach Tzidkeinu,

And according to the prayer of Dovid, *ne'im zemirot Yisrael*: "G-d, to save me, Hashem, to my aid, hasten"—speedily in our days, literally.

With the blessing of *Kesivah V'Chasimah Tovah* for a good and sweet year,

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 1012

1012

B”H, Days of Selichos, 5731
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed Rabbi, the esteemed Chassid, G-d-fearing, and involved in communal needs, etc.
[R’](#_ftn_860) Ephraim Eliezer, may he live, HaKohen

Peace and blessing!

Approaching the New Year, which comes upon us and upon all of Israel for good and for blessing, I hereby express my blessing to your honor and to all that is yours: a blessing of *Kesivah V’chasimah Tovah* for a good and sweet year, in both material and spiritual matters.

With blessing.

P.S. Thank you for the letter dated 23 Elul and the enclosure. The *pidyon nefesh* will be read at a time of favor at the holy gravesite, and may you bring good news.

Regarding the promptness of your correspondence—this is in response to the promptness of my confirmation and reply. And primarily—out of respect for you and the holy Torah of the Alter Rebbe (even though it is alluded to [in the references](#_ftn_861) to my letters from the days of Selichos).

Regarding what I asked of you concerning what is written in *Likutei Torah*, beginning of *Parshas Nitzavim*, on the verse “Your heads, etc.”—that these are ten levels, unlike Rashi’s interpretation that “Your heads, your tribes” is one [concept], “Your heads to your tribes.”

And to note that according to Rashi’s interpretation of “and your convert”—it is a **generalization** that includes “from the hewer of your wood to the drawer of your water,” meaning that according to Rashi, **eight** categories are enumerated.

As the Alter Rebbe’s interpretation is **explicit** in *Zohar Chadash* (82a). And see also *Targum Yonasan ben Uziel*.

Rashi’s interpretation is according to the **literal meaning**—which requires study: 1) What is the practical difference between “your tribes” and “every man of Israel”? 2) The change in phrasing: **from** (the hewer of your wood) **to** (the drawer of your water)—and it must be that “your heads to your tribes,” and the hewer and the drawer—are an explanation of “and your convert.”

According to Rashi, the *Yerushalmi* at the end of *Horayos* is understood—which is addressed [in *Torah Or*](#_ftn_863) on the verse.

The interpretation that is copied in your honor’s letter: “Your heads, your tribes, etc.—captains of thousands, captains of hundreds, etc.”—I did not merit to understand, for if so, where are the *Nesi’im* (princes)?

1313

[B"H], Days of Selichos, 5731
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, learned, and accomplished individual, etc.,
R' Shlomo Zalman, may he live.

Shalom u’Bracha!

Approaching the New Year, which is coming upon us and upon all of Israel for good and for blessing, I hereby express my blessing to you and to all that is yours: a blessing of *kesivah v’chasimah tovah* for a good and sweet year, both materially and spiritually.

With respect and blessing.

Thank you for your thoughtfulness in sending me what you have written and published. I trust you will continue this good practice in the future, and I thank you in advance.

I read with **great** astonishment the discussion in the press, etc., regarding how to "resolve" the moon landing in a way that does not undermine faith, Torah, and the contemplation of man’s insignificance, etc.

Naturally, it begins with the "explicit contradiction" of the verse [that states]: "The heavens are the heavens of Hashem, but the earth He has given to the children of man."

Yet, there are many interpretations of "heavens," starting from the interpretation of ["the birds of the heavens"] all the way to "G-d is in the heavens and you are upon the earth" (Koheles 5:1). It is worth noting [the prayer of Shlomo], where both appear together: "When the heavens are shut up and there is no rain... the heavens, the place of Your dwelling," etc.

[In general, from the outset, there is no place for this difficulty, and the matter speaks for itself: "The high mountains are for the wild goats; the rocks are a refuge for the rock badgers" (Tehillim 104:18). **There are many** such verses.]

Regarding the "difficulty" from the blessing of *Kiddush Levanah*, "and I am unable to touch you"—

The refutation is contained within it, and precedes it: "Just as I **dance toward you** and am unable (by means of this dancing) to touch you, so may they be unable," etc.

[Regarding what is brought] in Chazal as an impossible thing, "on the condition that you ascend to the firmament"—even if we were to say that the moon landing falls under this category, since [it is said], "And G-d set them in the firmament of the heavens" (though this itself requires further study)—it would have been more appropriate to raise the difficulty from **many other** verses. (For example, Iyov 38:16-17. And consider the "depths of the sea" or the "rivers of Egypt"—these are diverted into channels through human action, etc., etc.)

Regarding the insignificance of man and the like—

I am extremely surprised that not one of those offering resolutions (whose words I have seen in print, or in writing and speech) addressed the fact that as a scientific innovation and an addition to the "scientific understanding of creation," the moon landing (which did not trigger **any** scientific revolution **at all**, nor even a **surprising** innovation) cannot be compared to the penetration into the atom, which led to the undermining and **negation** of several **foundations** of science—and which has implications regarding the concepts of free choice, miracle, and nature, etc.

And similarly for **many other** "innovations" that preceded it.

Furthermore, and most importantly, even in this regard, it would have been more appropriate to say that even concerning the Torah itself and its laws, Hashem said, "My children have defeated Me," and not only that, but He smiled when He said it (*Bava Metzia* 59b).

And regarding all such matters, the *Moreh Nevuchim* states in his *Yad HaChazakah*, at the beginning of *Hilchos Avodah Zarah*: In the days of Enosh, mankind erred greatly, and the counsel of the wise men of that generation became foolish... "G-d created these stars," etc., and "gave them honor," etc. And as time passed, the glorious and awesome Name was forgotten, etc. And see there at the beginning of chapter 2: "And not one of all the created beings among them, even though the worshiper knows that Hashem is G-d," etc. And they conclude with good.

## 10216

10216

[B"H], Days of Selichos, 5731
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed and G-d-fearing, who engages in communal needs,
Rabbi Yaakov Emanuel 
Shalom u’Bracha!

... Regarding your inquiry concerning the Tzimtzum—I have already responded to this to many others, and surely it has reached you as well. The point is: *koach* (potential) and *po'al* (actual), *pnim* (internal) and *chitzon* (external)—are not identical at all.

The notion that Tzimtzum is literal—because He is **all-powerful**—does not in any way contradict the command to "**know** the G-d of your father..." and the *avodah* of *Chabad*. Just as there is no contradiction from the concept of *briah* (creation) *me'ayin l'yesh* (ex nihilo), which is also constant and beyond our understanding, etc. This is similar to what is explained in *Iggeres HaKodesh*, end of Chapter 4: that the intellect cannot grasp the essence of *Tzimtzum*, just as it cannot grasp the essence of *briah*, etc.

## 10:233

[B"H](#_ftn_899), [Between Rosh Hashanah and Yom Kippur](#_edn_172], 5732
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the sons and daughters of Israel, wherever they may be,
May Hashem grant them life,

Peace and blessing!

Coming from the days of Rosh Hashanah, when all Jews as one accepted upon themselves the Kingdom of the Holy One, blessed be He, willingly and in an open manner in their daily lives, in accordance with the request, "**Reveal** the glory of Your kingdom upon us"—

Which, as written in the [previous](#_edn_173) letter, involves both things: (a) **"You are standing today, all of you"**—that **all** Jews stand firm and [together](#_edn_174) on the day of Rosh Hashanah, *kulchem ke'echad* (all of you as one), and simultaneously (b) in a differentiation from "your heads" to "your water-drawers," and as explained in the previous letter in detail, that both things are connected and dependent upon one another, which then constitutes a complete *kumah* (stature) that contains all parts in perfection, from the "head" to the "heel"—

I wish to dwell here on another point that the [Alter](#_edn_175) Rebbe brings out while discussing the aforementioned matter. This is that in certain respects, the "heel" plays the role of a "head," and the head follows it—as one sees this also in the physical realm, that although the head directs the entire body, the feet and the heels have a quality that they cause the entire body, together with the head, to [go](#_edn_176) from one place to another.

One must understand how this can also be in the *nimshal* (in spirituality), that the "water-drawer" can rise to the level of a "head" and become a model for the "heads," so that they, too, are influenced by the "water-drawer." In spirituality, "your heads" refers to intellect, understanding, and depth, while "your water-drawers" refers to those whose approach to spirituality (the performance of mitzvos) is often no more than mechanical, as in the analogy of a "water-drawer," which does not require deep contemplation or special understanding, etc., but rather doing the thing with faith. How, then, is it possible that the "water-drawer" could actually be the "head," and the "heads" should follow him?

Furthermore: in the category of "your water-drawers," in this last type of Jew—there are also differences, to the point that it includes even those who, like a water-carrier in the literal sense—he was born with the simplest faculties, without any aptitude for intellectual pursuits, and grew up in poverty; having no possibility to learn, he became a "water-drawer."

However, since his absolute ignorance and simplicity is **entirely** [not](#_edn_177) his fault—*anus hu* (he is coerced/compelled)—he, too, is included and unified with *kulchem* (all of you).

But how can even this type rise to the level of a "head" as mentioned above?

***

This leads to another question: Since the Almighty Himself has indicated and demanded of every Jew how he should conduct himself in daily life, how is it possible at all that there should be a situation where a Jew does not have the possibility to conduct himself in all details according to the will of the Almighty—[the](#_edn_178) Master of the entire world? And yet, as we know and see, there is such a situation, where Jews, even with the best of intentions, and even with *mesiras nefesh*, are truly not in a position to fulfill the will of Hashem in all details, due to external circumstances over which they have no control. And as the analogy goes, *mesiras nefesh* helps one jump down from a roof, from above to below, but it does not help one jump up from the ground onto the roof.

***

[The](#_ftn_905) answer to the above-mentioned questions—in short, at any rate:

It is true indeed that **the deed is essential**—the main thing is the action **in practice**—but on the other hand, **feeling** and **kavanah** are also of the highest importance. So, when there is sometimes a situation where it is impossible for a Jew, even with *mesiras nefesh*, to fulfill a directive of the Almighty in actual deed, it brings out in that Jew a pain and sorrow as to why he cannot fulfill the designated mitzvah—a true and deep sorrow that permeates the person through and through, until it touches his [very](#_edn_179) soul. And this brings him to a deep connection with the Almighty and with Torah and mitzvos and *Yiddishkeit* in general, which, without this painful experience, he would not have reached. In such a case, not only does he not receive any punishment, Heaven forbid, for not fulfilling the mitzvah **in practice**—for he is *anus*—but on the contrary, he receives a reward for the fact that [he](#_edn_180) truly wanted to fulfill the mitzvah. And what is even more important: through this deep experience, his soul-life acquires, [from](#_edn_181) now on, a [depth](#_edn_182) and perfection that (it may be) he could not have reached otherwise.

Furthermore: also in regard to actual deed, one sees that when the Almighty subsequently helps and takes him out of that situation and places him in a lifestyle where he can fulfill also the mitzvah, or mitzvos, that he could not fulfill in the previous situation, he now fulfills the mitzvah with a depth, brightness, and heartiness that he did not have until then.

Thus, the "water-drawer" becomes a "head" in the performance of mitzvos in the most perfect way, with his whole heart and feeling, and those who have not gone through the refining process of the ["iron furnace"](#_ftn_908) can learn from him, be inspired, and follow him.

***

In this, however, a very important point must be cautioned:

The [yetzer hara](#_ftn_909) is a master of his craft, a great specialist, especially since he mixes in the greatest type of bribe—**self-love**. And one of his methods is to persuade a person not to do a mitzvah with the excuse that he is in this an "anus," and he finds various explanations and "proofs" for this, and does not let up, and makes a commotion about it without ceasing.

Since ["a person is close to himself"](#_ftn_910) and it is very difficult for him to be objective in a matter that concerns him personally, he must know that the fact that it seems to him that he is an *anus* is not yet any proof that it is truly so. Therefore, in order to clarify the situation, he must turn to someone who is not biased in this, also not biased by wanting to find favor in the eyes of another, but specifically to someone who stands entirely in the perspective of the Torah of **truth**, where truth means—without compromises. Only he can illuminate the situation for him and clarify whether this is truly a case of *ones* (compulsion), or—the imaginings of that [old and foolish one, the yetzer hara](#_edn_183).

***

May the Almighty help that, standing in these days when **teshuvah is most effective and is accepted immediately**—a very favorable time for *teshuvah*, which is accepted at once—one should utilize the time as the Almighty [requests](#_edn_185) and instructs Jews: **"Seek Hashem when He is found, call to Him when He is near"**; and that the matter of *teshuvah*—the returning of each and every one to his true "self," which every Jew, man and woman, is [literally](#_edn_187) a *chelek Elokah mima'al* (a part of G-d from above)—should express itself in all details of daily life, in thought, speech, and action, in the most perfect measure, as written above.

And may the Almighty give, and He will give, to each and every one the fullest possibility that in a healthy and joyful manner one should learn Torah and fulfill the mitzvos—**as the mitzvah of Your will**—in the full sense.

With blessings to each and every one within the entirety of the Jewish people for a *chasimah v'gmar chasimah tovah* for a good and sweet year, in both material and spiritual matters together.

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 1024

[B"H], Between Rosh Hashanah and Yom Kippur, 5732

Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed and distinguished, who engages in communal needs,
R' Shmuel Amsalem, may he live
Barcelona

Shalom u’Bracha!

It was a pleasure to receive your letter with your New Year’s greetings. [And whoever blesses is blessed] from the Source of all blessings, Hashem, may He be blessed and exalted, [from His] full, open, holy, and expansive hand.

I was pleased to read in your letter about the activities of spreading Yiddishkeit and the wellsprings in your community. May it be His will that the [statement of our Sages], of blessed memory, "He who has one hundred wants two hundred," etc., be fulfilled in you and in all the members of the community. That is to say, the success and achievements thus far should stimulate and increase the desire and will to [ascend in holiness] and to go [from strength] to strength, with the power of Torah.

Especially since in the country of Spain, there is a special imperative to revive and disseminate matters of Torah and Yiddishkeit, for it was there that Jews sacrificed their lives for them. How much more so now, when one can observe and fulfill them with abundance, which should certainly be done with joy and a glad heart.

Special thanks for your letter regarding the visit of the esteemed Rabbis, the shluchim, and double thanks for taking it upon yourself to distribute the booklets and printed materials that have been published. You will surely do everything in your power to ensure that the booklets achieve their effect in actual practice, for [the deed] is the essential thing.

This is particularly fitting given your note that your birthday falls on the [Holy Day]—to enter the new year with firm resolutions to spread the Torah of Hashem, the Torah of life, and His mitzvos, [of which it is said] "and he shall live by them," wherever one’s reach extends, and all the more so in one’s immediate surroundings.

And when one provides a living example and speaks [words] that come from the heart, it is certain that they will enter the heart and achieve their effect.

Enclosed is a copy of a general letter, in which you will surely find interest and benefit.

With the blessing of a *Chasimah v'Gmar Chasimah Tovah* and for good tidings,

**M. Schneerson**

The secretariat does not write in French, and therefore this was written in Lashon HaKodesh. However, you may continue to write in French in the future, provided you let us know in which language it is more convenient for you to receive the response: Lashon HaKodesh, Yiddish, or English.

## 1015

This is especially true when the subject concerns the sons and daughters of Yisrael, a holy nation dwelling and living in the Holy Land. Words that come from the heart enter the heart and accomplish their effect, and there is nothing that can stand before the will.

Regarding your question concerning a shidduch for your sister, may she live—whether the father must make a special effort in this, etc.—it is known what our Sages, of blessed memory, said regarding the great importance of the commandment, based on the instruction of the verse, "I gave my daughter to this man," and the great level of hishtadlus that must be invested in this, to the point that they said that it is regarding this that it is said, "To love Hashem your G-d and to cleave to Him," and it is a positive commandment from the Torah.

Regarding your notification of the condition of your wife, may she live, may the Holy One, blessed be He, fulfill the days of her pregnancy properly and with ease, for the birth of a healthy child in a good and auspicious hour.

[Secretariat letter regarding the three previous letters]

B"H, 6 Marcheshvan, 5732

Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the great Gaon and Chossid, who engages in communal needs, etc.,

[Rabbi Shlomo Yosef](#_ftn_960), may he live,

Peace and blessing!

Minutes from the telephone conversation in which Rabbi Zevin, may he live, asked several questions regarding the management of Kollel Chabad and the administration of the institutions, Talmud Torah, Beis Chana, etc., in continuation of the letters received from the Rebbe shlita on the aforementioned matter, and regarding the fact that a meeting of the committees is now taking place at the home of Rabbi Zevin, may he live.

1) The members of the committee declare that they stand ready to fulfill the instruction of the Rebbe shlita to manage the aforementioned institutions, but due to their heavy burdens, they see a necessity to hire a technical person to carry out their decisions, and they ask if they are permitted to do so, and who should decide on the appointment.

The response: They are indeed permitted to employ a technical person for the above, and to propose to the Rebbe shlita the candidates they find suitable. However, it is understood that this refers only to a strictly technical worker; the responsible "owner" — and not merely an advisor — is the committee, and they are only using the appointed official as a technical executor.

2) Their question as to whether one technical person is sufficient for the aforementioned work, or if two are needed — one for the Kollel and one for the institutions.

The response: A specific worker is needed for the Kollel and a specific worker for the educational institutions. However, this does not necessarily mean two "entities"; one person may be appointed whose work is specifically dedicated to both of these matters as distinct areas.

Since the official must be someone who is familiar with the affairs of Jerusalem, may it be built, one should not transfer to this position someone who is already occupied with other work in any of the institutions outside of Jerusalem, may it be built.

3) I stated that without delay they should hire an official accountant to organize the accounts, both of the Kollel and of the institutions, and to send a copy of this here, as well as to send here a list of those receiving support from the Kollel.

With a blessing for all the best,

Rabbi Ch. M. A. Hodakov

## 1095

B"H, Rosh Chodesh Cheshvan, 5732
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the G-d-fearing, distinguished, and upright, engaged in communal needs,

The [teaching of our Sages, of blessed memory,](#_ftn_971) [on the verse](#_ftn_972) "This is my G-d and I will beautify Him — beautify yourself before Him," etc., is well known. This is especially relevant to seforim on the inner dimensions of Torah in our generation, the generation of the footsteps of Moshiach. Also well known are the words of Eliyahu and the Rashbi: "**They will be sustained** through this composition of yours when it is **revealed** below at the end of days, and through it [you shall proclaim](#_ftn_974) **liberty** throughout the land," as is also brought in the introduction of the author of **Be'er Lechai Ro'i**. [And it is explained in many places](#_ftn_975) the precision of this language: "**They will be sustained**," analogous to physical sustenance, meaning comprehension and understanding, to the point that it becomes evident in one's daily life and conduct. And surely for one such as yourself, there is no need to elaborate on this.

May it be the will of Hashem that "knowledge, wisdom, and truth will increase," and "Israel will be great sages and know the hidden matters, etc. [as it is written](#_ftn_976): 'For the earth shall be full of the knowledge of Hashem as the waters cover the sea'" (Rambam, Hilchos Teshuvah, end of chapter 9, and Hilchos Melachim at the end), and may we merit very soon the liberty throughout the land, in the true and complete Geulah through Moshiach Tzidkeinu.

With respect and blessing.

## 10,248

10,248

B”H, 3 Menachem Av, 5732

## 10,249

[5 Cheshvan, 5732]

Regarding your question concerning the order of the chapters in Iggeres HaTeshuvah, where Chapter 3—which discusses specific details—precedes Chapter 4, the content of which is the general concept of Teshuvah:

The reason is that in Chapter 4, the **expansion** of the explanation begins, following the conclusion of the matter in brief, etc.

Regarding the order of his study, etc.—he should speak with the Mashpia, may he live, etc.

## 10,151

[9 Cheshvan, 5732]

There is a strong basis and logic to say that the fact that her mother, may she live, is caring (to the extent of her ability) for her son (her brother), may he live, gives her strength and reinforcement. And if they were to be separated, it is difficult to imagine the consequences.

Therefore, make it easier for her mother as much as possible, but do not separate them, etc.

## 10252

B"H, 13 Cheshvan, 5732
Brooklyn, N.Y.

[Mrs. Shifra Yehudis, may she live]

Greetings and blessings!

I acknowledge receipt of your letter. May Hashem fulfill your heart’s desires for the good in all the matters you write about, both personal and general. As we have discussed many times, may you raise all your children to Torah, to the chuppah, and to good deeds, with Chassidic *nachas*. Furthermore—and this is also essential—may you soon be settled with a good *shidduch*. We have spoken about this at length many times as well. Above all, this is the instruction of our Torah, which is called the Torah of Truth and the Torah of Life—a true instruction for daily life.

Naturally, I am very surprised that you ask for my reaction regarding your activities on behalf of the widows and orphans, may they live, in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established. In our conversation here, I emphasized the great importance of this activity in general, and especially when it is performed by someone in a similar situation, etc., and particularly when the actions are permeated with Chassidic light and vitality.

The words of our Sages, of blessed memory, are well known regarding the immense value of such actions, as they are included in every act that brings encouragement to widows and orphans. We are commanded to emulate the "Father of orphans and Judge of widows," the King of kings, the Holy One, blessed be He. This, too, adds assurance that Hashem will grant you success in your activities and in being settled with a good marriage, with true Chassidic *nachas* from your children, may they live, as mentioned above.

Regarding your comment and question in your letter as to the explanation for the suffering and pain, etc., of the aforementioned: in truth, this is part of the general question of what is the explanation and reason for the existence of pain and suffering in the world at all. After all, the Creator and Guide of the world is the essence of good, and [in the well-known phrasing], it is the nature of the Good to do good.

Many attempts have been made to resolve this question. Among the most fundamental and understandable is the language of the verse: "Can you find the depths of G-d?" etc., in the Book of Iyov. This book is one of our Holy Scriptures, and its entire point is the question mentioned, along with its answer and resolution. Therefore, it is somewhat surprising that people ask these questions as if they had never been asked or discussed before.

Furthermore, it should be added that faith in Hashem is surely in the nature of every Jewish man and woman, down to the youngest child. This necessitates that there must be a simple explanation that is acceptable to the minds of children as well. Indeed, such an explanation exists. It is best understood through a well-known analogy: Imagine a person who has no knowledge whatsoever of the science of medicine or medical treatment. He enters the surgical ward of a hospital and sees a group of people dressed in white, with masks on their faces. They hold all sorts of knives, scalpels, and various instruments. They are standing around a person lying on a table, whose hands and feet are tied to it with straps. The people in the uniforms are anesthetizing the person and operating on him, and his blood is flowing, etc. Surely, this person who happened upon the scene would be shocked by what his eyes see, and he would alert the entire neighborhood to such a horrific act, etc. It is no wonder, for he has no concept of what surgery is. Even though it causes temporary minor harm, it saves the person's life and brings him to a healthy, whole life for decades to come. It is also not graspable to his mind how it is possible that by wounding the body—with the body bleeding and then suffering pain, and even having to be anesthetized during the procedure—the body will be healed, become healthy, and have its life extended. Seemingly, there is no room to say that specifically through this, the body will be healed and become healthy and live longer.

[The analogy] to our situation is understood. A human being only knows what occurs before his eyes during his life on earth—seventy years, or eighty years if by reason of strength, and his days may be one hundred and twenty years. He has no concept of what was before this or what will be after this. In comparison to the time after the "surgery" (the suffering and pain), this life is but a small moment. How, then, could his calculation be a calculation of justice?

If you were to say that this is an explanation not only for children but is true in its own right—there is much more to elaborate on this, but this is not the place.

In this context, it is appropriate to quote [the words of our Rabbeinu HaZaken] (even though he wrote them regarding a different question). These are his holy words: "It is a simple faith among the general Jewish people, handed down to them from their holy ancestors who walked in innocence with Hashem, without investigating with human intellect the matter of G-dliness, which is infinitely beyond the intellect."

With blessings for great success in your most lofty activities, in accordance with the attribute of the Holy One, blessed be He, of whom it is said that He encourages the [orphan] and widow, and [makes the heart] of widows sing, and in all your personal and general matters as written above, and for good tidings.

P.S. You are surely planning extensive activity in connection with the upcoming days of Chanukah. May it be G-d's will that it be with great success.

## 1255

 B"H, 13 Cheshvan, 5732
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and learned man, who occupies himself with communal needs, whose work is the work of Heaven, a man of energy and many accomplishments, R' Chaim Yaakov, may he live and be well,

Shalom u’Bracha!

 We begin with a blessing, especially in connection with the visit of several students of the Beis Rivkah Seminary in France—who came here for the festival of Sukkos and caused much nachas through their conduct, etc.

May it be the will of Hashem that each and every one of them, along with all the students of the Seminary and Beis Rivkah in general, go from strength to strength in their studies and in their conduct, as is fitting for daughters of Yisroel. Each of them is called a daughter of Sarah, Rivkah, Rachel, and Leah, in accordance with the hope of our Rebbes, the founders of these educational institutions and similar ones—for this hope itself provides the strength. Fortunate is the portion of each and every one who acts in this, occupies themselves with this, and strives for this, and the merit of the many assists them.

Continuing from what was written above regarding the conduct of the daughters of Yisroel, and particularly in our generation, the "orphaned generation," and in connection with the question that many have asked me regarding the length of dresses: my opinion on this is well known, that the standard which applies to **every** soul (may the daughters of Yisroel live) and in **every** place is that the knees must be covered, even while sitting.

What is written above is, as stated, a standard that is **at the very least**.

However, because there are places where the above is not sufficient—for in matters of tznius and the like, in addition to the boundaries of tznius which may not be changed in any place, there are also details that depend on the custom of the place—these are matters in which one should be stringent, but certainly not lenient. Therefore, it is for every Rav and teacher in that place to clarify and instruct regarding the practical application.

Furthermore, and this is also essential: that which one must be stringent about in accordance with the conditions of the place does not necessarily mean that it is merely a stringency (*chumra*). It is possible that due to the conditions of the place, the matter is forbidden by Torah law. In many areas, we find similar instances.

It is my prayer that the entire administrative staff, the teachers, may they live and be well, will see much nachas from their labor in Beis Rivkah, in all its departments and among all its students—true nachas, Torah-true nachas, permeated with the light and vitality of Chassidus, and in a manner that is "increasing and adding light." The mission of Beis Rivkah is to raise daughters in Yisroel who will, in time, each and every one of them be an *akeres habayis*, a faithful home in Yisroel, in accordance with what is said: "The wisdom of women builds her house."

With respect and blessing for good tidings in all the above,

**M. Schneerson**

May it be the will [of Hashem] that there be fulfilled at this gathering the words of our Sages, "Pleasant for them and pleasant for the world," as explained in the maamar "Hechalutzu" (implying all of you [edn_189]),

that you should not part, Heaven forbid. On the contrary, the farbrengen should **unite** all the participants—those who have recently made aliyah, those who arrived previously, and those born in the Holy Land—all of you as one, for an ascent in our Torah, the Torah of truth, and in its mitzvos in daily life.

May those who have arrived from there ignite all our people with their mesiras nefesh for authentic Yiddishkeit, and may they continue, with abundance, to be a living example of Jews who rejoice throughout the entire year in the Torah of Moshe, and the Torah rejoices in them throughout the entire year,

educating their sons and daughters in this path,

without taking into account at all any confusions or difficulties,

and paving the way so that those who follow them will do likewise, as promised by Hashem, "A great congregation shall return here," all of this with Chassidic vitality and light.

With respect and blessing for appropriate resolutions regarding all of the above, and for their successful implementation.

**Menachem Schneerson**

With respect,

Secretary

## 10258

10258

[B"H](#_ftn_1018), 20 Marcheshvan, 5732

Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the congregation of Yeshurun, lovers and supporters of Torah and mitzvos,

May Hashem grant them life,

Peace and blessing!

In connection with the upcoming annual celebration of the Merkaz Yeshivos Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch, and on this day—20 Marcheshvan—the birthday of the Rebbe Rashab, the founder of Tomchei Temimim in Lubavitch,

I come with a reminder and a request to the lovers and supporters of Torah, and to Anash in particular, to place yourselves in the front ranks of the activists and supporters of the Yeshiva, with the goal of ensuring, with the help of Hashem, the success of this undertaking.

A businessman understands a good deal and knows how to appreciate a good "investment." The best investment is not only when the capital brings in the highest dividends, but when the dividends themselves serve as further capital for subsequent dividends, and so on, without end.

Such an "investment" is **chinuch al taharas hakodesh**, where the **students** become **educators** and the **recipients** become **influencers**, creating an endless continuity of fruit and fruit-of-the-fruit in an ever-growing measure.

This was, after all, the intention of the founder of Tomchei Temimim over [71](#_ftn_1019) years ago, when he placed the emphasis on the students—the *Temimim*—being **neros leha'ir**—lights that shine and illuminate their surroundings—with the light of Torah and mitzvos in daily life, among all strata and circles. And as for the extent to which this intention has been and is being realized in practice, and the, B"H, very great success in this—that is well-known and famous. It is simply impossible to estimate the great and widespread activity of spreading Torah and Yiddishkeit by the *talmidim Temimim*, not only here in this country but also in various parts of the world.

Therefore, I hope and am certain that everyone will want to have the largest possible share in this "investment" and will do their utmost to ensure the success of this annual undertaking, to provide the full financial and moral support that the Yeshiva requires to continue its holy work, and in a manner of *mosif v'holech mosif v'or* (increasing and continuing, increasing and shining).

By doing so, one also creates broad channels and vessels to receive the Ribono shel Olam’s blessings, for oneself and one’s family, in everything one needs, both in material and spiritual matters alike.

With respect and blessing for success and good tidings,

**M. Schneerson**

## 1066

Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, distinguished, and noble individual, who seeks the good of his people and possesses lofty character traits, a scion of noble ancestors, R' Schneur [Zalman](#_ftn_1025) Shlita,

May it be the will of Hashem that your prayers be accepted amidst the prayers of all our brethren, the Children of Israel. This is especially significant as it is a prayer offered within Jerusalem, the Holy City—and in the language of Rabbeinu HaZaken in his Shulchan Aruch, that in prayer, one should turn his face toward Jerusalem, [as it is said](#_ftn_1028), "And they shall pray to Hashem toward the city which You have chosen" (Orach Chaim, beginning of Siman 94)—and may they be fulfilled completely, in a revealed and manifest good.

The matter [is written](#_ftn_1029) in the chapter of Tehillim [that corresponds](#_ftn_1030) to your years, for long days and good years, [as is known](#_ftn_1031) our custom in this, according to the Alter Rebbe, who received from "his teacher, in the name of his teacher, the Baal Shem Tov," to recite the chapter of Tehillim "corresponding to the number of his years": "[Elokim](#_ftn_1032) stands in the congregation of G-d." [Our Sages](#_ftn_1033) of blessed memory explained this to mean that the Holy One, Blessed be He, is present in synagogues. [It is known](#_ftn_1034) the precision in the word **"stands" (natzav)**, which implies a firm stance, one that withstands all trials, [and in the well-known](#_ftn_1035) expression, "standing firm and enduring."

With appreciation, honor, and heartfelt wishes for long days and good, active years—in health, joy, and goodness of heart,

**M. Schneerson**

## 10272

B"H, 27 Cheshvan, 5732
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Mr. Yaakov Rosenthal
8 Amatzia St., Jerusalem

Peace and Blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from the 24th of Tishrei and the one preceding it, along with the enclosures.

Many thanks for your attention to this, for it is superfluous to emphasize how interested I am in information such as that contained in your letter and the enclosures. It is understood that I would be interested in receiving what you call the "protocol" of the well-known visit.

Regarding the visit itself, the rule is well known that before an event takes place, there may be differences of opinion as to whether it is desirable and good or the opposite, etc. But after the fact, in addition to the instruction that "this, too, is for the good," or at the very least that "everything the Merciful One does, He does for the good," these instructions must be expressed first and foremost by making every possible effort to utilize the event—in this case, the visit—for the greatest possible good.

May it be His will, since you wrote at the conclusion of the month of Tishrei—the conclusion of whose special Yomim Tovim is Simchas Torah, and the purpose of the holidays and festivals is to carry their influence throughout the entire year—that this should be a year of "Simchas Torah" in both senses: Jews rejoicing in the Torah, and the Torah itself rejoicing with the Jews who observe Torah and mitzvos. For every Jew, being one of the members of "a wise and understanding people," will not contradict himself by dancing with the Torah on Simchas Torah, and then tomorrow or later doing something against the Torah, contrary to halacha, etc. And surely, for someone like yourself, there is no need for elaboration.

With respect and blessing.

## 10263

10263

B.H., 27 Cheshvan, 5732

Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Mr. S.M. Tamir (Katznelson)
P.O. Box 1889, Tel Aviv

Greetings and blessings,

I have just received the book *Perfidy* by Ben Hecht. Since I see that the dedication was written in 5730, and it is quite extraordinary, I wish to acknowledge receipt immediately, in accordance with the injunction, "[And you shall be] clean from Hashem and from Israel".

I express my heartfelt thanks to you for your thoughtfulness in sending me the book, through which one can gain a close acquaintance with the author and the main characters of the narrative, in addition to our personal meeting at the farbrengen.

Surely, for someone like yourself, it is unnecessary to emphasize that the sorrow and pain are still great. It is not as the mistaken ones think—that since Hitler, may his name be erased, died many years ago, all the phenomena associated with him have also ceased and passed. This is not the case; for to our great regret, he left behind students who follow in his footsteps, and they are alive and active even in our days, in various strange areas, with all the sorrowful and painful phenomena connected to this, including grievous harm ("crippling") to the bodies and souls of many of our brethren, the Children of Israel.

I feel it is my duty not to miss this opportunity regarding the following matter, as in my opinion it is a vital issue that concerns the existence of our people, the Children of Israel, wherever they may be—in the Holy Land and in the Diaspora. I refer to the terrible matter of the "Who is a Jew" legislation.

It is surprising that I have not yet heard your protest on this matter—a protest in your sharp, emphatic style that hits the mark. For I have no doubt at all regarding your position on this issue. As I have said on another occasion, this unfortunate law is one of the rare laws where one must search to see who benefits from it (except perhaps for the creators of the law, who can say "we have been victorious"), and from day to day, those harmed by it increase. There has never been such a thing: that a government should declare openly before all that a document issued by it is not to be taken into account at all, and that what is written therein—Jew or Christian, etc.—is only for the population registry, and beyond that, it is nothing, even though the Ministry of the Interior issues this document in the name and capacity of a government representative. I heard just these days that a famous Zionist leader in a large city complained to a government representative, saying, "This is the greatest slap in the face I have received" from the Israeli government following the aforementioned law, because he is forced to tell those who come to him that they should not take an Israeli passport or what is written in it into account at all, for every man does what is right in his own eyes to instruct the clerk how to register him or her, and the clerk, as a government representative, writes and signs it.

I am not here to recount the entire saga of the damage caused by this law from a religious, national, or security perspective, etc., which are surely known to you, and have already been written and spoken about extensively. Apparently, just as there is a "miracle" for the good, so too, to one's great astonishment, there is a "miracle" in the opposite sense—the very fact that this law was passed, and that it is still in force even though nearly two years have passed, the damage is growing, and the law remains in place.

It is understood that my intention here is not to complain and cry over the past, but rather in the hope that you will utilize the talents with which you have been gifted and the influence you possess in circles and wherever your hand can reach, to respond to this strange law, which sabotages, harms, and alienates itself from the very existence of our people, the Children of Israel, wherever they may be.

It is said in the name of Hitler, may his name be erased, that he was accustomed to say that a small lie eventually disappears, but a large and absolute lie can have a lifespan of years and generations. There is no need to dwell at length on something that is contrary to the faith of Israel in the Creator of the world and its Guide, and furthermore, contrary to the faith in the people of Israel, who will eventually shake off the shackles of partisanship and utilize the healthy sense with which the "wise and discerning people" have been gifted, and will abolish this law from its foundation, along with several laws similar to it.

I would be happy to hear from you regarding all that has been said above, and I thank you in advance.

With respect and blessing,

## 1070

[B"H], Rosh Chodesh Kislev, 5732
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the congregants, and first and foremost, the Gabbaim of the Chabad-Lubavitch Ahavas Yisroel Synagogue, Bnei Brak,
May Hashem grant them life,

Peace and blessing!

With pleasure and joy, I received the news regarding the celebration of the completion of the writing of a Sefer Torah and its installation into the shul.

[It is fitting] that a meritorious event be scheduled for a meritorious day; the celebration will take place on the 10th of Kislev, the Yom HaGeulah of the Mitteler Rebbe, with a procession and great joy, as is befitting the magnitude and importance of the occasion.

It is worth noting and illuminating that [it is known] that the Geulah of the Mitteler Rebbe followed the path of the Geulah of the Alter Rebbe, who filled his place. They received the news of his Geulah when they recited the [verse] in Tehillim: "He has redeemed my soul in peace from the battle against me, for there were many with me," as recounted in the [Iggeres HaKodesh] of the Alter Rebbe.

However, [regarding] the Mitteler Rebbe, this occurred during his monthly Tehillim cycle, while regarding the Alter Rebbe, it included the addition of the weekly cycle [on the third day, on which "it was good" was doubled], as the calendar alignment then was the same as it is this year.

The interpretation of our Sages, of blessed memory, regarding the verse is well known: "What is the meaning of 'He has redeemed my soul in peace'? The Holy One, blessed be He, says: Whoever occupies himself with Torah and acts of loving-kindness and prays with the congregation, I account it to him as if he had redeemed Me and My children from among the nations of the world" (Berachos, beginning of the eighth page).

Indeed, the installation of a Sefer Torah into a synagogue encompasses these three matters: praying with the congregation, which is the essence of a synagogue; acts of loving-kindness, as the Sefer Torah is made for many to read from—a Sefer Torah of the many; and occupying oneself with Torah, with even greater intensity and strength, [as is known] that through the reading of the Torah, even one who does not understand what is being said fulfills the mitzvah of Talmud Torah.

May it be the will of Hashem that very soon the conclusion of the aforementioned interpretation of our Sages will be fulfilled, and in actual practice—"He has redeemed Me and My children from among the nations of the world."

With respect and blessing for good tidings regarding the above, and with the blessing of the Chag HaGeulah,

**M. Schneerson**

## 1097

1097

[7 Kislev, 5732]

Agudas HaRabbonim has **just now** decided—and has **publicized** this decision—to convene a preliminary assembly here (to be followed by an assembly in Europe with the participation of many countries) for the purpose of repealing the law, etc.

In my opinion, there must be **great** effort to ensure that this assembly succeeds **to the utmost** (since it is the **first** one being conducted by an organization of Rabbis, etc.), and in particular, the members of Agudas HaRabbonim must exert themselves in this, and especially you, in your capacity as a member, etc. Therefore, in my opinion, this is not the appropriate time for the proposal you wrote—which would weaken the aforementioned, etc.

***

There is no concern **at all** regarding the Agudas HaRabbonim assembly (which is a one-time event)—and this is not the first time that such a thing has been done.

If other rabbinical organizations gather with the goal of repealing the law, may a blessing come upon them, but one must not delay the aforementioned assembly for this purpose (in order for them to join together—for in the current situation, their joining is **not at all** practical, as is known to all. And a word to the wise is sufficient).

Any proposal to cancel, Heaven forbid, the Agudas HaRabbonim assembly, or even to postpone it, means, in effect: assisting in the **non**-repeal of the "Who is a Jew" issue.

The resignation of the ministers from the government—since "there is no agent for a sinful act"—is an obligation according to the Torah. And after the Rabbis (whom they themselves accepted as Rabbis, and with full authority—**even now**) have issued a *psak din*, and they are not fulfilling that *psak din*, this adds the element of *chillul Hashem*, and in public, **etc.**

Following the above—even if it were clear that "he will not accept from him, one must still protest," **etc.** Especially since silence is interpreted—**and publicly so**—as agreement and an expression of *yasher koach* for not resigning.

Regarding the resignation of the Rabbis in Eretz Yisroel—aside from the **main point**: according to the *Shulchan Aruch*, I do not see a basis to demand this, because they were **explicitly** told (and such is the situation **in practice**—**for the time being**) that the registration does not obligate them **at all**. They ruled **clearly that it is forbidden** for the official to register and for the minister to remain in the government, and they added that "since Israel departed from Judah, etc."—and all of this was accepted **unanimously** at their assembly. And after all this—the government is still paying their salaries for the time being.

Furthermore, and this is also essential: those sitting in the government are **waiting** for them to resign so that they can immediately install others in their place ("temporarily"—and afterwards, etc.) who will rule that the law is a religious achievement.

In general, it is not relevant in practice, because Rabbi . . . *shlita* (and others like him) will not resign.

This is not the appropriate time for a letter demanding that Eretz Yisroel and all its laws be according to the laws of the Torah—and **consequently** that the Law of Return must be amended, etc.—because this phrasing destroys all chances for amending the law.

For they will immediately "pounce on the opportunity," claiming that the demand for the amendment implies, intends, and in its entirety means that this must be a **Medinas HaHalacha**, and consequently, the "Knesset," the Supreme Court, etc., are nullified. And it is easy to understand.

## 10,282

10,282

[B"H](#_ftn_1102), 10 Kislev, 5732
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mr. [Aharon](#_ftn_1103) Cohen
Shalom u'Bracha!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from the 4th of Kislev, along with the enclosed materials and your previous correspondence.

I begin by asking your forgiveness for the delay in my response. This is due to the multitude of pressures I am under, primarily pressures mingled with sorrow, such as the terrible decree (which, due to the great confusion and obfuscation, they have termed a "law") regarding ["Who is](#_ftn_1104) a Jew."

I thank you for bringing to my attention your efforts to annul this appalling decree. It is my firm hope that you will not be satisfied **at all** with your efforts thus far, but rather—following up on our conversation on this matter during your time here—that you will increase these efforts significantly, until the decree is nullified at its root. If in many matters it is said that ["the zealous](#_ftn_1105) hasten to perform mitzvos," then how much more so in this instance, where it is justly said that "an hour earlier is better" (not in the sense of a 60-minute hour, but literally, a brief moment), without any respite.

Regarding such a situation, our Sages of blessed memory [said](#_ftn_1106), ["I am asleep](#_ftn_1107) in exile, but my heart is awake to His Torah and His mitzvos." They said this regarding those who find themselves in spiritual exile, in darkness doubled and redoubled, to the point of the enactment of such a law as mentioned above—a law that even they, among themselves, know is a subversion of the existence of our entire people in the Diaspora and in Eretz Yisrael, for we are one people. Their only argument is: How can one begin to rectify this when the religious representatives, who claim to represent the religion of Moshe and Yisrael, continue to sit in the government, and furthermore, are the very ones executing this law in practice?

Beyond this, it is a public desecration of Hashem’s name (*Chillul Hashem*) the likes of which has no equal, since they have declared many times, in the name of the party and the government, that the Chief Rabbinate are their rabbis who determine matters of Halacha. And the Chief Rabbinate ruled **clearly** at the session of the Chief Rabbinate on Thursday, Erev Rosh Chodesh Sivan 5730, as follows:

Any conversion performed, whether in Eretz Yisrael or abroad, that is not according to the law and the Halacha established and standing from Sinai until now—is not a conversion. A non-Jew does not become a Jew except through a conversion according to Halacha.

Regarding remaining in the government, the Chief Rabbinate of Israel [ruled](#_ftn_1108) at that same session, as follows:

If, G-d forbid, the law is not amended as stated above, the religious representatives must leave the government, for it is impossible to share responsibility for this matter as members of the government.

A year and a half has passed since then, and one cannot say that the situation remains unchanged; it has changed for the worse, **etc.** There is no need to elaborate on such an appalling matter.

May it be the will of Hashem that you bring good news regarding all of the above, one hour sooner. We are approaching the days of Chanukah, the victory of Matisyahu the High Priest, the Chashmonai, over the Hellenists—the few against the many, etc.

With respect and blessing for good tidings regarding the above, and regards to your colleagues (to whom, of course, the above is also addressed. And fortunate is the one who merits this),

**M. Schneerson**

P.S. Please be so kind—and I thank you in advance for the trouble—as to convey my regards to your [sister](#_ftn_1109) (tichyeh). After asking her forgiveness, please also express my **greatest** astonishment: at a time when she was in need of actual *mesiras nefesh*, she acted fearlessly in several areas where she saw a defense of the existence of a Jewish community in a single settlement or city, etc. Now, in a time of expansion, when there is no visible danger, and on the other hand, the issue at hand concerns the existence of our entire people wherever they may be, she does not raise her voice in meetings or in conversations, and she withholds the fruit of her pen from newspapers, periodicals, etc. Yet, Divine Providence has gifted **her** with a special talent for speaking, for sounding the alarm, and for writing.

There is more to add on this, but my intention is not to preach morality, but to spur action and the energy required to annul the decree. In any case, if she is willing, the above will suffice; and if she is not prepared for this for whatever reason, what is the use of an extended discussion on the matter?

There are certainly many explanations for silence—but the Jewish people were never saved from those who rose against them by silence, even if that silence was justified.

10,883

B"H, 10 Kislev, 5732
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Dr. [Avner](#_ftn_1110) Ch. Shaki, may he live and be well,

Shalom u’vracha!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from 27 Cheshvan, and I thank you for your thoughtfulness in writing to me, notwithstanding the fact that regarding responding to letters, I am a great debtor, even to the most distinguished correspondents, due to the multitude of preoccupations which, to my great regret, do not diminish but rather the opposite, and a word to the wise is sufficient.

It is understood that I frequently receive reports of your activities, especially those concerning the survival of our people everywhere—in Eretz Yisrael and in the Diaspora—for we are one people. And I extend special thanks for your efforts to annul the terrible decree which, due to the great confusion and obfuscation, they called the "Who is a Jew" [law](#_ftn_1111).

My hope is strong that you will continue to increase your efforts in this area, more and more, until this decree is annulled from its very root. And if in many matters it is said that "the zealous hasten to perform mitzvos," how much more so in the matter at hand, regarding which one can justly say, "better one hour sooner"—and not in the sense of an hour of 60 minutes, but literally, a brief moment. And surely, for someone like yourself, there is no need for further explanation as to how essential this annulment is, and with the greatest possible urgency.

I derived special satisfaction from seeing in your letter your interest and activity in narrowing the gap between the different ethnic communities in Israel, for in this, too, there is a common background with the activities of the people of Chabad; indeed, this is one of the primary points of Chabad’s activity. Surely you witnessed this during your visit to the institutions in Kfar Chabad, where one sees an actual ingathering of exiles, and a true blending in every respect. Likewise, it is surely known to you that Chabad’s activity is concentrated within the Sephardic communities, in Morocco and Tunisia, which began immediately following the passing of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, and similar activity in generations prior to that among the Jews of Georgia [and the Caucasus](#_ftn_1113)—a Jewish community that was closed and sequestered within its own four cubits. My father-in-law, the Rebbe Rashab, sent several shluchim there more than sixty years ago, and the fruits of that shlichus, and the fruits of their fruits, are those who are now ascending from there to our Holy Land, in the [well-known style](#_ftn_1114) of "with our young and with our old, with our sons and with our daughters." This is also the foundational line in the education of the boys and girls in Europe, to where many have emigrated from Morocco and Tunisia—not only to narrow the gap, but also to blend the students together, as is done in our educational institutions in Yerres, near Paris, the "Beis Rivkah" school and seminary, and the like.

With respect and with a blessing for success in your blessed activities, and for good tidings regarding all of the above.

## 10,284

10,284

[13 Kislev, 5732]

**Precision** in the laying of tefillin for those in need of a blessing, their parents, etc. — and in this, there is a connection that is understood even in simple terms (and according to the conduct, which is also understood in simple terms — *midah k’neged midah*):

"Schizophrenia" (whatever its **cause** may be) **consists of** a lack of alignment between reality (the environment) as it is, and how the patient "sees" and perceives it **in his mind**. **Consequently**: 1) There are born within him (**emotions** corresponding to this **intellectual** perception), such as fear, or the dread that others wish to harm him, etc. 2) From time to time, there are **fluctuations**, even to the opposite extreme: from fear with no basis in reality, to an elevated spirit with no basis, etc., a splitting of the soul and perspective, etc.

Tefillin — **part** of the mitzvah **and its segulah** — is **to subjugate** the heart (the emotions) and the mind (the intellect) to the **true** [Elokus], of Whom it is said, [Ani] Hashem have not changed — **and consequently**: alignment between the intellect, the emotions, and reality, etc.

I will mention this at the holy gravesite.
