191

191

B"H, 20 Kislev, 5732
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the Board of Directors of the Tzemach Tzedek Shul and Beis Medrash in the walled city of Jerusalem, may it be rebuilt and established;
To the Board of Directors of Kolel Chabad in the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt and established, and all its branches;
To the Board of Directors of the Chabad Educational Institutions in the Holy City of Jerusalem, may it be rebuilt and established;
May Hashem grant them life,

Greetings and blessings!

Since the following points are common to all three of the aforementioned boards, this letter is addressed to all of them together.

In response to the letters and the report that were received:

(1) The proposal to appoint the esteemed and distinguished Chossid, a man of many accomplishments, R' Yehoshua Yuzewitz, as a member of the board of the Shul and Beis Medrash is approved.

(2) The proposal to improve the exterior appearance of the Shul, etc., is likewise approved. Naturally, promptness in this matter is commendable, and the sooner it is done, the better.

(3) The proposal to accede to the request of the distinguished activist R' Y. D. Weiss to build the Aron Kodesh in the aforementioned Shul is also approved, provided that it is—as he phrased it—spacious and magnificent. This was also the basis and condition for my agreement to his proposal when he spoke with me about it.

(4) Regarding a related matter that also requires special urgency: this concerns the area surrounding the Shul and Beis Medrash, including the shops in the courtyard, and furthermore—and this is essential—regarding the Chabad housing in its vicinity. As discussed several times, their absolute affiliation with Chabad is mandatory.

(5) It is a great wonder that, although it was communicated by telephone —and I believe more than once—that first and foremost, the boards, and specifically the Kolel board and the Educational Institutions board, must clarify the expenditures incurred until now (naturally, by a professional expert, as this is the necessary foundation for securing the future of all the aforementioned), no information has been received regarding this to date. My intent is not only that there is no such accounting, but that there is not even any word that they have hired someone to investigate and compile the aforementioned. I am referring to the past. It is surely understood that a vague report stating that the sum of past debts is such-and-such and the budget is so-and-so is not sufficient at all. How is it possible to know the aforementioned without an audit of the accounts?

(6) It is also understood that there is no point in sending the documents or receipts of those receiving support, etc., to here. On the contrary, doing so would preclude the possibility of conducting a proper accounting of the past, which must be as accurate and detailed as possible (which necessitates that it be done not by the board members—especially since they do not have the time for such things—but by a hired professional whose trade this is). As mentioned above, the sooner this is done, the better.

(7) Since, until Sukkos, matters were conducted as in previous years—meaning, more than a month after the school year had already begun—it is certain that the accounting of the past will also provide guidance regarding the budget for this year, which must be in accordance with the start of the school year, especially since more than a month had already passed.

(8) From the above, it is also understood why the urgent and frantic notification that there are debts of over 50,000 Lirot, and that they are urgent and pressing, etc., aroused surprise here. For why did the debt suddenly become pressing and urgent, etc., when for over a month matters were conducted without any alarm or fear-inducing telegram?

(9) Regarding the mailing list of donors that is not in the hands of the Educational Institutions board: it is known that there are no secrets involved here, only a waste of money. I mean that they are buying addresses for money. If each and every one of us is obligated to support Chabad institutions, then all the more so is it incumbent upon the Kolel board and the Toras Emes board to prevent the waste of money by the aforementioned Chabad Educational Institutions board and to provide them with a copy of their mailing list (naturally, with a warning not to cause harm to the donor). Our Sages of blessed memory have promised us: "The Jewish people are asked and they give."

(10) Regarding the office for the Educational Institutions board: if it is not possible otherwise, it is worth allocating a room for this in the Toras Emes office or in the Kolel office, as the board members shall discuss and decide.

(11) It is understood that I approve the decision regarding the signatory and the signatories on the documents, etc., and likewise regarding the signatories on the checks—as they have decided. May the merit of the public assist them in ensuring that the writing and the signing are in accordance with the will of our Rebbes and their hopes.

This is also their empowerment and blessing to perform all the aforementioned in good health, with joy and a glad heart, and in a manner that "adds and continues, adds and shines."

With blessings for success in all the aforementioned—great success—and awaiting good news regarding the above,

**M. Schneerson**

1027

1027

B”H, 20 Kislev, 5732

Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, Torah-learned, and distinguished individual, a man of noble character, a scion of a noble lineage, R’ Schneur [Zalman] Shlita,

Peace and blessing!

As we have just passed a day of special spiritual potency (*yom segulah*), may it be the will of Hashem that all the spiritual influences associated with this day be drawn down into actuality, in both private and communal matters alike. This is especially so given that, according to the teachings of Chassidus, these matters are so interconnected and bound to one another that they have become as one.

If you wish to say so, this is already hinted at by our Sages in their Mishnah: "Therefore, man was created alone, to teach you... that whoever sustains a single soul of Israel, Scripture accounts it to him as if he had sustained an entire world" (Sanhedrin 37a). According to the well-known, absolute precision of our Sages’ style, we see a great innovation in this statement—even though many do not pay attention to it, despite its simplicity. It is that this statement nullifies a common misconception rooted in a sense of human insignificance, particularly in these latter generations. For even though it is true that the "earlier generations were like angels" and we are, etc., the Mishnah nevertheless states that in order to teach us that a single soul in Israel—even in the latter generations—is an entire world, the very manner of the creation of the first man was established accordingly. This is the meaning of the expression **"Therefore"** man was created alone; that is to say, his creation had to be in a different manner (similar to other creatures, which were created in pairs), and his creation was **altered** for the sake of the lesson regarding the importance of a single soul throughout all generations.

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter with thanks. It is understood and obvious that I will be interested to see and read what has recently been printed of your writings, and I thank you in advance for the instruction to those who do His will, as you wrote in your letter, to send them here.

From one auspicious day to the next, from 19 Kislev to the days of Chanukah, may it be the will of Hashem that all the blessings and spiritual influences, etc., be in a manner of "increasing and adding light," as is the lesson of the Chanukah [candles]. Furthermore, may it be "at the entrance of his house from the outside," [to illuminate also the darkness] that is outside, until the fulfillment of the promise that [He will perform] a great salvation for His people Israel, leading to the true Redemption through Moshiach Tzidkeinu. As the great teacher (at the end of Hilchos Melachim) expresses it, he will build the Beis Hamikdash in its place and gather the dispersed of Israel, at which time they will light ["candles] in the courtyards of Your holiness, etc., to thank and praise Your great Name."

With appreciation, honor, and a blessing for an illuminating Chanukah,

**M. Schneerson**

P.S. It is understood that your notification, and the comment and insight contained therein regarding the [publication] of more of the holy manuscripts of the Alter Rebbe, caused great satisfaction. This is from the time that they began to create an index of his *maamarim* that are scattered in various booklets, some of which have not yet been printed, or were printed with many variations. This is especially true of the [maamarim] that are short (in quantity, though full of great content). Based on the first impression, it seems there are hidden treasures within them that have not yet seen the light of print. In the well-known style, may it be the will of Hashem that soon, regarding these teachings of Chassidus as well, the promise will be fulfilled: "Your springs will spread outward."

1093

1093

[B"H], Erev Chanukah, 5732
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To all participants in the annual dinner of
Merkaz Yeshivos Tomchei-Temimim Lubavitch
May Hashem grant them life

Greetings and blessings!

The annual gathering is taking place this year on the final night of Chanukah, the eighth candle.

One of the fundamental lessons of Chanukah in general, and of "Zos Chanukah" in particular, is that all "luminous" things—all matters of **ner mitzvah v'torah ohr**—must constantly be increased, even when it seems (and it may even be true) that one has already done everything one could. We learn this from the mitzvah of **ner Chanukah**: although on the first night, when one lit a single candle, one fulfilled the mitzvah of ner Chanukah to the **fullest** extent, the [law] is that once a day has passed, one must light two candles on the second night, and so on—always one more than the day before.

And even when a full seven days of Chanukah have already passed—each day of which possesses its own special virtue in matters of Torah and mitzvos, and one has fulfilled one's duty to the maximum extent on each of those days—when the eighth day of Chanukah arrives, one must not only refrain from diminishing the effort, but on the contrary, one must add yet another candle.

The Yom Tov of [Chanukah] is, after all, connected to the **Chanukas Beis HaMikdash**, as stated in the [text] of the prayer: **"And afterwards Your children came to the Holy of Holies of Your House... and they kindled lights... and they established these eight days of Chanukah..."**

On various occasions, it has been emphasized that the task of every Jewish home is to be a "Mikdash," a "dwelling place" for the Ribono shel Olam—a **luminous** dwelling, illuminated by ner mitzvah v'torah ohr.

But when is the true character of the home fully formed? It is when new generations of Jews arrive, who are raised and educated in **chinuch al taharas hakodesh**, so that they may continue to spread the light of Torah and mitzvos.

And this is also the primary task of Merkaz Yeshivos Tomchei-Temimim: to educate students who will bring light not only into their own homes, but who will bring light into the world; and not to be satisfied with the achievements of today, even when they are complete, but to add more tomorrow and the day after, and so on—**mosif v'holech, mosif v'ohr** (increasing and going forward, increasing and shining).

The response and support of the friends of the Yeshiva must be the same. Even if the support given last year was to the fullest extent, since a year has passed since the last annual gathering, increased support is now required, especially as the needs have also grown. Therefore, every man and woman must take a larger part in this endeavor—both financially and through communal involvement—to act personally and to merit others to participate in the luminous activity of Merkaz Yeshivos Tomchei-Temimim, in a manner of *mosif v'holech*, in harmony with the instructions and spirit of the luminous Yom Tov of Chanukah.

In this merit, Hashem will surely increase the light in every Jewish home: light in terms of *ner mitzvah v'torah ohr*, and also in the literal sense, that it should be truly bright in both *gashmius* and *ruchnius* together.

With respect and blessings for great success and for good tidings in all the aforementioned,

**M. Schneerson**

## 10,194

10,194

B"H, Erev Chanukah, 5732
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the Organization of Disabled Veterans of the War of Independence and the IDF in our Holy Land,
May it be built and established by Moshiach Tzidkeinu speedily in our days,

Greetings and blessings!

It was a pleasure to receive regards from you through Lieutenant Colonel Ezra, may he live, Ahrenson, who also informed me of the shiurim you are holding in the study of our holy Torah. It is called **Toras Chaim** (for it is the guide that sets the order in life so that life is worthy of the name) and **Toras Emes** (for its instruction is truth), and truth rejects compromise.

Surely, as educators in the IDF who are primarily men of action, your study, [in the style](#_ftn_1165) of our Sages, is study that leads to action.

Furthermore, and this is essential, [as has been discussed](#_ftn_1166) many times, the entire existence of an army is founded upon two points: 
a) Discipline, or in the language of our Sages – *kabbalas ol* (acceptance of the yoke), or [in the well-known](#_ftn_1167) phrasing – *na'aseh v'nishma*, with *na'aseh* (we will do) preceding *nishma* (we will hear/understand). I mean to say that when a soldier receives an order, the procedure is to fulfill it with alacrity and in the best possible manner, without first asking for the reason, or whether he agrees with it, or if it is possible to do otherwise. Rather, first and foremost, one must fulfill the "na'aseh," and only after he has fulfilled the order—when he has free time and the opportunity, etc.—can he investigate, delve into, and understand, which is "nishma," a term denoting understanding ([as the verse states](#_ftn_1168): "And they did not know that Yosef was listening [shomei'a], for the interpreter was between them").

b) The second point upon which an army is founded is that when a soldier receives an order from his commander, it is completely irrelevant what their relationship is in other areas. Even if in their civilian status the situation were the opposite—where the soldier was the commander’s teacher in wisdom, science, or economics, etc., to the point of a vast disparity in value between them, where the soldier in his civilian life is the wealthiest person in material or spiritual assets, and the commander is poor in all of these—since within the framework of the army the commander has more knowledge and experience and has dedicated his life to studying the nuances of the military, the soldier fulfills the order without questioning it at all. It makes no difference whatsoever how things stand in other areas, and this does not interfere at all with the fulfillment of the order.

There is another point, and it too is essential: within the framework of the army, there is no room at all for the claim that one's actions in the army are a private matter and that no one has the right to interfere in one's business, for everyone to do [as he sees fit](#_ftn_1169). For it is understood and simple that one action by one soldier in one place can be fateful for his entire military unit, or even for the entire front, and up to the fate of the entire country and the people dwelling upon it.

All these things apply to every single person of the Jewish people wherever they may be, for every Jew is a soldier in the armies of Hashem. Therefore, at the Giving of the Torah, there was a prerequisite condition: "na'aseh" before "nishma"—the matter of accepting the yoke of the Kingdom of Heaven and fulfilling the instructions of the Sages of Israel, who dedicated their lives to the study of Torah and its understanding, even to the point of *mesiras nefesh* for this study. And here, too, it is completely irrelevant how things are in other areas, whether one is wealthier than them or not. And surely for you, there is no need for further elaboration.

A special and heartfelt thank you for the honor you bestowed upon me by presenting me with your organization's emblem.

May it be the will that each of us protects the Jewish people, the Land of Israel, and the Torah of Israel—which are all one—as much as depends on us, in action, in speech, and even in thought. This, too, will hasten the fulfillment of the promise [in Parshas](#_ftn_1170) Bechukosai: "If you walk in My statutes and keep My commandments and perform them... I will grant peace in the land... and I will be to you a G-d and you will be to Me a people," and up to the fulfillment of the promise, "And I will lead you upright"—in the complete and true Redemption through Moshiach Tzidkeinu.

With respect and blessing for the fulfillment of the heart's desires of each of you for the good, and in the manner and according to the instruction of the days of Chanukah approaching us for the good, for the primary mitzvah in these days is the mitzvah of lighting the Chanukah candle, [and we add](#_ftn_1171) to the candle, and through this, the light goes on increasing from day to day.

## 1025

B"H, Erev Chanukah, 5732
Brooklyn, N.Y.

[And in anticipation](#_ftn_1173) of the upcoming days of Chanukah, may it be the will of Hashem, blessed and exalted, that each one of us, within the entirety of Klal Yisrael, does what is incumbent upon him to spread the [ner](#_ftn_1174) mitzvah and the light of Torah in all three aspects of the mitzvah of the Chanukah lights:

[From the time the sun sets](#_ftn_1175) — meaning, not to be affected [because](#_ftn_1176) "darkness covers the earth," but rather the opposite;

At the entrance of his house, **on the outside** — meaning, to illuminate and bring close even those who are still standing on the outside;

Increasing and progressing, adding more light.

With respect and blessing for good tidings in all the aforementioned.

## 1070

B.H., Erev Chanukah, 5732
Brooklyn, N.Y.

In that same vein, I enjoyed seeing you seated at the table at the farbrengen in Kfar Chabad in the photograph that was sent to me.

May it be Hashem’s will that you succeed in this responsible and lofty position, and that you establish and strengthen the region in both gashmius and ruchnius alike. For if, regarding every nation and every place, these two are interdependent, then all the more so regarding our people, a holy nation, in Eretz Yisrael, the Holy Land, where they are not merely interdependent but are one and the same, and the rest is understood.

May it be His will that you conduct this work with proper health, joy, and a good heart, and may the merit of the many assist you.

With respect and blessings for the fulfillment of your heart’s desires for the good in all the matters you write about, and in the manner and according to the instruction of the days of Chanukah approaching us for the good—for the primary mitzvah of these days is the lighting of the Chanukah candle, and we add [to the candle](#_ftn_1179) and the light from day to day, increasing and growing—and may you bring good tidings in all the aforementioned.

P.S. It is surprising that you wrote that you did not receive a response to your previous letters, as I believe I had already answered them long ago.

## 10th of Teves

B"H, Erev Chanukah, 5732
Brooklyn, N.Y.

**From the time the sun sets** — meaning, not to be deterred by the fact that "darkness covers the earth," but on the contrary, [to illuminate it];

**At the entrance of his house, on the outside** — meaning, to illuminate and bring close even those who are still standing on the outside;

**Increasing and continuing** in candle and light from day to day.

This serves as a conduit and vessel for receiving Hashem’s blessings in a manner of "increasing and continuing," both in one's personal affairs and in one's general affairs, which, for a Jew in general and for a communal activist in particular, go hand in hand.

With blessings for illuminating days of Chanukah and for good tidings in all the aforementioned.

199

[B"H], Tuesday, the second day of Chanukah, 5732. Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of the letter...

As we complete seven days from the 19th of Kislev, it is appropriate to note:

The calendar placement of this year—

Regarding the day of "good tidings," which is the 19th of Kislev, the anniversary of the 19th of Kislev of the Alter Rebbe’s redemption (in the year 5559)—

Is unique in that it is a day on which "it was doubled that it is good,"

One of the descriptors and praises of the time of the Alter Rebbe’s redemption, as he himself wrote in his letter announcing his redemption: "The day that Hashem has made for us, the day of the 19th of Kislev, the day on which it was doubled that it is good, the day of the great hillula of our holy Rebbe, of blessed memory."

There are several aspects to this "doubling of the good"—starting with the words of our Sages: "good to Heaven and good to people," Torah ("good instruction") and mitzvos (good deeds, and in their entirety—the mitzvah of tzedakah). And in the language of the Alter Rebbe, citing the Arizal, there are two types of souls in Israel: the souls of Torah scholars who occupy themselves with Torah all their days, and the souls of the "people of mitzvos" who occupy themselves with tzedakah and acts of loving-kindness.

And as with all holy matters, each of the above is included in the other. For example: Torah—includes teaching Torah to the many; tzedakah and acts of loving-kindness—are like the deeds of the Patriarchs, the acts of loving-kindness of Avraham, who planted an eshel, and every passerby would eat and drink, etc., and he would say to them, "Eat and drink from that which belongs to the G-d of the world; thank, praise, and bless the One who spoke and the world came into being."

And the essential point is that (also) the calendar placement of this auspicious day—the 19th of Kislev—of this year (like the year of the redemption) on a day on which "it was doubled that it is good,"

Should awaken each and every one, with greater intensity and greater strength, to a doubled and redoubled effort: Torah study and teaching Torah to the many, acts of loving-kindness in both the physical and spiritual realms alike,

Founded upon and permeated with the love of Hashem (which is one of the foundations of the Torah, its root, and the source of all 248 positive mitzvos) and the love of Israel (the fulfillment of which is the entire Torah, and the rest is but commentary, etc.),

Action as it ought to be done, and even more—the performance of *mehadrin*, and even more—*mehadrin min hamehadrin*,

As is the instruction of the days of Chanukah—where the simple custom regarding the mitzvah of the day, the lighting of the Chanukah candles, is that of *mehadrin min hamehadrin*.

With blessings,

**M. Schneerson**

## 1030

[B"H], Tuesday, the second day of Chanukah, 5732. Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, etc. [Rabbi] Yehoshua, may he live:

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter dated the 8th of Mar-Cheshvan and those preceding it.

[Upon the completion of seven days, etc.]

... With blessings regarding your writing about their relocation (in due time) to Kfar Chabad — that "a change of place brings a change of fortune" for the good and for blessing, both materially and spiritually.

**M. Schneerson**

P.S. In response to your notes:

a) [Regarding the letter] of the Rebbe Maharash — it is explicitly stated (in the copy) that it was written to "Sarake" (one of the colonies).

b) [Regarding the citation] of the source for the relevance of the content of the *parsha* and its timing to the Shelah — this is how the Tzemach Tzedek cited it (*Vayeshev* 168:1). What the Menachem Azaryah wrote regarding this (*Maamarim* 206:2) — I have seen since then.

c) [Also], [Rashi's commentary] on Nach is in the style of *peshat* (as it is a continuation of his commentary on the Torah). However, it is not as rigorous as his commentary on the Torah (as is evident **here and there** — in many places). Perhaps the reason is that the age of one who studies Nach is more mature. And this is well-understood.

d) ["The year of] Torah" — this is the total of the entire *alef-beis* (including the *tav*), and it is based on the phrasing of the blessings of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, in *Sefer HaMaamarim* 5710 (p. 84) and in many other places.

e) [The opinion] of Rabbi Akiva regarding Ben Koziba the King — does not contradict what the Rambam wrote in *Hilchos Melachim* [chapter 11, law 3] — because it was Rabbi Akiva’s initial thought that this was the **beginning** of the period of his revelation.

f) [Regarding "to bind] a prohibition upon himself" — this refers to vows (*nedarim*). [Sifri] on the verse: "Upon his soul, etc. — his own vows, etc., his wife's vows, etc." (And the Ramban's difficulty regarding Rashi there is resolved — according to his version). See the commentaries on *Zohar Chadash* (115b). And these are ancient matters.

g) [Regarding Samson] — there are two opinions in *Sotah* (9b and there): The Sages taught, etc., "He rebelled (against his Creator), etc."; Rabbi Yehuda said, "He protected [the Jewish people] like the Holy One, Blessed be He." And in *Zohar Chadash* (127a) — it follows the Sages, **and it resolves** the difficulty there: "But you might say, was Samson not a Nazir of G-d, etc.?"

Now, it is known among the rules of the Rambam that he does not rely on a forced interpretation. When there are two opposing opinions in the Talmud and the Talmudic conclusion follows one of them, he provides the refutation of the other opinion within his own words [(see] *Yad Malachi* and the sources cited there) — therefore, the Rambam elaborates (*Hilchos Issurei Biah* 13:14): "Let it not enter your mind, etc., that Israel, etc." And it can be said that the fact that he elaborates afterward: "**The secret** of the matter is thus" — is to hint that even according to *Sod*, his opinion is the same.

Surely you are keeping up with the three daily study portions that are equal for every soul: Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya; and in any case, you should do so from now on.

The *pidyon nefesh* that was in your letter will be read at an auspicious time at the holy gravesite.

## 1133

[Teves, 5732]

Regarding your citation from the sefer *Otzar HaTefillos*, which explains the miracle of "delivering the impure into the hands of the pure" based on the Chazal, "The nations who eat creeping things—their bodies are weak" (*Shabbos* 86b), [and who are the weak ones? The Rabbis, etc.]—in my humble opinion, this does not appear correct **at all**, for it has already been stated, "the strong into the hands of the weak."

What appears to me—prefaced by the fact that the true definition of *tumah* and *taharah*, as well as matters regarding a *tzaddik* who is engaged in *Torah*, applies only to *Bnei Yisrael*—is that the reference to the three categories of "impure," "wicked," and "presumptuous" refers to the Hellenists. The thanksgiving for this is in the manner of what is stated many times in *Tehillim*, etc., regarding the victory of the *tzaddik*, and the like.

## 1404

[4 Teves, 5732]

It is well known that it is not in accordance with the ways of *tzniyus* to prolong the time between the decision to become engaged and the wedding. This is especially true when both parties live in the same city. And the wise will understand.

## 1015

B"H, 5 Teves, 5732
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the members of the Association of Teachers of Torah Shebe'al Peh,
May Hashem grant them life,

Peace and blessing!

Many thanks for the letter that reached me some time ago, and just now the "Shema'atin" booklet was received. I thank you for your thoughtfulness, and naturally, also for the [opportunity](#_ftn_1235) to become acquainted with the new approach to studying the commentary of Rashi—the *Parshandasa*, as [Ibn Ezra](#_ftn_1236) calls him.

It is well known what is brought in the Shulchan Aruch, which is *halacha lema'aseh* for every Jew, from the greatest to the smallest, regarding *shnayim mikra v'echad targum*. There is an opinion that one who reads the *mikra* twice and, on the third time, reviews the entire *parsha* with the commentary of Rashi—which is built upon the foundation of the Talmud—is better served than by the *targum*, as it provides a deeper explanation. And although it continues that the primary ruling does not follow this opinion, it concludes that, in any case, every *yirei shamayim* should read both the *targum* and the commentary of Rashi (Shulchan Aruch of the Alter Rebbe, Orach Chaim, 285:2).

Furthermore, the words of [our Rebbes](#_ftn_1237), the Nesi'ei Chabad, are well known: that within the commentary of Rashi, the "wine of Torah" (the secrets of the Torah) is concealed.

With respect and blessing,

## 10,108

B"H, 15 Teves, 5732
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter, in which you request a blessing and include a *pidyon nefesh* dated Monday, 2 Teves.

At an opportune time, it will be read at the gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

With regards to your father-in-law, the distinguished Rabbi, may he live and be well.

P.S. In response to your comments:

a) It is understood that the main thing in *ta'amulah*—especially in our times—is regarding *ma'aseh b'fo'al*. [And it is not worthwhile to enter into arguments (which, for the most part, stir up contentiousness and "who is in charge," etc., rather than a genuine search for truth). Likewise, it is advisable to avoid debate on matters that the listeners are not prepared to accept in their current state—but it is **essential** that the possibility of interpreting this as giving a "hechsher" or agreement, etc., be ruled out. In any case, the time for meetings is extremely limited.]

b) The study—based on the above—should ideally be in areas that relate to daily life, and for the most part, these are matters where the laws for women are equated to those for men, and everyone is obligated in this knowledge.

c) It is simple that according to *Torah*, [one's own city comes first;] he must continue in the dissemination of Judaism, etc., in his current location—

And in addition to this, and most importantly—this *avodah* in Africa and abroad in general is literally *pikuach nefesh* (from assimilation, etc., *rachmana litzlan*), which is not the case in *Eretz Yisrael*. And this is understood.

And I have already [spoken] to many—that any Rabbi, *rosh yeshivah*, or spiritual guide who leaves his circle abroad (in our times) and relocates to *Eretz Yisrael*—is like a **general** of an army fleeing the front lines during a war and at a time of enemy attack. And this is understood.

## 1010

B"H, 25 Teves, 5732
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed brothers, engaged in the holy work, 
Those who contemplate a good matter and bring merit to the many,
Mr. [Michal](#_ftn_1244) Yehoshua and Mr. Shmuel Shulsinger, may they live,

Peace and blessing!

I hereby acknowledge with many thanks the receipt of the *Siddur* "Avodas Yisrael," in two volumes. My thanks are twofold: firstly, for your thoughtfulness in sending me the aforementioned, and secondly, because it gives me hope that despite the interruption, you will restore the crown to its former glory. I refer to the tradition of your publishing house, which should be in the manner of "one engaged in holy work"—that is, to continue printing and publishing holy books, and more precisely, books that elucidate our Torah, the Torah of life, the Torah of truth.

Based on the [statement](#_ftn_1246) of our Sages, of blessed memory (and it is emphasized here specifically **our Sages**, even though they are also our Rabbis), which begins, "One who is engaged in a mitzvah is told to complete it," I am here to urge you once again to complete the series of fundamental books in our Torah, especially to publish the [Talmud](#_ftn_1247) Yerushalmi. There is a necessity for this, both on behalf of the many—the community of learners—and for your own sake and merit.

It should be published with the same beauty and quality as you published the Rambam, the Shas Bavli, etc., and with internal beauty—by adding the notes and insights of the great scholars of Israel—in addition to the external beauty, which is also an instruction of our Torah, the Torah of life. This is especially so, as mentioned above, since you have already begun and have actually carried out the publication with the beauty of the Written Torah, the *Nach* with *Mikraos Gedolos*, the Talmud Bavli (where you skipped the Talmud Yerushalmi), the Rambam, the *Shulchan Aruch Yoreh Deah*, etc.

Of course, I am aware of the Yerushalmi Talmud you published, which is a photographic reproduction of the Krotoschin edition. But surely, for people like yourselves, it is superfluous to emphasize that this edition has more of a bibliographic value, or at most, serves as a comparison with subsequent editions regarding textual variations and the like. However, as a study text for anyone interested in the Torah of Hashem—to learn it and to teach it—all subsequent editions are superior to the aforementioned, due to the commentators and explanations added to them, culminating in the Vilna edition with all its additions.

It is understood that my primary intention in the above is **all** the additions, and perhaps it is possible to also include, **in its entirety**, the commentary "Ahavas Tzion V'Yerushalayim" by [Rabbi](#_ftn_1248) Ratner. Furthermore, a few years ago, the [book](#_ftn_1249) of Rabbi Rabinowitz on the Yerushalmi was printed; he is the father of the merchant Mr. Rabinowitz from Boston (for the moment, the author's first name and the name of the book have slipped my mind, but it can easily be clarified).

Regarding the doubt as to whether my request will be effective, I am repeating my request once again, and I have the *bitachon* to ask for this, since in my clear opinion, this is a merit for the many and a necessity for the many, especially in these most recent years, in which there has been an increase in the study of this Talmudic *Shas*.

May it be the will that I receive good news that you have actually begun the publication of the aforementioned, with the alacrity appropriate to the magnitude of the project and its content, [for](#_ftn_1250) there is nothing that can stand before the will, and the merit of the many will assist you.

With respect and blessing in general, and with a special blessing for success in the aforementioned, and in good health,

**M. Schneerson**

P.S. As is the ancient Jewish custom, and according to the [well-known](#_ftn_1251) saying that it is easier to be a critic than an author—and primarily because this also concerns the many—I wish to express my wonder that in the publication of the *Siddur* "Avodas Yisrael," while there is external beauty, [the adornment](#_ftn_1252) of performing the mitzvah, there is a lack of the appropriate attention regarding several details of the content, as was done regarding the precision in the quality of the photography, etc. For example, I did not find any attention paid, at the very least, to noting the *nusach* of the *Siddur* (which apparently, in the author's time and country, there was no need for, because there was a uniform custom regarding the *nusach*, etc., which is not the case when one publishes it now).

Also, apparently as a result of a lack of sufficient attention to the content, the addition of "Derech HaChaim" by R. Yaakov of Lissa is labeled as a "commentary," whereas it is nothing more than a compilation of laws and has no connection to this specific *Siddur*, nor to a prayer book in general.

There is more to add along these lines, but since my hope is that you will eventually publish the Yerushalmi, this is not the way to dwell on details that would not contribute to a positive attitude toward my request and the aforementioned urging.

The letter is sent as "fast/urgent"—in order to emphasize with greater strength how much I value the matter of the publication of the Yerushalmi, which is also "fast/urgent," and "better one hour earlier."

## 1016

[4 Shevat, 5732]

It is not entirely clear what is difficult for him: is it Moshe Rabbeinu’s question, “A tzaddik and it is bad for him,” or is it the one that Rashi answers with, “perhaps the sin will cause it” (Parshas Vayishlach)?

**I was alarmed** by the content of the letter. **The situation is the opposite**—specifically when the aforementioned person was in the government (Ben-Gurion, his son, etc.), the law (according to his will) was for conversion **“according to Halacha,” and only afterwards** did they ruin it, etc.

The reason for my demand is **simple**: If they resign from the government, 1) the **appalling chillul Hashem** will be nullified: that religious people informed him of a *psak din*—**his own** rabbis—that he must resign, and that this concerns **Klal Yisrael**—**and he did not heed the judgment, and he commanded all his officials** that **they too should not heed it** (because regarding them, too, there was a **clear** *psak din* from the rabbis). 2) The current situation there is such that it is **highly likely** they will ask them to return and will add “according to Halacha,” meaning that their failure to resign is what keeps the law in place. 3) When they are in the government, it is a “hechsher” that it is possible to be religious and permit a gentile to enter the congregation of Israel. And one who remains silent—it is as if he agrees—and whoever has the power to protest, etc.

## 10th of Shevat

[7th of Shevat, 5732]

1) Abba Eban – he is a Jew, his mother lives in London, and his wife is also Jewish – and her sister was the daughter-in-law of the late Rabbi Herzog.

2) He has no say in the government – **as is known**, and it has even been publicized in the newspapers of **Eretz Yisrael Tizkeh V'tikonen** (though in the U.S. they silence this, since he is supposed to be the **official** representative in Washington).

3) He is one of the **very** few in the government who, throughout the **entire** time, has **not** involved himself in religious disputes, **as is well known**.

4) **A clear halachic ruling** – *Bari v'shema, bari adif* (a certain claim is preferred over an uncertain one): It is well known, and **now everyone** says and admits, that due to the establishment of the aforementioned law, many gentiles have **actually** been registered as Jews, and the officials are **commanded** to continue doing so (provided they have **any** sort of document, and all of this has been printed in **all the newspapers** of Eretz Yisrael).

And all the conjectures: 1) Are in the category of doubt. 2) All the parties in Eretz Yisrael have **clearly** declared their reasons **every day** for their silence (which is tantamount to admission), for their support, etc.

5) The argument that protest will not be effective, etc., and therefore one should not protest, etc. – even the leaders of the Mafdal **declared** that one must protest. And see also Shabbos (55a).

6) Those who support the law **here** – have obtained a copy of **his letter** and are now discussing how to publish it to prove that "even Rabbi Henkin *shlita* **ruled** that one should not fight against the law, **etc.**"

## 1019

[Shevat, 5732]

1. [In addition](#_ftn_1277) to the **explicit** ruling—that in all such cases an unspecified period is thirty days—it is **obvious** that in the office of **this minister (the Mizrachi one)**, he signs and issues a certificate to one who has not been converted according to Halacha—who is a Jew **transgressing** the halachic ruling, **willfully and publicly**, and many such certificates have been issued since.

2. To claim regarding [an open halachic ruling of a Rav](#_ftn_1278) that it is a political threat is a desecration of the honor of the Rabbinate **the likes of which has never been seen**. After all, they would **say the same** about a halachic ruling of Rav Henkin.

## 1022

1022

[B"H], 4th of Shelah, 10 Shevat, 5732
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the activists and friends of the Bais Rivkah schools — in general, and to the participants in the annual Melaveh Malkah — in particular,

Hashem should keep them alive.

Shalom u’Brachah!

In response to the news that the annual Melaveh Malkah for the benefit of the Bais Rivkah schools will take place this year on Motzaei Shabbos Kodesh Parshas Beshalach, Shabbos Shirah, 13 Shevat,

It is worth recalling the [well-known] sicha of the Alter Rebbe, Baal HaTanya and Shulchan Aruch, in connection with this week’s parsha: Although the parsha contains two songs—the song that Moshe sang with the Jewish men, and the song of Miriam HaNeviah with the women—it is specifically a song of a woman—the song of Devorah HaNeviah—that was chosen for the Haftorah.

This emphasizes that there are matters and areas in Jewish life in which the Jewish woman has a special and highly important shlichus and task.

One of these areas is the management and safeguarding of the Jewish home, ensuring that it is a Jewish home in the fullest sense of the word, permeated with the light and warmth of Torah and mitzvos.

This is further indicated in the current parsha and Haftorah when one considers the circumstances that prompted the aforementioned songs:

The parsha speaks of the time when the Jews were in the desert on the way to conquer Eretz Yisrael and fight for a home for themselves. In that instance, the men led the way, and the song of Moshe Rabbeinu took precedence. The Haftorah speaks of when the Jews were already in Eretz Yisrael and it was necessary to ensure the protection and maintenance of the Jewish home—here, [Devorah] HaNeviah led the way, and Barak ben Avinoam was secondary to her.

And so, in all times and generations, the Jewish woman occupies the primary place in maintaining and securing the foundations of the Jewish home, which is why she is called **Akeres HaBayis**.

In the Bais Rivkah schools, Jewish daughters—future Jewish mothers—are educated in the spirit of Torah and mitzvos, imbued with Chassidic light and good character traits, so that they may fulfill to the fullest extent their highly important task in Jewish life, in the footsteps of Miriam HaNeviah and Devorah HaNeviah. It is to be expected that these institutions of chinuch habanos al taharas hakodesh will receive the fullest support.

May Hashem Yisbarach help that this annual undertaking and all the activities of Bais Rivkah throughout the entire year should be with great success, and may this merit assist all the activists, friends, and helpers to receive the Almighty’s blessings in everything they need, both materially and spiritually.

With respect and with a blessing for success and good tidings,

**M. Schneerson**

## 10,323

[B"H], 4th day of Parshas Beshalach, 10 Shevat, 5732
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the students of the Beis Rivkah Seminary in Yer
May Hashem grant them life

Blessings and peace!

Your letters were received, and at an auspicious time, I will mention you at the resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, the author of the day of the Hillula, for the fulfillment of your heart’s desires for the good—desires befitting the daughters of Israel, daughters of our matriarchs Sarah, Rivkah, Rachel, and Leah, who [built] the house of Israel.

Regarding the theme of the day, it is [well-known] that the Alter Rebbe spoke about this parsha, Shabbos Shirah, noting that although there are two songs in this parsha—the song of Moshe and the Bnei Yisrael, and the song of Miriam the Prophetess and all the women after her—the Haftorah emphasizes the song of Devorah the Prophetess. The lesson in this is that there are matters in which the women and daughters of Israel have a special mission and a unique role that exceeds that of the men. In general, this is the matter of managing the home and guiding the members of the household in the path of Torah and mitzvos, regarding which it is [said], "The wisdom of women builds her house."

To explain further: the parsha speaks of the Bnei Yisrael while they were in the desert, on the way to conquering Eretz Yisrael and building a home in Israel. It is the [way] of a man to conquer, and therefore the song of Moshe and the Bnei Yisrael comes first and is primary. However, the Haftorah speaks of a time when the Bnei Yisrael were already on their land, and it was necessary to protect the house of Israel from enemies and ambushers. In this, the woman’s portion is superior to the man’s, which is why she is called the **Akeres HaBayis** (the foundation of the home). This is emphasized in the Haftorah of the song of [Devorah], who held the position of leadership, while Barak ben Avinoam was secondary to her.

May it be the will of Hashem that each and every one of you follows in the footsteps of Miriam the Prophetess and Devorah the Prophetess, and fulfills her lofty mission and purpose: to be daughters who build a home in Israel, for pride and for glory.

With blessings for success and for good tidings,

**M. Schneerson**

## 10,224

B"H, 11 Shevat, 5732
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Professor [Shlomo](#_ftn_1295) Shoham, shlita

Greetings and blessings!

I am writing to acknowledge receipt of *Israel Studies in [Criminology]*, which brought to mind the content of our conversation when you were here. It is my hope that you, too, have kept these matters in mind, especially regarding the point that the merit of the many depends upon him. After all, you possess influence in several circles, particularly in a circle that is in dire need of guidance and influence (in order to set it upon the straight path). Furthermore, the importance of this influence is immense, as a significant portion of them are young people—those who are just beginning their independent lives, or are preparing to enter them. At such a stage, influence has the power to shape the entirety of one’s life, including that of their family and environment.

[We are promised](#_ftn_1297) that one who comes to purify himself—[and specifically](#_ftn_1298) as the Alter Rebbe, author of the Tanya and Shulchan Aruch, explains: to purify oneself and to purify others—is assisted. This applies to every good deed, and especially, as mentioned, regarding the merit of the many.

With respect and blessings,

P.S. I am sure you will send your future publications as well, and I thank you in advance.

## 1039

[B"H,] Motzaei Shabbos Kodesh, Parshas Beshalach,
Erev Sunday, Parshas Yisro,
5732. Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Anash and to all those engaged in the dissemination of Judaism, Torah, and its mitzvos—among all lovers of Torah and mitzvos,
May Hashem keep them and grant them life.

Greetings and blessings!

As we have just emerged from the day of the Hillula of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe—
Just as with every matter of [remembrance][edn_217] according to our Torah, the Torah of life and the Torah of truth, the ultimate intent is to be stirred by the content and the inwardness of the matter mentioned, so that it may rise, come, and reach into thought, speech, and action—[and action] is the essential thing—so too is it, understandably and simply, regarding the day of remembrance of the passing of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe. It must lead to contemplation of his activities during his lifetime in this world, and to draw conclusions, each and every one of us, regarding our own thought, speech, and action.

I have come here to highlight and illuminate a [fundamental][edn_218] matter and a central point, one of many, among the activities of the Baal Hillula, in which he labored all the days of his life, even to the point of literal mesiras nefesh:

This is the matter of chinuch al taharas hakodesh (education in accordance with the purity of holiness) for the sons and daughters of Yisrael, wherever they may be.

In this area specifically, he labored tirelessly himself, and he commanded all those who listen to his voice—and even appealed with a soulful request to everyone to whom his call would reach—

To engage—with the appropriate energy—in matters of chinuch al taharas hakodesh in general, and in particular to educate their sons and daughters, and likewise to educate themselves with this education—an education founded upon Torah and mitzvos that defines and establishes one’s daily conduct and daily life.

He was [one who] practiced what he preached; he strove with all his might to establish institutions of chinuch al taharas hakodesh wherever his hand could reach, both institutions for boys and institutions for girls, as is well-known and famous.

And I am acting as his emissary—to awaken once again each and every one who has studied his Torah and followed the path he taught us, who surely continue to do so now, as well as all those who wish to join his legacy, and all lovers of Torah and mitzvos—to act in the aforementioned direction and with the necessary energy, with devotion of soul and body, and all the more so with money, both in establishing the existing institutions of chinuch al taharas hakodesh and in founding new such institutions wherever possible. As our Sages of blessed memory expound on such a matter: "Hashem desired, for the sake of His righteousness, to make Torah great [and glorious]."[edn_219] And above all—to educate all their sons and all their daughters in institutions of chinuch al taharas hakodesh.

And behold, [as our Sages of blessed memory said,] the zealous are quick to perform mitzvos, and all the more so is [zeal][edn_220] necessary in matters of chinuch, especially in this era of ours, when there are many who lie in wait and scheme against the younger generation to trap them, draw them in, and capture them in educational institutions that are the opposite of kosher education, etc., and a word to the wise is sufficient.

Therefore, "one hour (one moment) sooner" is better in all the above.

And surely my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, will arouse great mercy for all [those who act] and perform in the matters mentioned above—for everything they and their families need, and in the inner point—to see much true nachas [from their descendants][edn_221], with abundance in both the physical and spiritual realms alike.

And since [we have been commanded] to ascend in matters of holiness, [and by the measure] with which a person measures, it is measured out to him, surely from time to time they will increase in the aforementioned activities, and the Holy One, Blessed be He, the Giver of the Torah and the Mitzvah, will add [His blessings] in a measure far exceeding the primary [from His] full, open, holy, and wide hand.

And with zeal, [and until] speedily His word will run—the blessings of Hashem, and ultimately the fulfillment of the prophecy: "O [G-d][edn_222], to save me; Hashem, [hasten][edn_223] to my aid... O G-d, hasten to me"—

To hasten [the true and complete Redemption][edn_224] through Moshiach Tzidkeinu, speedily in our days.

***

Indeed, all that has been said is related to the themes of the Torah portions of these days: the [portion][edn_225] of the Redemption and the Song (of the Splitting of the Sea), which [they][edn_226] (the children of Yisrael) recognized first, to the point of tangible recognition, as it is written: "**This** [is my G-d][edn_228] and I will glorify Him," pointing Him out with a finger; and the portion of the Giving of the Torah, which was given [to the house][edn_229] of Yaakov (these are the women) and to the children of Yisrael (these are the men)—through a guarantee (in the language of Chazal)—"**Our children** are our guarantors."

With respect and with blessings for great success in all the above,

**M. Schneerson**

## 10,331

B"H, 15 Shevat, 5732
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the Administration of Kolel Chabad in Jerusalem, the Holy City,
May it be built and established by Moshiach Tzidkeinu,
May Hashem grant them life,

Peace and Blessing!

As we are but a few days removed from the day of the Hillula, and on this day of Rosh [Hashanah]( #_ftn_1324) for the trees—and [man]( #_ftn_1325) is the tree of the field—our Sages of blessed memory explained that this is connected to the study of Torah and in a way that "from it you shall eat," which is to say, the dissemination of Torah (Taanis 7a).

I hereby acknowledge receipt of the reports, although time does not permit me to review them with the necessary attention, and we shall return to this at a later time.

It is understood that regarding the practical application, I am coming [to this request] because it is consistent with the intent of our Rebbes, the Nesi'im, in founding the Kolel, that this be connected to the study of Torah (Nigleh and Chassidus) and the avodah of tefillah.

And in addition to the above, in these days, the aforementioned should be connected not just to Jerusalem in general, but to the Old City of Jerusalem (and in the Tzemach Tzedek shul and beis medrash).

Because of the importance of the matter, I have made my aforementioned request, with the addition that all details in such a matter are commendable, including—and this is primary—proposals from the administration regarding what is possible in all of the above, etc. And because of the importance, an early response in all of this would also be commendable.

Awaiting good news in all of the above, and I sign with a blessing for great, abundant, and extraordinary success in the establishing and expansion of the Kolel,

**M. Schneerson**

P.S.
a) It is worthwhile that you also discuss whether, if the study were to be in the aforementioned shul, there is room to establish a special library there.

b) Based on the Chabad custom in recent years regarding the activities of N'shei U'Bnos Chabad, I am interested in also receiving proposals from them regarding the activities of the women and daughters of the Kolel, may they live. And a word to the wise is sufficient.

And I thank you in advance for all of the above.

## 1032

B"H, 15 Shevat, 5732
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the participants in the celebration of "Ohalei Yosef Yitzchak" and the "Beis Rivkah" institutions, and foremost among them the esteemed Rabbis and Chassidim, etc., of the holy community of Casablanca, may Hashem grant them life,

Peace and blessing!

It was with pleasure that I received the news regarding the celebration with the participation of the esteemed Rabbis, community activists, and lovers of Torah and mitzvos in the holy community of Casablanca, shlita.

[It is a merit that is brought about on a meritorious day](#_ftn_1326) — the days between the parsha of the giving of our Torah and the parsha of Mishpatim, which, [in the style](#_ftn_1327) of our Sages, of blessed memory, teaches that just as the former (the Ten Commandments) were from Sinai, so too these (the laws of Mishpatim) were from Sinai.

[On the face of it](#_ftn_1328), since Mishpatim are matters of logic, what is the necessity for the emphasis that these, too, are specifically from Sinai? But it is known, and we have also seen it tangibly, that even matters agreed upon by human intellect—if they are not founded upon the pillars of faith in Hashem, may He be blessed and exalted, the Creator of the world and its Guide, and in His Divine Providence, and if their foundations are not in the Halacha transmitted to us from Sinai—can be distorted from one extreme to the other. For [a person](#_ftn_1329) is biased toward himself, to the point of calling justice "wickedness," and wickedness "justice," and in the style of [the verse](#_ftn_1330), "who call darkness light and light darkness."

This is also emphasized in the Ten Commandments, where the rational mitzvos contained within them, such as [honor](#_ftn_1331) your father and your mother, do not steal, etc., have validity only if their source and foundation is [I am](#_ftn_1332) Hashem your G-d... you shall have no other gods, etc.

[And the tzaddikim](#_ftn_1333) who resemble their Creator—their activity in matters between man and his fellow and between man and Hashem is with that very same mesiras nefesh. This was the conduct of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, in whose name these institutions are called. He conducted himself in this manner throughout his entire life in this world and paved the way for the generations after him to walk and act in the aforementioned manner, beginning first and foremost with the education of the boys and girls—the children of Avraham, Yitzchak, and Yaakov, and the daughters of Sarah, Rivkah, Rachel, and Leah—wherever they may be, and especially and particularly in the educational institutions named after him, "Ohalei Yosef Yitzchak Lubavitch," including the educational institutions for girls, "Beis Rivkah."

Great is the merit of each and every one who engages and strives in the establishment of these institutions and their expansion, both in quantity (increasing the number of students) and in quality (increasing their knowledge of our Torah, the Torah of life), and in a manner [of study](#_ftn_1334) that leads to action: the fulfillment of mitzvos in daily life, in accordance with Halacha, without compromise and with hidur.

This merit will surely continue the blessing of Hashem to all those who strive and engage, whether with their bodies or their means, or both together, to be blessed with everything they need, both materially and spiritually.

And surely, from a position of tranquility and expansion, they will add even more to the assistance, effort, and activity mentioned above. The merit of the many—the students, may they live—will stand for them and for all that is theirs in all of the above.

I am certain that my representative, the esteemed Rabbi, Chassid, and G-d-fearing man, a man of many accomplishments, etc., Rabbi B.A. Gorodetzky, shlita, will convey my personal regards. I reiterate my blessing in writing as well—for the success of the celebration in every respect.

With great respect and abundant blessing, looking forward to good news,

**M. Schneerson**

## 1033

[B"H], Tuesday, the day on which "it was good" was doubled,
Parshas "If you lend money to My people," 5732
Brooklyn, N.Y.

May Hashem protect them and grant them life,

Peace and blessing!

On the day that concludes and seals the period following the Shabbos of the Parsha of the Giving of the [Torah][edn_236]—which begins with *gemilas chasadim* and ends with *gemilas chasadim*—

On the third day of Parshas [Mishpatim][edn_237]—which begins with *gemilas chasadim* and ends with *gemilas chasadim*—

I hereby acknowledge receipt of the notice that on Motzaei Shabbos, Parshas "If you lend money to My people," Parshas Shekalim, the Society’s annual meeting will take place—within the framework of a "Melaveh Malkah" meal, the [meal][edn_238] of Dovid Malka Meshicha, as is your good custom year after year.

May it be the will of Hashem that it be at a good and auspicious time, and that it lead to good resolutions and their fulfillment in actual deed, and in general—to a great increase **in all** the Society’s activities from previous years.

And certainly, in accordance with the special situation in every place, and according to the [halachic ruling][edn_239] of our Sages, "Your poor neighbors and the poor of your city take precedence" [(including][edn_240]—the wealthy who are, at that moment, poor), there will be the necessary attention, commensurate with the importance and magnitude of the matter, to providing *gemilas chasadim* whose purpose and results are the establishing of the neighborhoods where Bnei Yisrael reside [(a proper][edn_241] dwelling—meaning, together with a shul, a beis medrash, kosher educational institutions, and *gemilas chasadim* institutions), a true establishment, meaning one that also includes improvement and expansion in both quantity and quality.

And may you do all of this with great alacrity, [in the words][edn_242] of our Sages, "Give it to him immediately." Especially according to the [explanation][edn_243] of our Alter Rebbe, that this was "the wondrous alacrity (of Avraham Avinu, peace be upon him) to show his joy and desire to fulfill the will of his Creator and to provide pleasure to his Maker," [from whom][edn_244] our Sages learned [regarding][edn_245] the fulfillment of all *mitzvos* in general, and in particular [the act][edn_246] of *tzedakah*, which excels over them all, as it protects and saves.

And may it be the will of Hashem that all of this—measure for measure, and indeed many times over—[hasten][edn_248] and speed the fulfillment of the promise: "[Hashem], save me; Hashem, hasten to my aid... Hashem, hasten to me"—to hasten [the][edn_250] true and complete Redemption through Moshiach Tzidkeinu, speedily in our days.

With respect and blessing and for good tidings in all the above,

**M. Schneerson**

Enclosed is my contribution, *bli neder*.
