1036

[B"H]( #_ftn_1361), Motzaei Shabbos Kodesh, Parshas Shekalim,
Entering the day of Sunday, Parshas Terumah,
5732. Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Anash, and in particular to all those who belong to my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, who walk in his ways and follow his paths, and among them all those who cherish Torah and mitzvos,
May Hashem grant them life,

Greetings and blessings!

In addition to the general [letter]( #_ftn_1362) of two weeks ago, and as a continuation of its content, I hereby appeal to each and every one of Anash—those with whom my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, had a bond of affection, who studied his Torah, and who walked in his ways and paths—who, as stated, are surely doing so now as well,

And especially now, as we have just come from a day of spiritual potency, the yom hilula of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe,

With an inner appeal and request: to awaken with true hisorerus and the necessary energy to establish the educational institutions that were founded by him during his lifetime in this world, including those institutions founded subsequently in his name that are conducted in his spirit and according to his instructions. To establish them as much as is necessary and even more, with mesiras nefesh, and it goes without saying with physical exertion, and all the more so with their financial resources; and to add to them new educational institutions of the same nature wherever possible, and to establish, expand, and glorify them. [And surely]( #_ftn_1363) they will educate all their sons and all their daughters in these institutions—in the spirit and according to the Torah and instructions of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe.

It is understood that this does not, chas v'shalom, diminish the value and importance of the educational institutions of pure holiness of all our brethren, the Children of Israel. However, as the obligation of a student to his teacher (an obligation which is a privilege and a source of nachas for the teacher)—it is incumbent upon each and every one of Anash—in addition to activities on behalf of educational institutions of pure holiness in general—to strive specifically to establish the institutions of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, to expand them, and to educate their sons and daughters in these institutions,

Where they will surely succeed in their education and grow within them, [and go]( #_ftn_1364) from strength to strength,

And through all this, they will influence their surroundings, so that those who are close and friends, and even those who are currently distant, will see and do likewise.

And all of this with zerizus, etc.—as explained in the aforementioned letter, [and zerizus]( #_ftn_1365) leads to holiness, etc.

And as my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, requested and urged many times during his lifetime in this world—as is known and famous.

And surely my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, will arouse great compassion for all [those who act]( #_ftn_1366) and perform in the direction mentioned, regarding everything they and their families need, and in the most essential point—to see much true Chassidishe nachas from all their sons and daughters.

And in accordance [with the command]( #_ftn_1367) to ascend in holiness and with zerizus, may they hasten and increase the aforementioned activities, and whoever adds, is granted [an addition]( #_ftn_1368) that is greater than the main thing, immediately from Hashem’s [full]( #_ftn_1369), open, holy, and wide hand—and with zerizus, [until]( #_ftn_1370) His word runs swiftly.

With respect and blessing for great success in all the above,

**M. Schneerson**

1037

[B"H], 1st of Rosh Chodesh Adar, 5732
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the Honorable Dr. Zerach Warhaftig,

Greetings and blessings,

I acknowledge receipt of your letter dated the 26th of Shevat. After requesting your utmost forgiveness, I must say that I was surprised by its content, particularly by the beginning of the letter, in which you write that you view it as a "religious-moral obligation to set the record straight with truth and precision. Even when a dispute for the sake of Heaven rages regarding a certain situation and all the ways of dealing with it, one must guard the line of truth with all vigilance." Likewise, your conclusion mirrors the opening: "Even in times of dispute, it is a duty to know and to make known the legal and practical facts as they truly are."

After having reviewed all eight pages of your letter, I saw that the **main** point of the entire matter is **completely** absent from it. That point—to use your phrasing—concerns whether the [amendment] to the law is the root of all the problems, and whether, if it were only amended, everything would return to peace. The intention here, as is also proven by the continuation of your letter, is the amendment of the law by adding the definition "kehalacha" (conversion in accordance with Halacha), as well as regarding the rights granted to mixed couples, etc.

The main point in this, and the legal and practical fact—which, as mentioned, you did not touch upon at all in your letter—is that there is a clear *psak-din* from the Chief Rabbinate—and it must be emphasized that this *psak-din* was accepted unanimously—which determines the facts in an unequivocal manner. As has already been publicized, it states:

The Council of the Chief Rabbinate of Israel, in its session on the 5th of Erev Rosh Chodesh Sivan 5730, deliberated with gravity upon the dangerous situation that will arise if it is not explicitly emphasized in the law that the conversion must be *kehalacha*—a matter that will shake the entire House of Israel from one end of the world to the other, and will divide the people with a division the likes of which has not been seen since Ephraim departed from Judah—and it decided unanimously:

a. Any conversion performed, whether in the Land or abroad, that is not according to the law and the Halacha established and standing from Sinai until now, is not a conversion. A non-Jew does not become a Jew except through a conversion *kehalacha*.

b. It is forbidden according to the law of the Torah for the registrars of the population registry and those responsible for them to register a non-Jew as a Jew as long as they have not converted *kehalacha*.

c. The Chief Rabbinate appeals to the government with an urgent request to bring an amendment to the law in the Knesset by adding the word "kehalacha."

d. If, Heaven forbid, the law is not amended as above, the religious representatives must leave the government, for it is impossible to participate in the responsibility for this matter as members of the government.

The above concerns the beginning and end of your letter (the content of which was intended to explain that beginning and end).

2. Furthermore, and essentially, what must be added to this, following the aforementioned *psak-din*—which, according to my knowledge of the history of our people, the Children of Israel, in all periods, I have not found a similar case—is that they declare, with a loud voice and in the greatest publicity, that so-and-so is their authorized Rabbi and his authority must be accepted by each and every one, and upon this depends the survival of the religion, etc., etc. Yet, simultaneously with this declaration, and also publicly and openly, they act in complete opposition to the clear *psak-din* of that same authorized Rabbinate.

My meaning is simple: it refers to the aforementioned clause (d), which determines that it is impossible to participate in the responsibility for the matter, and therefore the religious representatives must (leave the coalition) and depart from the government. It also refers to clause (b), which forbids the clerks and those **responsible for them** to register a non-Jew as a Jew as long as they have not converted *kehalacha*.

3. What will you answer to the question: By what authority can you and your colleagues demand that the government heed religious demands, at the very same time that you yourselves violate the clear *psak-din* mentioned above, which was issued by the same Rabbinic authority whose office pays him a salary for his Rabbinic activities and engages in discussions regarding the details of the Rabbinate’s administration, etc.?

One could elaborate further on all that has been said, as well as on several points in your letter. But to my great sorrow, I have observed that if one adds anything, several people latch onto a secondary issue or even a detail that does not belong to the entire matter under discussion—despite the seriousness and vitality of the subject—just so that there might be a formal response, even if the response is in the category of "they argued about wheat and he admitted to barley," or even worse. As the well-known claim goes: how can a person who has never visited the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt, say what is written in the books regarding a specific matter in the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt?

I sign with great sorrow over the alarming situation, especially since, as is apparent from the content of your letter, you wish for the main point of this matter to be overlooked, "covering" it with discussions that, in the current situation, are not relevant at all.

May it be the will that, in your own style, each and every one will know the legal facts (and surely the *mishpat* of our Torah, the Torah of truth, is not inferior, Heaven forbid, to their idle chatter) and the practical facts as they truly are—the reality as it is: that there is a *psak-din* of the Rabbis in an unequivocal format, etc.

With respect and blessing.

P.S.
a. Surely it is also known to you regarding the rumor that certain circles close to you have been trying for some time to pressure the Chief Rabbinate regarding the above.

b. And likewise regarding the rumor that you called here to one of the directors of the office of the [Mazkeret HaMizrachi] here, after the decision of the Agudas HaRabbanim and the Rabbinical Council, **etc.**, regarding conversion *kehalacha*, and that their opinion is identical to the *psak-din* of the Chief Rabbinate, especially the aforementioned clause (d). Your argument was: how is it possible that such a decision was accepted and the activists of the Mazkeret HaMizrachi here did nothing? The results of this were that an advertisement was printed in a newspaper here stating that there is no necessity to leave the government, signed by "several" Rabbis and laymen without their knowledge at all. As it was clarified afterward, this was the **opposite** of their worldview (and that of the Mazkeret HaMizrachi in general) regarding the upholding of the *psak-din* of the Rabbinate, and clause (d) in particular, which must be upheld.

That is to say: they are introducing into the atmosphere of the Children of Israel **in the United States** three "inventions":

(a) That it is permitted for each and every one to rebel against a clear *psak-din* of his Rabbi, and even so, it will not harm his religious standing, etc.

(b) That it is possible to obtain signatures from people without their knowledge and in opposition to their worldview.

(c) That it is permitted to do this even in a matter connected to the faith and religiosity of these people, or in other words, to sign a person onto a viewpoint which, in his opinion, is a rebellion against the Torah he has accepted upon himself and against his conscience.

Surely for one such as yourself, there is no need to explain what the legal and practical side of the above is, in the style of your letter—and in a clearer style: the foundational point of the worldview of every believer, and all the more so of a people of believers, [children] of believers. *D'l* (a word to the wise is sufficient).

## 10 Shevat

[B"H](#_ftn_1380), 1st day of Rosh Chodesh Adar, 5732
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Mr. [Uri](#_ftn_1381) Tzvi Greenberg, may he live and be well,

Shalom u’vracha!

Following a long silence—even though I had requested in the interim that regards be conveyed to you, and I hope they were delivered in due time—I received the unpleasant surprise that your health is not as it should be. It is my hope that by the time you receive this letter, there is already improvement, and may it be His will that you continue to improve until your recovery is complete.

The merit of the many—whom you have the ability and power to bring closer to our Father in Heaven, the [Healer](#_ftn_1382) of all flesh who performs wonders—through the talent with which you have been gifted, and through which you have already demonstrated your strength and influence upon public opinion, and especially upon the select individuals among the public—will surely stand by you. May you continue and increase this work, with health, joy, and a good heart; for these have been strengthened and established through faith in the power of the Jewish people, a [wise](#_ftn_1383) and discerning nation. It is only that the yetzer finds many agents who entice, confuse, and obscure all values, especially the spiritual and eternal values of our people and our eternal Torah. Therefore, the task of the one who awakens is merely to remove the covering—in the style of the verse, a [stormy](#_ftn_1384) wind and a great cloud, etc.—which in truth possess no substance at all, just like darkness, which has no substance whatsoever and therefore is naturally repelled by light (Tanya, Chapter 29).

I look forward to hearing the pleasant news that your health is steadily improving in a satisfactory manner, especially as we enter the month in which we [increase](#_ftn_1385) in joy.

I sign with respect and blessing,

**M. Schneerson**

## 1029

 Rosh Chodesh Adar, 5732
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the Editorial Board of "Di Yiddishe Heim,"
May they live,

Blessings and peace!

I was pleased to receive the news regarding the special Adar-Nissan issue that will mark the 13th anniversary of "Di Yiddishe Heim."

On this occasion, I send my greetings and blessing to the members of the editorial board, as well as the contributors and readers—may they live. May Hashem Yisbarach help that this important organ should continue to fulfill its inner mission, and in an even greater scope, both in quantity and in quality.

In connection with the months of Adar and Nissan, the [Gemara] expresses: **"Connect one redemption to another."** This expression highlights the inner point of both months: the **redemption of Purim** and the **redemption of Pesach**.

As with all matters of Torah, which contain many instructions and allusions, so too with this mentioned expression, one of which lies in the very concept of **geulah**—redemption.

There are levels in geulah. The geulah of Purim saved the Jews from the decree to [destroy] and so on, in one day; however, that redemption was **limited** to that, for the Jews remained in galus ("We are still the servants of Achashverosh"). On the other hand, the geulah of Mitzrayim was a **complete** liberation, to the point that "the Children of Israel went out with a high hand."

In the expression **"Connect one redemption to another,"** there is also an indication that a Jew must know that every Jew has the power to elevate the geulah of Purim to the geulah of Pesach—that is, to transform a limited redemption (while Jews are still in galus) into a complete redemption. In other words: even when **externally**—in material and peripheral matters—a Jew is in galus, nevertheless **internally**—in essential matters, in all aspects of the life of the neshamah—he can be, and must be, completely free. This depends on him alone. And on the contrary, by bringing geulah into one's spiritual life, through Torah and mitzvos in daily life, he brings a geulah into his material life as well—liberation from decrees, from worries of parnassah, from worries regarding health, etc., etc.

Another common point in these two mentioned redemptions is the role of the Jewish woman and daughter, as our Sages, of blessed memory, express: **"They, too, were included in that miracle"** (Pesachim 108b), and as Rashi interprets on the spot: **"Through the merit of the righteous women of that generation, they were redeemed"** (Pesach)... **"Through Esther they were redeemed"** (Purim). This shows that women had an essential part in these redemptions.

A **practical** lesson from the above, as from all matters in [Torah]—Toras-Chayim (a guide for life)—is an instruction for daily life: even in the current galus, there exists the aforementioned possibility to be entirely free in all matters connected to Yiddishkeit. And also in this current generation of *Ikvesa D'Meshicha*—the final days of galus, on the eve of the geulah through Moshiach Tzidkeinu—women have an essential part in the general geulah of Klal Yisrael.

And we have the assurance that the conduct of righteous women, together and in tandem with the conduct of all Jews in the path of Torah and mitzvos, permeated with the light and vitality of Toras HaChassidus, will hasten and bring down the true and complete geulah through Moshiach Tzidkeinu.

With blessings for success and good tidings,

**M. Schneerson**

## 1040

B"H, 1 Adar, 5732
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the women and daughters of Israel from Georgia who are in our Holy Land,
May it be built and established by Moshiach Tzidkeinu,
May Hashem grant them life,

Blessing and peace!

It was a pleasure to receive your letter, in which you share the good news regarding the shiurim in Yiddishkeit in general, and in the laws of Taharas Hamishpacha in particular. May Hashem fulfill your hearts' desires for the good, and may you succeed in your learning—a [learning](#_ftn_1392) that leads to action—and in all the work of your hands for good and for blessing.

Surely you are aware of the words of Rabbi Akiva, that the mitzvah of [“Love](#_ftn_1393) your fellow as yourself” is a great principle of the Torah. This means that one should not be satisfied with one’s own personal achievement; rather, one must strive to ensure that one’s "fellow" also becomes "like you."

This is also related to the concept of the "half-shekel," for on the [first](#_ftn_1394) of Adar we make announcements regarding the shekalim. [As is explained](#_ftn_1395) in the allusion to this, a Jew on their own is only a "half," and only together with another Jew are they a complete whole. This is also one of the reasons [that "the rich](#_ftn_1396) shall not give more, and the poor shall not give less than the half-shekel."

It should be added that even one who considers themselves "poor"—whether in their own eyes or in reality—should not think, "What can I possibly do or accomplish for others?" For in matters of goodness and holiness, every man and woman, according to their own standing, can influence their entire environment—both through speech, and all the more so through a living example.

This is also emphasized in the Torah by the words ["in the shekel](#_ftn_1397) **of the Sanctuary**," for all the sons and daughters of Israel are holy seed, sons and daughters of a ["holy](#_ftn_1398) nation." This is unlike the opinion of those who err and lead others astray, who claim there are "religious" Jews and "non-religious" Jews. For in truth, all the sons and daughters of Israel are [believers](#_ftn_1399), the children of believers. It is only that there are some whose yetzer has led them astray due to various and strange reasons—in the vast majority of cases, external factors—but [their hearts are awake](#_ftn_1400) to Torah and mitzvos if only there is someone to awaken them in the appropriate manner.

May it be the will of Hashem that, since [when Adar enters](#_ftn_1401) we increase in joy, your joy may increase, and may the verse be fulfilled for you: ["For the Jews](#_ftn_1402) there was light, and gladness, and joy, and honor," in both material and spiritual matters alike.

With blessings for success, for good tidings, and for a happy Purim.

## 10,243

[5 Adar, 5732]

I read your letter with **great** astonishment. I have said many times, and **definitely** so, that my friends should **not** exert themselves to ensure that so-and-so visits me, and it goes **without saying** that they should not **pressure** them to take from their time and do a favor to those pressuring them (and a favor to me as well) by visiting me.

This is not a favor to those who are pressuring, nor is it a favor for the activities (the hope being that through a visit with me, the visitor will pledge a larger donation).

Since it is understood that I consider him among my friends, it is obvious that the aforementioned instruction applies to him as well.

The reason for this instruction is **understandable**: there is benefit in a visit with me when the visitor wishes to visit me **of his own accord**. But when he agrees to it because **so many** people (whom he views as my **shluchim**) each one prods him about it, and informs him that they are **telegraphing** me about it, and **telephoning** me about it, and **speaking** about it with my chief secretary, and doing so **many** times—then, as a polite person, he has **no choice and is compelled** to fulfill **my request** (as presented by these **many** shluchim), disrupting his own plans to visit me, **only so that they will not bother him further and will not bother his father, shlita, and his wife, tichyeh** (who, as you wrote in your letter, would be forced to travel from the pleasant climate of Bermuda to the cold and ice of New York) to fulfill the **requests and entreaties of my shluchim and friends in Manchester**.

[Even if there were no such **explicit** instruction—as a **public activist**, you surely would agree that **this activity is not desirable at all, and it does not** add honor to Lubavitch in Manchester or to Lubavitch in New York. And it is my hope and **request** that, as a public activist, you will explain all this **to all those whom you wrote** have started all this.]

Regarding his question of what he should answer to the aforementioned [Hubert, shlita]: The truth. And **in my name** (I have conveyed this to him [to Yaffa, shlita] so that he may convey it to Hubert, with the preface that those who spoke with him about visiting me did so **on their own initiative** and did not know about my schedule of visits here this winter; and when they informed me of this, I asked my chief secretary to call him in order to convey this to Hubert):

That I am **sorry** that even though he came to New York for only a few **hours**, they suggested he disrupt his plans and cause himself (and his wife, tichyeh) inconvenience to visit me in the dead of night, **etc., etc.** And although the intention of those who suggested it was good (out of their great hiskashrus to me and their Chassidishkeit), I rebuked them for taking advantage of his *eidelkeit* and his positive attitude toward Lubavitch to suggest such a thing and cause him trouble, etc. And I ask him **in my name** not to change his original plans **at all**, and not to travel to Brooklyn in the dead of night for a short conversation with me (especially in the current weather conditions).

And when it happens that he is in New York at a time that is more relaxed and in good weather, **and they will know about it in advance** (in order to reserve more time), and he wishes to visit me—it will certainly be a pleasure for me to meet him in person and to express (and through him, to his father, shlita) my gratitude for their assistance to the affairs of Lubavitch in England, *poh el poh*—assistance with their money and also through their encouragement, etc.

The above is **final**. And surely they will not pressure me further on this.

And also in the future—they should **not** pressure people to visit me (**not the aforementioned person**, nor others, and not the aforementioned person's father).

## 1070

1070

B"H, 16 Adar, 5732
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Your letter of 9 Shevat, along with its enclosure, reached me with some delay.

Furthermore, and most importantly, I have heard much about your brother’s activities regarding the settlement of Eretz Yisrael, our Holy Land, and especially for the benefit of those who have immigrated to our land from abroad.

I would add my hope that your brother, as well as you and all those working in this field, will strive to ensure that this immigration is in the sense of "aliyah" in both meanings of the word: an aliyah in spirituality as well, so that the people dwelling there may justly and proudly bear the title of a ["kingdom](#_ftn_1437) of priests and a holy nation." And I emphasize **proudly**, [in the words of the verse](#_ftn_1438): "And all the peoples of the earth shall see that the name of Hashem is called upon you, and they shall fear you." May the land be worthy of its name, that it be called the Holy Land, to the point that it is referred to as such by all nations—in Russian and the like.

With respect and blessing.

## 10,352

B"H, 16 Adar, 5732
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Mr. David Ben-Shushan, may he live and be well,

With blessings for success and for good tidings.

10,353

10,353

B”H, 16 Adar, 5732
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Dr. Chaim Chamiel,

Greetings and blessings,

Your letter regarding the campaign for children of Israel in the Diaspora to write a Sefer Torah in connection with a birthday reached me with some delay.

After requesting your forgiveness for the following words—which I am certain you will receive in the same spirit in which they are written—

Surely there is no need to explain the importance of the matter of writing a Sefer Torah in general, and especially by the children of Israel, and particularly in our current era. It is also understood that this is the most sublime gift in connection with a birthday, etc.

However, along with this, it is understood and also simple that there is no place at all to link the aforementioned campaign to conditions whereby only someone who accepts a certain viewpoint or a certain action—and all the more so a matter of a political party or the like—can participate in it.

And it makes no difference what the importance or value of the party or the worldview, etc., may be. Consequently, it is entirely irrelevant whether one accepts them one hundred percent, or ninety-nine percent, or does not accept them at all. For the principle here is that it is forbidden to link a campaign intended to instill love for our eternal Torah—which was given to every single man and woman of Israel—with a side issue. As our [Sages] of blessed memory stated, this is the reason that at the Giving of the Torah, the words were stated specifically in the singular: "I am Hashem **your G-d**," "who **brought you out**," "you shall have no [other gods] **before Me**," etc.

Therefore, when I became aware of the campaign and the manner of its actual execution—where it was announced at every opportunity that it is operated by such-and-such department of such-and-such organization—my reaction was in accordance with what is written above. However, based on the well-known [adage] that "one does not fight against advice," and especially since I learned of the matter after it had already begun, I adopted a stance of "sit and do nothing."

On the other hand, since I have received your letter regarding the matter, I no longer have the license not to express my reaction. In my opinion, it is connected to the importance of the matter itself, and also to the honor of the one whom they wish to cause nachas ruach—and even more than that, etc.—through the aforementioned campaign. Therefore, I have written these lines.

I would add that the intention here is not to withhold honor from those whose hearts were stirred to do good and who initiated the aforementioned campaign, whether the initiative came from a party, a department, or an individual associated with a department in a private capacity. Rather, my point is that while it would have been permissible to announce and publicize that the initiative for the campaign came from such-and-such organization or such-and-such person, the campaign itself should have been an entirely independent matter, without any connection to any other issue whatsoever, even the most sublime thing.

I am aware of the [statement] of our Sages of blessed memory that one does not cry out over the past. Nevertheless, I am writing the above because this is not a cry over the past, as it is possible that a similar matter may arise in the future. Furthermore, I wish to clarify my position on this, for the verse explicitly states, "And you shall be clean before Hashem and before Israel."

With respect and blessing.

10,358

B"H, 24 Adar, 5732
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Organization of Israeli Students in Bologna
May they live

Greetings and Blessings!

I was pleased to receive your letter of 21/2/72, as well as the telegram received prior to that.

(In addition to the report I received from Rabbi Yosef Weinberg after his visit with you, his farbrengen with you, and his impressions, etc.) I was also pleased to see from your letter your serious attitude toward Jewish values and your sincere efforts to advance in all of this. Following this, I am writing the following lines:

The great importance of youth has always been known, as an active force with special energy, which does not tend toward compromise, is not afraid of challenges, and aspires to tangible achievements, etc.—qualities in which young people particularly excel. This is as we have seen throughout the history of the Jewish people in general, and especially in the book of instruction for all sons and daughters of Israel in their path through life—I refer to our Torah, which is **Toras Chaim** (instruction for daily life) and **Toras Emes**.

If this is true in all places and at all times, it is all the more so in our current era, which is pregnant with confusion and the blurring of values, to the point where some say, [in the style of the Scripture](#_ftn_1459), that light is darkness and darkness is light.

Therefore, especially for those who come from our Holy Land to abroad and serve—whether they intend to or not—as an example of Israeli life and Israeli culture, their privilege, and along with it their responsibility, is many times greater.

Based on the above, it is also understood that if in every good and holy matter we are promised that Hashem, the Creator of the world and its Guide, assists in every good deed, good word, and even a good thought, then this is certainly true in the area and matters mentioned here, which involve a form of sanctification of the name of Eretz Yisrael, sanctification of the name of the Jewish people, and above all, sanctification of the name of the Torah of Israel.

Based on the [statement](#_ftn_1460) of the Sages that one only encourages those who are already diligent, it should be added that, as is customary in our world, every good thing and good endeavor is connected with difficulties, and one must overcome obstacles and delays, etc. But when taking into account the magnitude of the matter—and especially regarding our subject, which has implications in the place of the activity itself, and influence on the Jewish youth in the city where you are located, in the country, and even influence to a certain but important extent on Jewish youth in all countries and in Eretz Yisrael in particular—then what is the effort to overcome the difficulties compared to the magnitude and importance of the matter?

It is understood that one could elaborate on this further, but surely what is written here will suffice to bring about an increase in energy, initiative, and activities in this area.

May it be the will of Hashem that you do all of the above with vitality and enthusiasm—for these two are also the special qualities of young people—and may it be fulfilled in you [the teaching](#_ftn_1461) that one who has a maneh wants two hundred; one who has achieved two hundred wants four hundred (and is not satisfied with the addition of a single maneh). That is to say, the achievement in initial efforts should stir the desire and energy to achieve many times more. And we are promised in all of this: "You have labored and you have found."

With respect and with blessings for great success in all of the above, and for good tidings.

## 10362

[B"H], Erev Shabbos Kodesh, Mevarchim Chodesh Nissan, 5732
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the 30th Annual Gathering of the "Netzivei HaYeshiva" supporters of Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch in Montreal,
May Hashem keep them alive.

Peace and Blessing!

In these days that connect the months of Adar and Nissan, we stand under the impression of the common theme of both months — the concept of **Geulah**, the Geulah of Purim and the Geulah of Pesach.

One of the primary features that characterizes both Geulahs is the role of the chinuch of Jewish children.

The Geulah of Purim was—as [our] Sages of blessed memory relate—connected to the fact that Mordechai gathered Jewish children and taught them Torah, in a manner that awakened in them the greatest mesiras nefesh for Torah and mitzvos.

The Geulah of Pesach was also connected to Jewish children, against whom Pharaoh specifically aimed his decree: ["Every] son that is born, you shall cast into the river." But thanks to the [mesiras nefesh] of Jewish mothers, a new generation of children was raised, who were the first to recognize the Ribono shel Olam, proclaiming—**Zeh Keili**—"This is my G-d!"

If in those times, when the chinuch of Jewish children was connected to the greatest dangers, Jewish leaders and parents practiced mesiras nefesh for Torah-true chinuch, knowing that the existence of the Jewish people depended upon it—then all the more so when we live in circumstances that do not require a Jew to risk his life, Heaven forbid, but only a firm will and a readiness to give up a portion of his time, effort, and money for it. How gladly and happily a Jew should feel that he can—with a relatively small amount—accomplish so much!

And the main thing is that this chinuch should be in the spirit of Purim and Pesach—a Torah-true chinuch to the maximum degree, so that the younger generation will be able to say with the deepest conviction: **Zeh Keili**, **V'zos HaTorah**, and **Eileh HaChukim V'HaMishpatim**, and influence and inspire even those who are not yet in that state.

And this is indeed the chinuch that the Lubavitcher Yeshiva in Montreal gives its talmidim. It therefore deserves the fullest support of all friends of Torah, not only to free it from the burden of debt, but to give it the possibility to conduct its holy work with expansion, to magnify Torah and glorify it.

I greet all the participants in the gathering, especially the honored Netzivim and askanim, may they live, and I hope and wish to be certain that each and every one will do everything that depends on them, so that the undertaking will be with great hatzlacha in all respects.

With honor and blessing for hatzlacha and good tidings,

**M. Schneerson**

## 1063

1063

[B"H], Thursday, Rosh Chodesh Nissan, 5732
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the sons and daughters of Israel, wherever they may be,
May Hashem grant them life,

Greetings and blessings!

Pesach, the first and foremost of all Yomim Tovim, occupies a central place in Jewish life. The essence of this Yom Tov—the liberation and selection of the Jewish people to become a Torah-nation; the manner of this liberation: through open miracles, which confirmed clearly and unequivocally that the Ribono shel Olam is not only the Creator of the world, but also the *baal-habayis* of the world, and that Divine *hashgacha* reaches every detail and sub-detail of the entire creation—is indeed "the great foundation and firm pillar of our Torah and our faith." Therefore, we recall the concept of **Yetzias Mitzrayim** in our *tefillos* every day, and multiple times a day, so that these fundamental principles of our faith should illuminate and permeate our daily lives.

From this, it is understood that the Yom Tov of Pesach, in all its details, brings out essential and overarching themes that are connected to Yidden, Torah, and Yiddishkeit, and serve as fundamental guidelines in the daily life of the collective and the individual.

***

Torah, Yidden, and Yiddishkeit in general, as has been discussed many times, are not separate things—as if to say that a Yid connects with Torah and lives a Jewish life from time to time or at specific moments; rather, they are all **one** thing. In other words: in every detail of his being, both regarding his body and his *neshamah*, and in all details of his daily life, a Yid must be permeated with Torah and Yiddishkeit.

One of the points in this is: just as the Torah encompasses the entire world, and as our Chachamim, of blessed memory, express it, that the Torah is the Divine "blueprint" of the entire creation with all its particulars, so too a Yid, even as an individual, through his Torah-true life, has a connection to the entire world. This means that a Yid must strive and is capable of doing and accomplishing that not only he himself should be complete, but that the world, too, should be complete. And he does this directly and indirectly—through a full and uncompromising Torah life, showing thereby a living example of how one must conduct oneself in daily life, until he becomes "a light unto the nations" (*l'or goyim*)—an illuminator and guide also for all nations.

Knowing to what extent his personal conduct in daily life is relevant to his own completeness, to the completeness of his family, and to the entire Jewish people, up to the completeness of the entire world, gives special courage and *kochos* to overcome all difficulties; for what significance can his difficulties have in comparison to the achievements on such a scale?

***

If in different eras one had to seek and bring out in an open form the quality of a Yid as "a light unto the nations," this had to be openly and clearly illuminated at the time of the "birth" and beginning of the Yidden—*b'tzes Yisrael mi'Mitzrayim*—in a manner that would reach all nations and in a matter that encompasses their entire life.

At that time, Yidden were surrounded, as if swallowed up among the nations, and as the Torah says: "To take for Himself a nation from within a nation" (*lakach lo goy mikerev goy*); the Ribono shel Olam took the Jewish people out from within (*mikerev*) a nation that had the power and surrounded all nations.

And the first Divine command to the entire Jewish people, and then to every individual, right at the beginning of the month of redemption, Rosh Chodesh Nissan, was: "**Mashchu** u'kechu lachem tzon l'mishpechoseichem v'shichatu ha'Pesach"—"Draw [yourselves back from *avodah zarah*] and take for yourselves sheep for your families and slaughter the Pesach [offering]."

They were commanded to take a sheep, which was the *avodah zarah* of Mitzrayim, and which *avodah zarah* was then the foundation of the entire way of life in Mitzrayim and in the entire world, and to slaughter that *avodah zarah*.

And it was commanded to do this before everyone, in their eyes, so that all would know of it and ask. And the Yidden enlightened them.

With this, they also indicated to Yidden, and through them (as *or goyim*) to all nations, that a true redemption from physical enslavement must be connected with the redemption from spiritual enslavement.

***

Reflecting on the content of the Yom Tov of Pesach, every year when the days of preparation for Pesach arrive, and even more so during the days of Pesach itself, which is a "statute forever" (*chukas olam*) that you shall celebrate it for seven days—an eternal law that encompasses all seven days of the week, the total life of a Yid in every state in which he finds himself—

All the details of **Yetzias Mitzrayim** that a Yid must realize in life are refreshed, and in a strengthened form, the point of which is:

**Mashchu**—in the line of *sur me'ra* (turning away from evil)—rejecting every *avodah zarah*, and especially that which prevails in his time and his place.

**U'kechu lachem**—in the line of *aseh tov* (doing good)—not looking at how his previous way of life was, to take upon himself a new path, the path of true freedom, which is the path of Torah and *mitzvos* (*charus*—freedom—engraved upon the Tablets), and doing so openly and with pride, *b'yad ramah* (with a high hand), until this will have the deepest effect to transform the world around—*or goyim*.

And this leads to the *geulah peratis* (personal redemption), overcoming and freeing oneself from all difficulties that hinder the attainment of one's own completeness; and the **geulah peratis** becomes a preparation and a part of the **geulah klalis** (collective redemption), the complete and true redemption of the entire Jewish people, when the entire world will receive its true and complete *tikkun*, in the line of *mashchu*—to remove idols from the earth, and in the line of *kechu*—that the prophecy will be fulfilled: "And nations will walk by your light,"

At the time when "Hashem will shine upon you and His glory will be seen upon you,"

With the coming of Mashiach Tzidkeinu—and according to the prayer of Dovid Melech Yisrael, the sweet singer of Israel, in the name of all Yidden and of every Yid: "Hashem, hasten to my aid... Elokim, hasten to me"—

Immediately, in our days, literally.

With blessings for a kosher and happy Pesach,

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 10,365

10,365

B"H, 4 Nissan, 5732
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letters: It is understood that it is impossible from here to mediate the differences of opinion between the *anash* *shluchim* *shiy* in the Holy City [Jerusalem], as it requires hearing all the arguments, opinions, and responses, etc.

Therefore, they must—on the spot—strive to speak with one another as much as possible. Regarding matters where they cannot reach a single consensus, they should strive to divide the tasks among themselves. And it goes without saying that each one should have a "good eye" and take pleasure in the success of his fellow in his own activities.

When it is impossible, for whatever reason, to enroll a student or a new immigrant in the *Chabad* vineyard, it is obvious that one should assist them in being enrolled in other *chareidi* institutions.

**It is obvious** that every activity regarding *yiras shamayim* and *Torah u’mitzvos*, etc., etc., is good and necessary. However, as I have written previously, **they must not incur debts**. This has already happened with others, etc., and they were, G-d forbid, badly burned, and their loss outweighed their gain, etc., and a word to the wise is sufficient.

[Likewise,](#_ftn_1496) *anash* *shiy* should not join political parties. And a word to the wise is sufficient.

With blessings for success in the holy work,

**M. Schneerson**

It is surely unnecessary to point out what I have written regarding "in the multitude of counselors there is safety," and as our Sages, of blessed memory, said in their teachings, "Do not judge alone, for there is no sole judge but One."

## 11 Nissan, 5732
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the sons and daughters of Israel everywhere,
May Hashem grant them life,

Greetings and blessings!

Standing on the eve of the Yom Tov of Pesach—the Yom Tov that marks the "birth" and the beginning of the Jewish people—the thought is awakened to reflect: What should be the life-path of this people, and how should it be lived, in order to most swiftly and effectively reach the purpose and goal of its existence?

This is a broad and multifaceted subject, and we will pause here to consider only one point: Should the people strive for a life with a minimum of effort and a maximum of satisfaction? Or should life be one of toil and maximum achievement—a life of doing **much** and accomplishing much?

This question applies equally to the individual in his own life.

It is superfluous to note that this is not an abstract question, for the resolution of this issue lies at the foundation of how a person conducts his life, and how he reacts to what happens to him and around him—even in matters that are not directly dependent on him, and certainly in matters that are directly connected to him.

***

On the surface, and based on our faith and our Torah—*Toras Chaim* and *Toras Emes*—that the Creator and Guide of the world, and of this *olam katan* (small world) which is man, is *etzem* **HaTov** (Goodness itself) and that *teva hatov leheitiv* (the nature of the Good is to do good), it would seemingly stand to reason that the greatest perfection is when one receives maximum *taanug*—*taanug amiti*—without any difficulties or hardship. In that state, one sees the "nature of the Good to do good" in its fullest measure.

Despite this, however, the Torah—which is *Torah*—*ohr* (illuminating), states: **"Adam le'amal yulad"**—"Man is born to toil." Even Adam HaRishon, before the sin of the Tree of Knowledge, had his existence in Gan Eden established as: *le'ovdah u'leshomrah* (to work it—the Gan Eden—and to guard it).

The explanation for this, which resolves this apparent contradiction, is also given in the Torah:

Precisely because the Ribono shel Olam desires that a person should enjoy the good *beshlimus* (in perfection), and the nature of a person is such that he experiences true *taanug* only when he becomes a "partner" in the accomplishment and achieves it through his own toil and hardship—on the contrary, if he receives it as a gift, it is actually a degradation for him, and this is called *nahama dekesufa* ("bread of shame")—therefore, the perfection of *taanug* is when he achieves it specifically through toil. The greater the toil, the more delicious the fruit of the achievement.

***

So it was at the birth of the Jewish people. The order of *Yitziyas Mitzrayim* was as the Ribono shel Olam said to Moshe Rabbeinu: *Behotziacha es ha'am mimitzrayim ta'avdun es HaElokim al hahar hazeh* ("When you take the people out of Egypt, you will **serve** the Ribono shel Olam on this mountain [Sinai]"). Even though *Yitziyas Mitzrayim* itself was a matter of a gift from Heaven, occurring through wondrous and open miracles, it was nevertheless connected from the outset with *ta'avdun* (serving as an *eved*) *es HaElokim*. This was the merit of the **am** (people), their participation in the *behotziacha es ha'am mimitzrayim*.

***

And as this is regarding *Klal Yisrael*, so it is with every individual. The striving of the individual must be that he should do and accomplish; and not merely do, but do with a toil that *Toras Emes* calls "amal." Only then does he elevate himself from the level of "Adam—dust from the earth" to the level of "Adam—resembling, *kivayachol*, the One Above."

***

The birth and life of an individual are also connected with miracles. Even when it appears that everything is "by way of nature," our Sages of blessed memory have said: **"Ein ba'al haneis makir beniso"**—a person does not recognize the miracle that has occurred for him. Therefore, we thank the Ribono shel Olam three times a day *al nisecha sheb'chol yom imanu* (for Your miracles which are with us every day).

And as Dovid, *ne'im zemiros Yisrael* (and King of Israel), says in the name of every Jew (and in the name of *Klal Yisrael*): *Mime'ai imi atah gozi... kemofes hayisi larabim... avo bigvuros... ve'ad hena agid niflosecha... techayeni.* ("From my mother's womb You have drawn me out"—the **Midrash** says this means (also) *Klal Yisrael*: You took us out of the hand of Egypt—"I have been a wonder to many"—(Midrash: how many miracles You have done for me)—"I will enter with the mighty deeds"—"and until now I will tell of Your wonders"—(Midrash: in every period, time, and moment)—"You will revive me"—(Midrash: take me out of exile)."

This means that the entire life of a person, from birth—and of *Am Yisrael*—is in a state of constant miracles, even if one does not always see it, until the miracle of the *Geulah* *amitis* and *sheleimah* of the individual and of the entire *Am Yisrael*.

And through our *ma'aseinu* **va'avodaseinu** throughout the duration of the exile—the day-to-day life of the individual and of the collective according to the Ribono shel Olam's instruction—the ultimate perfection of the entire world is accomplished,

The *Geulah* *amitis* *vehasheleimah* through Mashiach Tzidkeinu, immediately, when it will be fulfilled:

*Kimiy tzeischa me'eretz Mitzrayim areinu niflaos* (As in the days of your exodus from the land of Egypt, I will show you wonders).

With blessings for a kosher and happy Chag HaPesach,

**M. Schneerson**

## 1083

 Rosh Chodesh Iyar, 5732
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To all participants in the annual dinner
For the educational institution "Oholei Torah"
May Hashem protect them and may they live

Greetings and blessings!

I was pleased to receive the news regarding the upcoming annual celebration on the 16th of Iyar, may it be Hashem's will that it should be with the greatest success in all respects.

 The month of Iyar, as has been discussed previously, is distinguished from the other months of the year in that every day of this month has a special mitzvah – the mitzvah of Sefiras HaOmer.

In connection with this, it is worthwhile to emphasize two points:

First, that although in certain respects there is a difference between the days of the week and the month—weekdays, Shabbos, Erev Rosh Chodesh, Rosh Chodesh, etc.—they are all equal in that **all** days, without exception, must be filled with holiness—the holiness of Torah and mitzvos in all the details of daily life. This is emphasized in the blessing of Sefiras HaOmer **every day** of this month: "Who has sanctified us with His mitzvos and commanded us."

Second, although one has already fulfilled the mitzvah the previous day, one fulfills the mitzvah the second day, and the third day, and every day—with the **same** preciousness and vitality as the first time. On the contrary, every day there must be an addition in the vitality and enthusiasm of the fulfillment of the mitzvah. And so it is in all matters of Torah and mitzvos, in accordance with the command: **"Every day they should be in your eyes as new"**—every day a Yid must receive them as if they were just given at Mount Sinai.

In other words, fulfilling the mitzvos in daily life, day in and day out, must not become a *mitzvos anashim melumada*—a habit without *chayus* and enthusiasm. On the contrary, every day one must experience it more deeply and on a higher level, in accordance with the command: **"We ascend in matters of holiness."**

It is understood that in order to reach this level, a child must receive his Torah-true education from the earliest childhood, in an educational institution and environment that are permeated with *yiras Hashem* and *ahavas Hashem*. Then the promise is fulfilled: **"Educate the child according to his way; even when he grows old, he will not depart from it."**

And this brings us back to the educational institution "Oholei Torah," whose task is to provide the correct Torah education, as mentioned above, and which, *b"H*, has had great success in this. Surely all participants and friends of this most important educational institution will give it their fullest support, with a generous hand, to enable it to continue and expand its educational activities. And this merit will stand for each and every one to receive the Ribono shel Olam's blessings in everything one needs, both materially and spiritually.

With respect and blessing for success and good tidings,

**M. Schneerson**

## 1075

[2 Iyar, 5732]

I will mention at the holy gravesite that it should be with great success.

A **primary** note – the purpose of all the above is **actual implementation**, as is obvious and simple. Based on this, it is also simple that the decision must not be merely to make various decisions, but rather – and this is **the main thing** – that they are for the purpose of fulfilling them in actual practice. And this is what is meant regarding oneself, quite simply – not as a way of preaching morality to **someone else**, but to do it oneself, [as the](#_ftn_1571) Mishnah says: they do (so much so that it is) much (compared to what they decided and) said.

And in order for the above to be brought into **actual implementation** – once a month a committee appointed for this purpose shall gather to "collect" a report **on the actual implementation** (and not to accept "good" excuses).

**And we are promised** regarding the above, that one who comes to purify himself is **assisted**.

And may it be the will [of Hashem] that all this comes to fruition in action.

## 1088

1088

B"H, 10 Iyar, 5732
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Mr. Yosef Zeira, Lieutenant Colonel, may he live,

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from 27 Nissan, regarding the *avreich*... It appears there are some unclear details here.

The question from the outset was that since, according to the law, he is exempt from military service, and his dilemma is purely a matter of livelihood, the consideration was—as I recall—that if he were to enter the IDF as a civilian, he would be able to spend Shabbos at home with his family, which would not be the case if he were to enter the IDF as a soldier. Based on my knowledge of him and his family, my opinion was that his being with his family on Shabbos is more important than the financial gains.

On the other hand, if his material situation is such that the financial gain carries more weight, then he must calculate the profit and loss and decide for himself what he prefers.

Since everything is by *hashgacha pratis*, including the letter from Mr. Eli, I wish to express the personal satisfaction I felt in reading in your letter that you, as his commander, commit yourself not to bring him to a violation of Shabbos or Yom Tov, and on the contrary, etc. Although I had assumed this from the start—especially following my conversation with the Chief Rabbi of the IDF, Rabbi M. Piron, may he live, when he honored me with a visit here—it is understood that when one receives such a "commitment" from the commander himself, filled with sincerity and heartfelt emotion, it causes special *nachas ruach*.

May it be the will of Hashem that the promise of our holy Torah, the Torah of truth, be fulfilled for you and your colleagues, may they live, within the entirety of the IDF: "Hashem your G-d walks in the midst of your camp, and your camp shall be holy", and may we soon merit the fulfillment of the prophecy: "And I will grant peace in the land, and you shall lie down, and none shall make you afraid... and no sword shall pass through your land".

With respect and blessings for success.

## 10th of Iyar

By the Grace of Hashem
10th of Iyar, 5732
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Rabbi Yitzchak Chalmish, may he live and be well
Deputy Military Rabbi, IDF

Greetings and blessings,

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter dated the 27th of Nissan. Enclosed is a copy of my letter to Mr. Yosef Zeira, Lieutenant Colonel, which speaks for itself.

On this occasion, I would like to express once again the satisfaction I derived from Mr. Yosef Zeira’s letter, especially since its content will certainly facilitate your fulfillment of your duties as a military rabbi.

[As has been discussed on various occasions,](#_ftn_1581) it is precisely the military framework that prepares military personnel for precision in observing the Torah and its mitzvos. After all, one of the foundations of the military is the acceptance of the yoke and the fulfillment of orders in the manner of "we will do" preceding "we will hear," and the rejection of the approach that an individual’s conduct is a private matter that does not affect the many—let alone the entire Jewish people—despite the declaration of our Sages that all of Israel are responsible for one another. For this, too, is among the foundations of the military’s existence: that a deviation from the precise fulfillment of the commander’s order is liable to endanger, Heaven forbid, the position of the entire company, or even the entire army, and ultimately the nation that the army protects. Furthermore, the decision in this matter does not belong to the one fulfilling the order at all, but rather to those who have invested their best efforts, energy, and time in studying the tactics of war, etc. The analogy is understood regarding the study of Torah with exertion, [of which it is said](#_ftn_1584) that it is your wisdom and your understanding.

With respect and blessings,

1091

13 Iyar, 5732
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Mr. Gad Yaacobi,

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter, which brings the good news of your recovery and that you have already returned to your work. Although I inquire about and receive updates regarding you from our mutual friends, and particularly from our friend Mr. Shlomo Madjincik, it is not the same as receiving a direct update.

Since there is always room to increase in goodness—as the source of all goodness is the Ein Sof, blessed be He—may it be His will that your recovery be truly complete. You will surely utilize your talents for the benefit of the many with even greater intensity, and the merit of the many will assist you.

In the manner of the Jewish people, who find joy in a play on words, since your position is that of Deputy Minister of Transportation, may it be His will that you contribute your share with a generous eye to connect the segments of the Jewish people who are in need of closeness and connection—those you write about in your letter: the various ethnic communities, the veteran settlers and the new immigrants, and the secular and the religious. If every energetic person is compelled by their nature to utilize their energy, this is all the more true in the areas which, to use your phrasing in your letter, you are concerned about, or in an even sharper expression, which "are our very life."

Here I have the opportunity to dwell on the expression in your letter, which is repeated in several places—an expression that has always aroused my wonder—I refer to the contrast of "secular and religious." For the concept of *chol* (secular/profane) has as its opposite *kodesh* (holy). My intention is not merely for the sake of grammatical precision, but primarily for precision in substance. Based on the source in our language, the Lashon HaKodesh (in our Torah, the Written Torah and its explanation in the Oral Torah, down to these days), the standard expression is *yemos hachol* (the weekdays) and *Shabbos-Kodesh* (the holy Shabbos). From this, the content is also understood: there is no difference in beliefs, opinions, worldview, etc., between the weekdays and the holy Shabbos, but only in the **conduct** of the weekdays—in the language of the Talmud, *ovdin d'chol* (weekday activities)—and the conduct on the day that is holy for true rest of the soul and for cessation from physical labor, and certainly from materialism, when a person naturally dedicates their time to spiritual matters and to spiritual life in general.

I was pleased to see that you included all three of the aforementioned areas together. This is also from my own worldview: just as the division between ethnic communities is artificial and caused by external conditions—and therefore touches only the external part of life, but does not change the inner essence—so too is it regarding the veteran settlers and the new immigrants. And (to me) it is simple that this is also the case regarding what you call "secular and religious."

Everyone admits, and recently even those standing at the head of the government (in the discussion on religion and state at the "Labor" center), the necessity of religion for the existence of the Jewish people at all times, and now as well. Even though some things were said at that same event—and sharp things, at that—against religious people, that is not the innovation in the aforementioned discussion; rather, it is the principled admission of the necessity of religion for the existence of the Jewish people and for the existence of Eretz Yisrael. And if even the Labor center admits this, surely all other parties are of this opinion.

Another point on the matter, which has already been said and repeated several times: for a religious person to behave as a secular person is against their conscience, whereas for a secular person to behave as a religious person, it is merely against their convenience. Furthermore, and this is also essential: when there is a difference of opinion between a party that has a majority in the Knesset and a party that is in the minority, there is no danger for the majority party to concede more than it feels is right, for this does not affect its position (as the majority party). This is not the case regarding the minority party, whose concession could lead to deterioration, etc., etc.

I will admit the truth: what is written above is not my primary approach, especially in my relationship with you. The primary thing is that I believe in every Jewish man and woman who, in the language of our Sages, are "believers, the children of believers." It is just that due to secondary and external reasons, as mentioned above, some of them observe mitzvos in all their details, and some of them—for the time being—observe some of the mitzvos. And even the one who emphasizes that they only observe mitzvos whose foundations are in logic and between man and his fellow, etc., etc.—at the moment of performing that mitzvah, they suddenly feel in their soul that this is their connection with their father, their grandfather, and their great-grandfather, and this is their connection with all our people, the children of Israel, wherever they may be, from the days of old, starting from the Exodus from Egypt and the Giving of the Torah at Mount Sinai. At that time, Hashem "took for Himself a nation from within a nation" with trials, signs, and wonders, and declared regarding it, "And you shall be to Me a treasure more than all the peoples," etc., "And you shall be to Me a kingdom of priests and a holy nation." Just as a person is not master over their essence, but only regarding action, speech, and thought—the external *levushim* (garments) upon the soul—so too is it regarding our people, who from the day they left the land of Egypt were declared by the Creator of the world to be a holy nation. And this announcement, this declaration, and this proclamation relate not only to the nation as a whole, but also to each one as an individual.

In other words, I do not believe there is any of the sons and daughters of Israel who is "secular" in the sense used today—that is, a secular reality—for they are a child and a part of a holy nation. Rather, there are those among them who are occupied with matters of *chol*, there are those who are occupied with matters of *kodesh*, and there are those who are occupied, in the well-known phrasing, with *chulin* (mundane matters) on the purity of *kodesh*.

I have written more than I initially intended, but the style of your letter encouraged me to do so. And by way of wit, may it be His will that what is written above also helps to increase the "transportation" between all parts of our people, the children of Israel, who in truth are one nation in the land.

With respect and with blessings for a complete recovery,

**M. Schneerson**

P.S. I would like the letter to reach you directly, therefore it is being sent via our aforementioned friend.

## 1092

[b"h], Pesach Sheni, 5732
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the 17th Annual Convention of N'shei U'bnos Chabad,
May Hashem grant them life,

Blessings and peace!

I was pleased to receive the news regarding the upcoming annual convention, Shabbos Mevarchim Chodesh Sivan. May it be His will that it be successful in every respect.

In recent weeks, it has come up to mention several times [the verse] that Dovid Hamelech said in the name of every Jew, man and woman, and in the name of Klal Yisrael:

**"I have been as a wonder unto many, but You are my strong refuge"** (Tehillim 71:7).

One of the points here is that every Jew as an individual, and the Jewish people as a nation, in addition to the personal perfection they must achieve, bear a responsibility for the surrounding world and must serve as a **"wonder unto many"** (*mofes larabim*).

Seemingly, one might think: How can a small nation serve as a model and inspiration for the entire world, when the world is so immersed in physicality and is impressed by quantity more than by quality? And a Jew, a *shomer* Torah and *mitzvos*, might think the same: How can I, an individual among the many, accomplish anything?

The answer to this is found in the same verse: **"But You are my strong refuge"** (*v'atah machsi oz*). Jews go with the strength of the Almighty, and with the powers they receive from the Divine Torah and *mitzvos*.

In this sense, [our Sages] of blessed memory tell us that when the Almighty gave the Torah to the Jews at Mount Sinai—in the desert of Sinai, isolated from the entire world—the Ten Commandments nevertheless resounded in all corners of the world and shook all the nations. They were calmed, however, when they learned the reason for this: that Hashem had given the Torah to the Jews. Then they said: **"Hashem will give strength unto His people; Hashem will bless His people with peace"** (Tehillim 29:11)—"Since Hashem gives strength (the Torah) to His people, Hashem will bless His people with peace."

This emphasizes that the power which Jews receive through the Divine Torah is not a brutal power to dominate the nations, but on the contrary, the Torah brings peace to the world—peace for the individual, peace for the collective, and will ultimately bring peace among the nations as well.

In the present time, when there is tremendous confusion and *bilbul hamochos*, the [voice]—*kol Yaakov*—the clear call of Torah and *mitzvos*, must resound loudly wherever Jews who are *shomrei* Torah and *mitzvos* are found.

And just as at *Matan Torah*, when the Almighty instructed Moshe Rabbeinu to speak [first] to the women ("Beis Yaakov") and then to the men ("Bnei Yisrael"), so too today, Jewish women have a very important role in the maintenance and dissemination of Torah and *mitzvos* in daily life. Especially considering that when it comes to influence—being a **"wonder unto many"**—a warm feeling has a stronger resonance than cold intellect, and women are, after all, gifted with a greater measure of feeling and tenderness than men.

Since the annual convention is taking place on Shabbos Mevarchim Chodesh Sivan, the month of *Matan Torah*, everyone will surely stand under the impression of these days, as mentioned above. In this spirit, an expanded and strengthened activity of N'shei U'bnos Chabad will surely be formed, with renewed and increased strength.

With blessings for success in *ruchniyus* and *gashmiyus*, and for good tidings in all the above,

**M. Schneerson**

1039

[B"H], Pesach Sheni, 5732
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the 17th Annual Convention of N'shei U’Bnos Chabad
May Hashem grant them life

Blessings and greetings!

It was with pleasure that I received the news regarding the annual convention to be held on Shabbos Mevarchim the month of Sivan. May it be the will of Hashem that it be successful in both material and spiritual matters alike.

Recently, the [verse] that Dovid Hamelech said in the name of every individual Jew and in the name of the entire Jewish people has been mentioned several times:

**"I have been as a wonder unto many, but You are my strong refuge"** ([Tehillim] 71:7).

One of the points here is that every individual Jew, and our people, the Children of Israel, as a nation, in addition to the perfection they must achieve for themselves, have a responsibility toward their environment and must serve as a **"wonder unto many"** (a model for the many).

On the face of it, one might think: How can a small nation, [the fewest] of all peoples, be a model and example to all the inhabitants of the world, at a time when the world is so immersed in materialism and is more impressed by quantity than by quality? Similarly, a Jew who observes Torah and mitzvos might think: How can I, one individual among many, accomplish anything at all?

The answer to this is found at the end of the aforementioned verse: **"But You are my strong refuge."** This means that a Jew does not act on his own strength, but through the strength of the Ribono shel Olam and through the power and might from Above that he receives through the Torah of Hashem and the mitzvos of Hashem.

This concept is also alluded to in the [story of our Sages, of blessed memory], that when the Ribono shel Olam gave the Torah to His people Israel at Har Sinai, in the wilderness of Sinai—when they were separated from the entire world—the Ten Commandments were heard from one end of the world to the other, until all the nations were shaken. But when they understood the matter—that the Ribono shel Olam was giving the Torah to His people Israel—their minds were put at ease, and they then declared: **"Hashem will give strength to His people; Hashem will bless His people with peace."** That is to say, since Hashem gave the Torah, which is called "strength" (oz), to His people, surely Hashem will bless His people with peace.

This emphasizes that the power and strength which the Children of Israel receive from the Torah of Hashem is not a matter of "[my power] and the might of my hand" or a desire to dominate the nations. On the contrary, the Torah brings peace to the world—peace to the individual and peace to the collective—and ultimately, it will bring peace among the nations of the world as well.

In our current era, a time of blurred values and confusion of mind, it is incumbent upon [the voice]—the voice of Yaakov, the voice of Torah and mitzvos—to be heard with force, a great, mighty, and strong voice, in every place where those who observe Torah and mitzvos are found.

And just as it was then, at the time of the giving of the Torah, when the Ribono shel Olam commanded Moshe Rabbeinu to address [first] the women of Israel ("Beis Yaakov") and only afterward to speak to the men ("Bnei Yisrael"), so too now, the women and girls of Israel have a most important role in upholding the Torah and spreading the Torah and its mitzvos in daily life. Especially when considering that the matter at hand is influence—being a **"wonder unto many"**—the warm emotion is more effective than cold intellect. And women, in general, are gifted with more sensitivity and heart-felt emotion than men.

Since the annual convention will take place on Shabbos Mevarchim the month of Sivan, the month of the giving of the Torah, surely all the participants will be under the impression of these auspicious days, as mentioned above. In this spirit, the firm resolution to strengthen and expand the scope of the activities of N'shei U’Bnos Chabad with renewed and ever-increasing strength will be expressed.

With blessings for success in spiritual and material matters, and for good tidings regarding all the above,

**M. Schneerson**

[B"H](#_ftn_1624), 16 Iyar, 5732
