10-166

By the Grace of Hashem, Lag B’Omer, 5732
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the distinguished Rabbi [Zarach]—may he live—known as Dr. Warhaftig,

Shalom u’Bracha,

I acknowledge receipt of your letter dated 12 Nissan, along with the enclosed documents, which arrived with a delay. Thank you.

Regarding the content of your letter, and its opening, you refer to my previous letter where I stated that "the main point, and the legal and practical fact... is that there is a clear *pask din* from the Chief Rabbinate." In response to this, you send photocopies of letters, etc. Seemingly, the implication is that through this, it will be clarified that the conduct regarding registration, participation in the coalition, etc., is in order and just, etc.

I doubt whether it is your intention to enter into an argument for the sake of argument, for the goal is to clarify matters according to their truth. As mentioned above, the legal and practical fact is connected to a clear *pask din* of the Chief Rabbinate. You will forgive me, but I must say that the addition of these photocopied letters has only increased the bewilderment and the difficulty, to put it mildly. Let me explain:

1. When you and your colleagues—may they live—the world center of the [Mizrachi-Hapoel Hamizrachi] (= [Mafdal]) publish the aforementioned photocopies, this is a publication confirming that at the time, there was a clear *pask din* of the Chief Rabbinate, and that this *pask din* reached the ministers to whom the *pask din* refers. That is to say, they knew about this *pask din*, and specifically about section 4 within it. The conclusion from this is that all those who **denied with force** (the emphasis is that of the Mafdal newspaper, based on my recollection) that such a *pask din* existed, and later claimed that they did not receive it—meaning it did not reach them—the aforementioned *pask din*—well, now the Mafdal and all its representatives and leadership are publishing that **they did not speak the truth**. Certainly, every public activist (and his party) should draw the conclusions from this, all the more so when the matter concerns not just any public, but a religious public, where a matter of *Kiddush Hashem* or its opposite is involved.

And what are the conclusions? Surely you are aware of the debate in the Knesset regarding the [Foreign Minister], where someone accused him of saying something in the name of a person from the U.S., and the latter denied the words. The debate was not what the conclusion should be, but only whether the accusation was based in fact or not.

2. The photocopied letters speak only regarding the fourth section of the *pask din*, namely—participation in the coalition. This means that the Mafdal and its representatives are publishing that the other sections remain in force, among them a **clear *pask din***, which states: "b) It is forbidden according to the law of the Torah for those who register the population registry and those responsible for them, to register a non-Jew as a Jew while they have not converted according to *halacha*." ["Whether in Eretz Yisrael or abroad" (there, section 1)].

And the practical fact in the current situation is, as has been publicized many times in the newspapers and also in the Knesset, that non-Jews are being registered as Jews even though they have not converted according to *halacha*. [The debate is whether this practice is only regarding abroad, or also in Eretz Yisrael, where an official has no authority to investigate and ask about this].

That is to say, the Mafdal is publishing that anyone who acts in opposition to the aforementioned section 'b' of the *pask din* is violating a clear *pask din* of the Chief Rabbinate, and nevertheless does so with full knowledge. In other words—a self-contradiction.

And I repeat and emphasize that the publication means that someone is publishing that the aforementioned section remains in force, yet he continues with the registration as it was until now despite this *pask din*, and requests the branches of the Mafdal in Eretz Yisrael and abroad to publicize this conduct of his as well.

3. The *pask din* of the Chief Rabbinate was accepted unanimously by the members of the entire Council. Surely for someone like you, who is an attorney, and as I have heard, also holds *semicha* for the Rabbinate, there is no need for any explanation that no individual, whoever he may be, has the power to nullify this *pask din*. Furthermore, one cannot even interpret it in a matter of principle without the participation of those who issued the *pask din*, who must express their opinion and publish it in the same manner as the *pask din* was published. The matter is so simple that one does not need clarification from a Rabbi or an attorney, for it is also simple common sense that one partner, or a portion of the partners, cannot nullify a decision of all the partners, all the more so a decision that was accepted unanimously.

I do not wish to enter into a debate regarding the letters themselves, as they are not your letters, nor are you responsible for them. In any case—since you are one of those publishing them and encouraging others to publish them, I will dwell at least on one point in the photocopy of the letter from 11 Nissan, which states: "We expressed our opinion this way, among other things, because at that time a question of immediate recognition of a conversion performed not according to *halacha* was pending for immediate decision."

And this is the text of the aforementioned *pask din*, in its fourth section: "d) If, *chas v'shalom*, the law is not amended as above, the religious representatives must leave the government, for it is not possible to participate in the responsibility for the matter as members of the government."

This is a clear *pask din*—the ruling itself and the condition for the existence of the ruling or its nullification: one condition and nothing more—amending the law as above. And in the entire *pask din*, from beginning to end, there is no mention of an "immediate decision," etc., but only the amendment of the law.

And it should be noted that in the photocopy of the second letter from 6 Nissan, it is also emphasized twice that the *pask din* depends only on the amendment of the law, and there is no mention at all of an "immediate decision," etc.

I bring the above only as a remark, for as mentioned regarding a final *pask din* of the Council of the Chief Rabbinate, it is not in the power of an individual or even several individuals to change it, as stated above.

To summarize the above: The practical and legal fact even now—as it was at the time of my previous letter—is that there is a clear *pask din* of the Chief Rabbinate, which now even the Mafdal and its representatives and its leadership admit publicly, except that they add that there are letters from individuals regarding the fourth section of it, and one letter contradicts the other. In any case, these are letters from individuals, and the content of the letters themselves confirms once again that there is a final *pask din* of the Rabbinate with their participation.

What must be added to this, after asking your forgiveness, is that anyone who publishes these photocopies of letters is not causing the honor of the Chief Rabbinate to be raised, nor the prestige of religion in general, for all the points listed above are understandable and simple to the eyes of all. And the explanation given for how the situation evolved in this matter until the publication of the aforementioned letters is well-known.

In conclusion of your letter, which mentions that there are rumors and reports that are sometimes far from the truth, etc., I can assure you that before I speak in public about a rumor without prefacing that it is merely a rumor, I check the rumor very thoroughly in all possible ways. Thank G-d, until now **all** the rumors that I checked were proven to have been checked properly. And in this matter itself: when I said there is a clear *pask din*, and they denied it with force, it was proven as above; when I said that the *pask din* was sent to so-and-so, and they denied that too, it was proven as above, etc.

Regarding the matter you write about—that they pressured a famous Rabbi in connection with an apartment, etc.—at the time, the pressure reached such a point that a certain landlord, whom I know personally (an enthusiastic friend of the Rabbi—and he also confirmed the matter), offered and was ready to buy the apartment with full payment in order to nullify the pressure.

With respect and blessing.

P.S. I did not want to include the following above for several understandable reasons.

a) I saw a debate in the press that the religious ministers did not pressure regarding the apartment. What I said, and I repeat once again, is that the representatives of the Mafdal pressured.

I also know the name of the one who started this pressure, a member of the presidium of the Mizrachi-Hapoel Hamizrachi, but I see no benefit in naming him, since you surely know this as well.

b) Regarding what you wrote in your letter about the relationship throughout the two years between the Chief Rabbinate and the ministers, etc.:

(1) The rule of our Sages, "one does not leave a permitted thing and eat a forbidden one," is not a matter without reason or a decree of the Torah, but rather it is in the nature of human beings. And if it were true that immediately after the event that was pending for immediate decision the *pask din* was nullified, how do you explain the phenomenon that (1) they had to deny with force the existence of this *pask din*, at the very time that it would have been possible to say simply as above; (2) why did they need to say something "strange"—that the *pask din* did not reach those to whom the *pask din* pertains; (3) what place was there for the publication by the **Mafdal** of the letter of one of the aforementioned individuals, a letter written in the month of **Shevat**, **5732**, **that there is** a clear opinion on all four sections (of the aforementioned *pask din*)?

(2) **In your letter** that preceded this one, an eight-page letter, there is not a single word about the nullification of the *pask din* following an immediate decision, etc. Seemingly, this is the greatest bewilderment, [in addition to the point—that you do not mention this at all, and all the more so do not explain it, in this letter of yours from 12 Nissan].

## 10,398

[19 Iyar, 5732]

There is no reason for him to be discouraged; we have the promise of the Alter Rebbe that we will emerge victorious.

Regarding the words of the Ramban that the holier something is, the greater the difficulties that confront it—one should not be affected by this.

As for the state of his health—do not take it to heart; however, maintaining one's health is one of the ways of Hashem, and one is obligated to do so. This also pertains to avodah, and for the sake of avodah, one must safeguard one's health.

As for him, he should feel extra joy that he knows his role and the greatness of his privilege.

## 1039

27 Iyar, 5732
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Mr. Eliezer Wiesel,

Shalom u’vracha,

I hereby acknowledge with many thanks the receipt of your book, "Souls on Fire," and it goes without saying that I have perused it with the interest appropriate to its content.

It is my hope that you will not mind if I express great satisfaction—and even more than that, in continuation of our previous conversation—that you have begun to write on subjects similar to your aforementioned book. For although it is difficult to demand, and seemingly doubtful whether one should demand, a distraction from the subject of the Holocaust and all that it entails, on the other hand, we live in a time of opportunity the likes of which has never been seen to draw the hearts of our brethren, the Children of Israel, closer to their heritage and the inheritance of their forefathers, Avraham, Yitzchak, and Yaakov, until it permeates their daily lives. This takes precedence over all other matters. And if this is true regarding every individual, it is all the more so regarding a person whom Divine Providence has endowed with special talents to influence those in his immediate circle—through face-to-face conversation—and those further away—through writing, compositions, and so on.

And if you will, perhaps this is the best response to the Nazis and their cohorts and heirs who rose up to destroy us: to show them that not only was their counsel frustrated, etc., but on the contrary, in the style of the verse: "And as they afflicted him, so he multiplied and so he spread." Our Torah is a Torah of **life**, and especially according to the explanation of the teachings of Chassidus and its subjects, which is (Chassidus) "the life of the Torah of life," or in other words—the inwardness of the Torah of life.

I believe I have written to you previously regarding the above, but I did not receive an acknowledgment, and "two are better than one."

May it be His will that in this matter, as in every good thing, the statement of our Sages of blessed memory will be fulfilled in you as well: "He who has one hundred, wants two hundred; having attained two hundred, he wants four hundred." From now on, may you write and also speak in a manner and style that will kindle the "candle of Hashem, the soul of man" that is within every single Jew, until, in the style of our Sages of blessed memory, "the flame rises by itself," and may you illuminate the lives of those you influence with the "candle of mitzvah and the light of Torah," in thought, speech, and action—and "action is the essential thing"—in daily life, leading to the fulfillment of practical mitzvos in the literal sense.

Although it is delayed due to many preoccupations, I hereby express my gratitude for your best wishes, especially as they were accompanied by your aforementioned book.

As is the ancient Jewish custom, that one cannot do without a remark, etc., it is understood that I focused primarily in your book on the chapter that deals with the area I know better, in the country of Russia where I was born and raised, which is the chapter discussing the Maggid of Mezritch. The remark is that it is a pity regarding what you write concerning the reason for the Maggid’s moving from city to city, etc. With a request for your forgiveness, these things are not accepted at all—and not only by the heart of a Chassid—when one takes into account the character of the Maggid’s students, even in his final years. They were not merely his Chassidim, but also students who contemplated the teachings of their master and delved into them, etc. Among them was the Alter Rebbe, author of the Tanya and the Shulchan Aruch, who did not shy away from instituting new customs and innovations even in the teachings of Chassidus. Yet, even in a question regarding the revealed Torah and a halachic ruling, in a responsum written many years later, he bases his words and brings proof from a ruling of the Maggid in the summer of the year 5732—that is to say, in the last year of the Maggid’s life in this world, many years after he had moved his residence—and there he writes of him with the title: "Our master, our teacher, the great Rabbi, the famous Gaon, Moreinu Harav DovBer, of blessed memory." (See Responsa, Siman 14, printed at the end of the Shulchan Aruch of the Alter Rebbe). And if this is so regarding the revealed Torah, then in matters of Chassidus, it is all the more so.

It is understood that I saw in your introduction to the book that your intention was not a scientific composition, etc., but rather a description of the teacher, leader, and Nasi as he appears in the stories of the people of his generation, etc. But in such a case, the influence on the reader is what matters, and the reader perceives things as they are written. I ask for your forgiveness for this remark.

 From the negative you hear the positive regarding the book's beneficial influence on the reader.

Although the acknowledgment is late, "one brings about merit through meritorious days," the eve of Rosh Chodesh, the time of the receiving of the Torah. I express to you my blessing, in the well-known style, for the receiving of the Torah with joy and inwardness.

With respect and blessing,

## 10th of Sivan

B”H, Rosh Chodesh Sivan, 5732
Brooklyn, N.Y.

The Glikas Family, may they live and be well,

Shalom u’Bracha!

From time to time, I inquire about you and receive greetings regarding you from R’ Yisroel Aryeh Leib Zayantz, may he live and be well. Recently, I heard from him that the mood in your home is not as it should be.

This surprised me, especially as I recall you and know of your bitachon in the Ribono shel Olam. For when a Yid relies on the Ribono shel Olam, there is surely no room for worries and the like. And although the holy Torah says that a Yid must do what depends on him through natural means, the same holy Torah says that this must go hand-in-hand with a strong bitachon in the Ribono shel Olam, who is the Master of the world and watches over each and every one. It is simply that the Ribono shel Olam Himself desires that one should do what is normally required. Consequently, when it comes to health, one must visit a doctor and follow his instructions; regarding parnassah, one must seek ways to improve business; and if there are problems concerning children, one must consult with friends and good acquaintances, and so on. But together with this, one must know and be entirely certain that the beracha and hatzlacha come from the Ribono shel Olam, from His full, open, holy, and wide hand.

It is understood that a person cannot know the Ribono shel Olam’s "calendar" as to when the beracha will arrive, but the stronger the bitachon, the sooner the beracha comes. This is especially true in your case, as you have increased the "keilim" to receive the Ribono shel Olam’s berachos by strengthening the observance of Torah and mitzvos in your daily life—kashrus, tefillin, shmiras Shabbos and Yom Tov, and so on. Furthermore, you have the zechus that through your example, you have influenced and brought other Yidden to conduct themselves as the Ribono shel Olam desires, and you have brought Jewish families closer to Yiddishkeit, which is a very great zechus.

Therefore, I hope that I will receive happy news from you, that not only has your bitachon in the Ribono shel Olam not weakened, chas v’shalom, but on the contrary, it has become even stronger, and in this spirit, you are fulfilling the doctor’s instructions, as well as the other matters in a natural way. Then, I hope, and I pray, and I am certain that you will see the Ribono shel Olam’s berachos openly.

We are currently in these especially auspicious days, when Yidden go anew to receive the Torah and mitzvos on the Yom Tov of Shavuos, Zman Matan Toraseinu, during which, together with Torah and mitzvos, Yidden receive the Divine berachos in everything they need, both materially and spiritually.

With wishes for health, strong bitachon, parnassah, and nachas from all the children, may they live.

## 1017

[9 Sivan, 5732]

The essence of *kiddushin* and marriage is: **"Behold, you are betrothed to me"** — that two people become connected **only** to one another. When those gathered express their joy and offer their blessings to the couple, it must be in that same spirit, or at the very least, not **the opposite and in contradiction to it**.

The **essence** of mixed dancing is that a married woman dances with **another man**, or that an unmarried girl dances with a young man, rendering the entire concept of marriage and *kiddushin* unnecessary, etc. And this is done **publicly and with great noise**, etc.!!!

*Is'arusa d'letata* [arousal from below] is a reflection of *is'arusa d'le'eila* [arousal from above] — when it is demonstrated **below** that the couple’s marriage leads to the joy of closeness as described above, then, *rachmana litzlan*, etc., and the wise will understand.

1018

[B"H, 11 Sivan, 5732]

Regarding the printing of the Tanya and the Siddur, please add the following via offset:

1) In the Tanya (**at the end**), the small [letter/note].

On the title page of the Tanya, it should state: "Seventieth Edition, 11 Nissan, etc." (as in the most recent edition).

The Siddur should state: "Twentieth Edition, 11 Nissan, etc."

**In my name**, give one to each of the students (from Toras Emes, Toras Chabad, Bais Lechem Yehuda, Bais Rivkah, Reshet, Bais Chana, etc. — the Chabad educational institutions) who sent a letter of blessing for 11 Nissan, a Tanya, or a Siddur — according to the discretion of their teacher.

The *avreich* . . . *shiy*

## 1011

[B"H](http://#_ftn_1680), Motzaei Shabbos Kodesh, Parshas Beha'aloscha, 5732
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the participants in the annual undertaking of the N.Y. Committee for the Teachers' Seminary and girls' schools in Kfar Chabad, in our Holy Land, may it be rebuilt speedily:

May Hashem grant you life,

Blessings and peace!

The parsha of **Beha'aloscha** which we read this Shabbos begins with the mitzvah of lighting the Menorah. Although the mitzvah itself is connected to a specific place (the Beis Hamikdash), a specific time (when the Beis Hamikdash stood), and a specific person (the Kohanim), the Torah is eternal, and all matters [in](http://#_ftn_1681) the Torah are eternal in their inner content and in their guidance for the daily life of all Jews, in all times and in all places.

The inner point of **Beha'aloscha es haneros** is that a Jew must kindle light—the light of **"The candle of Hashem is the soul of man"**—both within oneself and within others, so that they may shine with the radiance of **"The mitzvah is a candle and the Torah is light."**

And this must be done in the manner of **"Beha'aloscha—that the flame rises by itself"**—that the flame should ascend of its own accord.

This is the foundation of Torah education in general, and of Chabad educational institutions in particular, where Jewish children are raised in such a way that even later, when they complete their education, they should shine and illuminate their surroundings with the radiance of Torah and mitzvos, permeated with Chassidic vitality and warmth.

In this regard, the Teachers' Seminary and girls' schools in Kfar Chabad have a special importance, for here the students are prepared to take their place in education and to be a true [akeres habayis](http://#_ftn_1686)—a "light-kindler" in the fullest sense.

It is therefore a great merit for all those who participate in the work of helping to provide the necessary financial assistance for the aforementioned institutions, so that they may fulfill their task of **Beha'aloscha es haneros** to the fullest extent.

May Hashem Yisbarach help that this annual undertaking be met with great success, and may this merit assist all participants in receiving the Almighty's blessings in everything they need, together with their families, both materially and spiritually.

With blessings for success and for good tidings,

**M. Schneerson**

## 1012

B.H., 23 Sivan, 5732
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To my dear friend, Mr. [Avraham](#_ftn_1687) Shlansky, may he live:

Shalom u’vracha!

I ask for your great forgiveness for not having acknowledged in writing the receipt of your birthday greeting and your most precious gift—the [collection](#_ftn_1688) of your writings (in ten volumes). I wish to interpret this [as written](#_ftn_1689) in the first volume: that this is a sign that together with "flesh and blood" (*she'er basar*), there is also "a remnant of spirit" (*she'er ruach*). However, with a slight change—not *she'er* (with a kamatz under the aleph), but rather, in this as well, *she'er* (with a tzeirei under the aleph, meaning "remnant/remainder").

My intention in the above is simple, following up on what we discussed during your visit here: that I believe [that you](#_ftn_1690) believe, and that we both believe—in the well-known phrasing, with complete faith—in all those principles included in the three that are unified as one: [Yisrael](#_ftn_1691), the Torah, and the Holy One, Blessed be He, as we spoke then regarding that same content.

And even though there is room for a skeptic to come and raise objections—as there are actions and words which, on the face of it, prove the opposite of what is written above—the explanation for this is based on the popular [proverb](#_ftn_1692): a mere skeptic is an *am ha'aretz* (an ignoramus). That is to say, he only has what pertains to external and "earthly" (*aretzi*) conduct, and he does not discern at all what comes from the outer layer of a person, or the most external layer, and what its source is in the interiority of the person—in the language of Chassidus, "his essence and being." And it is understood that "spirit" (*ruach*), and consequently "a remnant of spirit" (*she'er ruach*), are primarily about interiority and essence.

To add to the above: even from the perspective of externality and earthliness—even with this *am ha'aretz* in the literal sense—it is ultimately a necessity that the essence and the interior will rebel against the external layer that opposes it, and will find expression to reveal itself.

It does not matter so much if this was specifically intended, but the opening to the collection of your writings and your treasure is "revelation": ["And the lad](#_ftn_1693) was serving Hashem... 'Speak, for Your servant is listening,'" and only after this does the collection itself follow. My hope, as mentioned, is that this is not a coincidence, and certainly that it is not a "peshatel" (a forced interpretation) of my own.

With a blessing regarding the opening, that there be fulfilled in you what [is said](#_ftn_1694), "I will bless those who bless you"—that whoever blesses a Jew is blessed by Hashem, the Source of blessing, the Source of blessing in both material and spiritual matters alike, and with good tidings regarding the above—your friend.

P.S. Just as I rejoiced at the Divine Providence in how the entire collection opened according to the verse mentioned above, so too, after asking your forgiveness, it is a pity that the conclusion is "departing to the sound of mournful music." Even though this is a translation from the work of a non-Jew, it is nevertheless a pity. For the task of every person, and especially of a Jew—and particularly one who has merited a Chassidic atmosphere and knowledge of it—is to fulfill ["Serve](#_ftn_1695) Hashem **with joy**" in all the details of their lives. And if, for whatever reason, there is involvement with a non-Jew, even in that it is [good](#_ftn_1696) to conclude with joy.

Knowing you, I am certain that you will continue with writing, printing, etc., and my hope is that you will continue to send your publications here in the future, and thank you in advance.

## 1313

B"H, 23 Sivan, 5732

To the honorable Rabbi, the famous Gaon, wise and understanding, G-d-fearing, a man of noble character, etc. [Rabbi R. A. Y.] shlita, Chief Rabbi,

Yesterday I learned from our friend, the G-d-fearing, wise and understanding man, who is involved in communal needs and multi-faceted activities, Mr. [Daniel] HaKohen sheyichyeh, that my letter responding to your letter, which was delivered by him, was not received.

I am hastening to confirm receipt herewith—along with my great thanks for your attention in informing me of this matter, etc.

May it be the will [of Hashem] that the desire of Hashem in your hands will succeed in protecting the honor of the Torah and its matters, including the honor of the Rabbinate, and especially in the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt and established. May this be with proper health, for long, good days and years, and with joy and goodness of heart—by continuing to serve, as you do now, in your position as Chief Rabbi for many years, many in the literal and simple sense.

[It is a certainty] that a messenger fulfills his mission, Mr. Daniel HaKohen sheyichyeh.

With great respect and with a blessing for long, good days and years, and for good tidings,

**M. Schneerson**

## 1014

B”H, 23 Sivan, 5732
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished individual, occupied with the needs of the community,
R’ Yosef, may he live, Triki

Shalom u’Bracha!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter and the accompanying manuscript, your composition on the *Pardes* of Torah.

With a request for your forgiveness, according to the custom of [the Rebbe](#_ftn_1701), my father-in-law, of saintly memory—that one does not provide *haskamos* or the like for compositions, for reasons that are understood—it is not in my power to fulfill your request in this matter, and I ask for your pardon.

Surely, in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, you will find many who will examine your composition and express their opinions.

Since you mention that you teach Torah in public, it is my hope that the *shiur* is founded upon the aforementioned path of the *Pardes* of Torah—I mean to include the *pnimiyus haTorah*, including the *sod* of the Torah, as is known from the statement of the *Zohar* that through this, they will emerge from exile with mercy (Ra’aya Mehemna, *Zohar* Vol. 3, 124b).

With respect and blessing.

## 10,615

10,615

[B"H](#_ftn_1702), 25 Sivan, 5732

Brooklyn, N.Y.

Blessings and peace!

In response to your letter of 18 Sivan,

[Since](#_ftn_1703) the delay in receiving Hashem’s blessing for living and enduring offspring sometimes stems from a lack of precision and care in observing the laws and regulations of Taharas HaMishpacha (niddah, hefsek taharah, immersion in a kosher mikveh, etc.), and since a lack of knowledge leads to a lack of observance, you should clarify all the details regarding this with a rav who is a teacher of halacha, with the intention of observing them from now on as required.

All of this should be within the context of daily conduct that conforms to the instructions of our Torah—Torah of life—and the fulfillment of its mitzvos, [of which it is said](#_ftn_1704) "and he shall live by them." Beyond the fundamental point that this is the command of the Ribono shel Olam, this is also the path to receiving the blessing for what a person requires.

And indeed, in matters of Torah and mitzvos, no matter how good the situation may be, there is always room to add, since they are connected to the Ribono shel Olam, who is Ein Sof.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

S. M. Simpson, Secretary

## 18

[B"H](ftnref_1708), 3 Tammuz, 5732
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed Rabbi, the esteemed Chassid, G-d-fearing and learned, occupied with communal needs, etc.,
Rabbi [Chananya](ftnref_1709) Yom Tov Lipa, shlita

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter, along with the final volume of your sefer **Taharas Yom Tov**, following the previous volumes:

May your strength be fortified in Torah, in your elucidation of the words of the [Rishonim](ftnref_1710) who were like angels, and especially the great halachic authorities of the Jewish people, by whose light we walk and from whose waters we drink. Regarding such [it is said](ftnref_1711), "Turn it over and turn it over [for everything is in it]."

Especially since, in your case, this is [Torah](ftnref_1712) accompanied by labor—the holy labor of immense and great effort in the purity of the Jewish people through the establishment of mikvaos. You have merited that the verse is fulfilled in you: "[You have labored](ftnref_1713) (in the aforementioned) and you have found (in many and various places where the Jewish people reside)."

May it be His will that for many years to come you continue in the aforementioned with peace of mind, joy, and a good heart, and may the merit of the many assist you.

And may we very soon merit the fulfillment of the promise, as the Sages say in their Mishnah (end of Perek Yom HaKippurim): "[The Mikvah](ftnref_1714) of Israel is Hashem... [and I will sprinkle](ftnref_1715) upon you pure waters and you shall be purified... and I will give you a new heart... and you shall dwell in the land that I gave to your fathers," in the true and complete Redemption through Mashiach Tzidkeinu.

With respect and with a blessing for success in the above,

**M. Schneerson**

P.S. In accordance with your request in the aforementioned letter, I have enclosed my response letter, even though [I am limited](ftnref_1716) by the custom of the house of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, regarding letters of recommendation, etc.

I have received your sefer, Taharas Yom Tov, volume 16. Thank you, thank you. Regarding a topic of current relevance, concerning what you wrote at the beginning of the sefer (p. 72) regarding the contradiction from the Magen Avraham (606:8) that the immersion on Erev Yom Kippur due to *keri* applies even when one sees "divided waters," etc.—versus the Magen Avraham (288) that there is no immersion for *Ezra* when one sees "divided waters":

It can be said that this is explained in the language of our Rebbe (the author of the Tanya and Shulchan Aruch) in his Shulchan Aruch (606:11), which states: "And some say that the reason for this immersion is because of *keri*, 'so that they may be clean and pure on Yom Kippur,' unlike the reason for the immersion of *Ezra*, which is so that [Torah scholars](ftnref_1717) should not be common with their wives like roosters." For only this reason—which is the reason of the Shulchan Aruch—did the Alter Rebbe copy into his Shulchan Aruch (there, 288), and not the reason of the Tur (lightheadedness). And the question of the Perishah, "From where do we know this reason?"—this is found in the Rambam (Hilchos Tefillah 4:8), and it has already been noted in the Yerushalmi (Berachos 3:4). In the Mishnah Berurah on the Shulchan Aruch (there), he added the reason of the Tur as well. Seemingly, this is the opposite of the Shulchan Aruch, which changed from what was written in the Beis Yosef and omitted it, bringing the reason of the Rambam instead. Especially since, as mentioned above, it can be said that there is a practical halachic difference.

Regarding the conclusion of Maseches Yoma: "Rabbi Akiva said, 'Happy are you, Israel...'" (p. 11 and onwards): See *Ohr HaTorah* by the Tzemach Tzedek, the *drushim* for Yom Kippur, on the discourse beginning "Rabbi Akiva said, 'Happy are you...'"

At the end of the sefer (p. 331), that even though they have nullified their immersions, one should be careful, etc.: See *Likutei Torah* (by the Alter Rebbe—author of the Tanya and Shulchan Aruch), Parshas Tavo (43b), that even though they have nullified, etc., according to all opinions, the prayer is more accepted with the immersion. And one can say there is a slight reason for this in what is said, "Prayer is greater than Torah," etc. See there.

I have now seen that in your sefer (pp. 39, 259) you discuss the Yerushalmi and Rambam mentioned above.

## 1019

1019

B”H, 3 Tammuz, 5732
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the Honorable Rabbi, the Chassid, G-d-fearing, and distinguished scholar, etc.,
Rabbi Shlomo Goren
Chief Rabbi and Head of the Rabbinical Court of Tel Aviv-Yafo and the District

Greetings and blessings!

I wish to thank you for your letter of the 17th of Sivan, along with the three books enclosed: *Shaarei Taharah* on *mikvaos*, Volume I of the *Yerushalmi HaMeforash*, and *Toras HaMoadim* — in continuation of our conversation during your visit here.

I thank you in advance for writing in your letter that you will continue to send future publications of yours.

Furthermore, and most importantly, I thank you for your efforts regarding the primary matter we discussed: the nullification of the decree—G-d forbid that it should come to pass—known as the "Who is a Jew" law in connection with the Law of Return. This is alluded to in the conclusion of your letter, where you write: "And may we all merit to fulfill the word of Hashem through His prophet: 'And I have set you apart from the peoples to be Mine'."

Hashem already promised at the Giving of the Torah: "And you shall be to Me a kingdom of priests and a holy nation." However, it was His will—in the words of the Rambam —that "the choice is given to every person; if he desires to incline himself to the good path and be a tzaddik, etc., and this is a great principle and the pillar of the Torah and the mitzvos." It is incumbent upon each and every one to do their part in this regard. Fortunate is the merit of all those who have the authority (and the ability) to accomplish great things in this matter. Surely, "the desire of Hashem will succeed in his hand," especially since the merit of the public—and in this case, the merit of all our people, the Children of Israel, wherever they may be—is a source of assistance.

With respect and blessings for success and good news in all the above,

**M. Schneerson**

Naturally, immediately upon receiving *Toras HaMoadim*, I looked through it (at least cursorily), and I was pleased to find at its beginning (the section on *teshuvah* and *viduy*) points in common with what I have written on this subject previously, which is enclosed.

**Regarding the end of the book** (the section on *shemitah*)—I did not find (nor in other books I have seen) an answer to the question: Does the security situation of Eretz Yisrael and matters of security (*pikuach nefesh*) make the matter of selling the land (especially to a non-Jew) even worse than a mere legal fiction? Seemingly, it would be better to declare it *hefker* (after the sale—in any event) and [rely on] the IDF, which in certain places acts in the manner of "guardians of the *sefichim* for the *omer*." I write this in haste.

After some time: I delayed sending my letter in anticipation of perhaps receiving news of good tidings regarding the aforementioned matter, in continuation of what you have done in this regard. It seems, from your silence, that you are fulfilling the principle that "one does not respond to..."

1021

1021

[B"H](#_ftn_1738), 3 Tammuz, 5732
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Mr. [Yaakov](#_ftn_1739) Rosenthal,

Shalom u’vracha!

In response to your letter of 22 Sivan, following the personal message I received from my secretary, Mr. Nissan Mindel, upon his return from his visit to Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established:

First and foremost, I must apologize to you for the lack of a timely response, which is contrary to proper etiquette, and for not even sending a simple acknowledgment. However, a mere acknowledgment does not hold much meaning for me, and furthermore, there are those who might interpret it as a lack of attention. Due to the pressure of many preoccupations, I was forced to delay my response, and afterwards—as our Sages have already said [in their Mishnah](#_ftn_1740), "Do not say, 'When I am free I will study,' lest you never become free." It is my hope that you will understand the aforementioned and judge me favorably.

I was happy to hear from Dr. Mindel, and also to see from the press, that you continue your publications, at least from time to time. This strengthens my hope that you are still active in the primary role of every Jewish person, [as the Mishnah states](#_ftn_1741): "I was created to serve my Maker"—by disseminating the Torah of one's Maker, that is, Hashem, and by encouraging the fulfillment of His mitzvos wherever your reach extends.

Moreover, it is not merely as I wrote above—that you continue as before—but on the contrary: since your time is now more free from other occupations, your involvement in the aforementioned should be with greater intensity and strength, especially since the demands of the hour are constantly growing and intensifying. And if this applies to every place, it is all the more so in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, [the land](#_ftn_1742) upon which the eyes of Hashem your G-d are at all times, from the beginning of the year to the end of the year.

You are surely aware of the story of 12-13 Tammuz, the days of the redemption of my father-in-law, the Rebbe. [And I have already](#_ftn_1743) stated that one of the primary lessons from this entire episode is that it is within the power of a single Jewish person to fulfill his true mission, even when a powerful government and its entire regime oppose it.

And although [in the well-known phrase](#_ftn_1744), "Who is he and where is he whose heart prompts him" to say that he is endowed with the spiritual strengths of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, and his immense mesiras nefesh, etc., nevertheless, once he paved the way [and opened](#_ftn_1745) a path in this, and in an open and public manner, it is certainly much easier for others who follow in his footsteps. Furthermore, and most importantly, the difficulties we face now in the dissemination of Yiddishkeit are of no comparison at all—not in the slightest. And surely, for someone like you, further elaboration is unnecessary.

With respect—and as is customary to sign in these days—and with the blessing of the Chag HaGeulah, with the added prayer that from this redemption we may soon arrive at the true and complete redemption of the entire Jewish people, wherever they may be, through Moshiach Tzidkeinu,

**M. Schneerson**

## 1022

[B"H](http://www.chabad.org/library/article_cdo/aid/1746#_ftn_1746), 3 Tammuz, 5732
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the students of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch,
May Hashem protect them and grant them life,

Greetings and blessings!

As we stand in these days, and those adjacent to them—and as is the custom to connect the events of the week with the weekly parsha, and especially in our case, with the parsha of the Chag HaGeulah of 12-13 Tammuz, which begins in the week leading up to the conclusion of the week—

One must contemplate—as per the instruction of the verse: "[My people,] remember now what Balak... counseled, and what [Balaam] answered"—the introduction of that same [subject] by the one who [said] that he could not speak anything except the word that Hashem would place in his mouth, which is: **"For from the top of the rocks I see him, and from the hills I behold him."** As Rashi explains: I look at their beginnings and the start of their roots, and I see them established and strong like these rocks and hills—through the Patriarchs and Matriarchs.

The explanation for this is that it is manifest and known to all who enter the world, even the nations of the world, that the existence, strength, and might of the people of Bnei Yisrael have their foundation and root in the Patriarchs and Matriarchs of this nation. It is an inheritance from them to every single son and daughter of Yisrael, like a nature in our souls, in all times and in all places. This is what makes us a single entity in the world—**"Behold, it is a people that shall dwell alone, and shall not be reckoned among the nations."**

From this follows the immediate conclusion—**"Who can count the dust of Yaakov, and the number of the fourth part of Yisrael?"** The intent here is the importance of the holy seed, the sons and daughters of Yisrael; meaning, that the sons and daughters of Yisrael are the seed of Yaakov and Yisrael, and they [conduct themselves] as is fitting for the children of Avraham, Yitzchak, and Yaakov, and the daughters of Sarah, Rivkah, Rachel, and Leah. This ensures that the entire people of Bnei Yisrael will be established and strong like these rocks and hills, both literally and in its deeper meaning—that the Patriarchs and Matriarchs are compared to rocks and hills.

These virtues exist and are ultimately revealed in every one of our people, the Bnei Yisrael, both small and great. But it is understood that they are expressed with full force in the Nasi of Yisrael, and specifically the Nasi of our generation, the master of the celebration and the Geulah, who did not take into account the enemies of the religion of Yisrael who sought to uproot Torah and mitzvos, etc. He fought them without fear and with true mesiras nefesh, until he brought victory and Geulah not only for himself, but also the Geulah of "all who cherish our holy Torah, observers of mitzvos, and even those who are called by the name of Yisrael."

[As Rashi explains] in the weekly parsha: The Nasi of the generation is like the entire generation, for the Nasi is everything.

This means: that the mesiras nefesh and the activities of the Nasi of the generation add strength and might to every single person of the generation to walk in the straight path that he has taught us, and to continue his activities in strengthening Torah and Yiddishkeit and disseminating them in every place and at every time and era.

This is all the more so for the students and alumni of the yeshivos and educational institutions that are conducted in his spirit, or which he himself founded.

May it be the will that all the students and alumni of these yeshivos and educational institutions in every place, may they live and be well, go from strength to strength, and act and accomplish in the study of Torah with diligence and the fulfillment of its mitzvos with hiddur, joy, and a good heart.

Until each one of them can justly say: "I have been as a wonder unto many, but You are my strong refuge."

With blessings for great success and for good tidings in all the aforementioned,

**M. Schneerson**

## 1023

1023

[B"H](#_ftn_1759), 3 Tammuz – Parshas [Vayomer](#_ftn_1760) Hashem, etc.

"I am your portion and your inheritance" –

5732. Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and blessings!

In these days, beginning from 3 Tammuz—the day of the [liberation](#_edn_337) of the master of the celebration and the redemption of 12-13 Tammuz, my father-in-law, the Rebbe—from the house of imprisonment,

It is appropriate to contemplate [with greater](#_edn_338) intensity and strength the episode of the imprisonment and the redemption:

The cause of the imprisonment—his tireless engagement in the dissemination of Yiddishkeit and Torah and mitzvos in every place, without regard for obstacles and hindrances, etc., and with the most [extensive](#_edn_339), broad, and profound dissemination.

And the redemption—which was, in the words of the master of the redemption, not only his own redemption, but also the redemption of ["all](#_edn_340) those who cherish our holy Torah, who observe mitzvos, and also those who are called by the name of Israel."

Contemplation that will lead to action—conduct in practice that corresponds to the hopes of the master of the celebration, and even to the perfection of this, as is fitting for Bnei Yisrael, who are [the portion](#_edn_341) of Hashem, His people, and regarding each and every one of them it is [said](#_ftn_1763): "And you shall be to Me a [kingdom](#_edn_342) of **priests** and a **holy** nation."

And as is known, the [halachic ruling](#_edn_344) of the Rambam that the word of Hashem [spoken](#_edn_345) to the Kohanim and Leviim, "I am your portion and your inheritance," does not apply to them alone. Rather, "any person from [all](#_edn_346) [the inhabitants of the world](#_edn_348) whose spirit [moved](#_edn_349) him and whose knowledge [convinced](#_edn_350) him [to set himself apart](#_edn_351) [to stand](#_edn_352) before Hashem [to serve Him](#_edn_353) and to worship Him, to know Hashem, and he walked [upright](#_edn_354) [as](#_edn_355) G-d made him, and he removed from his neck the [yoke](#_edn_356) of the many calculations that people seek—this person is sanctified as a holy of holies, and Hashem will be his portion and his inheritance [forever](#_edn_357) and for all eternity, [and He will provide](#_edn_358) for him in this world [that which](#_edn_359) is sufficient for him, just as He provided [for the Kohanim](#_edn_360) and the Leviim. [Indeed, David](#_edn_361) of blessed memory [says](#_edn_362): 'Hashem is the portion of my inheritance and my cup; You [support](#_edn_363) my lot.'"

May it be the will [that everyone](#_edn_364) will act as stated above, and with joy, and Hashem will redeem them from every matter that hinders and prevents, and they will go [from strength](#_ftn_1772) to strength in the study of the revealed Torah and Chassidus and in the performance of its mitzvos with beauty,

Until it can be justly said: "[I have been](#_edn_365) as a wonder [to many](#_edn_366), but You are my strong refuge."

With the blessing of the Festival of Redemption,

**M. Schneerson**

***

[With the blessing](#_ftn_1775) that, finally, they will begin to utilize the blessings of the founder of the village—the master of the redemption—for the village **in practice**.

***

[I acknowledge](#_ftn_1776) receipt of the letter from the aforementioned date, etc. And the lack of [progress in holiness](#_ftn_1777) [(Chabad education,](#_ftn_1778) etc.) in their holy community is **alarming**—and it is simple that it is incumbent upon each and every one, etc. And a word to the wise is sufficient.

. . . And may it be the will that I finally merit to receive at least the beginning—of good news from them regarding the education [of each and every one](#_edn_347) of their children, may they live, specifically—and it is simple that I do not mean excuses and the like—

***

[With respect](#_ftn_1779) and with the blessing of the Festival of Redemption and for an active and successful farbrengen.

## 1029

B"H, Yom HaGeulah, 13 Tammuz, 5732
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Dr. [Avner](#_ftn_1789) Chai Shaki, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

I was pleased to receive your letter of 5 Sivan, though it reached me with some delay.

Standing under the impression of our conversation during your visit here, I am confident that the actions you write in your letter that you intend to undertake—especially in the area of [who is a Jew](#_ftn_1790)—you will carry out, and with the vigor with which you have been endowed by Divine Providence. My hope is that you will not be satisfied with a one-time action, but will repeat it again and again as necessary.

To put it wittily, since your role is in the administration of education and culture, the aforementioned action falls within the sphere of education in its deepest and truest sense—education that touches the conscience of the individual soul, the collective, and the entire nation. [In the style](#_ftn_1791) of Rabbeinu Saadia Gaon, "Our nation is a nation only through the Torah." And true culture rejects and nullifies—[in the style](#_ftn_1792) of the Torah—the culture of sinful men.

This auspicious day, 13 Tammuz, the day of the redemption of my father-in-law, the Rebbe—and I trust that you are aware of the significance of [the day](#_ftn_1793)—teaches us that the effort of even one Jew, if it is for the sake of truth, justice, and integrity, and with the appropriate strength, without fear of the decrees and laws of men, will ultimately have its effect and succeed.

May it be the will that this should happen sooner rather than later, and that the verse, "[He makes] even his enemies be at peace with him," [also](#_ftn_1794) be fulfilled in this regard.

For surely the initiators of the aforementioned unfortunate law and those who defend it know that it is a threat to the existence of our people; it is only that for various strange reasons they have not yet changed their unfortunate position. May the Good Hashem enlighten their eyes and hearts.

With respect and with the blessing of the Festival of Redemption and with good news regarding all the above.

## 1030

B"H, Yud-Gimmel Tammuz, 5732
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Regarding them, we see tangible proof of the truth of the statement of our Sages, of blessed memory, that even an iron partition does not separate the Children of Israel from their Father in Heaven.

And there is a special *segulah* for this assistance: that those who are being helped are, at the same time, also helping in this *avodah* by being a living example of a life of *mesiras nefesh* maintained throughout the daily grind for more than fifty years.

May the Ribono shel Olam grant that the good news regarding the success of all the above exceeds all expectations. [As has been discussed several times](#_ftn_1796), according to the precise language of our Sages : "You labored and you found"—for the results of the labor are not merely commensurate with the labor, but rather in the manner of a "finding" (a windfall), and this is easy to understand.

With blessings for success in all the above, and for good tidings. Especially since your letter was written on Gimmel Tammuz, the day of the release of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, *Nasi Yisrael*, from prison, and this response is written on the day of his *geulah*, Yud-Gimmel Tammuz, the merit of the master of the *geulah* stands for you and for all of Israel.

## 1031

B"H, 14 Tammuz, 5732
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mr. Netanel HaKohen Basin
Johannesburg

Shalom u’Bracha!

I have just received your letter of June 20, in which you write about some details regarding yourself, as well as your thoughts concerning the causes of antisemitism, and in general about the history of the Jewish people and what they have endured.

It goes without saying that one could and should elaborate on this at great length. However, the point of the matter, as you yourself write, is that the answer is already present in many places in the Torah, which is **Toras Emes**, to the extent that this has also been incorporated into various prayers, summarized in four words: **"U’mipnei chata’einu galinu me’artzeinu"** (And because of our sins we were exiled from our land).

It is also understandable and clear that this was said not merely to explain a phenomenon and all that it entails, but so that one should contemplate it, and consider what each person can and must do about it. This also clearly indicates that everyone has a shlichus to fulfill and to accomplish according to their capabilities.

What this shlichus consists of is also very simple: Since **"u’mipnei chata’einu galinu me’artzeinu,"** with all the phenomena associated with galus, it is understood that the only way to emerge from galus, and while in galus—to diminish these undesirable phenomena—is to remove the cause: **"u’mipnei chata’einu."** Only afterwards is there a place to consider what must also be done *b’derech hateva* (through natural means).

There is a well-known analogy for this: When a person jumps into boiling water, it must bring about unavoidable consequences and pain regarding his skin, flesh, bones, etc. It is understood that it is senseless to smear the skin with an ointment or give him pills to lower his temperature, etc., while doing nothing, or not doing as much as one can, to take him out of the boiling water. Only after one takes him out of the boiling water can and should one do everything possible to heal him from the wounds that the boiling water caused. The analogy is understood.

It is also self-evident that by writing to you, I do not mean the philosophical treatment of this matter, but rather the main point is regarding **l’fo’al** (practical application).

Since you originate from the "old country" and have seen a true Jewish life in the shtetl, and this has been etched into your memory and outlook—as is also evident from your writing—first and foremost, one must ensure that for everyone one can reach, there should be an increase in matters of Yiddishkeit. This means quite simply: living according to the Torah and fulfilling the mitzvos in daily life. And the way to begin doing this is by showing a living example that, as good as it is, one can always add so that it should be even better. A living example is the best propaganda, especially when it is followed by **"devarim hayotzim min halev"** (words that come from the heart), which, according to the promise of our Sages, **"nichnasim el halev"** (enter the heart) and are not lost.

And one sees in practice that when this comes from a Jew who is not a Rav or a Maggid, etc., it has a greater effect.

May it be Hashem’s will that you should be able to report good tidings regarding all of the above.

With respect and blessing.

## 1035

1035

[B"H]( #_ftn_1806), 14 Tammuz, 5732
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Association of Torah-Observant Academics
From the USSR and Eastern Europe
May Hashem keep them alive

Peace and Blessing!

In response to your letter, in which you write regarding the need to reprint certain books from the list that we have published in the Russian language for distribution among immigrants from Russia,

I have forwarded your request to those who handle this matter, with instructions that they should begin fulfilling your request.

It is somewhat surprising that your letter contains no plan as to how you intend to distribute the aforementioned books in a way that will yield the greatest possible benefit. Furthermore, you do not write on what basis you determined the number of copies, and whether you have already come into contact with those who are in need of this and possess reliable information regarding the matter, etc. Surely you will provide these details as much as possible at the next opportunity.

Although it is understood, I will nevertheless mention this explicitly: it is in the **nature** of people that something given to them for free, without any effort on their part, holds no importance in their eyes. This is especially true when the item is given without a request from the recipient, but rather through the initiative of the giver. Certainly, money should not be an obstacle to providing a book to anyone who needs it, but at the same time, one must also take into account the aforementioned psychological factor.

It is my hope that at the next and soonest opportunity, you will provide details regarding the work of your association in general, in addition to the area mentioned above. It is understood that a greater level of detail is to be commended.

With blessings for much success, and soon, in all that is written,

**M. Schneerson**

P.S. Although for technical reasons it is easier to respond from here in Lashon HaKodesh, it is understood that you may continue to write in Russian.

1038

1038

15 Tammuz, 5732
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter.

As we have just emerged from the days of redemption, 12-13 Tammuz—the redemption of the Rebbe, and together with it, the redemption of "all who cherish our holy Torah, those who observe the mitzvos, and also those who are called by the name of Israel,"

The necessary *hisbonenus* regarding this is that it should bring about strengthening and an increase in the study of Torah and the performance of its mitzvos with *hiddur*.

This itself—*esek* in Torah and mitzvos—is a matter of redemption. As our Sages of blessed memory stated, "There is no free man except one who engages in Torah study," and the performance of a mitzvah is the fulfillment of the mission of the King of the world (as is understood from our Sages of blessed memory, that those who were engaged in a mitzvah were considered messengers), and "a servant of a King is a king."

Especially since in all this, *zechus avos mesayes* (the merit of the forefathers assists), as is also understood from the words of the Baal HaGeulah immediately at the *aschalta* (beginning) of the redemption (3 Tammuz), when he opened:

"We pray to Hashem, 'May Hashem our G-d be with us as He was with our forefathers; may He not forsake us nor abandon us.' Hashem should be with us, and will be with us, as He was with our forefathers."

And one should add an explanation to this: Through "holding" the deeds of their forefathers in their hands, the heir is in the place of the bequeather, and as it is written, "Instead of your fathers shall be your children"—it comes into revelation and is expressed in actual deed, to the point that through these deeds, they are the forefathers themselves.

And although the continuation in that opening was: "Although we are not equal to our forefathers, who were *baalei mesiras nefesh* in actual deed for the sake of Torah and mitzvos,"

The pain over this, the regret, and the *kabbalah tova* (good resolution) for the future are effective (as is known regarding the matter of *teshuvah*). Especially when one adds to this—in accordance with the explanation of the *Admur HaZaken*—*mesiras nefesh* (*nefesh* meaning *ratzon*), a *mesiras haratzon* (surrender of the will).

And the teaching of the Baal Shem Tov is well known: "In the place where a person’s will is, there he is entirely."

And the verse explicitly states—in the portion of Shabbos, 12 Tammuz:

"For from the top of the rocks I see him, and from the hills I behold him"—that each and every one of the Children of Israel is "founded and strong like these rocks and hills through the fathers and mothers (who are called rocks and hills)."

May it be the will that everyone acts as stated above, out of the aforementioned *mesiras haratzon*, and with the appropriate strength and firmness, in a manner of "He shall dwell alone and not be reckoned among the nations (and the ways of the nations)."

Until one can rightfully say: "I have been as a wonder to many, but You are my strong refuge."

And as our Sages of blessed memory stated, the garment of the Holy One, Blessed be He, is *oz* (strength), as it is said, "Hashem has clothed Himself with *oz*, He has girded Himself," and He gave it to Israel, as it is said, "Hashem will give *oz* to His people; Hashem will bless His people with peace."

With blessings for good tidings in the above,

**M. Schneerson**

***

I hereby acknowledge receipt of the letters and the *pidyon nefesh* contained within them, which will be read at the holy gravesite. Many thanks for the *zichronos* (memoirs), and you will certainly continue and write here regarding this. Many thanks in advance.

P.S. Regarding your note on Maseches Sotah (page 34), the Maharsha explains that the matter of the "different spirit" that was in Calev was for the good—this is also mentioned in the *Likkutei Torah* of the Arizal.

2) Regarding your note in *Likkutei Torah*, Parshas Shelach Lecha, the text "the matter of the spies who were princes of the congregation, men of renown"—the intention is not to the writing in the congregation of Korach (for "the chosen of the assembly" was omitted), but rather to the matter itself.

***

Regarding your note from some time ago in the *Hadran* on Maseches Pesachim—that the relationship of the blessing of the *Zevach* to the blessing of the *Pesach* is not similar to the relationship of the blessing of the *Regel* (festival) to the blessing of *Shehecheyanu*, for in the latter it is not considered *over l'asiyasan* (prior to their performance) (Rambam, Hilchos Brachos, ch. 11, law 7)—the comparison is in that the *Shehecheyanu* of the 14th is fulfilled by the blessing of the 15th—meaning, not during its performance at all.

***

With blessings for good tidings in the above, and for great success in spreading Judaism and the *maayanos* (wellsprings) in particular.

**Addition after some time**

A. Regarding what I wrote at the end of the notes for the letter of 15 Tammuz concerning the words of the Rambam (end of Hilchos Chanukah) that "the entire Torah was given to make peace in the world, as it is said, 'Its ways are ways of pleasantness and all its paths are peace,'" that perhaps the source for this is the statement of the Midrash (*Bamidbar Rabbah* 11:7) that "the Torah was compared only to peace, as it is said, 'and all its paths are peace,'"

Seemingly, it is preferable to say it is from the Gemara, *Gittin*: "The entire Torah is also for the sake of the ways of peace, as it is written, 'Its ways are ways of pleasantness and all its paths are peace.'"

But from the continuation of the Gemara there, it is proven that the intention of "the entire Torah is also for the sake of the ways of peace" is to the instructions and laws of the Torah, such as "a Kohen reads first, etc." which is in the Mishnah there. And there is no necessity in this for the *chiddush* (novelty) in the Rambam that the entire matter of the Torah is "to make peace in the world"—even though there is the study of Torah, which is "study and receive reward," and likewise—"He will magnify Torah and make it glorious."

But according to this, there is also no necessity from the Midrash for this *chiddush*—for the language of the Midrash is that the Torah was compared "to peace," peace in general, and it can be explained as peace between Israel and their Father in Heaven, similar to what our Sages of blessed memory said, that anyone who engages in Torah for its own sake brings peace to the Heavenly entourage, etc. (which is relevant also to the study of "study and receive reward," etc.), and it is not a matter of "peace in the world" as explained in the Rambam (and in *Gittin* there).

Therefore, it is more certain to say that the source is in *Gittin*, and since it emphasizes and repeats "the entire Torah," it is certainly not referring only to the laws of the Torah, but to the entire Torah.

And according to this, it will also be resolved simply why the beginning of the verse, "Its ways are ways of pleasantness," is also cited in the Gemara and the Rambam—unlike in the Midrash.

B. And since we have brought this up: this change (between the Gemara (Rambam) and the Midrash) requires a reason.

Now, the reason the Gemara brings (also) "Its ways are ways of pleasantness" is simple—because it is referring to the Mishnah regarding the laws of "ways" of peace, and it explains that the end of the verse, "peace," also applies to its beginning, "ways."

And regarding the Rambam, it can be said:

The difference between "ways" (*derachim*) and "paths" (*netivos*) is that a way is broad and divides and splits into several paths, for a path is a small and short trail, and likewise in Torah, there are generalities and details. If the Rambam had brought only "and all its paths are peace," there would be room to say that only the "paths" of Torah are for the sake of "making peace in the world," but the generalities of the Torah, and certainly "the entire Torah," are above this and are not in this category. Therefore, he brings also the beginning of the verse, "Its ways," etc., that the ways of the Torah also have the matter of peace (as is proven in the Gemara there that "peace" applies also to "ways," as mentioned above).

And there is still lacking the necessity that not only the generalities (the laws) of the Torah, but that "the entire Torah" has the matter of peace.

And this is explained by the precise language of the Rambam, who added the word (and the matter) "given"—the giving of the Torah, and not the Torah in and of itself, before its giving.

And the difference is explained in *Shabbos*, that just as the Torah in and of itself is a "hidden treasure," and it should have been "place Your glory upon the heavens" and not given to flesh and blood, and the fact that it was given (the entire Torah) is because the Ten Commandments, etc., had to be fulfilled—generalities that were stated at Sinai—and this is impossible except below.

And in the Midrash, it is satisfied with the end of the verse, in which is the *essence* of the proof (and the matter)—"peace."

C. And what seems more likely to me in the explanation of the Midrash, with a preface:

Seemingly, the verse brought in the Midrash is proof *to the contrary* to say that the Torah was compared only to peace,

For it is explicitly stated in this verse, "Its ways are ways of pleasantness," meaning that it was also compared to pleasantness.

And the explanation: The common denominator of what is discussed in *Gittin*, in the Midrash, and in the Rambam is that this is regarding the entire Torah in its totality, and this is compared only to peace, as it is written, "and all its paths are peace," unlike "its ways," where "all" is not stated.

And it can be said that according to this, the reasoning of the *makshan* (questioner) "say 'kufra'" will also be understood, even though it is stated "its ways are ways of pleasantness," because the change in this verse itself is emphasized, that it does not say "all its ways," even though it concludes "and all its paths are peace."

D. And now, if we do not emphasize in *Gittin* the repetition of the words "the entire Torah" (as mentioned above), but rather the simple reading of the *sugya* (discussion) that it is speaking of the laws of the Torah,

It can be said that the source of the Rambam is from the aforementioned Midrash, as mentioned above.

And one should add to this: The Midrash emphasizes that the Torah was *compared* to peace (and not "called," etc.),

For the benefit and necessity of a parable is when the teacher needs to explain the parable to a student whose intellect is small, and he brings a parable from a matter that is in proportion to the small intellect of the student, as is explained in many places regarding what is written, "and under His feet, etc."

And this is the precision of the Midrash that the Torah was *compared*, as it descended from the level of "hidden treasure" and was enclothed and given (in the language of the Rambam), etc., into the world. And this is clear.

(From the *sicha* of Shabbos Parshas Pinchas, 19 Tammuz, 5732)

[B"H](#_ftn_1856), 25 Tammuz, 5732

[Regarding your question](#_ftn_1857) – your traveling here is **not a matter at all**. And if it pertains to a vow, you should have the vow annulled according to the instruction of a Rav. And this is clear.

With blessings,

**M. Schneerson**

## 1048

1048

[B"H](#_ftn_1862), Motzaei Shabbos Kodesh, Parshas Chazon,
[The eve of](#_edn_414) the 5th of Menachem Av, 5732
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and blessings!

On this day, the day of the [histalkus](#_edn_415) of the AriZal HaChai, and especially as it marks four [hundred](#_edn_416) years since his histalkus,

It is a particularly opportune time to contemplate the upright paths which—in the words of our Alter Rebbe in his [Iggeres](#_edn_417) HaKodesh—he taught us from **his ways**, so that we may walk in **his paths**.

For this is surely one of the reasons why these specific ways and paths were revealed by him and his disciples, and became publicized throughout all the dispersions of Yisrael.

[And although](#_edn_419) who is there whose heart would dare to say that he can perform the holy avodah of the ["city](#_edn_420) and holy one who descended from heaven, the great, divine, and Chassidic Rabbi," the AriZal—

[Nevertheless,](#_edn_422) a small fraction and a mere glimmer of his immense goodness and light shines upon the entirety of Yisrael in every generation. Together with the revelation and publication of these practices and instructions, this also provides great strength and assistance to walk in these ways and paths, akin to the holy avodah mentioned above.

And here are two or three of these upright paths and general practices brought down in the writings of the AriZal:

**In Torah**: [I have seen](#_edn_423) my teacher, of blessed memory, exerting himself with the strength of a lion when he was engaged in Halacha, until he was weary and perspiring, etc. The Torah is called *tushiyah* (counsel/strength) because it exhausts the strength of the one who engages in it, and therefore it is fitting to toil and exhaust one’s strength while engaged in Halacha.

**In Mitzvos**: [And regarding](#_edn_425) tzedakah and the mitzvos, [he](#_ftn_1865) was not stingy at all, etc., as is written in the Zohar, Parshas Terumah.

(The [Zohar](#_edn_426) there states: "One who wishes to engage in a mitzvah, etc., should not engage in it empty-handed and for free, but rather, etc., with a complete vessel." See there.)

**In all Torah and Mitzvos**: [One should](#_edn_427) [rejoice](#_edn_428) while performing that mitzvah, etc. This is the meaning of the [verse](#_ftn_1867): "Because you did not serve Hashem your G-d [with joy](#_edn_430) and a good heart."

May it be the will of Hashem that this contemplation—in addition to contemplating [what](#_edn_431) the AriZal wrote in the introduction to Shaar HaMitzvos, that a person is obligated to fulfill all the mitzvos, and as long as he has not completed them, his soul is lacking and it is [said](#_ftn_1868) of him, "Anything that has a blemish shall not approach," [and likewise](#_edn_432) regarding engagement in Torah: to toil in *peshat, remez, derush,* and *sod*—in every aspect of them that he is able to grasp, to toil and to make for himself a teacher who will instruct him—

May this contemplation lead to action, to the actual fulfillment of the above with genuine joy,

—And he will surely succeed, as it is written: [In You,](#_edn_433) Hashem, [have I taken refuge;](#_edn_434) let me never be ashamed—

And this will also hasten the fulfillment of the prophecy that [these days](#_edn_435) will be turned into joy and gladness, with the coming of Mashiach Tzidkeinu, speedily in our days, truly.

With blessings,

**M. Schneerson**

***

Your [letter](#_ftn_1872) from the 11th of Tammuz, etc., was received. In response to your questions: Regarding the scope of the *takanos*—**in general**, the instruction is known to proceed from the easier to the more difficult, and [if you seize](#_ftn_1873) too much, you will not grasp it. In particular (what is "too much" in this case)—this requires an on-site assessment, of course, and to discuss it again from time to time if circumstances change, and this is understood.

It is simple that there must be a *seder* in the yeshiva for *D'Chassidus* "also" on Erev Shabbos, **and on the contrary**; however, this belongs to the administration of the yeshiva.

***

[Regarding](#_ftn_1874) the above, your letter from the 15th of Menachem Av and the preceding one, along with the enclosure, were received. Many thanks. [May the desire](#_ftn_1875) of Hashem succeed in their hands to establish the *neiros* of Chassidus and to expand them in both quantity and quality, and with good tidings in all of this.

## 1050

[B"H], 7 Menachem Av, 5732
Brooklyn, N.Y.

In response to your letter,

...The introduction of non-Jews who have not undergone a proper *giur* according to *halacha* into *Klal Yisrael*.

In addition to the many fundamental matters that have already been discussed [and written about] many times,

This also underscores, more and more, the profound pain and mourning of these current days, when non-Jews [entered][edn_436] the *Beis Hamikdash* (on the 7th of Av), leading up to the burning of the *Beis Hamikdash* on the day of Tisha B'Av.

[Every][edn_437] Jew—whoever they may be, and in whatever state of *Torah* and *mitzvos* they may find themselves—is a *Beis Hamikdash* of the *Ribono shel Olam*.

And the introduction of non-Jews (one, or two, or more) into *Klal Yisrael*, or assisting in this, or even standing on the sidelines and ["reassuring"][edn_438] oneself that it is not one's own affair,

Deepens even further the sorrow of the more than 1,900-year-old mourning of Tisha B'Av.

In the words of [Yirmiyahu][edn_439] the Prophet: "Shame has covered our faces, for strangers have come into the sanctuaries of the house of Hashem."

And it must lead everyone—or every woman, and especially those who have any influence whatsoever—to stop "reassuring" (confusing) themselves (and consequently, others as well), and lead to *teshuvah* and *maasim tovim* in practice, specifically regarding the matter of *giur* according to *halacha*,

And regarding the matter of "our sins" in general.

And by nullifying the cause—the "because of our sins" —the effect (the result)—"we were exiled from our land"—will be nullified,

[Immediately][edn_440] redeemed from the internal *galus* and from *galus* in the literal sense—through the *Geulah Amitis Ve'shleimah* through *Mashiach Tzidkeinu*.

With blessings.

## 10,551

[7 Menachem Av, 5732]

To speak in the beis medrash on Tisha B’Av (if that is not possible – on Shabbos Nachamu, since its theme is consolation regarding the matters of Tisha B’Av) about the fact that the entry of non-Jews, Heaven forbid, by way of a conversion not according to Halacha, into the ranks of the Jewish people—who are a [holy nation](#_ftn_1883) (analogous to the Beis Hamikdash)—highlights the memory of the matter of Tisha B’Av: the entry of non-Jews into the Beis Hamikdash, literally.

And therefore, etc., from every beis medrash, send a telegram:

1) To the Prime Minister, that conversion must be *kehalacha*.

2) To those **who voted in favor** (the entire beis medrash will choose for itself whether to include everyone, or only some) – encouragement, etc.

3) To [Rabbi Unterman](#_ftn_1884) *shlita* – a telegram, encouragement.

So that afterwards there will be **publicity** in the newspapers that on Tisha B’Av we spoke, etc., and sent, etc.

By the Kosel Hamaaravi – if possible – shifts throughout all 24 hours of Tisha B’Av: in Torah study and the recitation of Tehillim that are **permitted** on Tisha B’Av, of course. They should rotate every few hours – so that it does not harm the health of those fasting.

**In particular**

How good it is: Torah and Tzedakah [in accordance with what is written](#_ftn_1885), "Zion shall be redeemed with justice, and those who return to it with Tzedakah," [as discussed last year](#_ftn_1886).

## 10,552

10,552

B"H, 11 Menachem Av, 5732
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mrs. Tamar Bar-Lev, may she live

Blessings and peace!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter—albeit with a delay due to the press of many preoccupations, for which I ask your forgiveness—and I offer many thanks for your good wishes. In the meantime, you have surely received regards from here and my letter addressed to both you and your husband.

This is the place to comment on your expression, "my lowly status": While it is characteristic of the sons and daughters of Yisrael to humble themselves, as our Sages of blessed memory explained regarding the verse, "For you are the fewest of all peoples," nevertheless, every person must appreciate their standing and position in society, for the fulfillment of their role in its entirety depends upon this. I am referring to your position as a university lecturer, which gives you the privilege and the opportunity to influence the young people who listen to your teachings. We see in practice that whatever the subject matter may be, the students are influenced not only by the acquisition of knowledge in that field, but are also influenced by the personality of the lecturer.

You certainly know that one of the foundations of our faith and religion is that a single soul is an entire world, to the extent that our Sages of blessed memory, in their concise and poignant style, explain that this is the reason the first man was created alone—unlike all other creatures, which were created in multitudes—in order to inform all generations that one person is an entire world.

There is another point in this: since the profession of lecturing, whatever it may be, is a part of a person’s thought, and even of their practical life, it certainly has implications for their life in the true sense of "life"—I refer to a moral, pure, and holy life. Therefore, when Divine Providence has provided you with the opportunity to utilize your talents in the aforementioned direction, it is clear that this is done as part of your duty, and lecturing on the subject matter alone is not enough.

With blessings for success and with respect, and regards to your husband, may he live.
