And furthermore, and most importantly, may the parnassah that is provided for your expenses be spent on good, healthy, and joyous matters, including matters of Torah and mitzvos that gladden the [heart](#_ftn_1891). And the merit of the many assists him.

With respect and with blessings for success in doing good, tzedakah, and chessed with joy.

## 10,554

13 Menachem Av, 5732
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Mr. Chaim Grade,

Shalom u’vracha!

I feel guilty for not having responded until now to your letter from some time ago. The reason for this is that I wanted to reply at length and was waiting for a free moment. Unfortunately, however, my burdens only increase.

Now, however, since Rabbi Leib Groner informed me that he received a letter from your wife, tichyeh, I have torn myself away from various preoccupations in order to at least briefly thank you for your good wishes.

May it be the will of Hashem that what the Torah says be fulfilled for you and your wife: **"And I will bless those who bless you,"** for anyone who blesses a Jew is blessed by the Almighty Himself, whose blessing is, as is known, from His full, open, holy, and expansive hand.

It goes without saying that I follow what is printed by you in the *Forverts*. In addition to the content, it is for me a sign that your health is in order, and that you are continuing with your descriptions of the Jewish past—which is close in terms of time, but unfortunately much further away in content, especially in comparison with America.

May it be the will of Hashem that your writing should contribute to not letting the heritage be forgotten—the true heritage that stretches like a golden thread through tens and tens of generations; a heritage that every Jew receives through his grandfathers and great-grandfathers, up to the first Avos and Imahos: Avraham, Yitzchak, and Yaakov, Sarah, Rivkah, Rachel, and Leah.

And as is emphasized in the term "heritage," according to all laws, since one is a son and grandson, etc., regardless of what his own status and situation is, his measure, intelligence, or level of piety, etc.—he inherits the property of his father, grandfather, and great-grandfather, back to the beginning of the generations.

And the true heritage is not the physical property, which Bavel and Rome and **their** heirs took away, but the true Yiddishkeit that permeates the life of a Jew from birth.

And as has been discussed several times, the difference between the Jewish way of life and the way of life of other nations is that their faith touches upon and is limited to specific times and occasions, whether a Sunday or a Friday, but has nothing to do with eating, drinking, and weekdays. For Jews, however, Yiddishkeit is a way of life, a daily life that continues without any interruption. And on the path of *tzachus* (witticism)—*Chaim* (life) in a straight, uninterrupted path and continuity.

I was pleased to learn from your wife's letter that you are in contact with our friend, President Shazar, shlita. May it be the will of Hashem that there be good tidings regarding everyone in all details.

With respect and blessing for success,

A greeting to Mrs. Grade, tichyeh, and thanks once again for the greetings in her letter.

With respect and blessing.

## 1075

Regarding the conclusion of your letter concerning settling in a suitable place, etc., it is understood that from here it is impossible to determine whether my friends in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, can assist you in this. But certainly, if it is within their power to help, they will do so willingly. You should contact the Vaad of Kfar Chabad, and when they see this letter of mine, there will be no need for further recommendation; in general, there is no need for a recommendation, knowing their good hearts.

With blessings for health and for a good settlement in both material and spiritual matters alike, and for good tidings,

**M. Schneerson**

## 1061

1061

[B"H,] Erev Shabbos Mevarchim Chodesh Elul, 5732
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the Gathering of N'shei U’Bnos Chabad in our Holy Land,
May it be rebuilt speedily by Moshiach Tzidkeinu,
May Hashem grant them life,

Blessings and peace!

As we stand ready to enter the month of [Elul] — *Ani L’dodi V’dodi Li* ("I am to my Beloved and my Beloved is to me"), the month of conclusion and reckoning for the year passing, and of proper preparation for the year coming upon us and upon all Yisrael for good (the concept of *Ani L’dodi*), and [the month of] great success in all of this, as we pray [in the psalm recited twice daily] throughout this month: "[Hear,] Hashem, my voice when I call; be gracious to me and answer me" (the concept of *V’dodi Li*),

It is certain that the gathering taking place during the week of Rosh Chodesh Elul will be consistent with these two points: a righteous reckoning regarding the past, and preparation and good resolutions for the future, permeated with light and vitality.

And even though this is a great *avodah*, since [we have been commanded] regarding this *avodah*, it is certain and clear that beforehand, all the ability and strength were granted to perform it in actuality, in its fullness, and with joy; the matter depends only on one’s will.

The month of Elul is especially auspicious for all of this, as is known from the [explanation] of Rabbeinu HaZaken regarding Elul: It is like a king who, before entering the city, is met by the townspeople who go out to greet him in the field. At that time, anyone who wishes is permitted to go out to greet him, and he receives everyone with a pleasant countenance and shows a smiling face to all.

When the King is in the field with a pleasant countenance, it is certainly an opportune time for good and great resolutions, and to carry them out in their proper time and in their fullness.

Especially so for the women and daughters of Yisrael, who have been gifted with special traits regarding the emotion of the heart, and consequently, with a special influence regarding the *avodah* of the month, as stated in the aforementioned psalm: "[To You,] my **heart** said, 'Seek [My face]' (the inwardness of the heart)—Your face, Hashem, I will seek."

This is also hinted at in the *parsha* of the week of the gathering: "[And] his heart shall not turn away." A woman has a special influence on the heart of her husband to be an [*ezer*] (a help) to him, and through this, she is also the [*akeres*] (the mainstay) of the home. Regarding her [it is said,] "The wisdom of women builds her house"—the entire house: the men, the women, and all that is in the house.

It is understood that the education of daughters in this direction must begin from early childhood.

May it be the will that the gathering be successful in all that has been mentioned, and that it add strength and fortitude to all the activities of N'shei U’Bnos Chabad in our Holy Land and everywhere.

And may the Holy One, blessed be He, bless you in all of this and in all that is needed, [as it is written:] "In You, Hashem, I have taken refuge; let me never be ashamed."

With blessings for good tidings and for a *Kesivah V’Chasimah Tovah* for each and every one and for all family members—*shlita*,

**M. Schneerson**

## 10,752

10,752

[B"H](#_ftn_1938), Elul, 5732
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of the letter . . .

As we stand in the month of Elul, the month of days that are a time for teshuvah, and it is granted as an atonement for anyone who has erred and committed any sin throughout the year, that they may then return in teshuvah and be accepted; and in this month it is said, "Hashem is near to all who call upon Him."

Together with this, it is a month in which Bnei Yisrael and the King of Kings, the Holy One, Blessed be He, are in the analogy of a king who, before coming to the city, the people of the city go out to meet him and receive his face in the field. At that time, anyone who wishes is permitted (and able) to go out to receive his face, and he receives them all with a pleasant countenance and shows a smiling face to all.

Similarly, this is also the case with the blowing of the shofar, for in this too is expressed the uniqueness of this month, in which every day (except for Shabbos and Erev Rosh Hashanah—due to a special reason for them) we blow the shofar, etc., as it is said, "Elokim has ascended with the teruah," and it is said, "If a shofar is blown in the city, etc."

Its purpose is to awaken to teshuvah, and also—because this is what is done for a king when he is crowned.

In both instances, it is a loud voice that is heard and awakens each and every one, without distinction of status or situation, and even the "sleeping" and the "slumbering," until, in the words of the verse: "All inhabitants of the world and dwellers of the earth, etc., when a shofar is blown, you shall hear."

May it be the will that each and every one will go out (including and primarily—a going out from the limitation of their nature, their character traits, and their intellect) to receive the face of the King, will reveal the hidden ahavah that is in each one, and Hashem will shine His face upon them, and it will dwell and be revealed within them through engagement with and the letters of the Torah and mitzvos, and especially the mitzvah of tzedakah and chessed.

And they will raise their voice like a shofar to awaken the sleeping and rouse the slumbering, so that they too will do likewise.

As it is written: "I will declare Your arm to a generation, to all who come, Your gevurah and Your tzedakah, etc., for You have done great things, etc."

And the King will receive us with a pleasant countenance and fulfill our prayer: "Sound the great shofar for our freedom, and raise a banner to gather our exiles, and gather us together, etc."

In the true and complete Geulah through Melech HaMoshiach, very soon.

With the blessing of Kesivah V'chasimah Tovah,

**M. Schneerson**

10,763

B"H, Beginning of Elul, 5732
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mr. Beni Chen, may he live
Chairman, Israeli Students Organization
Bologna

Greetings and blessings!

I received your letter some time ago regarding the kosher restaurant in Bologna. Naturally, I immediately contacted various parties regarding this, and they reported to me on the developments and the significant improvement, etc. It is my hope that the promise of these parties to assist in every way possible has been fulfilled, and I would be pleased to receive a letter with good news in this regard.

As we enter the month of Elul, the explanation of the Alter Rebbe regarding the unique quality of the days of this month is well known, based on the parable of a king who, before entering the city, is met by the townspeople in the field. At that time, anyone who wishes to greet him is permitted to do so, and he receives them all with a friendly countenance and shows a smiling face to everyone, etc. (Likutei Torah; see 32b).

It is also known that it was the custom of the Alter Rebbe that when he would state a parable, it was precise even in its details. This applies as well to the aforementioned parable of the king in the field, from which one can generally learn many things, including the following:

In terms of spirituality, when a person is "in the field," this generally implies that he is engaged in matters that are not directly connected to the fulfillment of mitzvos or the study of our holy Torah. Yet, even then, it must be like a "field" from which [bread](#_ftn_1958) is produced. In spiritual terms, this is what our Sages of blessed memory—who, as is their holy custom, express a complete system in a few words—call: ["All](#_ftn_1959) your deeds should be for the sake of Heaven."

In the month of Elul, there is an additional point: it is a particularly opportune time to contemplate and see even more emphatically the matters of Hashgacha Pratis of the Creator of the world and its Guide, [and that](#_ftn_1960) there is a Master of this palace. This [contemplation](#_ftn_1961) should reach the point that it awakens love for the Creator, may He be blessed, just as we say in the Shema twice every day: ["And you shall love](#_ftn_1962) Hashem your G-d." This is what the Alter Rebbe also brings as a preface to the aforementioned parable, as the foundation and beginning of the entire maamar: ["I](#_ftn_1963) (every one of the Jewish people) [am to my Beloved (this is the Holy One, blessed be He)](#_ftn_1964) and my Beloved is to me" — the acronym for Elul. For if one calls the Holy One, blessed be He, "my Beloved," this shows that he is in a state of "And you shall love Hashem your G-d."

Furthermore, regarding the aforementioned parable, that at that time He receives everyone with a friendly countenance: in the spiritual application, since the month of Elul is a preface and preparation for Rosh Hashanah, this month is the opportune time to prepare and to receive a good and sweet year, both in body and soul.

It is surely unnecessary to emphasize to you the great importance of the young people and the youth in all the aforementioned matters, [and as has been discussed](#_ftn_1965) many times, the youth are not yet so accustomed to compromises and are prepared to wage battles for every challenge, and are not deterred even by a great challenge that requires significant effort, etc.

May it be His will that you bring good news regarding all the above. It is understood that everything written here is directed to all the members of the organization, may they live.

With respect and blessing for good news in all the above, and for a *Kesivah Vachasimah Tovah*.

In other words, they were risking their participation in the government for the sake of this amendment. This completely refutes the content of the letter.

How great is the power of smooth speech, that even when it is in complete contradiction to what that same person said himself in the very same breath, the "explanation," etc., etc., is still accepted.

I have not even touched upon the fact that the entire letter is the opposite of the [halachic ruling](#_ftn_1967) of the Chief Rabbinate from the year 5730, the opposite of the public proclamation of 32 rabbis in the year 5730, and so on. On the contrary, it is worth making a big "trask" (commotion) about this, for how is it possible that a minister writes in the aforementioned manner and contradicts his own words and those of his party, etc., etc.

It is surely known to you that in the decision of the aforementioned assembly during the day of the vote, there was a clause, phrased decisively, that for the next elections there would be an unchangeable condition that conversion must be "KeHalacha."

With respect and with a blessing for a *Kesivah V’Chasimah Tovah* for a good and sweet year.

## 1743

1743

B”H, 14 Elul, 5732
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, distinguished, and elevated individual, who seeks the good of his people and possesses noble character, a scion of a noble lineage, R’ Schneur [Zalman](#_ftn_1989) Shlita,

Peace and blessing!

I have just received your letter, in which you write with great emotion regarding the health of your [wife](#_ftn_1990) shlita. In the meantime, however, I have received word by telephone from Anash shlita that her health condition has improved. May it be the will of Hashem that by the time you receive this letter, it will have improved even further.

While your agitation is seemingly understandable, it is somewhat surprising. Often, irregularities in speech and the like are a result of the medications being administered—a temporary side effect. That is to say, when the dosage of the medication is reduced, or when they are discontinued entirely, the aforementioned phenomenon passes, and there is no basis for such agitation.

It is understood that the doctors take this into account as well, though sometimes the positive aspect of the medication outweighs the aforementioned negative effect. Furthermore, it is not always possible to predict with precision a patient’s reaction to certain medicinal substances, especially those to which they are not accustomed. This is in addition to the fundamental principle that [every](#_ftn_1991) person is a complete world unto themselves, and all general rules in medical treatment and the like are, [in the](#_ftn_1992) well-known phrasing, only speaking of "the majority."

Surely all of the above—and more—has been explained to you. Nevertheless, I have written to you in response to the emotional tone of your aforementioned letter.

I anticipate that my letter will be received on Chai Elul (or close to it)—the birthday of the two great luminaries, the Baal Shem Tov and the Alter Rebbe. Both of them emphasized the great value of the body of a Yid. As is well known, the Baal Shem Tov’s teaching on the verse "You shall surely help [him]" ([copied](#_ftn_1994) in the letters of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, in **Hayom Yom**, 28 Shevat), and the teaching of our Rebbe, the Alter Rebbe, in Tanya, end of Chapter 49—"And You have chosen us from every [nation](#_ftn_1995) and tongue"—refers to the material body.

With appreciation, honor, and a blessing for good tidings regarding all the above, I reiterate my blessing for a *Kesivah Vachasimah Tovah*, in both body and soul alike.

## 1078

1078

18 Elul, 5732
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the sons and daughters of Israel everywhere,
May Hashem keep them alive,

Greetings and blessings!

The time of preparation for Rosh Hashanah, the day when the Ribono shel Olam completed the creation of the world with the creation of the *bechir* (the choicest) of all creations—man—is also a time to reflect upon the creation and the manner of its creation. And—as with everything—to derive from it guidance for our daily life, *vehamaseh hu ha'ikar* (and the deed is the essential thing).

According to the will of the Creator, that there should be *mah rabu ma'asecha* (how manifold are Your works), the world consists of countless, distinct, and varied things. Yet, at the same time, all things possess certain internal traits that connect and unify them all into one unity.

This is also understandable, taking into account that all things in the world were created by the one and only Creator, through *Havayah Echad*; therefore, there is an internal and true unity in all things that He created, from the *domeim* (inanimate) to the *medaber* (speaking/human). It stands to reason that this unity is more apparent in things that belong to the same category: *domeim, tzomei'ach, chai,* or *medaber*.

Our Sages, of blessed memory, have highlighted this thought specifically in connection with the human species. Our Sages tell us that the Creator fashioned all people with the same *chosem* (seal), the seal of Adam HaRishon. Yet, at the same time, all people are distinct, such that there are no two people in the world who are identical in all respects: *b'parzufin damin* (their facial features are not alike), and people differ from one another in three things: *b'kol* (in voice), *b'mar'eh* (in appearance), and *b'da'as* (in intellect).

***

The principle of diversity alongside unity in all things of the world is valid also regarding *zman* (time). Time is divided into day and night, weekdays, Shabbos, and Yom Tov, etc., where each segment of time has its unique qualities and meanings in general, and for the person in particular. Yet, at the same time, there are matters that connect and unify all times into one continuum.

So too regarding Rosh Hashanah: all Rosh Hashanahs are the same in many matters, such as in the general instructions for the *shanah chadashah* (new year), and as it is often mentioned, that Rosh Hashanah is the "head" of the year. Together with this, every Rosh Hashanah is a new thing and unique—it brings a unique renewal into the world, new *kochos* (powers) and qualities.

The uniqueness of Rosh Hashanah is especially prominent compared to the majority of Rosh Hashanahs when *Yom Tov* of Rosh Hashanah falls on Shabbos—when the first day of Rosh Hashanah falls on Shabbos, as is the calendar arrangement this year. In this case, the *kedushah* of Rosh Hashanah unites with the *kedushah* of Shabbos, and gives this Rosh Hashanah a new meaning and content, which, as the "head" of the year, as mentioned above, must be reflected in the daily life of the entire year.

***

The general difference between the weekdays and Shabbos, and in particular regarding a person, is that the weekdays are workdays (*sheshes yamim ta'avod v'asisa kol melachtecha*) and Shabbos is a day without work (*lo sa'aseh kol melachah*), a day of rest.

Seemingly, this is difficult to understand: from birth, as the Torah points out, *adam l'amal yulad*—"man is born to toil" (with an interruption of rest, sleep, etc., in order to be able to continue with that *amal*). According to this, it would seem that Rosh Hashanah falling on Shabbos—where Rosh Hashanah also emphasizes its role as the "head" and leader of all and every day of the coming year—the concept of *lo sa'aseh kol melachah* is in contradiction to the principle of *adam l'amal yulad*?

One of the explanations that resolves this aforementioned contradiction is: a person is composed of all sorts of different things and traits, and in general—of body and *neshamah*. Consequently, in all his matters and activities, there is this composition of body and *neshamah*; in other words—*ruchniyus* and *gashmiyus*. Also in the matter of *adam l'amal yulad*, there is *amal gashmi* (physical toil) and *amal ruchni* (spiritual toil), or as our Sages, of blessed memory, call it: *amal melachah* and *amal Torah*. More specifically: the division of *gashmiyus* and *ruchniyus* exists in both types of *amal*; in *amal melachah* (as well as in *amal Torah*) there is *amal gashmi* and *amal ruchni*, and in each of them—the spiritual side of it and the physical side of it.

And analogously, just as Shabbos is a Jew’s *adam l'amal yulad* in *amal Torah*—so too is the special instruction of *Yom Tov* of Rosh Hashanah falling on Shabbos: that in all the days of the coming year, the primary *amal* should be in *amal Torah* (and *mitzvos*), and also in *amal melachah*, the *ruchniyus* that is within it should be brought out and emphasized.

In other words: it is expected of every Jew, man or woman, young or old, that he should bring "Shabbos-dikkeit" into his entire *amal*—also into the weekday *melachos*; to bring *ruchniyus* and *kedushah* also into the ordinary and weekday matters of daily life, until they become completely permeated with "Shabbos-dikkeit."

To give a simple example: when someone has a job, business, etc., the *kavanah* in it is the earnings, *parnasah*. But there must be the *ruchniyus* and *neshamah* of it, the *kol ma'asecha l'shem shamayim* (all your deeds for the sake of Heaven): one must give *tzedakah*, have a calm head to learn Torah, pay tuition for children to learn Torah, etc.—he occupies himself with his *amal* in order to achieve these aforementioned goals.

And when he becomes **permeated** with this spiritual *kavanah*—it is self-understood that his *amal* does not hinder him from learning Torah and fulfilling *mitzvos*, that he will give the best and finest for *tzedakah*, etc.

***

One might ask, how can everyone, and furthermore—every day of an entire year, reach such a *madreigah*? The answer is understandable to everyone: since the Creator, the Creator of man, gave him this instruction, it is certain that everyone, regardless of his upbringing and *madreigah*, has previously received the *kochos* to be able to carry this out in life, and even more—*b'simchah* and *b'tuv leivav*.

And as it is said: (since) *bach Havayah chasisi*—(it is certain that) *al evoshah l'olam*.

And especially since this begins from Rosh Hashanah—when Jews crown the Creator, *umalkuso* they accept upon themselves with will, then every Jew is—*eved melech*—*melech*.

With blessings for *kesivah v'chasimah tovah* for a good and sweet year,

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 1079

1079

B"H, 18 Elul, 5732
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, learned, and diligent in his holy work,
Rabbi Shmuel [Azimov](#_ftn_2025)
Greetings and blessings!

It was a pleasure to learn of the development of the work of Tzeirei Agudas Chabad in Paris and its surroundings. My hope is strong that they will not be satisfied with the current situation, and that the [statement of our Sages](#_ftn_2026) will be fulfilled in each of them: "He who has one hundred, wants two hundred; he who has two hundred, wants four hundred."

This is especially relevant now that the purchase of the Tzeirei Agudas Chabad headquarters has been realized, in a good and auspicious hour.

The development of the work in the present—and all the more so the development in the future, according to the hope I mentioned—requires the full activity of all those who have merited and succeeded in working in this until now, in addition to the inclusion of new individuals and forces suited for this. The magnitude of the merit surely requires no explanation.

2) Since success depends on a person’s *ratzon*, and as is explained at length in *Chassidus* that the *ratzon* governs all the powers of the soul—starting with *Chabad*—[as our Sages said](#_ftn_2028), "A person should always study in a place that his heart desires," and a person’s *ratzon* is stronger when he feels that it is his own handiwork (with the help of Hashem), there must be a significant degree of autonomy. Regarding the present: autonomy in the activities connected to the shul on Rue Dieu. I am certain that not only will there be no loss in this, but on the contrary, this autonomy will assist the development of those activities, and also the development of the activities at the Tzeirei Agudas Chabad headquarters, as those active at the headquarters will be able to concentrate more on the activities of that house.

3) Since the esteemed, G-d-fearing, learned, and diligent Rabbi Pinchas Gedaliah [Paster] has stood at the head of the Rue Dieu branch activities until now and has succeeded, he will surely continue in this from here on as well—and on the contrary, in a manner of "increasing and growing" as mentioned above. As stated, if cooperation from the headquarters and the activists there is required for these activities, they will **certainly** do so with a generous eye and a good heart, and "each man will help his brother" [1](#_ftn_2029).

4) In order to facilitate the expansion of the activities, just as the central office supports the budget of the headquarters from time to time, it will do so regarding the activities of the Rue Dieu branch as well. The amount, the regularity of this, and the timing shall be as the administration of the central office sees fit.

5) Should there be differences of opinion between the administration of the headquarters and the administration of the Rue Dieu branch, they shall bring the matters before the esteemed Rabbis and Chassidim of *Anash* in France: Rabbi N. Nemoynov, Rabbi R. Pevzner, and Rabbi Y. Goldberg, who shall decide the matter, as is customary in Israel. It is also understood that the three aforementioned individuals have the authority to delegate the decision to two of them, etc., especially if not all of them are present in the city at the necessary time.

With blessings for success, and in accordance with the words of our Alter Rebbe in the holy *Tanya* (Chapter 32), that when we are all together, this draws down "Bless us, our Father," especially since the merit of the many assists them in spreading the *maayanos* within the framework of spreading Yiddishkeit in general, in a manner of "increasing and growing" and light.

With blessings for good news regarding all the above, and for a *Kesivah V'chasimah Tovah* for a good and sweet year.

1080

1080

[B"H](#_ftn_2030), 20 Elul, 5732
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mr. Eli and his wife, Mrs. Amikam,

Shalom u’Bracha!

I have just received your precious gift, the three volumes of the Talmud with English translation, along with your birthday wishes.

I begin by returning the blessing to the sender, for my words are already stated in our Torah—the Torah of truth and the Torah of life: "I will bless those who bless you," meaning that Hashem, the Source of blessing, blesses those who bless others with the blessing of the Holy One, Blessed be He, from His full, open, holy, and expansive hand.

In the phrasing of our Sages, "merit is brought about through the meritorious." Since we have entered the month of Elul, and the explanation of the Alter Rebbe regarding the unique quality of the days of this month is well-known—based on the parable of a king who, before entering his city, is greeted by the townspeople in the field, at which time anyone who wishes may greet him, and he receives them all with a pleasant countenance and shows a smiling face to everyone, etc. (Likutei Torah, Parshas Re’eh 32b)—may it be Hashem’s will that He fulfill your heart’s desires for the good, and in the style of the parable, with a pleasant countenance.

The primary point is that you should merit to succeed in utilizing the talents with which you have been gifted for the integrity of the people and the land, under the essential condition of this integrity: the integrity of our Torah, which, as mentioned, is called the Torah of truth. And truth precludes compromise—not only compromise or concession regarding the majority of a matter or half of it, but any compromise whatsoever. And since the Torah was given specifically to human beings and was given by the Creator of man who knows his nature, it is certain that beforehand, man was given the permission and the ability to utilize all possibilities in the aforementioned direction. Furthermore, this should be done with joy, in the style of the verse, "Serve Hashem with joy," and the matter depends on nothing but one’s will.

Great is the merit of all those who have influence in their environment, and even in a distant environment, through writing, publishing, etc.

I recall that you told me about your son, may he live, who is also gifted with the talent for writing and publishing, etc. Please be so kind as to convey to him my regards and the points from this letter that are relevant to him as well. If I may say, because your son is closer to the youth and the younger generation, his responsibility—and his merit—is even greater.

I will conclude with renewed thanks for the aforementioned gift, and with the blessing of *Kesivah v’Chasimah Tovah* for you and all that is yours.

With respect and blessing for good tidings,

**M. Schneerson**

## 10780

10780

B”H, Days of Selichos, 5732
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the Honorable Rabbi, the Chassid, G-d-fearing and scholarly, etc.,
Rabbi Shlomo Goren
Chief Rabbi and Av Beis Din of Tel Aviv-Jaffa and the District

Greetings and blessings!

As we approach the New Year, which comes upon us and all of Israel for good and for blessing, I hereby express my blessing to your honor and to all who are yours: a blessing of *Kesivah v’Chasimah Tovah* for a good and sweet year, in both material and spiritual matters.

With blessings.

P.S. Since I wish to maintain the relationship between us, and also in accordance with a general instruction of our holy Torah, I do not want the following to become known to your honor from a third party; therefore, I am writing this myself. It is as follows: Consistent with my position during the previous elections for the Chief Rabbinate—a position based on what is explained in many places, including the well-known *Shu"t Chasam Sofer*—I am against the removal of a Rabbi from his position upon the conclusion of a contract term or similar circumstances. This does not, G-d forbid, reflect poorly on the candidates running against him, just as I wrote in the aforementioned previous elections.

After requesting your honor’s forgiveness for what I am about to write—which, on the face of it, goes against the saying of our Alter Rebbe, "One does not get into a fight with advice"—nevertheless, based on our relationship, I feel I cannot remain silent on this. It is as follows: In addition to what is written above—which is also why I hoped that your honor would withdraw your candidacy, and why I waited to publicize my position on this, in the hope that perhaps it might help—there is another fundamental point regarding the unique situation in these elections: the candidacy of your honor is being exploited for a battle against precision in observing *Halacha*. In all matters of *Kiddush Hashem*, etc., what is primarily relevant is the interpretation and reaction of the ten Jews [of the community]; this is why even the *Amora'im*, the pillars of the world, would say, "If I were to take...". Furthermore, it is precisely those circles known for their stance on all matters of Torah and *mitzvos* who are supporting and agitating, etc., for your honor’s candidacy. Surely, for someone of your stature, no further explanation is needed, especially since it is difficult for me in general to "get into a fight" over these matters.

## 10 Tetzaveh

[5732]

(1) Regarding a man having the same name as the first husband—

See what is brought in *Sefer Shulchan HaEzer*, section 1, paragraph 12 (from *Sefer Chochmas HaNefesh*) regarding the name of a second **wife** being the same as the first—but the book is not before me. For the time being, I have not found anything similar regarding the names of a second and first **husband**.

In general, there is a distinction between a man and a woman, based on what is explained in many places (*Orach Chaim* 206, *Even HaEzer* 25) that this **interpretation** applies **only** to the thought (mind) of the man (even though, in passing—and not as a definitive ruling—the mind of the woman is also mentioned (*Pesachim* 112a)).

Furthermore, from the fact that the reason (that the name awakens the mind) is **not** mentioned even regarding a man—regarding the names of a bride and her mother-in-law—it implies that we are not concerned about this.

Nevertheless, if the name is the same, then [from the perspective of](#_ftn_2065) "it is good," etc.

(2) Regarding reciting Kaddish Yatom after Kiddush Levanah—

In the *Shelah* (*Shaar HaOsios*, page 74b), the **conclusion** of Kiddush Levanah is with the words of our Sages (Abaye), and therefore—Kaddish DeRabbanan. This is also in the *Siddur* of the Yaavetz. For us, since we conclude (according to the *Siddur* of the Arizal and others) with *Aleinu*, it is simple that Kaddish Yatom should be said. This is also stated explicitly in the *Siddur Kol Yaakov*, and elsewhere.

(3) I will mention at the Tziyun the contents of your letter, may you live.

Since, due to the pressures, etc., the writing of a structured letter has been delayed, I requested to telephone, and I ask for your forgiveness.

And now, after writing the above, I saw in the "Additional Warnings" in the manuscript for the *Tzava'ah* (Will) of Rabbi Yehuda HeChassid [printed in *Sefer Chassidim*—Jerusalem 5717, page 30], and it states:

"If a man has a wife and she dies, he should not marry another whose name is the same as the first; or if a husband dies, the woman should not take a husband whose name is the same as the first, for they will think of the first, and if this happens, they will never be in a good state, or one of them will die soon."

And in the editor's note there: See *Sefer Chochmas HaNefesh* by the Rokeach, 24b.

## 10,511

[5732]

When a member of Bnei Yisrael lives in a manner that is not in accordance with the Creator’s command to Bnei Yisrael, it is understood that he does not feel well (even if he is unaware of this and is mistaken regarding the **true** cause).

Therefore, first and foremost, one must rectify the aforementioned. And it is promised to **each and every one**—[you have labored](#_ftn_2079) **and you have found**.

Nevertheless, there must be the [precedence](#_ftn_2080) of **naaseh** (—**in actual practice**) over **nishma** (understanding through intellectual inquiry, etc.). [Especially](#_ftn_2081) since when a person is hungry (for his physical or spiritual sustenance), he is incapable of delving deeply and weighing intellectual matters and the like—which is not the case after he has satisfied his hunger. Therefore, postpone the **intellectual** resolution of questions regarding Yiddishkeit, etc., until you are established in observance in actual practice.

## 10,523

[5732]

It is certainly understood (and common) that youth are thirsty to find a challenge, something new, etc. Moreover, there is a basis for this in the directive of Chazal to act "like one who **desires** to act," meaning to utilize the strengths granted to one **to their fullest extent**.

On the other hand, it is also understood and **obvious** that it is not the right approach **at all** to seek out a challenge before arming oneself with the weaponry necessary to overcome it and rectify it (or at the very least, to know that there are **good** prospects for doing so)—and not to be defeated by it (for then, further damage will be added to the world and to oneself, etc.). In the language of Chazal, it is forbidden for a person to stand in a place of danger, and even more so—as in the prayer we recite **before** the [main] davening: "Do not bring me into a test."

Regarding Jews—and especially in our era, with this "secular education" mentioned above, and college in general—this is analogous to a healthy person who says that he has lived his whole life in healthy conditions, has been healthy, and has only seen healthy people, and consequently is not utilizing his strengths at all. What, then, is the purpose of his life? Therefore, he thinks he should move his residence to a place of contagious diseases, where there is danger, and only after that attempt to see if he is capable of beginning to study the science of medicine in that place, etc. The analogy is understood.

There is a **ready-made** challenge for daughters of Bnei Yisrael who are like her, which one is **obligated** to overcome, and that is: the shortcomings she mentions regarding the atmosphere of the seminaries (and schools in general) are **possible** to rectify, but only by those who have felt the shortcoming **themselves** and have been affected by it. However, like any good achievement, this requires self-preparation—to the point of **toil** in this. My meaning is: to acquire sufficient knowledge in the subjects taught in the seminaries, expertise in pedagogy, a firm resolve not to be discouraged if the fruits are not seen immediately, and not to be embarrassed by those who mock—and after that, to begin changing the atmosphere, etc., with enthusiasm and mesiras nefesh. And certainly, the Ribono shel Olam will grant success.

## 10,524

[5732]

**Regarding Section A.** It is understood that the concern regarding "revealing faces" (misinterpreting) the word "Halacha" in a way that is contrary to Halacha is valid. However, in the current situation, this is the best **possible** phrasing, since they are arguing for the "status quo," claiming that for the **entire** duration until now, this is how it was written in the instructions of **their own Ministry of Interior, and they committed** to maintaining the status quo. **Any** other phrasing would be an innovation and a loosening of the reins (especially since they are **already** trying to appease the "zealots" by proposing the phrasing "conversion according to the Chief Rabbinate." And a word to the wise is sufficient).

**Regarding Section B.** Any matter that can add to the strengthening of Torah and mitzvos, etc., is understood to be worthwhile (though one must consider the cost against the gain, etc.—the concern that, as is the way of those who distort, etc., they will respond: "Since Rashi does not explain the passage this way, this is proof that regarding the Conservatives, etc., Rashi’s opinion is also, etc." And I have already heard "logic" even more devoid of logic than that).

**Regarding Section C.** I read it in the "Yid," and the impression is understood. However, there is room to say that **now** it is better that the matters subside and not be mentioned again, even as a passing thought.

Many years ago, there was—if I recall correctly—a work on the teachings of the Baal Shem Tov, arranged alphabetically, but I only saw one volume. Seemingly, it would be worthwhile to continue it. And if those who transgress His will, G-d forbid, add to the book of darkness, how much more so must there be an addition to the book of light, and especially from the **Luminary** of the Torah. And the merit of the public assists.

## 10,527

10,527

[5732]

[It is understood]( #_ftn_2100) that there is **no basis at all** to be afraid to write to me—for my effort is to help to the best of my ability, and not, Heaven forbid, to burden or rebuke, or anything of that sort.

During **transitional** periods in a person’s life (from childhood to maturity, from maturity to adulthood, etc.), one is more sensitive and less stable. Therefore, it is **normal** that new questions or doubts arise at such times. When the period passes, the person will find the solution themselves, and easily; but during the transition, it seems to them that it is a great doubt, etc. Through speaking with another, they will explain that the solution is simple, etc. Therefore, what you are experiencing is the case for **many people**, and it passes with time.

Another, and greater, reason in your case is: **when you began** to "feel uncomfortable" in a minor way, instead of **increasing** your involvement in matters that strengthen Bnei Yisrael (which is Torah and mitzvos), you—as you wrote—**decreased** them! The results are understandable. And even though this decrease came about through the enticement of the *yetzer hara*—arguing that according to his **calculation** you do not deserve such a punishment at all (as you feel)—this is the opposite of integrity toward yourself. Therefore, you feel you must "settle the score," etc. And what connection is there, anyway, between keeping Torah and mitzvos and your feelings—that keeping them would help in this matter? (And to say that this is a matter of a *nissayon*—the *yetzer hara* does not agree with that, obviously.)

With a little contemplation, it is understood that this is an enticement of a "king who is old and **foolish**": 1) Perhaps it is a *nissayon*, as mentioned above. 2) The **yetzer hara’s** calculation that you do not deserve this, etc.—is a false calculation. And regarding the connection mentioned above: everyone (**and it is simple** that you are included in this) believes with simple faith, as is written in many places **and explained**, that our Torah is a Torah of kindness, and it is intended to benefit a person even in this world—a true good. (Therefore, it is possible that at first it seems difficult to fulfill—but the Torah **knows that specifically** through this, a great good will come after some time.)

It is also simple that the intellect of the Torah is greater and deeper than the intellect of the wisest person (and especially than the intellect of a person who is **personally involved** in the matter). Therefore, it is no wonder **at all** if it happens that a person does not understand for the moment what is good **for them** in this world by following the Torah’s instruction. (And if people follow a doctor’s instruction to take a [pill]( #_ftn_2101) that is not sweet, how much more so must one follow the instructions of the Torah.)

[Clarifying your doubts and lifting your spirits—specifically through conversation and discussion with a *bochur* about this, as you have already done several times—is, according to Torah, neither desirable nor advisable, neither for you nor for him. From this it is also understood: 1) that this is not good for you, 2) **that certainly** you will find another permitted way to achieve the aforementioned, if you wish.]

Another reason for your feeling, etc. (and this is also seen in your letter itself): throughout all the pages, not a single word was mentioned, not even a hint, regarding the **holy obligation** to help others—especially those who were not fortunate enough to have parents who educated them in the path of Torah and mitzvos, to inform them what Judaism is, **etc.**—even though (as discussed at some length at the *farbrengen*) they are **crying out** for help.

To such an extent has the *yetzer hara* succeeded in enticing you to be interested only in yourself and your feelings.

When you engage in the rescue of the aforementioned—at least by way of mediation—and do so with vitality and joy (over the wonderful **privilege** and ability that has been granted to you in this), your feelings will certainly improve, etc.

*

I have been delayed (which has been prolonged significantly due to the pressures of the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt, the matters of the year of the 70th anniversary, **and more**), and in this too, you can see how the enticement-explanation of the *yetzer hara* is the opposite of the truth. *Kal v'chomer.*

I will mention you at the holy gravesite and await good news.

## 10,251

[5732]

The later authorities [1] have raised a difficulty regarding the words of the Rambam, Hilchos Temidin U’Musafin, Chapter 8, Halacha 15, which states that the *Shtei HaLechem* (Two Loaves) and the sheep are mutually dependent—if the sheep are lost, the loaves are lost, and they must bring other loaves and other sheep. How is this possible? We hold that the baking of the *Shtei HaLechem* does not override *Yom Tov*, and even if they were rendered *pasul* (disqualified), we do not bring others, as is evident in *Yoma* 21a regarding the fact that no *pasul* was found in the *Shtei HaLechem*, and in Rashi there. This is also stated in *Menachos* 46a, that one brings other loaves. See *Responsa Imrei Yosher*, Vol. 2, Siman 127, where he cites this difficulty in the name of the Gaon of Kotzk.

Regarding the attempt to resolve this there (in the section *V’Beikara*), based on the opinion of the Tosafos in *Yoma* 46a (*s.v. Aval*), which suggests that if there was an *ones* (unavoidable circumstance) and they did not offer the communal sacrifice, they may offer it the next day—see the *Mishneh Lamelech*, Chapter 1 of *Hilchos Temidin U’Musafin*, who explains that the rule "once its time has passed, its sacrifice is nullified" applies only when there was no *ones*—if so, it could be argued that if the loaves were disqualified due to an *ones*, they could offer the sheep and the loaves the next day, on a weekday. However, the words of the *Mishneh Lamelech* on this require further study, as I have written in my book *Tal Torah*, *Yoma* 46, that *musafin* certainly cannot be offered once their time has passed. See also Rambam, *Hilchos Temidin U’Musafin*, Chapter 5, Halacha 2, where it is explicitly stated that any communal sacrifice whose time has passed is nullified, and it is implied there that this applies even in a case of total *ones*, and likewise for *temidin*. See what I wrote in the aforementioned *Tal Torah* regarding *temidin*; in any event, for *musafin* and *Shtei HaLechem*, this is certainly the law, as explained in *Temurah* 14a, that once its time has passed, the sacrifice is nullified.

Now, from what the *Mishneh Lamelech* says—that if there is an *ones*, we do not say "once its time has passed, its sacrifice is nullified" regarding *temidin*—it is evident from the words of the Alter Rebbe in his *Shulchan Aruch*, *Hilchos Tefillah*, Siman 108, Section 2, that he holds the opposite. He writes: "If one erred or was prevented by an *ones* and did not daven *Mincha*, he must daven *Maariv* twice—the first for *Maariv* and the second as a *tashlumin* (make-up). And even though the *tefillos* correspond to the sacrifices, we do not say 'once its time has passed, its sacrifice is nullified,' because the *tefillos* are requests for mercy, and whenever one davens, he receives the reward for *tefillah*, except that he does not receive the reward for *tefillah* at its proper time." It is clear from this that even though one was prevented by an *ones*, we *do* say "once its time has passed, its sacrifice is nullified" even regarding *temidin*, for he begins with "If one erred or was prevented by an *ones*" and regarding this he says [2] "we do not say 'once its time has passed, its sacrifice is nullified.'" It is explicitly clear from his language that even regarding *temidin*, and even if one was prevented by an *ones*, we *do* say that the sacrifice is nullified—contrary to the words of the aforementioned *Mishneh Lamelech* and the words of the Tosafos in *Yoma* 46a, which imply that regarding *temidin*, we do not say it is nullified if there was an *ones*. This requires study.

However, in the *Rashba* on *Menachos* 4a, regarding the statement of Reish Lakish that if one performed the *kometz* (handful) of the *Omer* offering not for its own sake, it is valid, etc., and he brought another *Omer* offering—the *Rashba* wonders in his *Chiddushim* there how one can offer another *mincha* on that same day, when its harvesting is at night; if so, one must wait until another *mincha* is harvested at night. I have not merited to understand this, for what relevance is there to say we should wait until the next day to harvest a second one at night, which is after the day of the *Omer* offering [when] the day of its offering has already passed?

If so, it is evident from the words of the *Rashba* that if there was an *ones* such that they could not offer the *Omer* at its proper time, they can offer it the next day [3], and we do not say in this case that "once its time has passed, its sacrifice is nullified." The reason may be that the principle "once its time has passed, its sacrifice is nullified," which we derive in *Temurah* 14a from "in its time" or "the burnt offering of Shabbos in its Shabbos," applies specifically to *musafin* or *temidin* for which those verses were stated. But regarding the *Omer*, we do not find this, so it can be said that we do not say it is nullified. The reason may be that we do not derive it from *temidin* and *musafin*—that we should say it is nullified—because it [the *Omer*] permits [the new grain]. See *Menachos* 5b: "Just as the *Omer* offering, for it permits the new grain." Therefore, the *Rashba* correctly says that the *Omer* can be offered the next day as well.

According to this, it can be said that the *Shtei HaLechem* permits bringing *menachos* to the *Mikdash*. Even though they only permit it *lechatchilah* (initially), as explained in *Menachos* 68b, nevertheless, since it permits it *lechatchilah*, we also do not derive it from *temidin* and *musafin*, and if *tumah* or an *ones* occurred, they can offer it the next day.

Consequently, the words of the Rambam are resolved: how can one bring other loaves on *Yom Tov*, given that the baking of the *Shtei HaLechem* does not override *Yom Tov*? [The answer is] that if there was an *ones* and they did not offer them, they can offer them the next day.

## 10,538 

 B"H, Zos Chanukah, 5732
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mr. Tzvi, shiyeh,
Peace and blessing!

[Russian]

With blessings for success in your arrangements and for setting fixed times for Torah study—both in Nigleh and Chassidus—every single day, and for increasing in this as per the directives of these days of Chanukah, and for good tidings,

**M. Schneerson**

[Free Translation]

In response to your letter, may Hashem grant that you be settled successfully in both spiritual and material matters, and in that specific order, since for a Jew the primary focus is the spiritual, and only afterward is there room for the material. However, even the material must be transformed into spirituality, or in the language of Chassidus—"to make a *keli* for Elokus."

Regarding teaching subjects, this depends on your preparation, the nature of the students, etc. But in general, to teach three subjects seems like too much.

In response to your question as to whether, when a person is punished or is suffering, he should strive to be rid of it or whether he should bear it without complaint—it is self-evident that everyone must strive to improve their situation, and all the more so a group or a nation. This is, after all, part of the instructions of the Torah: "And you shall guard yourselves very well". At the same time, until he succeeds in improving his situation, he must bear it without complaint, since everything in the world is by *hashgacha pratis* and with justice and righteousness.

There is no contradiction in what is written above, for it is possible that the unpleasant situation is a form of trial, and in truth, something good is hidden within it. But even if it is a punishment, in many cases it is possible to soften or even completely nullify the punishment through *teshuvah*.

I hope that when you discuss this with a *mashpia* of Tomchei Temimim, it will be clearer than what can be conveyed in a letter.

## 10546

[10546](#_ftn_2127)

B"H, 23 Sivan, 5732
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mrs. Rosa Shlansky, may she live and be well,

Greetings and blessings!

[Russian]

[Free translation]

I have just received your letter, which apparently arrived via regular mail rather than airmail.

Thank you very much for your good wishes, especially those relating to memories of the past—or, as they say in such cases, the distant past. In this instance, due to the revolutions and upheavals that have occurred since those times, the distance of that past is far greater than the distance measured by the number of years that have passed [since then](#_ftn_2128).

I was pleased to read in your letter that you are engaged in creative work in your field, and I wish you success in this and all the best in everything.

With regards and best wishes.

## 10,747

10,747

B"H, 3 Tammuz, 5732
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mrs. Rivka, may she live,
Nachalat Har Chabad 1165/7
Kiryat Malachi

Blessings and peace!

[Russian]

With blessings for success and good tidings.

[Free Translation]

In response to your letter,

May Hashem grant that each of you and the entire family be settled in the best possible way, both materially and spiritually.

It is self-understood that the best settlement is in Kiryat Malachi. However, since there are unknown details regarding the apartments there—whether they are available now or will become available in the near future—this matter should be clarified locally.

If there is no apartment in Kiryat Malachi, you should make efforts in Kfar Chabad or in the Shikun Chabad in Lod.

I hope and am confident that your studies at the Kfar Chabad seminary will be successful, and that you will study there until you complete the seminary.

May Hashem grant that you have good news regarding all that was written above.

## 10,548

10,548

B”H, 3 Tammuz, 5732
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mr. L., may he live and be well,

Shalom u’Bracha!

[Russian]

With blessings for good tidings, with peace of mind and a good heart.

[Free Translation]

In response to your letter,

May Hashem grant that your health improves in the near future. I assume you are following the doctors’ instructions fully. I hope that your mood will also improve, and that this will be evident in your next letter. After all, this, too, has a positive influence on one’s state of health and the success of the medical treatment.

It is understood that your mood is, in part, dependent on the difficulty of adjusting to a new country and new circumstances—a difficulty experienced by every immigrant. Yet, these difficulties diminish automatically with each passing day, especially when the immigrant desires to overcome them. And for a Jew who has striven and labored, and ultimately succeeded with the help of Hashem in coming to Eretz Yisrael, the Holy Land, this desire to acclimate quickly should be all the more powerful.

Every person is subject to fluctuations in mood and desire, but ultimately, the primary, inner will rises to the surface and remains—in your case, the desire to move to Eretz Yisrael, which is evidenced by your actions, submitting the application, etc., to receive the immigration permit.

I hope that by the time you receive this letter, there will be a change for the better, and I thank you in advance for the good news regarding all that was written above.

## 10,749

10,749

B"H, 7 Tammuz, 5732

Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

[Russian]

With blessings.

[Free Translation]

In response to your letter of 28 Sivan—and I am responding out of turn, in accordance with the serious nature of the issue:

1) According to the commandment of our holy Torah, one must be extremely careful regarding *lashon hara*, especially when it concerns the honor of a *bas Yisrael*.

2) When it concerns personal life, the caution must be at a maximum level. Since no person can be objective if they are personally involved, and since there are specific laws in the *Shulchan Aruch* regarding the honor of a *bas Yisrael*, you must therefore consult a Rav and receive a precise *psak* from him. Until then, stop speaking about this.

3) Regarding your personal issue, since there were conditions involved, you must also seek the guidance of a Rav in this matter.

## 10,553 

B”H, Rosh Chodesh Elul, 5732
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Chaya, may she live,
Tziporah, may she live,

Blessings and peace!

[Russian]

May you be inscribed and sealed for a good and sweet year.

[Russian]

[Free translation]

I received your letter, as well as the telegram regarding your successful arrival in Eretz Yisrael.

May Hashem grant that each of you continues to actualize your daily life in the full sense of Yiddishkeit, and especially the observance of mitzvos, including the study of Torah, as it should be, and at such a level that you will serve as a good example to all those in your surroundings. Especially since your parents educated you with mesiras nefesh, and each of you must justify this mesiras nefesh to the fullest extent. May Hashem grant that you do so in good health and under good conditions.

As we are at the beginning of the month of Elul, you are surely aware of the explanation of our Rebbe [the Alter Rebbe] regarding the special character of this month, that it is like a king who is in the field, etc.

May Hashem grant the fulfillment of your hearts' desires for the good.

And may you be inscribed and sealed for a good and sweet year.

In your account of the discussion at Camp Emunah here, you mention that you were asked how one can demand that people live as religious Jews, when some of them do not even treat other Jews with proper human decency.

The answer to this question is simple, as explained in several places, and here are two examples:

1) When one meets a person leaving a hospital walking with a limp, after a long stay and medical treatment there, an outsider who does not know what a hospital is, or how this limping man was before and without the treatment, could pose the same question: What is the benefit of the treatment in the hospital, and the waste of time and money on it, if after the stay there the man is limping? But if he knew that while in the hospital he was cured of a serious heart condition and a serious mental illness that had placed him in mortal danger, and the treatment had not yet succeeded in healing his legs, he would be filled with admiration for the success of the hospital and its medical methods.

2) A second example: When one meets a person who is not healthy, it is illogical to say that since he is not healthy in one part of his body, there is no need to protect him from other illnesses, or—worse—to act to worsen the health of the rest of his body. On the contrary, strengthening the health of the rest of the body will influence—sometimes indirectly—the healing of the entire body.

## 10,554

[10,554](#_ftn_2133)

B"H, 4 Elul, 5732
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mr. Yaakov, shiyeh,

Shalom u’vrachah!

[Russian]

[Free translation]

After a long hiatus, I received your letter of 12.7.72, in which you also mention the matter of the clinic.

In general, it is a pity that this matter has dragged on for so long, as I recall it being discussed many times. As long as the plan is not implemented, the olim are scattering and being lost, each going their own way. This is detrimental not only to the general needs of the olim, but also to their individual integration.

It is true that there are successes in the area of integration, livelihood, etc., on an individual basis, without waiting for organized efforts, etc. However, there is no doubt that the current lack of organization—until such organization is established—will be compensated for with an added boost if the effort is directed toward the unification of the olim, and subsequently through organized advocacy in both the material and spiritual realms.

To tell the truth, I am uncertain whether this approach is correct for olim who have already been in the country for several weeks, and the main intent of what is written above is that perhaps it will help with regard to those arriving now or in the near future.

It goes without saying that you may show this letter, or convey its contents, to those who you believe can do something in this direction.

I hope [10,554](#_ftn_2134) that you will follow my suggestion to print your article regarding the method of prostate surgery. Surely among your physician acquaintances there will be those who can translate it into Hebrew, if it is not worthwhile to publish it in Eretz Yisrael in the Russian language.

With wishes for a *Kesivah Vachasimah Tovah* for you and your entire family, and for good news regarding all that was written above.

## 10,550

B"H, 14 Elul, 5732
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mr. Yehuda, may he live and be well,

Peace and blessing!

[Russian]

With blessings for a *Kesivah Vachasimah Tovah* for a good and sweet year.

[Free Translation]

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter, in which you write regarding the approaches made to you by several different circles concerning work among academics, and that they promise they will not interfere, etc.

Presumably, you are already aware that in such communal activity, one must be especially careful not to involve extraneous factors, as this can cause opposition from certain circles that, otherwise, would have helped in this important work. Therefore, I was very pleased to hear the news that you—the academics of your circle—have organized yourselves and are consulting with Rabbi Leivov. May Hashem grant that all of this should be with great success.

With wishes for great success in your private life as well, together with your spouse.

## 10,557

B"H, 14 Elul, 5732
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mr. Elchanan Betzalel, may he live and be well,

Peace and blessing!

[Russian]

With the blessing of *kesivah v’chasimah tovah* for a good and sweet year, and for good tidings.

[Free Translation]

I received your letter with much delay, in which you write about the initial meetings of the organization for academics that was discussed here.

It is self-understood that this matter requires the organizer to work in a state of tranquility, and therefore the organization must relieve him of any concern for his livelihood. In other words, this work should be a paid position.

According to the information I have received in the meantime, you are already consulting with Rabbi Leivov.

May Hashem grant that all of this should be with great success.
